## F-024

- fact: Vanilla Doom 1.9 has 16 hardcoded engine limits across 6 categories (demo, game, renderer, save, screen, specials). The most parity-critical are MAXVISPLANES (128, I_Error on overflow), MAXSPECIALCROSS (8, spechit memory corruption), SAVEGAMESIZE (0x2C000 = 180224 bytes), and MAXDEMOSIZE (0x20000 = 131072 bytes). MAXOPENINGS (20480) is derived from SCREENWIDTH \* 64.
- source: Doom 1.9 source code, Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 enforcement (step 01-005)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 04-001, 07-006, 09-010, 17-010

## F-025

- fact: The shareware title/demo loop cycles through 6 states (demosequence modulo 6): TITLEPIC (170 tics, D_INTRO music), DEMO1 (E1M5), CREDIT (200 tics, inherited music), DEMO2 (E1M3), HELP2 (200 tics, inherited music), DEMO3 (E1M7). Shareware uses HELP2 at state 4; retail uses CREDIT; commercial uses TITLEPIC. Total cycle is 11566 tics (~330.5s). Only TITLEPIC explicitly starts music; CREDIT and HELP2 inherit the preceding demo's level music. pagetic values (170, 200) are hardcoded in D_DoAdvanceDemo.
- source: Chocolate Doom d_main.c D_DoAdvanceDemo, DOOM1.WAD lump directory (step 01-006)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 07-005, 16-010, 17-010

## F-026

- fact: Vanilla Doom has 22 documented rendering and audio behavioral quirks across 4 categories: renderer (10), audio (6), music (3), palette (3). Key parity-critical quirks include hall-of-mirrors no-clear (framebuffer never zeroed between frames), discrete light diminishing (16 levels via LIGHTLEVELS/LIGHTSEGSHIFT), sound-reject-table propagation (REJECT table doubles as acoustic barrier affecting game state), sfx-priority-eviction (hardcoded per-effect priority), and DMX lump format (8-byte header, 11025 Hz unsigned 8-bit PCM).
- source: Doom 1.9 source code, Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 behavior, reference default.cfg (step 01-007)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 05-003, 05-004, 05-010, 15-007, 17-010

## F-027

- fact: PLAYPAL contains 14 palettes (0=normal, 1-8=damage red via STARTREDPALS/NUMREDPALS, 9-12=bonus pickup via STARTBONUSPALS/NUMBONUSPALS, 13=radiation suit via RADIATIONPAL). Berserk contributes to the damage red counter, not a separate palette. Palette selection follows strict precedence: damage/berserk > bonus > radiation > normal. COLORMAP contains 34 colormaps: 0-31 light levels, 32 invulnerability inverse grayscale, 33 all-black.
- source: Doom 1.9 st_stuff.c ST_doPaletteStuff, r_draw.c (step 01-007)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 05-003, 05-004, 09-010

## F-028

- fact: Sound effect distance attenuation uses S_CLOSE_DIST (200 map units, full volume) and S_CLIPPING_DIST (1200 map units, silent) with strictly linear rolloff. Stereo separation is computed from listener-to-source angle centered at 128 with S_STEREO_SWING (96). The DMX sound lump format uses a 3-field 8-byte header (uint16LE format=0x0003, uint16LE sampleRate=11025, uint32LE sampleCount) followed by unsigned 8-bit PCM with 2 padding bytes (first and last sample).
- source: Doom 1.9 s_sound.c, i_sound.c (step 01-007)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 05-010, 15-007, 15-011

## F-029

- fact: The Doom engine defines 4 game modes (shareware, registered, retail, commercial) and 4 game missions (doom, doom2, pack_tnt, pack_plut). Shareware uses DOOM1.WAD; registered and retail both use DOOM.WAD (differing only in episode count 3 vs 4). Commercial mode covers Doom II (DOOM2.WAD), TNT (TNT.WAD), and Plutonia (PLUTONIA.WAD), all with 32 MAPxx-named maps. Doom 1 family uses ExMy map naming with 9 maps per episode. All targets emulate version 1.9.

- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 02-001, 07-003, 17-010

## F-030

- fact: The compatibility target progression is C1 (shareware) → C2 (registered) → C3 (retail/Ultimate Doom) → C4 (Doom II). Final Doom targets C5 (TNT) and C6 (Plutonia) branch from C4 independently. C4 introduces 8 new monster types, the Super Shotgun, TEXTURE2 lump, commercial intermission screens, and sky texture transitions at MAP12 and MAP21. C3 changes the title/demo loop to use CREDIT instead of HELP2 at demosequence state 4.
- source: Doom 1.9 source code, Chocolate Doom d_main.c D_DoAdvanceDemo

- verified: verified

## F-034

- fact: The input script format defines 6 event kinds (key-down, key-up, mouse-button-down, mouse-button-up, mouse-move, quit) as a discriminated union keyed by the `kind` field. Keyboard events use Doom internal key codes (0–0xFF, single unsigned byte), not raw hardware scan codes or Windows virtual key codes. Mouse buttons are 0-indexed (0=left, 1=right, 2=middle, 3=extra1, 4=extra2, max index 4). Events are ordered ascending by tic number; multiple events at the same tic are permitted and processed in array order. A totalTics of 0 means no explicit duration limit.
- source: src/oracles/inputScript.ts (step 02-003)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 02-004, 06-004, 06-005, 17-010

## F-035

- fact: The state hash format defines 6 components (automap, combined, player, rng, sectors, thinkers) for per-tic game-state verification. Individual components are hashed independently as SHA-256; the combined component is derived by hashing the concatenation of all individual hashes in ASCIIbetical component-name order. The default sampling interval is 35 tics (one second at Doom tic rate). Entries are sorted ascending by tic. Tic 0 captures initial state before any game logic runs. The rng component isolates P_Random/M_Random index divergence for precise nondeterminism detection.
- source: src/oracles/stateHash.ts (step 02-004)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 02-005, 02-009, 17-010

## F-036

- fact: The framebuffer hash format captures the raw 320x200 palette-indexed byte array (64000 bytes, one byte per pixel) as a SHA-256 hash, paired with the active PLAYPAL palette index (0-13). The palette index is essential for parity because identical pixel data under different palettes produces different visible output. The default sampling interval matches the state hash format at 35 tics (one second). Entries are sorted ascending by tic.
- source: src/oracles/framebufferHash.ts (step 02-005), F-027 (14 palettes), F-033 (320x200 internal framebuffer)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 02-006, 02-008, 17-010

## F-037

- fact: The audio hash format captures the mixed SFX PCM output as a SHA-256 hash per tic period, paired with the active channel count (0-8). Each tic produces exactly 1260 samples (44100 / 35) of signed 16-bit stereo PCM at the output sample rate. DMX sound effects are resampled from 11025 Hz to 44100 Hz (4x factor). Music output is tracked separately by the music-event-log format. The default sampling interval is 35 tics (one second). Entries are sorted ascending by tic.
- source: src/oracles/audioHash.ts (step 02-006), F-028 (DMX format, distance attenuation), F-033 (44100 Hz, 8 channels)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 02-007, 15-007, 17-010

## F-038

- fact: The music event log format captures discrete music state transitions (4 event kinds: change-music, pause-music, resume-music, stop-music) rather than periodic PCM hashes, because music is event-driven and synthesized differently per device. ChangeMusicEvent carries the MUS lump name and looping flag. MUS format uses 16 channels with channel 15 as percussion (mapped to MIDI channel 9). Music volume operates on a 0-15 integer scale independently of SFX volume. The reference configuration uses music device 3 (General MIDI) and volume 8.
- source: src/oracles/musicEventLog.ts (step 02-007), F-025 (title/demo loop music), F-026 (music quirks), F-033 (music device/volume config)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 02-008, 15-007, 17-010

## F-039

- fact: The full GDI window capture pipeline (GetDesktopWindow → GetDC → CreateCompatibleDC → CreateCompatibleBitmap → SelectObject → BitBlt → GetDIBits → cleanup) is fully functional from Bun FFI using direct dlopen of user32.dll (3 functions: GetDesktopWindow, GetDC, ReleaseDC) and gdi32.dll (7 functions: BitBlt, CreateCompatibleBitmap, CreateCompatibleDC, DeleteDC, DeleteObject, GetDIBits, SelectObject). No @bun-win32 package dependencies are required; dlopen with FFIType definitions suffices. GetDIBits with negative biHeight in BITMAPINFOHEADER produces top-down BGRA scan order suitable for deterministic hashing. The capture buffer for the reference 640x480x32bpp display is exactly 1,228,800 bytes.
- source: tools/reference/windowCaptureProbe.ts (step 02-008), live desktop capture test
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 02-009, 17-010

Two sequential sandboxes always get distinct paths. The entire probe runs in ~200ms.

## F-041

- fact: Manual A/B gate verification defines 6 perceptual/behavioral domains (audio, input, music, timing, title-loop, visual) and 3 verdict types (fail, inconclusive, pass). Title-loop runs require all 6 domains to pass; demo-playback runs require only 4 (audio, music, timing, visual) because input is scripted (F-034) and the title-loop state machine is not exercised. A gate set is complete only when every required domain has at least one "pass" verdict; "fail" and "inconclusive" do not satisfy the requirement.
- source: src/oracles/manualGatePolicy.ts (step 02-010)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 03-001, 17-010

## F-042

- fact: The milliseconds-per-tic value (1000 / 35 ≈ 28.5714) is not an integer, but 35 tics always accumulates to exactly 1000ms due to IEEE 754 floating-point identity. Individual tic-to-millisecond conversions carry fractional values; tests and timing logic must not truncate or round prematurely. The nanoseconds-per-tic value (1e9 / 35 ≈ 28_571_428.5714) is similarly non-integer.
- source: test/\_harness/determinism.ts (step 03-007)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 06-001, 06-002, 07-006, 17-010

## F-043

- fact: FixedMul uses ((int64_t)a * (int64_t)b) >> FRACBITS with implicit int32 truncation on return. The full 64-bit product of two int32 values can reach ~2^62, exceeding JavaScript's Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER (2^53). A 16-bit decomposition (aHi*bHi*0x10000 + aHi*bLo + aLo*bHi + (aLo*bLo>>>16)) | 0 keeps all intermediates within safe-integer range. The arithmetic right shift means negative results round toward negative infinity, not toward zero — this is load-bearing for parity (e.g., (-3 \* 1) >> 16 = -1, not 0).
- source: Chocolate Doom m_fixed.c FixedMul, src/core/fixed.ts (step 04-003)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 04-004, 04-006, 17-010

## F-044

- fact: FixedDiv uses an overflow guard `(abs(a) >> 14) >= abs(b)` that returns FIXED*MAX or FIXED_MIN based on `(a ^ b) < 0`. When the guard does not trigger, the quotient is `(a * 0x10000) / b`truncated to int32. The product`a _ 0x10000`fits within Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER (at most 2^47 < 2^53). Division truncates toward zero, matching C99 integer division. The guard also handles division by zero (abs(b)==0 means guard always triggers). abs(FIXED_MIN) is undefined behavior in C but evaluates to FIXED_MIN on x86; the`(-a) | 0` pattern reproduces this exactly, causing the guard to miss overflow for a=FIXED_MIN (e.g., fixedDiv(FIXED_MIN, 1) = 0 instead of clamping). The overflow guard boundary is conservative: fixedDiv(16384 _ FRACUNIT, FRACUNIT) clamps to FIXED*MAX even though the true result (16384 * FRACUNIT) would fit in int32.
- source: Chocolate Doom m_fixed.c FixedDiv, src/core/fixed.ts (step 04-004)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 04-005, 04-006, 17-010

## F-045

- fact: Doom uses Binary Angle Measurement (BAM) with `angle_t` as unsigned 32-bit integer. A full circle is 0 to 0xFFFFFFFF (2^32 - 1). The four cardinal constants are ANG45 (0x20000000), ANG90 (0x40000000), ANG180 (0x80000000), ANG270 (0xC0000000). Eight ANG45 units equal exactly one full circle (0x100000000). Angle subtraction in the renderer produces negative signed values that reinterpret as large unsigned values via uint32 wrapping — this is load-bearing for FOV delta computation. In JavaScript, `>>> 0` reproduces C unsigned overflow semantics.
- source: Doom 1.9 doomdef.h angle_t typedef and ANG\* defines, src/core/angle.ts (step 04-005)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 04-006, 08-006, 09-010, 17-010

## F-046

- fact: The three Doom trig tables (finesine, finetangent, tantoangle) cannot be reproduced bit-for-bit from any single IEEE 754 formula. finesine has 33 values that differ by ±1 from trunc(65536 _ sin((i+0.5)/8192 _ 2\*PI)), finetangent has 204 mismatches (max diff 18994) from the closest formula, and tantoangle has 1874 mismatches. The original generation tool is lost. For parity, all three tables must be hardcoded from the canonical tables.c values. The finetangent table is perfectly antisymmetric: finetangent[i] === -finetangent[4095-i].
- source: Chocolate Doom tables.c, empirical formula verification (step 04-006)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-006, 09-010, 17-010

## F-047

- fact: SlopeDiv uses unsigned integer division: answer = (num << 3) / (den >> 8). When den < 512, it returns SLOPERANGE (2048). When the quotient exceeds SLOPERANGE, it clamps to SLOPERANGE. The left shift (num << 3) wraps modulo 2^32 for large inputs. In JavaScript, `<<` produces a signed 32-bit result and `>>> 0` converts to unsigned, and the division result must be truncated with `>>> 0` to match C unsigned integer division.
- source: Chocolate Doom tables.c SlopeDiv function (step 04-006)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-006, 09-010, 17-010

## F-048

- fact: Doom uses a 256-element lookup table RNG (m_random.c), not a formula-based PRNG. Two independent indices walk the same table: prndindex for the gameplay-deterministic stream (P_Random) and rndindex for the non-deterministic menu stream (M_Random). Both indices start at 0. P_Random and M_Random pre-increment the index before lookup, so the first call after M_ClearRandom returns rndtable[1] (value 8), not rndtable[0] (value 0). P_SubRandom consumes two P_Random values and returns first minus second. M_ClearRandom resets both indices to 0. Stream separation is load-bearing: menu RNG calls must never advance prndindex or demo playback desyncs.
- source: Chocolate Doom m_random.c, src/core/rng.ts (step 04-007)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 07-005, 09-010, 16-010, 17-010

## F-049

- fact: DOOM1.WAD marker ranges contain inner sub-markers: F_START/F_END encloses 56 entries (F1_START + 54 data flats + F1_END), P_START/P_END encloses 167 entries (P1_START + 165 data patches + P1_END), S_START/S_END encloses 483 entries (all sprite data, no inner markers). The outer markers F_START, F_END, S_START, S_END, P_START, P_END plus inner markers P1_START, P1_END total the 8 lumps in the "marker" category. Inner markers F1_START and F1_END are categorized with the flat lump group, not the marker group.
- source: DOOM1.WAD directory parse, wad-directory-summary.json (step 05-002)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 05-003, 05-007, 05-008, 17-010

## F-050

- fact: COLORMAP lump in DOOM1.WAD contains 34 colormaps of 256 bytes each (8704 bytes total). Colormaps 0-31 are light levels, 32 is invulnerability inverse grayscale, 33 is all-black (every entry maps to 0). Colormap 0 (full brightness) is near-identity but has exactly 7 non-identity entries at palette indices 168, 190, 191, 208, 224, 240, and 247 — these are remapped even at full brightness by the WAD build tools.
- source: DOOM1.WAD COLORMAP lump parse (step 05-004)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-010, 17-010

## F-051

- fact: The PNAMES lump in DOOM1.WAD contains 350 patch name entries (4-byte int32LE count header + 350 × 8-byte null-padded ASCII names = 2804 bytes). These names are indexed by TEXTURE1/TEXTURE2 composite texture definitions to reference patch graphics. The count (350) exceeds the 165 data patches between the P*START/P_END markers because PNAMES references patches from multiple WAD sections (wall patches, door patches, switch patches, etc.). The first entry is WALL00_3; the last is SW2_4. All names are uppercase ASCII matching [A-Z0-9*]+.
- source: DOOM1.WAD PNAMES lump parse (step 05-005)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 05-006, 13-005, 17-010

## F-052

- fact: DOOM1.WAD TEXTURE1 lump contains exactly 125 composite texture definitions in 9234 bytes. The lump format starts with a 4-byte int32LE texture count, followed by count × 4-byte int32LE offset directory (offsets relative to lump start), then variable-length texture definitions. Each texture definition is a 22-byte header (8-byte name, 4-byte masked, 2-byte width, 2-byte height, 4-byte obsolete columndirectory, 2-byte patchcount) followed by patchcount × 10-byte patch entries (2-byte originX, 2-byte originY, 2-byte PNAMES index, 2-byte stepdir unused, 2-byte colormap unused). Total patches across all 125 textures: 598. Maximum PNAMES index used: 162 (within the 350-entry PNAMES range). First texture: AASTINKY (24×72, 2 patches). All 125 names are unique. No masked textures in shareware TEXTURE1.
- source: DOOM1.WAD TEXTURE1 lump parse (step 05-006)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 05-007, 13-005, 17-010

## F-053

- fact: The MUS lump format has a 16-byte fixed header: 4-byte magic "MUS\x1A", 6 × uint16LE fields (scoreLength, scoreStart, channelCount, secondaryChannelCount, instrumentCount, padding), followed by instrumentCount × uint16LE instrument numbers, then score data starting at scoreStart. MUS uses 16 channels (0-15) with channel 15 as percussion (mapped to MIDI channel 9). The secondaryChannelCount is always 0 in practice. DOOM1.WAD contains 13 MUS lumps: D_E1M1 through D_E1M9, D_INTER, D_INTRO, D_VICTOR, D_INTROA. All parse successfully with valid channel counts (≤16) and non-empty score data.
- source: DOOM1.WAD MUS lump parse (step 05-010), Doom source mus2mid.c
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 15-007, 17-010

## F-054

- fact: The ENDOOM lump is exactly 4000 bytes: 80 columns × 25 rows × 2 bytes per cell (character + attribute). The character byte is a CP437 code point (0-255). The attribute byte encodes foreground color (bits 0-3, range 0-15), background color (bits 4-6, range 0-7), and blink flag (bit 7). Cells are stored in row-major order. DOOM1.WAD's ENDOOM lump contains non-space characters (it is a visual exit screen with colored text art).
- source: DOOM1.WAD ENDOOM lump parse (step 05-010), VGA text mode specification
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 07-008, 17-010

## F-055

- fact: The Doom 1.9 demo format stores tic commands as 4 raw bytes per active player per tic: int8 forwardmove, int8 sidemove, uint8 angleturn (shifted left 8 during G_ReadDemoTiccmd playback), uint8 buttons. The end-of-demo marker is a single 0x80 byte. Demo lump size equals DEMO_HEADER_SIZE (13) + ticCount × DEMO_TIC_SIZE (4) × activePlayers + 1 (end marker). This identity holds exactly for all 3 shareware demos.
- source: DOOM1.WAD DEMO1/DEMO2/DEMO3 lump parse (step 05-010), Doom source g_game.c G_ReadDemoTiccmd
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 07-005, 16-010, 17-010

## F-056

- fact: Win32 QueryPerformanceFrequency returns a constant value for the system's lifetime. On modern Windows (10+) it is typically 10 MHz (10_000_000). The value is always at least 1 MHz. Integer division of the frequency by 35 yields the QPC tick count for one Doom tic (e.g., 10_000_000 / 35 = 285_714 ticks per tic). QueryPerformanceCounter returns a monotonically non-decreasing bigint read as a little-endian int64 from an 8-byte LARGE_INTEGER buffer.
- source: Win32 QueryPerformanceCounter/QueryPerformanceFrequency documentation, confirmed by live test on current system (step 06-001)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 06-002, 07-006, 07-007, 17-010

## F-057

- fact: The Win32 MSG structure on 64-bit Windows is 48 bytes (0x30). Field offsets: HWND at 0x00 (8 bytes), UINT message at 0x08 (4 bytes + 4 padding), WPARAM at 0x10 (8-byte UINT_PTR), LPARAM at 0x18 (8-byte LONG_PTR), DWORD time at 0x20 (4 bytes), POINT.x at 0x24 (4 bytes), POINT.y at 0x28 (4 bytes + 4 tail padding). WM_QUIT (0x0012) is the only message that terminates a PeekMessage drain loop; it is never translated or dispatched, matching the standard Win32 message-loop contract. PeekMessage with PM_REMOVE (0x0001) provides non-blocking drain identical to Chocolate Doom's SDL_PollEvent pattern.
- source: Win32 SDK MSG structure documentation, canonical Win32 message loop pattern (step 06-003)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 06-004, 06-005, 06-006, 07-007, 17-010

## F-058

- fact: Doom's internal key code space uses a single unsigned byte (0x00-0xFF). The translation from DOS hardware scan codes to Doom key codes follows the xlatekey[128] table from vanilla Doom's i_ibm.c. Printable characters keep their ASCII values (lowercase for letters). Modifier keys use 0x80 + DOS scan code (RSHIFT=0xB6, RCTRL=0x9D, RALT=0xB8). Arrow keys use 0xAC-0xAF. F-keys also follow the 0x80 + DOS scan code rule: F1-F10 are 0xBB-0xC4 (DOS 0x3B-0x44), F11=0xD7 (DOS 0x57), F12=0xD8 (DOS 0x58). KEY_F12 (0xD8) and KEY_RCTRL (0x9D) are distinct — there is no collision. Scan code 0x45 (NumLock position) maps to KEY_PAUSE (0xFF), not KEY_NUMLOCK. On Win32, LPARAM bits 16-23 carry the DOS-compatible hardware scan code; the extended-key flag (bit 24) is ignored for Doom translation since physical arrow keys and numpad equivalents produce the same Doom key code.
- source: Vanilla Doom i_ibm.c xlatekey[], Chocolate Doom doomkeys.h, Win32 WM_KEYDOWN LPARAM documentation (step 06-004)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 06-005, 06-006, 06-007, 07-002, 17-010

## F-059

- fact: The reference default.cfg stores key bindings as DOS scan codes (not Doom key codes). The xlatekey table converts these to Doom key codes at runtime: key_right(77)→KEY_RIGHTARROW(0xAE), key_left(75)→KEY_LEFTARROW(0xAC), key_up(72)→KEY_UPARROW(0xAD), key_down(80)→KEY_DOWNARROW(0xAF), key_fire(29)→KEY_RCTRL(0x9D), key_use(57)→Space(0x20), key_strafe(56)→KEY_RALT(0xB8), key_speed(54)→KEY_RSHIFT(0xB6), key_strafeleft(51)→comma(0x2C), key_straferight(52)→period(0x2E). Config loading must apply this xlatekey translation to convert stored DOS scan codes into the Doom key codes used by G_BuildTiccmd and the menu responder chain.
- source: reference default.cfg, config-variable-summary.json (step 06-004, cross-referencing F-022)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 07-002, 17-010

## F-060

- fact: Doom uses 5 mouse buttons indexed 0-4 (left, right, middle, extra1, extra2) with a 5-bit bitmask for button state. Mouse acceleration is piecewise-linear: below the threshold (default 10) deltas pass through unchanged; above the threshold the excess is multiplied by the acceleration factor (default 2.0) and the result is truncated to integer. Y-axis is inverted at the OS layer (screen-down = Doom-forward). Deltas accumulate between tics and are drained/cleared at sample time, matching Chocolate Doom's I_ReadMouse pattern.
- source: Chocolate Doom i_video.c I_ReadMouse, reference config-variable-summary.json mouse_threshold=10, mouse_acceleration=2.0 (step 06-005)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 06-006, 06-007, 10-002

## F-061

- fact: Win32 mouse button messages map to Doom button indices: WM_LBUTTONDOWN/UP(0x0201/0x0202)→0, WM_RBUTTONDOWN/UP(0x0204/0x0205)→1, WM_MBUTTONDOWN/UP(0x0207/0x0208)→2, WM_XBUTTONDOWN/UP(0x020B/0x020C)→3 or 4 depending on HIWORD(wParam) XBUTTON1(1) or XBUTTON2(2). Each button-up message is exactly one greater than its button-down counterpart.
- source: Win32 API documentation, step 06-005 implementation
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 06-006, 06-007

## F-062

- fact: The ticcmd_t structure is 8 bytes with 6 fields: forwardmove (int8, offset 0), sidemove (int8, offset 1), angleturn (int16, offset 2), consistancy (int16, offset 4), chatchar (uint8, offset 6), buttons (uint8, offset 7). G_BuildTiccmd packs input using movement speed lookup tables (forwardmove[]={0x19, 0x32}, sidemove[]={0x18, 0x28}), angle turn speeds (angleturn[]={640, 1280, 320} for normal/fast/slow), mouse multipliers (turn: mouseX*0x8, strafe: mouseX*2), and movement clamping to MAXPLMOVE (0x32=50). Button flags: BT_ATTACK=1, BT_USE=2, BT_CHANGE=4, weapon bits in bits 3-5 (BT_WEAPONMASK=0x38, BT_WEAPONSHIFT=3). Doom uses counterclockwise-positive angle convention (positive angleturn = turn left). The demo format stores only 4 of 6 fields (forwardmove, sidemove, angleturn as uint8 high byte, buttons), omitting consistancy and chatchar.
- source: Doom 1.9 d_ticcmd.h, g_game.c G_BuildTiccmd, d_event.h button defines (step 06-007)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 06-008, 07-006, 10-002, 17-010

## F-063

- fact: Doom's internal framebuffer is 320x200 pixels (SCREENWIDTH=320, SCREENHEIGHT=200, 64000 bytes indexed). With aspect_ratio_correct enabled (the reference default), the display height is corrected from 200 to 240 (factor 6/5 = 1.2), producing a 4:3 display aspect ratio (320:240 = 4:3). The reference config uses screen_width=640, screen_height=480, which is exactly 2x integer scale of 320x240. Without aspect correction, the source aspect is 8:5 (320:200). Presentation in non-matching client areas uses pillarboxing (wider-than-source) or letterboxing (taller-than-source) with centered placement.
- source: Chocolate Doom i_video.c, reference chocolate-doom.cfg (screen_width=640, screen_height=480, aspect_ratio_correct=1), F-033 (step 06-008)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 07-001, 17-010

## F-064

- fact: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 M_CheckParm performs case-insensitive argument scanning starting at index 1 (skipping program name at index 0) and returns a 1-based index or 0 for "not found". M_CheckParmWithArgs additionally verifies that the required number of trailing arguments exist. Vanilla Doom was case-sensitive; Chocolate Doom changed this for usability.
- source: Chocolate Doom m_argv.c (M_CheckParm, M_CheckParmWithArgs, M_ParmExists)

- fact: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 config load precedence uses two disjoint config files loaded in order: default.cfg (43 vanilla variables, overridable with -config) then chocolate-doom.cfg (113 extended variables, overridable with -extraconfig). Both default to configDirectory + filename. Hardcoded defaults are overwritten by file values. Unknown variable names in files are silently ignored. Missing files cause no error. The config file format is name<whitespace>value per line, with double-quoted strings, decimal or 0x-prefixed hex integers, and decimal floats.

## F-066

For doom2/pack_tnt/pack_plut/pack_hacx → commercial. For pack_chex → retail. Unknown IWAD fallback checks MAP01 (→ commercial/doom2) then E1M1 (→ doom + episode check), else indetermined. The IWAD filename table maps 10 filenames (doom.wad, doom1.wad, doom2.wad, tnt.wad, plutonia.wad, chex.wad, hacx.wad, freedoom1.wad, freedoom2.wad, freedm.wad) to missions case-insensitively. ## F-067

- fact: The 15-step D_DoomMain init sequence falls into 3 contiguous phases: early (3 steps: Z_Init, V_Init, M_LoadDefaults — before WAD loading), wad-load (1 step: W_Init), and post-identify (11 steps: I_Init through I_InitStretchTables — after game mode identification and banner). OPL_Init is a side-effect sub-initialization triggered by I_Init's sound hardware setup and always appears at index 5 immediately after I_Init at index 4. Between the wad-load and post-identify phases, D_IdentifyVersion, InitGameVersion, and D_SetGameDescription execute but produce no "X_Init:" stdout messages.

## F-068

- fact: The D_DoAdvanceDemo state machine uses demosequence modulo 6 for all game modes. The initial state in D_DoomMain is demosequence=-1 with advancedemo=true. D_PageTicker uses pre-decrement check (--pagetic < 0), meaning pagetic+1 tics elapse before the advance triggers. The page timer at pagetic=0 does NOT trigger advance — only pagetic=-1 does. D_DoAdvanceDemo clears advancedemo, increments demosequence, then dispatches: even states (0, 2, 4) are page displays, odd states (1, 3, 5) are demo playbacks. State 4 page lump varies by mode: commercial=TITLEPIC+D_DM2TTL, retail=CREDIT, all others=HELP2. Commercial state 0 uses pagetic=385 (35\*11); all other modes use pagetic=170 for state 0. Interlude pages (states 2, 4) always use pagetic=200.
- source: Chocolate Doom d_main.c D_DoAdvanceDemo/D_PageTicker/D_AdvanceDemo, title-sequence.json (step 07-005)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 07-006, 07-007, 17-010

## F-069

- fact: TryRunTics (single-player, ticdup=1) follows a strict build-then-run ordering: NetUpdate builds ticcmds for all newly elapsed tics first (startTic → buffer guard → buildTiccmd per new tic), then runs all available tics (advancedemo check → ticker → gametic++). The ticcmd circular buffer depth is BACKUPTICS=12 (not a power of 2; uses modulo, not masking). When maketic - gametic >= BACKUPTICS, NetUpdate stops building but still calls startTic on the overflow iteration before breaking. At 35 Hz, 12 tics buffer ~342.86ms. In single-player, gametic == maketic after every complete tryRunTics call.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 d_loop.c TryRunTics/NetUpdate/BuildNewTic (step 07-006)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 07-007, 07-008, 17-010

## F-070

- fact: D_DoomLoop (non-singletics, testcontrols=false) executes 4 pre-loop steps in order before entering the while(1) loop: TryRunTics (initial tic pump), V_RestoreBuffer, R_ExecuteSetViewSize, D_StartGameLoop. The per-frame loop body calls 4 subsystems in strict order: I_StartFrame → TryRunTics → S_UpdateSounds → D_Display. S_UpdateSounds always executes after TryRunTics so positional audio sources reflect the latest game state. D_Display is unconditionally last (testcontrols=false path). In singletics mode (debugging only), D_Display is called twice per iteration — once inside the singletics block and once at the end — but singletics is not used in normal gameplay and is out of scope for C1.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 d_main.c D_DoomLoop (step 07-007)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 07-008, 17-010

## F-071

- fact: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 uses a LIFO (last-in-first-out) linked-list stack for cleanup via I_AtExit. Handlers are registered during initialization and executed in reverse registration order by I_Quit (all handlers) or I_Error (only runOnError=true handlers). For shareware Doom, 8 handlers are registered chronologically: M_SaveDefaults (M_LoadDefaults), I_ShutdownTimer (I_InitTimer), I_ShutdownSound (I_InitSound), I_ShutdownMusic (I_InitMusic), S_Shutdown (S_Init), D_QuitNetGame (D_CheckNetGame), D_Endoom (D_DoomMain), I_ShutdownGraphics (I_InitGraphics in D_DoomLoop). All 8 are registered with runOnError=true in 2.2.1, so I_Error and I_Quit produce the same execution sequence. LIFO execution order: I_ShutdownGraphics → D_Endoom → D_QuitNetGame → S_Shutdown → I_ShutdownMusic → I_ShutdownSound → I_ShutdownTimer → M_SaveDefaults.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 i_system.c I_AtExit/I_Quit/I_Error, d_main.c D_DoomMain/D_DoomLoop (step 07-008)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-001, 17-010

## F-072

- fact: mapthing_t is a 10-byte struct with 5 signed int16LE fields (x, y, angle, type, options). MTF flags are MTF_EASY=1, MTF_NORMAL=2, MTF_HARD=4, MTF_AMBUSH=8, MTF_NOT_SINGLE=16. E1M1 has 138 things (1380 bytes), E1M8 has the fewest at 126, E1M6 the most at 463. Total across all 9 shareware maps is 2511 things. Every map has exactly one player 1 start (type=1). Player and deathmatch starts use options=7 (all skills). 14 things in E1M1 are multiplayer-only (MTF_NOT_SINGLE set).
- source: Chocolate Doom doomdata.h mapthing_t, p_setup.c P_LoadThings, DOOM1.WAD parse (step 08-001)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-002, 08-010, 09-002, 17-010

## F-073

- fact: mapvertex_t is 4 bytes (2x int16LE: x, y), maplinedef_t is 14 bytes (7x int16LE: v1, v2, flags, special, tag, sidenum[0], sidenum[1]), mapsidedef_t is 30 bytes (2x int16LE offsets + 3x 8-byte ASCII texture names + int16LE sector index), mapsector_t is 26 bytes (2x int16LE heights + 2x 8-byte ASCII flat names + 3x int16LE: lightlevel, special, tag). P_SetupLevel load order is Vertexes→Sectors→Sidedefs→Linedefs (pointer dependencies). Vertex and height int16 values are left-shifted by FRACBITS (16) to become 16.16 fixed-point. Linedef flags ML_BLOCKING=1 through ML_MAPPED=256 (9 bits). Slopetype derived from dx/dy: ST_HORIZONTAL=0, ST_VERTICAL=1, ST_POSITIVE=2, ST_NEGATIVE=3. BBOX indices: BOXTOP=0, BOXBOTTOM=1, BOXLEFT=2, BOXRIGHT=3. E1M1 counts: 467 vertexes, 475 linedefs, 648 sidedefs, 85 sectors. E1M8 fewest linedefs (333), E1M6 most (1352). Sidedef count = linedef count + two-sided linedef count.
- source: Chocolate Doom doomdata.h, p_setup.c P_LoadVertexes/P_LoadLineDefs/P_LoadSideDefs/P_LoadSectors, DOOM1.WAD parse (step 08-002)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-003, 08-006, 08-010, 17-010

## F-074

- fact: mapseg_t is 12 bytes (6x int16LE: v1, v2, angle, linedef, side, offset). mapsubsector_t is 4 bytes (2x int16LE: numsegs, firstseg). mapnode_t is 28 bytes (4x int16LE partition line x/y/dx/dy + 2x4 int16LE bbox[right][left] + 2x uint16LE children[right][left]). NF_SUBSECTOR=0x8000 flags a child as a subsector reference (lower 15 bits = subsector index). Seg angle is int16 << 16 (BAM format), offset is int16 << FRACBITS (fixed-point). Node partition and bbox fields are int16 << FRACBITS. BSP tree invariant: numNodes = numSubsectors - 1. E1M1 counts: 732 segs, 237 subsectors, 236 nodes. Subsector seg ranges are contiguous and cover all segs exactly.
- source: Chocolate Doom doomdata.h, p_setup.c P_LoadSegs/P_LoadSubsectors/P_LoadNodes, DOOM1.WAD parse (step 08-003)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-004, 08-005, 08-006, 08-010, 17-010

## F-075

- fact: BLOCKMAP lump format: 8-byte header (4x int16LE: originX, originY, columns, rows), followed by columns×rows uint16LE word-offset table, followed by block lists. Each block list is a sequence of int16LE values: leading 0 entry, linedef indices, terminated by -1 (0xFFFF unsigned). Origins are stored as map units in the header and left-shifted by FRACBITS at load time. Offset table values are absolute word indices from the start of the lump. MAPBLOCKSIZE=128 map units per cell, MAPBLOCKSHIFT=FRACBITS+7=23, MAPBTOFRAC=7. Vanilla P_BlockLinesIterator does NOT skip the leading 0 entry (it processes linedef 0). Multiple cells may share the same block list offset.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_setup.c P_LoadBlockMap, p_maputl.c P_BlockLinesIterator, DOOM1.WAD parse (step 08-004)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-005, 08-008, 08-010, 09-003, 09-004, 17-010

## F-076

- fact: REJECT lump is a flat bit-array of sectorCount² bits stored row-major with little-endian bit order within each byte. Size formula: ceil(sectorCount² / 8) = (sectorCount _ sectorCount + 7) >>> 3. Lookup formula from P_CheckSight in p_sight.c: pnum = s1 _ numsectors + s2; bytenum = pnum >> 3; bitnum = 1 << (pnum & 7); bit=1 means "reject" (no LOS), bit=0 means "might see" (needs full BSP trace). Matrix is NOT required to be symmetric. Diagonal entries (same sector) are zero in all DOOM1.WAD maps. Chocolate Doom's PadRejectArray handles undersized lumps by filling with zone allocator values to reproduce vanilla buffer overread behavior. E1M1: 85 sectors → 904 bytes, exactly matches lump size.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_setup.c P_LoadReject, p_sight.c P_CheckSight, p_rejectpad.c PadRejectArray, DOOM1.WAD parse (step 08-005)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-006, 09-003, 17-010

## F-077

- fact: R_PointOnSide, R_PointOnSegSide, and R_PointInSubsector are all defined in Chocolate Doom's r_main.c (not r_bsp.c). R_PointOnSide determines which side of a BSP partition line a point falls on (0=front/right, 1=back/left of direction of travel). It has three fast paths: (1) vertical partition (dx===0): result depends on x<=node.x inverted by sign of dy, (2) horizontal partition (dy===0): result depends on y<=node.y inverted by sign of dx, (3) sign-bit XOR quick-reject using ((dy^dx^dx_point^dy_point) & 0x80000000). The fallback uses a cross-product via FixedMul with one operand truncated by >>FRACBITS to avoid 32-bit overflow: left=FixedMul(dy>>16, dx_point), right=FixedMul(dy_point, dx>>16); right<left=>front(0), else back(1). On-line points return 1 (back). R_PointInSubsector walks from root node (numnodes-1) using pointOnSide at each internal node, stopping when NF_SUBSECTOR flag is set in child index.
- source: Chocolate Doom r_main.c (step 08-006)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-007, 08-009, 09-003, 17-010

## F-078

- fact: Vanilla Doom assigns each subsector's sector in P_GroupLines (p_setup.c) via the first-seg chain: subsector.firstseg → seg.linedef → linedef.sidenum[seg.side] → sidedef.sector. The seg.side field (0=front, 1=back) is load-bearing: back-side first segs resolve through sidenum1, producing a different sector than sidenum0 when the linedef separates two sectors. In E1M1, at least one subsector's first seg has side===1, confirming both code paths are exercised. The BSP tree covers the entire 2D plane, so R_PointInSubsector always returns a valid subsector index for any coordinate, including points far outside the playable area.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_setup.c P_GroupLines, verified against DOOM1.WAD E1M1 (step 08-007)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-008, 09-001, 09-002, 17-010

## F-079

- fact: P_BlockLinesIterator in p_maputl.c processes the leading 0 entry in every block list as linedef index 0 — it does NOT skip it. The validcount mechanism (per-linedef stamp compared to a global generation counter) deduplicates linedef visits across multiple cells within a single spatial query. Out-of-bounds cell coordinates silently return true (continue). Block lists are iterated in on-disk lump order. The cell index is row-major: y \* columns + x. World-to-block conversion is (coord - origin) >> MAPBLOCKSHIFT where MAPBLOCKSHIFT = FRACBITS + 7 = 23.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_maputl.c P_BlockLinesIterator, verified against DOOM1.WAD all 9 maps (step 08-008)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-009, 09-003, 09-004, 17-010

## F-080

- fact: P_InterceptVector uses >> 8 shifts (not >> FRACBITS) for the denominator and numerator partial products, giving coarser but overflow-safer precision. P_PointOnDivlineSide also uses >> 8 shifts in its FixedMul fallback, distinct from both R_PointOnSide (>> FRACBITS with sign-bit quick-reject) and P_PointOnLineSide (>> FRACBITS without sign-bit quick-reject). PIT_AddLineIntercepts selects between pointOnDivlineSide (for trace dx/dy > ±16 FRACUNIT) and pointOnLineSide (for shorter traces). P_PathTraverse nudges x1/y1 by FRACUNIT if exactly on a block boundary (mask = (1 << MAPBLOCKSHIFT) - 1 = 0x7FFFFF). The DDA walk is capped at 64 cells. P_TraverseIntercepts uses O(n²) selection-sort, marking consumed entries with FIXED_MAX. PT_ADDLINES=1, PT_ADDTHINGS=2, PT_EARLYOUT=4, MAXINTERCEPTS=128.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_maputl.c P_InterceptVector, P_PointOnDivlineSide, P_PointOnLineSide, PIT_AddLineIntercepts, P_PathTraverse, P_TraverseIntercepts (step 08-009)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-010, 09-003, 09-004, 17-010

## F-081

- fact: P_GroupLines in p_setup.c resolves each linedef's frontsector from sides[sidenum[0]].sector and backsector from sides[sidenum[1]].sector only if (flags & ML_TWOSIDED && sidenum[1] != -1); otherwise backsector is NULL (index -1). It then iterates all linedefs per sector to build line lists, computes sector bounding boxes via M_AddToBox (which uses else-if branches for x and y axes), derives sound origin as the integer center of the bbox, and computes sector blockboxes by expanding by MAXRADIUS (32\*FRACUNIT) and clamping to blockmap grid. P_SetupLevel parse order: blockmap, vertexes, sectors, sidedefs, linedefs, subsectors, nodes, segs, grouplines, things, reject.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_setup.c P_SetupLevel and P_GroupLines, verified against DOOM1.WAD E1M1 (step 08-010)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-001, 10-001, 13-001, 17-010

## F-082

- fact: The Doom thinker list (p_tick.c) is a circular doubly-linked list with a sentinel node (thinkercap). P_InitThinkers sets sentinel.prev = sentinel.next = sentinel. P_AddThinker inserts at the tail (before sentinel). P_RemoveThinker marks thinker->function as (actionf_v)(-1) for deferred removal (does NOT unlink). P_RunThinkers iterates from sentinel.next: removed nodes are unlinked, active nodes have their function called. Critically, for active thinkers the next pointer is captured AFTER calling the action function, so a thinker added during another's action IS visited in the same tic. Null function pointers are skipped but the node is not removed.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_tick.c, d_think.h (verified against source, step 09-001)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-002, 10-001, 17-010

## F-083

- fact: Doom's state table (info.c) contains exactly 967 entries (NUMSTATES) and the mobjinfo table contains exactly 137 entries (NUMMOBJTYPES). The statenum_t enum has values S_NULL (0) through S_TECH2LAMP4 (966). The mobjtype_t enum has values MT_PLAYER (0) through MT_MISC86 (136). There are 138 sprite names (NUMSPRITES). Each state has 7 fields: sprite, frame, tics, action, nextstate, misc1, misc2. Each mobjinfo has 23 fields. State tics of -1 means infinite duration. Frame values include an FF_FULLBRIGHT flag (0x8000) in the high bit.
- source: Chocolate Doom info.h/info.c, src/world/mobj.ts (step 09-002)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-003, 10-001, 17-010

## F-084

- fact: P_SetMobjState chains through 0-tic states in a do-while loop, calling each state's action function. A cycle counter (MOBJ_CYCLE_LIMIT = 1,000,000) guards against infinite loops. When the target state is S_NULL, the mobj is removed via P_RemoveMobj. P_SpawnMobj sets lastlook = P_Random() % MAXPLAYERS before setting the initial state. Reactiontime is only set when gameskill != sk_nightmare (5). ONFLOORZ = INT_MIN (-0x80000000), ONCEILINGZ = INT_MAX (0x7FFFFFFF).
- source: Chocolate Doom p_mobj.c P_SpawnMobj/P_SetMobjState/P_MobjThinker (step 09-002)

## F-085

- fact: P_CheckPosition uses two distinct blockmap iteration ranges: thing checks expand the bounding box by MAXRADIUS (32\*FRACUNIT) in all directions because mobjs are keyed by origin point and can overlap adjacent cells, while line checks use the raw bounding box without expansion. P_BoxOnLineSide uses slopetype-based fast paths for horizontal (BOXTOP/BOXBOTTOM vs v1.y) and vertical (BOXRIGHT/BOXLEFT vs v1.x) lines, with XOR sign inversion for reversed dx/dy, falling back to P_PointOnLineSide (pointOnSegSide) for diagonal lines. PIT_CheckLine's AABB non-overlap test uses <= and >= (edge-touching does not constitute crossing). P_LineOpening computes opentop as min(front ceiling, back ceiling), openbottom as max(front floor, back floor), and lowfloor as the lower of the two floors (for dropoff tracking). The validcount mechanism prevents duplicate line visits when a linedef appears in multiple blockmap cells within a single query.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_map.c P_CheckPosition/PIT_CheckThing/PIT_CheckLine, p_maputl.c P_BoxOnLineSide/P_LineOpening (step 09-003)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-005, 09-007, 09-010, 17-010

## F-086

- fact: P_TryMove checks five conditions in order after P_CheckPosition succeeds: (1) ceiling-floor gap must fit thing height (gap < height rejects, floatok stays false); (2) floatok is set true once gap is sufficient; (3) ceiling-thing.z must fit height unless MF_TELEPORT (< comparison); (4) floor-thing.z must not exceed 24\*FRACUNIT (MAXSTEPHEIGHT) unless MF_TELEPORT (> comparison, so exactly 24 map units is allowed); (5) floor-dropoff must not exceed MAXSTEPHEIGHT unless MF_DROPOFF or MF_FLOAT (> comparison). MF_NOCLIP skips all five checks and all special line processing. MF_TELEPORT skips checks 3-4 and special line processing but still checks 1-2 and 5. After a successful move, special lines from checkResult.specials are processed in reverse order (matching vanilla numspechit-- loop), and P_CrossSpecialLine is called only when P_PointOnLineSide(newPos) differs from P_PointOnLineSide(oldPos) and the line has a non-zero special. P_PointOnLineSide uses >> FRACBITS shifts (not >> 8 like R_PointOnSide), making the precision difference parity-significant.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_map.c P_TryMove (step 09-004)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-005, 09-007, 09-010, 17-010

## F-087

- fact: P_XYMovement (p_mobj.c) handles horizontal movement in a do-while sub-step loop. Momentum is clamped to MAXMOVE (30\*FRACUNIT = 0x1E0000) per axis before the loop. The sub-step trigger tests ONLY positive overflow: `if (xmove > MAXMOVE/2 || ymove > MAXMOVE/2)` — there is NO corresponding `xmove < -MAXMOVE/2` check, so negative-dominant momentum (e.g. momx near -MAXMOVE with small/zero ymove) calls P_TryMove exactly once per tic while positive-dominant momentum calls it twice. This is a vanilla quirk preserved for demo / blockmap-iteration parity. Inside the sub-step branch ptryx is computed as `mo->x + xmove/2` (C integer division, truncate toward zero) while xmove is updated via `xmove >>= 1` (arithmetic right shift, toward negative infinity). For the axis that triggered sub-stepping both values are positive and identical; for the paired axis, which may be negative odd, the asymmetry preserves total displacement across the two sub-moves. When blocked: players invoke P_SlideMove (or stop without it), missiles check the sky-ceiling hack (backsector->ceilingpic == skyflatnum via the ceilingline from CheckPositionResult) then call P_ExplodeMissile, other mobjs zero momx/momy. Friction phase: missiles/skull-fliers skip friction entirely; airborne mobjs (z > floorz, strict greater-than) skip friction; corpses on steps (floorz != subsector->sector->floorheight AND momentum > FRACUNIT/4 in either axis, strict greater-than) skip friction to slide off; below STOPSPEED (0x1000, strict less-than on both axes, player also needs zero forwardmove/sidemove) zeroes momentum and resets player walking frame (PLAY_RUN1..+3 → PLAY); otherwise friction = FixedMul(mom, 0xE800). P_ExplodeMissile: zeroes all momentum, P_SetMobjState to deathstate, tics -= P_Random()&3 (clamped to >= 1), then clears MF_MISSILE.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_mobj.c P_XYMovement / P_ExplodeMissile (step 09-005)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-006, 09-007, 17-010

## F-088

- fact: P_ZMovement (p_mobj.c) handles vertical movement, gravity, floor/ceiling clipping, MF_FLOAT chase, and lost soul bounce. Constants: GRAVITY=FRACUNIT (0x10000), FLOATSPEED=4*FRACUNIT (0x40000), VIEWHEIGHT=41*FRACUNIT. Gravity is version-independent: first airborne tic applies -GRAVITY*2 (when momz==0), subsequent tics apply -GRAVITY. MF_NOGRAVITY skips gravity entirely. Floor clipping uses z<=floorz (less-than-or-equal), ceiling uses z+height>ceilingz (strict greater-than). Lost soul floor bounce is version-dependent: in exe_ultimate/exe_final/exe_final2/exe_chex, momz=-momz fires BEFORE momz=0 (correct bounce). In exe_doom_1_9 and earlier, the bounce fires AFTER momz=0 (dead code, no actual bounce). Ceiling bounce is always active (not version-dependent). MF_FLOAT chase: when MF_FLOAT is set and target is non-null and neither MF_SKULLFLY nor MF_INFLOAT, the mobj floats toward target.z+height/2 at FLOATSPEED if horizontally within 3x the z-delta (using P_AproxDistance). P_AproxDistance: abs(dx)+abs(dy)-min(abs(dx),abs(dy))/2. Missile floor/ceiling explosion calls P_ExplodeMissile and returns, bypassed by MF_NOCLIP. Player smooth step-up adjusts viewheight when z<floorz before z correction. Player landing squat triggers when momz<-GRAVITY*8 (strict less-than).
- source: Chocolate Doom p_mobj.c P_ZMovement / p_maputl.c P_AproxDistance (step 09-006)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-007, 10-001, 17-010

## F-089

- fact: P_SlideMove (p_map.c) uses three leading-corner traces via P_PathTraverse to find the nearest blocking wall line, then decomposes the movement into a flush approach (minus fudge factor 0x800) and a wall-parallel slide via P_HitSlideLine. Constants: fudge = 0x800 (half a fractional unit), hitcount cap = 3 (retry limit before stairstep fallback), stairstep = try P_TryMove(x, y+momy) then P_TryMove(x+momx, y). PTR_SlideTraverse checks ML_TWOSIDED for two-sided lines, then openrange/opentop/openbottom/MAXSTEPHEIGHT for passability; one-sided lines skip back-face hits via P_PointOnLineSide. P_HitSlideLine has ST_HORIZONTAL (zeroes tmymove) and ST_VERTICAL (zeroes tmxmove) fast paths; for diagonal lines it uses R_PointToAngle2(0,0,dx,dy), deltaangle wrapping via += ANG180 when > ANG180, and finecosine/finesine LUT projection. Remainder fraction = FRACUNIT - original_frac, clamped to [0, FRACUNIT]. Momentum is updated to the slide vector components (momx = tmxmove, momy = tmymove) before the final P_TryMove. secondslidefrac/secondslideline are tracked but never read (dead variables).
- source: Chocolate Doom p_map.c P_SlideMove, PTR_SlideTraverse, P_HitSlideLine (step 09-007)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-008, 17-010

## F-090

- fact: P_ChangeSector (p_map.c) re-clips all things in a sector's blockbox after floor/ceiling height changes. Uses P_ThingHeightClip (calls P_CheckPosition at same x,y to recompute floorz/ceilingz; on-floor things follow floor, floating things clamped only if exceeding ceiling; returns false if clearance < height). PIT_ChangeSector processes crushed things in priority order: (1) dead bodies (health<=0) → S_GIBS state, MF_SOLID cleared (except exe_doom_1_2), height=0, radius=0; (2) MF_DROPPED items → P_RemoveMobj; (3) non-MF_SHOOTABLE → ignored; (4) living shootable → sets nofit=true, crush damage (10 HP with null inflictor/source) every 4 tics (leveltime&3==0), blood spawned at z+height/2 with P_SubRandom()<<12 momentum per axis. PIT_ChangeSector always returns true (never stops blockmap iteration). P_ChangeSector iterates x=[BOXLEFT..BOXRIGHT], y=[BOXBOTTOM..BOXTOP].
- source: Chocolate Doom p_map.c P_ChangeSector, PIT_ChangeSector, P_ThingHeightClip (step 09-008)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-009, 09-010, 17-010

## F-091

- fact: P_RadiusAttack (p_map.c) applies explosive damage using Chebyshev distance (max(|dx|,|dy|)) with linear falloff (bombdamage - dist). Distance is computed as (max(|dx|,|dy|) - thing.radius) >> FRACBITS, clamped to >= 0. Things at dist >= bombdamage are excluded. MT_CYBORG and MT_SPIDER are immune (boss concussion immunity). Line-of-sight check via P_CheckSight(thing, bombspot) required before damage. Blockmap range uses (damage + MAXRADIUS) << FRACBITS which overflows int32 (MAXRADIUS contribution is lost since MAXRADIUS << FRACBITS === 0). PIT_RadiusAttack always returns true (never stops early). Bombspot is passed as inflictor, bombsource as source to P_DamageMobj. Self-damage is possible if bombspot is MF_SHOOTABLE and in blocklinks.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_map.c P_RadiusAttack, PIT_RadiusAttack (step 09-009)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 09-010, 10-006, 17-010

## F-092

- fact: P_UseLines (p_map.c) casts a ray of USERANGE (64*FRACUNIT = 0x400000) from the player's position in the facing direction using P_PathTraverse with PT_ADDLINES. PTR_UseTraverse processes intercepted lines: non-special lines with openrange <= 0 play sfx_noway and stop; non-special lines with a positive opening are skipped; the first special line triggers P_UseSpecialLine(usething, line, side) and stops traversal. Only one special line can be activated per use-press. The side parameter is determined by P_PointOnLineSide(usething.x, usething.y, line) — 0 for front, 1 for back. The endpoint calculation uses integer multiply: x2 = x1 + (USERANGE >> FRACBITS) * finecosine[angle], avoiding fixedMul.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_map.c P_UseLines, PTR_UseTraverse (step 09-010)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 10-001, 17-010

## F-093

- fact: Vanilla Doom's spechit[8] buffer in PIT_CheckLine (p_map.c) overflows when more than 8 special lines are contacted during a single P_CheckPosition call. In the original doom2.exe memory layout, overflow writes corrupt adjacent globals: indices 9–12 overwrite tmbbox[0..3], index 13 overwrites crushchange, index 14 overwrites nofit. The written value is a synthetic pointer: DEFAULT_SPECHIT_MAGIC (0x01C09C98, matching PrBoom-plus) + lineIndex \* 0x3E (line_t struct size = 62 bytes). Chocolate Doom expands the buffer to MAXSPECIALCROSS=20 but preserves MAXSPECIALCROSS_ORIGINAL=8 and emulates the overflow via SpechitOverrun() for demo compatibility. The -spechit command-line argument can override the base address.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_map.c SpechitOverrun, PIT_CheckLine, p_local.h (step 09-010)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 17-010

## F-094

- fact: EV_Teleport (p_telept.c) iterates sectors by tag, then walks the thinker list for MT_TELEPORTMAN (doomednum 14, MF_NOSECTOR|MF_NOBLOCKMAP, spawnstate S_NULL) in the matching sector. P_TeleportMove (p_map.c) finds the destination sector via R_PointInSubsector, iterates blockmap cells (expanded by MAXRADIUS) calling PIT_StompThing for telefrag (10000 damage), then unlinks/relinks the thing. After successful move: z=floorz (Doom 1.9 behavior, exe_final skips this), fog spawned at source (oldx/oldy/oldz) and destination (dest + 20\*finecosine/finesine[angle>>ANGLETOFINESHIFT]), player reactiontime=18, angle=destination angle, momentum zeroed. Missiles (MF_MISSILE) cannot teleport. Back-side activation (side=1) rejected so players can walk out. PIT_StompThing: monsters cannot telefrag except on boss maps (gamemap==30 in Doom 2; never in Doom 1).
- source: Chocolate Doom p_telept.c EV_Teleport, p_map.c P_TeleportMove/PIT_StompThing (step 09-011)

P_SetupPsprites clears all psprites, sets pendingweapon=readyweapon, calls P_BringUpWeapon which sets sy=WEAPONBOTTOM(128\*FRACUNIT), calls P_SetPsprite to upstate, then sets pendingweapon=wp_nochange. ## F-096

- fact: P_Thrust (p_user.c) shifts angle >> ANGLETOFINESHIFT, then adds FixedMul(move, finecosine[angle]) to momx and FixedMul(move, finesine[angle]) to momy. P_MovePlayer applies angleturn << FRACBITS to mo.angle (unsigned wrap), checks onground = (z <= floorz), calls P_Thrust with forwardmove*2048 at mo.angle (if onground) and sidemove*2048 at mo.angle-ANG90 (if onground), triggers S_PLAY_RUN1 if moving and in S_PLAY state. P_CalcHeight computes bob = (momx²+momy²)>>2 clamped to MAXBOB(0x100000=16px), uses finesine[(FINEANGLES/20*leveltime)&FINEMASK] oscillation with bob/2 amplitude. Viewheight converges to VIEWHEIGHT(41*FRACUNIT) via deltaviewheight += FRACUNIT/4, clamped at VIEWHEIGHT/2 minimum, deltaviewheight prevented from reaching 0 (forced to 1). CF_NOMOMENTUM/airborne path has vanilla quirk: viewz set to z+VIEWHEIGHT (clamped to ceiling-4*FRACUNIT) then overwritten to z+viewheight (bypassing clamp).

## F-097

- fact: P_GiveAmmo (p_inter.c) takes num as clip loads (not individual rounds); num=0 gives half a clip via floor(clipammo[type]/2). clipammo[] = [10, 4, 20, 1] for clip/shell/cell/misl. Baby (sk_baby=0) and Nightmare (sk_nightmare=4) skills double the amount via <<1. Pickup is rejected if ammo==am_noammo or already at maxammo. When going from zero ammo to non-zero, an auto-switch fires: clip→chaingun(if owned) or pistol (only from fist), shell→shotgun (from fist/pistol), cell→plasma (from fist/pistol), misl→missile (only from fist). The am_misl case falls through to default:break in the original C (missing break; harmless). Auto-switch does NOT fire if the player already had non-zero ammo of that type. P_CheckAmmo weapon preference cascade: plasma(non-shareware) → SSG(commercial, >2 shells) → chaingun → shotgun → pistol → chainsaw → missile → BFG(non-shareware, >40 cells) → fist. BFG ammo-per-shot=40 (deh_bfg_cells_per_shot), SSG=2, all others=1. The do-while loop always terminates in one pass (fist fallback). P_GiveWeapon: netgame non-deathmatch-2 non-dropped path gives bonuscount+=6 (BONUSADD), weapon, deathmatch?5:2 clips, pendingweapon, sfx_wpnup for console player, returns false (weapon stays on map). Single-player/altdeath path: dropped→1 clip, placed→2 clips; weapon only given+pendingweapon set if not already owned; returns gaveweapon||gaveammo. Backpack (SPR_BPAK): first pickup doubles all maxammo, sets backpack flag; every pickup gives 1 clip of each type via P_GiveAmmo.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_inter.c P_GiveAmmo/P_GiveWeapon/P_TouchSpecialThing(SPR_BPAK), p_pspr.c P_CheckAmmo, deh_misc.h defaults (step 10-003)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 10-007, 10-008, 17-010

## F-098

- fact: The weapon state machine uses 9 psprite action functions (A_WeaponReady, A_Lower, A_Raise, A_ReFire, A_CheckReload, A_GunFlash, A_Light0, A_Light1, A_Light2) wired to 55 state table entries across all 9 weapons plus S_LIGHTDONE. P_SetPsprite calls psprite actions between setting the state and reading nextstate; actions can recursively call P_SetPsprite. A_WeaponReady applies weapon bob using (128*leveltime)&FINEMASK for sx (full cosine range) and angle&(FINEANGLES/2-1) for sy (half sine, downward-only). Missile and BFG have semi-auto gating (attackdown blocks refire). A_Lower/A_Raise use LOWERSPEED=RAISESPEED=6*FRACUNIT; raise cycle is exactly (WEAPONBOTTOM-WEAPONTOP)/RAISESPEED=16 tics. A_ReFire increments refire counter BEFORE calling P_FireWeapon. A_CheckReload is only wired to S_DSGUN6 (SSG). S_MISSILEFLASH2 has no action (NULL in info.c). S_CHAIN3, S_MISSILE3, and S_SAW3 all have A_ReFire at 0 tics (chained immediately by setPsprite). Both PLASMAFLASH1 and PLASMAFLASH2 wire A_Light1 (not Light1+Light2). P_FireWeapon calls P_CheckAmmo, setMobjState(S_PLAY_ATK1), setPsprite(atkstate), then P_NoiseAlert. P_DropWeapon simply calls setPsprite with the weapon's downstate.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_pspr.c, info.c (step 10-004)

## F-099

- fact: Hitscan weapons use 6 psprite actions (A_Punch, A_Saw, A_FirePistol, A_FireShotgun, A_FireShotgun2, A_FireCGun) and the shared helpers P_BulletSlope/P_GunShot; P_LineAttack/P_AimLineAttack stash results in p_map.c globals `bulletslope` (Fixed slope) and `linetarget` (Mobj|null). Constants: MISSILERANGE=32*64*FRACUNIT=0x800_0000, MELEERANGE=64*FRACUNIT=0x40_0000, bullet autoaim range=16*64*FRACUNIT=0x400_0000, bullet aim nudge=1<<26. P_BulletSlope tries three angles for autoaim: mo.angle, then mo.angle+(1<<26), then mo.angle-(1<<26); first with a non-null linetarget wins. P_GunShot damage is `5*((P_Random()%3)+1)`(5-15), angle spread`((P_Random()-P_Random())<<18)`, refire-accurate shots use bare angle. A_Punch: damage=(P_Random()%10+1)<<1, ×10 when player has PowerType.STRENGTH (berserk); angle gets `((P_Random()-P_Random())<<18)`spread; MELEERANGE with slope from P_AimLineAttack(mo,angle,MELEERANGE); plays sfx_punch and snaps angle to linetarget on hit. A_Saw: damage=2*((P_Random()%10)+1); angle +=`((P_Random()-P_Random())<<18)`; P_LineAttack uses MELEERANGE+1 (saw-specific reach); miss→plays sfx_sawful and returns; hit→sfx_sawhit, sets MF_JUSTATTACKED on player.mo, and does angle-snap: compute `angle=R_PointToAngle2(mo.x,mo.y,linetarget.x,linetarget.y)-mo.angle`then if`angle-ANG90 < ANG180`(unsigned: behind) use`angle < -ANG90/20 ? mo.angle-ANG90/21 : mo.angle-ANG90/20`, else `angle > ANG90/20 ? mo.angle+ANG90/21 : mo.angle+ANG90/20`. A_FirePistol: sfx_pistol, S_PLAY_ATK2, ammo[WEAPON_INFO[readyweapon].ammo]--, GunFlash setPsprite flash, P_BulletSlope, P_GunShot(mo, !refire). A_FireShotgun: sfx_shotgn, S_PLAY_ATK2, ammo--, flash, bulletSlope, 7 pellets of P_GunShot(mo, false). A_FireShotgun2 (SSG): sfx_dshtgn, S_PLAY_ATK2, ammo -= 2 (CLIP_AMMO[shell]=4 loads but doesn't apply here—raw -=2), flash, bulletSlope, 20 pellets each with `damage=5\*((P_Random()%3)+1)`, `angle=mo.angle+((P_Random()-P_Random())<<19)`(wider than normal <<18),`slope=bulletslope+((P_Random()-P_Random())<<5)`, then P_LineAttack with that damage/angle/slope/MISSILERANGE. A_FireCGun: plays sfx_pistol BEFORE ammo check (off-by-one quirk preserved from vanilla); if ammo=0 returns without firing; S_PLAY_ATK2, ammo--, flash cycles between S_CHAIN1 (even psp.state index) and S_CHAIN2 (odd) via `flashstate + (psp.state - &states[S_CHAIN1]) & 1`; bulletSlope; P_GunShot(mo, !refire). wireHitscanActions installs exactly 8 entries (PUNCH2, PISTOL2, SGUN2, DSGUN2, CHAIN1, CHAIN2, SAW1, SAW2). SSG per-pellet RNG order: damage first (pRandom%3), then angle pSubRandom, then slope pSubRandom (100 pRandom calls total for 20 pellets).
- source: Chocolate Doom p_pspr.c A_Punch/A_Saw/A_FirePistol/A_FireShotgun/A_FireShotgun2/A_FireCGun/P_BulletSlope/P_GunShot, p_map.c P_LineAttack/P_AimLineAttack (step 10-005)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 10-006, 10-007, 11-005, 17-010

## F-101

- fact: P_TouchSpecialThing dispatches ~35 sprite cases through four give-helpers (P_GiveBody, P_GiveArmor, P_GiveCard, P_GivePower) plus P_GiveWeapon/P_GiveAmmo/P_GiveBackpack from weapons.ts. Guards (in order): (1) delta = special->z - toucher->z; reject if delta > toucher->height OR delta < -8*FRACUNIT (Z reach clamp; the -8*FRACUNIT boundary is INCLUSIVE — `delta < -8*FRACUNIT` rejects strictly below the floor margin), (2) toucher->health <= 0 rejects (sliding corpse guard), (3) player = toucher->player; default branch calls I_Error (our port returns noop). P_GiveBody caps at MAXHEALTH=100 and syncs player->mo->health = player->health after clamp. P_GiveArmor threshold is strict: `if (player->armorpoints >= armortype*100) return false` (so equal armorpoints blocks). P_GiveCard uses RAW ASSIGNMENT `player->bonuscount = BONUSADD` (not +=); in netgame the card branches return BEFORE the generic tail so the map pickup persists, and the player still gets bonuscount=BONUSADD from the giveCard alone (not 2*BONUSADD). In single-player the generic tail adds another BONUSADD for a total of 2*BONUSADD=12. P_GivePower per-power tic durations from doomdef.h: INVULNTICS=30*TICRATE=1050, INVISTICS=60*TICRATE=2100 (also ORs MF_SHADOW=0x40000 onto mo->flags), INFRATICS=120*TICRATE=4200, IRONTICS=60*TICRATE=2100. STRENGTH (berserk) ALWAYS returns true even when held — the berserk heal `P_GiveBody(player, 100)` always fires — and sets powers[STRENGTH]=1. Generic powers (e.g., ALLMAP) return false if already held. Sprite-specific quirks: SPR_BON1/BON2 overfill to deh_max_health=200/deh_max_armor=200 (bypasses MAXHEALTH); SPR_BON2 sets armortype=1 only when armortype was 0 (does not downgrade class 2); SPR_SOUL adds deh_soulsphere_health=100 capped at deh_max_soulsphere=200, plays sfx_getpow=93; SPR_MEGA early-returns silently outside commercial (`if (gamemode != commercial) return`), sets health=deh_megasphere_health=200, hardcodes giveArmor(player, 2) — ignores deh_blue_armor_class entirely per vanilla comment; SPR_PSTR berserk also sets player->pendingweapon = wp_fist if readyweapon != wp_fist; SPR_STIM=10 HP; SPR_MEDI=25 HP with GOTMEDINEED emitted when player->health was < 25 BEFORE the giveBody call; dropped CLIP (MF_DROPPED=0x20000) gives num=0 (half-clip via giveAmmo's clipammo/2 path) while placed CLIP gives num=1; AMMO/BROK/CELP/SBOX give num=5; SHEL/ROCK/CELL give num=1. Weapon sprites: BFUG=BFG, MGUN=CHAINGUN, CSAW=CHAINSAW, LAUN=MISSILE, PLAS=PLASMA, SHOT=SHOTGUN, SGN2=SUPERSHOTGUN; MGUN/SHOT/SGN2 pass MF_DROPPED through to giveWeapon (affects half-ammo + no-respawn paths). Common tail (runs on successful non-netgame-card pickup): if (special->flags & MF_COUNTITEM=0x800000) player->itemcount++; P_RemoveMobj(special); player->bonuscount += BONUSADD=6; if (player == consoleplayer) S_StartSound(NULL, sound). Sound IDs (sounds.h enum): sfx_itemup=32 (generic), sfx_wpnup=33 (weapons), sfx_getpow=93 (SOUL/MEGA/PINV/PSTR/PINS/SUIT/PMAP/PVIS).
- source: Chocolate Doom p*inter.c P_TouchSpecialThing/P_GiveBody/P_GiveArmor/P_GiveCard/P_GivePower, deh_misc.h DEH_DEFAULT*\* constants, doomdef.h INVULNTICS/INVISTICS/INFRATICS/IRONTICS/MAXHEALTH, p_mobj.h MF_SHADOW/MF_DROPPED/MF_COUNTITEM, sounds.h sfxenum_t (step 10-007)
- confidence: high

## F-100

- fact: Projectile weapons use 3 psprite actions (A_FireMissile, A_FirePlasma, A_FireBFG) plus one mobj-state action (A_BFGSpray on S_BFGLAND5), all backed by the shared P_SpawnPlayerMissile/P_CheckMissileSpawn/P_ExplodeMissile primitives. P_SpawnPlayerMissile autoaim cascade matches P_BulletSlope: try source.angle, then +1<<26, then -1<<26; if all miss, reset angle = source.angle and slope = 0 (spawns horizontal). Spawn position: (source.x, source.y, source.z + 4*8*FRACUNIT = 32*FRACUNIT). After P_SpawnMobj: play info.seesound on the missile (ROCKET sfx_rlaunc=14, PLASMA sfx_plasma=8, BFG seesound=0), set target=source, angle=locked-on angle, momx = fixedMul(info.speed, finecosine[angle>>19]), momy = fixedMul(info.speed, finesine[angle>>19]), momz = fixedMul(info.speed, slope). MOBJINFO speeds: ROCKET=1310720=20*FRACUNIT, PLASMA=1638400=25*FRACUNIT, BFG=1638400=25*FRACUNIT. P_CheckMissileSpawn: tics -= P_Random()&3 (clamped >=1), then half-advance x/y/z by (momx|y|z>>1) (load-bearing arithmetic right shift for negative momenta), then P_TryMove at the advanced position — if blocked, P_ExplodeMissile is called. P_ExplodeMissile: momx/y/z=0, P_SetMobjState(mobjinfo[type].deathstate), tics -= P_Random()&3 (clamped >=1), clear MF_MISSILE, play info.deathsound (when non-zero; ROCKET sfx_rxplod=15, PLASMA sfx_bgdth2=17, BFG sfx_rxplod=15, EXTRABFG deathsound=0). A_FireMissile: decrement missile ammo by 1, P_SpawnPlayerMissile(MT_ROCKET). A_FirePlasma: decrement cell ammo by 1, setPsprite(flash, flashstate + (P_Random()&1)) — flash jitter P_Random runs BEFORE P_SpawnPlayerMissile — then P_SpawnPlayerMissile(MT_PLASMA). A_FireBFG: decrement cell ammo by deh_bfg_cells_per_shot=40, P_SpawnPlayerMissile(MT_BFG). A_BFGSpray (mobj state action signature `(Mobj)=>void` not psprite): 40 rays over ANG90 arc; for i=0..39: an = mo.angle - ANG90/2 + (ANG90/40)*i — exact integer truncation: ANG90/40=26843545, so full sweep covers ANG90-24 (last ray lands at +ANG90/2 - 24 BAM), not exactly +ANG90/2; P_AimLineAttack(mo.target, an, 16*64\*FRACUNIT); missed rays `continue` (NO RNG consumed); hit → P_SpawnMobj(linetarget.x, linetarget.y, linetarget.z + (linetarget.height>>2), MT_EXTRABFG), damage = sum of 15 rolls of `(P_Random()&7)+1` (range [15,120]), P_DamageMobj(linetarget, mo.target, mo.target, damage) — mo.target (player who fired) is BOTH inflictor AND source. Vanilla would crash on null mo.target; safe implementations early-return. wireProjectileActions installs exactly 4 entries: pspriteActions[MISSILE2]=aFireMissile, pspriteActions[PLASMA1]=aFirePlasma, pspriteActions[BFG3]=aFireBFG, STATES[BFGLAND5].action=aBFGSpray.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_pspr.c A_FireMissile/A_FirePlasma/A_FireBFG/A_BFGSpray, p_map.c P_SpawnPlayerMissile, p_mobj.c P_CheckMissileSpawn/P_ExplodeMissile (step 10-006)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 10-007, 11-005, 17-010

## F-101

- fact: BLOCKMAP offset-table signedness clarification (see F-075). Vanilla Chocolate Doom p_setup.c P_LoadBlockMap declares `blockmaplump` as `short*` (signed int16), so offsets are technically signed in vanilla. F-075 describes the offset table as uint16LE because Crispy Doom and modern Chocolate forks widen to `int32_t & 0xffff` to support blockmaps > 32767 words. For DOOM1.WAD shareware (PRIMARY_TARGET) the distinction is unobservable: all nine maps have BLOCKMAP lumps well under 65KB so no offset exceeds 32767. The existing parseBlockmap uses readInt16 for header+offsets and matches vanilla exactly. Do NOT widen offsets to uint16 solely to match F-075 wording — that would only matter if the target ever expands to DOOM2.WAD MAP29-scale blockmaps, and even then Crispy's `t == -1 ? -1 : (int32_t)t & 0xffff` terminator-preserving cast is what's needed (not a plain readUint16).
- source: Chocolate Doom p_setup.c P_LoadBlockMap, FACT_LOG F-075, audit pass on step 08-004
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 17-010

## F-102

- fact: Powerup tick direction and palette/fixedcolormap rules (p_user.c P_PlayerThink counter block + st_stuff.c ST_doPaletteStuff). STRENGTH counts UP every tic (drives berserk screen fade-in); INVULNERABILITY, INFRARED, and IRONFEET count DOWN by 1; INVISIBILITY counts down AND clears MF_SHADOW=0x40000 from player.mo.flags on the exact tic it hits zero (pre-decrement: `if (!--powers[invis]) flags &= ~MF_SHADOW`). damagecount and bonuscount each decrement by 1 toward zero, guarded by an explicit nonzero check — they never go negative. P_PlayerThink reassigns player.fixedcolormap every tic with precedence INVULNERABILITY > INFRARED > 0: while INVULNERABILITY, fixedcolormap=INVERSECOLORMAP=32 when timer > 4*32=128 OR (timer & 8); else 0. While INFRARED (and no invulnerability), fixedcolormap=1 ("almost full bright") under the same 4*32-or-(timer&8) blink rule; else 0. Constants for ST_doPaletteStuff: STARTREDPALS=1, NUMREDPALS=8, STARTBONUSPALS=9, NUMBONUSPALS=4, RADIATIONPAL=13, INVERSECOLORMAP=32. Palette selection: cnt=damagecount; if STRENGTH active, bzc=12-(strength>>6), cnt=max(cnt,bzc). If cnt>0, palette=min((cnt+7)>>3, NUMREDPALS-1)+STARTREDPALS → indices 2..8 (palette index 1 is unreachable because (cnt+7)>>3 is ≥1 for cnt≥1). Else if bonuscount>0, palette=min((bonuscount+7)>>3, NUMBONUSPALS-1)+STARTBONUSPALS → indices 10..12 (palette index 9 is similarly unreachable). Else if IRONFEET > 128 OR (IRONFEET & 8), palette=13. Else palette=0. Precedence is strict: damage/berserk > bonus > radiation > normal. BERSERK_STRENGTH timer saturation: bzc bottoms out at ≤0 once strength>=768 (12-(768>>6)=0), so the berserk screen tint fades to normal after 768 tics (~22 s) unless damage re-raises cnt.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_user.c P_PlayerThink counter/fixedcolormap block, st_stuff.c ST_doPaletteStuff (step 10-008)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 11-001, 13-009, 14-002, 17-010

## F-103

- fact: P_NoiseAlert (p_enemy.c) does exactly two mutations before calling into the recursion: `soundtarget = target; validcount++;` — then calls P_RecursiveSound(emitter->subsector->sector, 0). P_RecursiveSound runs an entirely depth-first flood with no sight check (P_CheckSight is never called from the recursion). The per-sector guard is `if (sec->validcount == validcount && sec->soundtraversed <= soundblocks + 1) return;` — it only skips a re-entrance whose soundblocks is equal-or-worse than the existing stamp, so a shorter (lower-soundblocks) path ALWAYS overwrites a longer one within the same generation. Each visit stamps three sector fields in this order: validcount, soundtraversed=soundblocks+1, soundtarget=target. Per-line traversal skips lines without ML_TWOSIDED=0x0004, then calls P_LineOpening and skips if openrange <= 0 (so a crushed door with exactly zero or negative range blocks). The "other sector" is the side whose sector is NOT the current sector. ML_SOUNDBLOCK=0x0040 lines are crossed only when soundblocks === 0 (and the recursion increments to 1); a second ML_SOUNDBLOCK encounter with soundblocks=1 is skipped entirely, never recurring. This gives sound at most two "reaches" across a chain of soundblock walls: 0 → 1 (first crossing) → blocked (second crossing). Vanilla walks the per-sector lines in the order P_GroupLines built them, which is the on-disk linedef order filtered by membership.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c P_NoiseAlert and P_RecursiveSound (step 11-001)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 11-002, 11-003, 15-005, 17-010

## F-104

- fact: Target acquisition and sight (p_enemy.c P_LookForPlayers/P_CheckMeleeRange/P_CheckMissileRange + p_sight.c P_CheckSight/P_CrossBSPNode/P_CrossSubsector/P_DivlineSide/P_InterceptVector2). P_CheckSight does: (1) REJECT lookup `s1*numsectors + s2` bit — true bit means "can never see", return false; (2) `validcount++` bumps the SAME global counter shared with blockmap iteration; (3) `sightzstart = t1.z + t1.height - (t1.height>>2)` (three-quarters eye slice — arithmetic right shift preserved); (4) topslope = `(t2.z + t2.height) - sightzstart`, bottomslope = `t2.z - sightzstart`; (5) `strace = {x:t1.x, y:t1.y, dx:t2.x-t1.x, dy:t2.y-t1.y}` and `t2x/t2y` cached; (6) descend from `nodes[numnodes-1]` via P_CrossBSPNode. P_CrossBSPNode folds side=2 ("on") to 0 for the descent decision but compares raw end-side against normalized side, so an exact on-partition target correctly falls through to cross the other subtree: `side = (startSide===1)?1:0; if (!cross(children[side])) return false; if (side === endSide) return true; return cross(children[side^1]);`. P_CrossSubsector iterates the subsector's segs, stamping `linedef->validcount = validcount` at the top (deduplicated across multiple subsectors sharing the linedef). For each non-stamped line it: divline-sides both line endpoints vs strace, `continue` if same side; computes divl from line and tests strace endpoints vs divl, `continue` if same side; reads front/back sectors from seg+line (`seg->side ^ 1` picks back); returns false if line is one-sided OR ML_TWOSIDED unset. With an opening: `continue` if floors equal AND ceilings equal (fast path); else openbottom=max(floors), opentop=min(ceilings); if openbottom>=opentop return false (closed opening / crushed door); compute frac = P_InterceptVector2(strace, divl); if floors differ, slope=(openbottom-sightzstart)/frac, bump bottomslope upward; if ceilings differ, slope=(opentop-sightzstart)/frac, push topslope downward; if topslope <= bottomslope return false. P_DivlineSide (p_sight.c variant, distinct from p_maputl.c) returns 0/1/2 and has a vanilla QUIRK: in the `!node->dy` branch the comparison is `if (x == node->y)` — comparing the point's X to the node's Y, not Y to Y. Preserve byte-for-byte. P_InterceptVector2 uses >>8 shifts (coarser than P_InterceptVector's >>FRACBITS; overflow-safer for sight spans) and returns 0 on parallel lines (the reference I_Error is commented out). P_LookForPlayers (p_enemy.c) is a for(;;) loop with post-expression `actor->lastlook = (actor->lastlook+1)&3` that fires on every continue. Body: `if (!playeringame[lastlook]) continue;` (infinite loop if no slot is in-game — vanilla depends on at least one true entry); `if (c++ == 2 || lastlook == stop) return false;` (post-increment — accepts 2 live candidates, fails on the 3rd); health<=0 or mo null → continue; `if (!P_CheckSight(actor, player.mo)) continue;` ; if !allaround, compute `an = R_PointToAngle2(actor, player.mo) - actor.angle`; if `an > ANG90 && an < ANG270` (unsigned wrap), require dist <= MELEERANGE=64*FRACUNIT else continue — so a target within melee-range behind the actor STILL acquires (ambush-from-behind wake-up). On success `actor.target = player.mo; return true`. `stop = (lastlook_start - 1) & 3` meaning the c<2 count almost always hits first; the `|| lastlook == stop` branch is only a safety net. P_CheckMeleeRange: pl=actor.target, null→false; dist=P_AproxDistance; for gameversion>=1.5 (ALL C1 targets emulate 1.9 per F-028) `range = MELEERANGE - 20*FRACUNIT + pl->info->radius`; if dist>=range return false; return P_CheckSight(actor, pl). P_CheckMissileRange: sight→reactiontime→distance gate with hard MF_JUSTHIT retaliation short-circuit. Order: (1) !P_CheckSight → false; (2) if MF_JUSTHIT set, clear it and return true with NO RNG consumed (retaliation always fires); (3) if reactiontime!=0 return false (NO RNG); (4) `dist = P_AproxDistance - 64*FRACUNIT`; if actor has no melee state (info.meleestate==0) subtract another 128*FRACUNIT; shift >>FRACBITS to integer; (5) per-type overrides: MT_VILE cap dist>14\*64→false (no halve); MT_UNDEAD floor `dist<196→false` then `dist>>=1`; MT_CYBORG/MT_SPIDER/MT_SKULL halve dist; clamp `dist>200→200`; MT_CYBORG additionally clamp `dist>160→160`; (6) `if (P_Random() < dist) return false;` — exactly one RNG consumption when gate reached, 0 when JUSTHIT/reactiontime short-circuited. The "no melee state" subtraction only matters for MT_CYBORG and MT_SPIDER in the base roster because every other missile-capable actor also has a melee state.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c P_LookForPlayers/A_Look/P_CheckMeleeRange/P_CheckMissileRange + p_sight.c P_CheckSight/P_CrossBSPNode/P_CrossSubsector/P_DivlineSide/P_InterceptVector2 (step 11-002)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 11-003, 11-004, 11-005, 11-006, 11-007, 11-008, 17-010

## F-105

- fact: A_Lower → P_BringUpWeapon (p_pspr.c) emits sfx_sawup=25 on the transition tic when `pendingweapon == wp_chainsaw`. The sound plays via S_StartSound(player.mo, sfx_sawup) AFTER the `if (pendingweapon == wp_nochange) pendingweapon = readyweapon` normalization and BEFORE pendingweapon is cleared to wp_nochange. In doom_codex, A_Lower (weaponStates.ts) must forward `context.startSound` through to bringUpWeapon's optional `startSoundCallback` — omitting the callback silently drops the chainsaw power-on sound during mid-lower weapon switches. The same emission path fires from P_SetupPsprites at level start when the saved readyweapon is chainsaw.
