## F-107

- fact: P_CheckMeleeRange constants and null-info fallback (p_enemy.c, exe_doom_1_5+ formula). MELEERANGE=64·FRACUNIT=0x40_0000; the 1.5+ adjustment constant is 20·FRACUNIT=0x14_0000; MELEE_BASE_CUTOFF = MELEERANGE - 20·FRACUNIT = 44·FRACUNIT. Cutoff is `dist >= MELEERANGE - 20*FRACUNIT + target.info.radius`, using the TARGET's info.radius (not the actor's). Practical cutoffs for DOOM1.WAD's base roster: PLAYER(16)=60, TROOP/SERGEANT/SHADOWS/POSSESSED(20)=64, HEAD/cacodemon(30)=74, BRUISER(24)=68, SKULL(16)=60, SPIDER(128)=172, CYBORG(40)=84. Distance is the octagonal P_AproxDistance (`ax+ay-min(ax,ay)/2`), not Euclidean — a target at (45,45) reads as 67.5 units not 63.6. Comparison is strict `>=` so exactly-at-cutoff is out of range. checkMeleeRange consumes NO RNG; it does call P_CheckSight which bumps validCount.current by exactly one per invocation and short-circuits on REJECT. Vanilla C crashes on null info.radius; the TS port falls back to targetRadius=0 (MELEE_BASE_CUTOFF=44\*F) for null-safety without changing any observable behavior for spawnable mobjs. The implementation lives in `src/ai/targeting.ts` alongside P_CheckSight; `src/ai/meleeRange.ts` re-exports it as the canonical entry point and exposes the load-bearing constants for reuse by hitscan/AI steps.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c P_CheckMeleeRange + info.c MOBJINFO radii (step 11-004)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 11-005, 11-006, 17-010

## F-108

- fact: P_CheckMissileRange constants and per-MobjType distance overrides (p_enemy.c). Evaluation order: (1) null target → false; (2) !P_CheckSight → false; (3) MF_JUSTHIT set → clear flag + return true (zero RNG); (4) reactiontime>0 → false (zero RNG); (5) raw dist = P_AproxDistance(dx,dy) - MISSILE_BASE_CUTOFF (64·F), then if `info.meleestate==0` also subtract MISSILE_NO_MELEE_CUTOFF (128·F); shift >> FRACBITS to map units; (6) per-type branches: VILE if dist > MISSILE_VILE_DIST_MAX (14·64=896) → false (zero RNG), UNDEAD if dist < MISSILE_UNDEAD_DIST_MIN (196) → false (zero RNG) else dist>>=1, CYBORG/SPIDER/SKULL dist>>=1; (7) clamp dist to MISSILE_DIST_CLAMP (200); CYBORG additionally clamped to MISSILE_CYBORG_DIST_CLAMP (160) AFTER the 200 clamp; (8) `P_Random() >= dist` → true (exactly one RNG consumption). The 160 clamp is CYBORG-specific and applies AFTER halving+200-clamp, so a high-raw-distance CYBORG sees dist=160 not dist=100. `info.meleestate==0` is only load-bearing for CYBORG and SPIDER in the base roster; UNDEAD has meleestate=335 so its dist is NOT reduced by 128 before the 196 minimum. `info === null` (TS null-safety path) skips the 128 subtract (conservative fallback — behaves as if actor had a melee state). The rejection paths in steps 3, 4, 6-VILE, and 6-UNDEAD all leave the RNG stream unchanged; only step 8 rolls RNG. Pre-computed base-roster distances (F-rounded, meleestate known): POSSESSED(meleestate=0) at 128 → raw 128-64-128=-64, clamped to 0 always fires; UNDEAD(335) at 300 → raw 300-64=236→118 halved; CYBORG(0) at 4000 → raw 4000-64-128=3808→1904→200→160; SPIDER(0) at 1024 → raw 1024-64-128=832→416→200; SKULL(0) at 800 → raw 800-64-128=608→304→200; VILE(0) at 1200 → raw 1200-64-128=1008 > 896 → reject. The implementation lives in `src/ai/targeting.ts`; `src/ai/missileRange.ts` re-exports it as the canonical entry point and exposes MISSILE_BASE_CUTOFF, MISSILE_NO_MELEE_CUTOFF, MISSILE_DIST_CLAMP=200, MISSILE_CYBORG_DIST_CLAMP=160, MISSILE_VILE_DIST_MAX=896, MISSILE_UNDEAD_DIST_MIN=196 for reuse by monster attack actions.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c P_CheckMissileRange + info.c MOBJINFO meleestate (step 11-005)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 11-006, 11-007, 11-008, 17-010

## F-106

- fact: Chase state machine (p_enemy.c A_Chase / P_Move / P_TryWalk / P_NewChaseDir). Eight walk directions plus DI_NODIR sentinel (`enum dirtype_t`, NUMDIRS=9); `opposite[]` and `diags[]` are source tables — DIAGS indexed by `(deltay<0 ? 2 : 0) + (deltax>0 ? 1 : 0)`. `xspeed[]`/`yspeed[]` use the vanilla 47000 quirk on diagonals (NOT 46340=cos(45°)·FRACUNIT) so diagonal moves cover slightly more ground than cardinals. FLOATSPEED = 4·FRACUNIT. **P_Move**: `if (actor->movedir==NODIR) return false;`, `if ((unsigned)movedir>=8) I_Error("Weird actor->movedir!");`, `tryx = actor.x + speed·xspeed[movedir]` (C uses native int32 multiply; Math.imul preserves wrap), call P_TryMove — on failure: (1) if `MF_FLOAT && floatok`, step z by ±FLOATSPEED toward tmfloorz, set MF_INFLOAT, return TRUE; (2) else if `numspechit==0` return false; (3) else movedir=NODIR, walk spechit in REVERSE order calling P_UseSpecialLine(actor, ld, 0), return true if ANY opened. On success: clear MF_INFLOAT, and for non-floaters snap `actor.z = actor.floorz`. **P_TryWalk**: `if (!P_Move(actor)) return false; actor->movecount = P_Random()&15; return true;` — the single RNG consumption for a successful chase walk. P_Move itself is RNG-free. **P_NewChaseDir**: I_Error on null target ("P_NewChaseDir: called with no target"); cascade = (1) direct diagonal via DIAGS when both deltas are outside ±10\*FRACUNIT and the diagonal is NOT turnaround; (2) cardinal candidates — `P_Random()>200 || abs(deltay)>abs(deltax)` triggers swap (RNG ALWAYS consumed here even if `abs(deltay)>abs(deltax)` already forced swap), then each candidate equal to turnaround is zeroed to NODIR; (3) olddir if != NODIR; (4) full 0..7 scan, direction chosen by `P_Random()&1` — truthy = forward EAST→SOUTHEAST, falsy = reverse SOUTHEAST→EAST, skipping turnaround; (5) turnaround as last resort if != NODIR; (6) `movedir = DI_NODIR`. CHASE_DEADZONE=10·FRACUNIT. **A_Chase**: strict order is (1) `reactiontime--` floored at 0 (vanilla `if (actor->reactiontime) actor->reactiontime--`); (2) `if (threshold) { if (!target || target->health<=0) threshold=0; else threshold--; }` — the 1.2 gameversion guard that wraps the threshold block is unconditionally true for 1.9 emulation so inlined; (3) angle turn — `actor->angle &= (7u<<29)` snaps top-3-bit quantum, then signed int32 `delta = actor->angle - (actor->movedir<<29)`: delta>0 → angle-=ANG45, delta<0 → angle+=ANG45, delta==0 → no-op. Crucially the snap happens BEFORE the sub, and the adjustment is exactly ±ANG45 per tic (not to the nearest snap point) — a 180° turn takes four tics, always CCW; (4) no-shootable-target branch: if `!target || !(target->flags&MF_SHOOTABLE)`, call `P_LookForPlayers(actor, true)`, if false call `P_SetMobjState(spawnstate)` and return; (5) MF_JUSTATTACKED branch: clear the flag, if `gameskill != nightmare && !fastparm` call P_NewChaseDir; return; (6) melee: `if (meleestate && CheckMeleeRange) { if (attacksound) S_StartSound; P_SetMobjState(meleestate); return; }`; (7) missile: if `missilestate` AND NOT `(gameskill<nightmare && !fastparm && movecount)`, if CheckMissileRange → P_SetMobjState(missilestate) + set MF_JUSTATTACKED, return; (8) netgame re-look: `if (netgame && !threshold && !P_CheckSight) { if (P_LookForPlayers(true)) return; }` — only fires in netgame, never triggers in single-player; (9) walk: `movecount--; if (movecount<0 || !P_Move) P_NewChaseDir(actor);`; (10) active sound: `if (activesound && P_Random()<3) S_StartSound(actor, activesound)` — exactly one RNG roll against the 3/256 threshold. Nightmare skill is `sk_nightmare=4` (doomdef.h skill_t), not 5; see weapons.ts SK_NIGHTMARE. ACTIVESOUND_THRESHOLD=3, MOVECOUNT_MASK=15, NEWCHASEDIR_SWAP_THRESHOLD=200.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c (A_Chase, P_Move, P_TryWalk, P_NewChaseDir) + p_pspr.c weapon state transitions for setMobjState semantics (step 11-003); reference cached at doom_codex/.cache/p_enemy.c
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 11-004, 11-005, 11-006, 11-007, 11-008, 15-005, 17-010

## F-109

- fact: Monster attack actions (p_enemy.c A_FaceTarget through A_PainAttack, 29 action functions). All actions consume module-level injected MonsterAttackContext (setMonsterAttackContext/getMonsterAttackContext; every action guards `if (!context) return;`). Context exposes 8 callbacks (spawnMobj, tryMove, damageMobj, lineAttack, aimLineAttack, radiusAttack, pointToAngle2, startSound) plus gametic, rng, thinkerList, targetingContext — checkMeleeRange/checkSight are imported DIRECTLY from ./targeting.ts, NOT via callback (tests must build a real BSP map fixture). Key constants: MISSILERANGE=32·64·F=0x20_0000·64, MELEERANGE=64·F, TRACEANGLE=0xC000000 (=3·ANG90/8), FATSPREAD=ANG90/8=0x08000000, SKULLSPEED=20·F, FIRE_OFFSET=24·F, PAIN_SKULL_Z_OFFSET=8·F, PAIN_SKULL_PRESTEP_BASE=4·F, SMOKE_MOMZ=F>>1, TRACER_SLOPE_STEP=F>>1, TRACER_SLOPE_Z_OFFSET=40·F, VILE_ATTACK_DAMAGE=20, VILE_RADIUS_ATTACK_DAMAGE=70, VILE_VICTIM_MOMZ_NUMERATOR=1000·F, MAX_SKULLS_PER_LEVEL=20, PAIN_SKULL_KILL_DAMAGE=10000, CPOS_REFIRE_THRESHOLD=40, SPID_REFIRE_THRESHOLD=10, MISSILE_TIC_JITTER_MASK=3, TRACER_TIC_MASK=3. Parity-critical vanilla quirks: (1) A_SPosAttack fires 3 shots consuming **9 RNG** each iteration (pSubRandom=2 + pRandom for damage=1, × 3); not 6. (2) A_VileTarget spawns fog at (target.x, target.x, target.z) — `y` is target.x, vanilla bug preserved byte-for-byte. (3) A_BruisAttack melee branch does NOT call A_FaceTarget (vanilla skips it; observable: pointToAngle2 never invoked when checkMeleeRange is true). (4) A_Tracer uses `(gametic & TRACER_TIC_MASK) !== 0` gate — only runs every 4th tic; other tics are no-ops with no RNG consumption. (5) A_Fire/A_StartFire/A_FireCrackle position tracer fire at `tracer.x + fixedMul(FIRE_OFFSET, finecosine[fineIndex])` — NOT `tracer.x + FIRE_OFFSET`; finecosine[0]=65535 (not FRACUNIT=65536) so even angle=0 gives 24·F − 24 = 1572840, not 1572864. Same applies to all prestep/spawn offsets using the finecosine/finesine tables. (6) painShootSkull requires strict `count > MAX_SKULLS_PER_LEVEL` (count > 20) to cap; count==20 still spawns. (7) painShootSkull tryMove-fail path calls damageMobj(newmobj, actor, actor, PAIN_SKULL_KILL_DAMAGE=10000); the skull is still instantiated. (8) A_CPosRefire/A_SpidRefire roll P_Random once; if < threshold (40/10) stay in attack; else if target null/dead/sight-lost, call setMobjState(seestate) which on null info falls back to StateNum.NULL → removeMobj → action === REMOVED. (9) A_FatAttackN angle mutations are strict: Attack1 adds +FATSPREAD before spawn then second missile sets angle+FATSPREAD\*2 with momx/momy rewrite; Attack2 subtracts FATSPREAD; Attack3 spans ±FATSPREAD/2.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c A_FaceTarget/A_PosAttack/A_SPosAttack/A_CPosAttack/A_CPosRefire/A_SpidRefire/A_BspiAttack/A_TroopAttack/A_SargAttack/A_HeadAttack/A_CyberAttack/A_BruisAttack/A_SkelMissile/A_Tracer/A_SkelWhoosh/A_SkelFist/A_VileStart/A_Fire/A_StartFire/A_FireCrackle/A_VileTarget/A_VileAttack/A_FatRaise/A_FatAttack1/A_FatAttack2/A_FatAttack3/A_SkullAttack/A_PainShootSkull/A_PainAttack (step 11-006); confirmed against src/ai/attacks.ts implementation (1276 lines)

## F-113

- fact: validcount-style generation counters must be kept in int32 range in the TS port. Vanilla C declares `int validcount` and increments with `validcount++`, which wraps signed-overflow from INT_MAX to INT_MIN; per-sector and per-linedef stamps live in `int` fields that wrap identically, so `sec->validcount == validcount` keeps working after the wrap. In the TS port the stamps live in `Int32Array` (which truncates writes to int32) while the ambient counter is a plain `number`. Without `| 0` on every increment the ambient counter escapes int32 after 2^31 bumps and the stamp comparison never matches again, causing flood-fill routines to re-enter every sector/linedef forever. Every `validcount++` call site must be rewritten `validcount = (validcount + 1) | 0;` (or equivalent). Discovered during audit of soundPropagation.ts; the same fix is needed in any future code that bumps a counter paired with an Int32Array stamp.
- source: Audit of 11-001 recursive-sound-propagation; Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c P_NoiseAlert (`validcount++` on global int); src/ai/soundPropagation.ts noiseAlert after fix
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 11-002 (sight/target generation counter), 13-002 (R_RenderBSPNode validcount sweep), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regressions)

## F-114

- fact: P_RecursiveSound's per-linedef P_LineOpening call in vanilla sets globals and is allocation-free; the equivalent `lineOpening(...)` helper in the TS port (src/world/checkPosition.ts) returns a fresh `{opentop, openbottom, openrange, lowfloor}` object on every call. That object allocation becomes dominant garbage on sound-propagation hot paths (noiseAlert on DOOM1 E1M1: ~27.8 µs/call with the helper vs ~22.6 µs/call with openrange inlined — 18% wall-clock win, one object per two-sided linedef per visited sector eliminated). Rule for future hot-loop callers that need only one field from a multi-field "opening/plane/bbox" record: read the needed fields directly from the underlying sector/line data instead of calling the object-returning helper. The helper remains correct and appropriate for cold callers (useLines, slideMove, checkPosition) where allocation cost is invisible.
- source: Audit of 11-001 recursive-sound-propagation; benchmark of noiseAlert across DOOM1 E1M1 (85 sectors, 50000 iterations, Bun 1.3.12); src/ai/soundPropagation.ts recursiveSound after fix
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-002, 12-003, 13-007 (any renderer/specials hot loop reading openings repeatedly), 17-010

## F-112

- fact: Boss and death special-case action functions (p_enemy.c A_KeenDie, A_PainDie, A_BossDeath, A_Hoof, A_Metal, A_BabyMetal, A_BrainAwake, A_BrainPain, A_BrainScream, A_BrainExplode, A_BrainDie, A_BrainSpit, A_SpawnSound, A_SpawnFly — 14 action functions in src/ai/bossSpecials.ts, ~600 lines, wired via 24 STATES[] entries by wireBossSpecialsActions). Module-level injected BossSpecialsContext singleton (set/get/clear) holds rng, thinkerList, startSound, spawnMobj, gameMode/isUltimateOrLater/gameepisode/gamemap/gameskill accessor functions, players + playeringame, exitLevel, doDoor, doFloor, spawnMissile, painShootSkullAction, chaseAction, lookForPlayers, teleportMove, removeMobj, setMobjState. checkMeleeRange/checkSight not needed by this module. SFX IDs from canonical sounds.h sfxenum_t (zero-based): SFX_TELEPT=35, SFX_BSPWLK=79, SFX_HOOF=84, SFX_METAL=85, SFX_BOSPIT=94, SFX_BOSCUB=95, SFX_BOSSIT=96, SFX_BOSPN=97, SFX_BOSDTH=98. Tag/geometry constants: KEEN_DIE_DOOR_TAG=666, BOSS_DEATH_FATSO_TAG=666, BOSS_DEATH_BABY_TAG=667, BOSS_DEATH_TAG=666, MAX_BRAIN_TARGETS=32, BRAIN_SCREAM_X_START=-196·F, BRAIN_SCREAM_X_END=320·F, BRAIN_SCREAM_X_STEP=8·F, BRAIN_SCREAM_Y_OFFSET=-320·F, BRAIN_EXPLODE_X_SCATTER=2048, BRAIN_ROCKET_Z_BASE=128 (NOT in fixed-point), BRAIN_ROCKET_Z_RAND_MUL=2·F, BRAIN_ROCKET_MOMZ_MUL=512, BRAIN_ROCKET_TIC_JITTER_MASK=7, ANG90/180/270, SK_EASY=1. Door/floor types projected as string-literal unions (BossDoorType="open"|"blazeOpen", BossFloorType="lowerFloorToLowest"|"raiseToTexture") since the specials subsystem (phase 12) hasn't been built yet — bootstrap layer translates to vldoor_e/floor_e enums when wiring. Module-level brain state (mirrors C statics): braintargets[32] array, numbraintargets cursor, braintargeton round-robin index, brainSpitEasy `static int easy` toggle. Test helpers: resetBrainTargets, resetBrainSpitEasy, getBrainTargets snapshot. Parity-critical vanilla quirks preserved byte-for-byte: (1) A_KeenDie clears MF_SOLID then walks thinker list with `mo2 !== mo && mo2.type === mo.type && mo2.health > 0` test — same-instance comparison prevents the dying Keen from blocking its own door; opens line tag 666 with vld_open ONLY when no other live Keen remains; consumes NO RNG. (2) A_PainDie does NOT call A_FaceTarget — uses pain elemental's CURRENT angle as fan center; clears MF_SOLID then fires three lost souls at angle+ANG90/+ANG180/+ANG270 via the painShootSkull mechanism wired in 11-006. (3) A_BossDeath gating order: mode/version → living-player → surviving-boss → action body. Commercial branch: requires map 7 AND (FATSO|BABY); FATSO → doFloor(666, lowerFloorToLowest), BABY → doFloor(667, raiseToTexture); each returns immediately so exitLevel fall-through never fires. Non-commercial pre-ultimate: only map 8 triggers; MT_BRUISER death on ep!=1 is ignored (baron is regular monster outside ep1); ep1 → doFloor(666, lower), ep4 map6 → doDoor(666, blazeOpen), ep4 map8 → doFloor(666, lower), anything else → exitLevel. Non-commercial ultimate (Ultimate Doom rework — the well-documented uac_dead.wad behavior change): each episode gates a SPECIFIC monster type — ep1 only MT_BRUISER@map8, ep2 only MT_CYBORG@map8, ep3 only MT_SPIDER@map8, ep4 MT_CYBORG@map6 OR MT_SPIDER@map8, default map==8. (4) A_BossDeath living-player check requires `players[i].health > 0 AND playeringame[i]` for at least ONE player; otherwise silent return (no exitLevel, no doors, no floors). Surviving-boss scan: ANY other live mobj of dying boss's type → silent return. (5) A_Hoof/A_Metal/A_BabyMetal play sfx_hoof/sfx_metal/sfx_bspwlk on the actor (NOT world-relative) and then call A_Chase normally — these are mid-step "footfalls" wired to RUN frames in info.c (CYBER_RUN1/SPID_RUN1+5+9+CYBER_RUN7/BSPI_RUN1+7), NOT to the seestate transition. (6) A_BrainAwake clears braintargets[] AND braintargeton (resets cursor to 0) at start, then walks the thinker list and pushes every MT_BOSSTARGET, capped at 32 (vanilla overruns the array if there are more than 32 — we silently drop overflow). Plays sfx_bossit world-relative (origin=null). (7) A_BrainScream: outer loop x in `[mo.x - 196·F, mo.x + 320·F)` step `8·F` — exactly 65 rockets when mo at origin. Per rocket inner pipeline (3 P_Random calls in strict order): z = `128 + P_Random()*2*FRACUNIT`, momz = `P_Random()*512`, then setMobjState(rocket, BRAINEXPLODE1) chains to S_BRAINEXPLODE2 (no action), then `tics = STATES[BRAINEXPLODE1].tics(=10) - (P_Random() & 7)` floored at 1. Total: 65×3 = 195 P_Random for the typical brain-death animation. Final action: sfx_bosdth world-relative. (8) A_BrainExplode same per-rocket primitive but x scattered as `mo.x + P_SubRandom() * 2048` (consumes 2 P_Random before z/momz/jitter), y is mo.y exactly (no scatter). TOTAL of 5 P_Random per call (subrandom=2, z, momz, jitter). No final sound — death-loop frames each call this individually. (9) A_BrainDie calls G_ExitLevel via context.exitLevel callback. Consumes no RNG. (10) A_BrainSpit ALWAYS toggles static `easy` flag (XOR with 1) regardless of skill. When `gameskill <= sk_easy(=1) && easy === 0` (post-toggle), early-return — net effect: 50% missile rate on Easy/Very Easy, 100% on Normal+. When numbraintargets=0 the C source crashes via NULL deref on braintargets[0]; we throw to surface the misconfiguration explicitly. After `spawnMissile(mo, targ, MT_SPAWNSHOT)` (which sets missile.target=mo as side effect), OVERRIDES `newmobj.target = targ` so the cube tracks its bosstarget not the brain, then computes `reactiontime = ((targ.y - mo.y) / momy) / state.tics` so A_SpawnFly fires at the right tic when the cube reaches its target column. Plays sfx_bospit world-relative. CONSUMES NO RNG (the `gameskill <= sk_easy` guard is comparison-only, not a roll). (11) A_SpawnSound plays sfx_boscub on the cube (NOT world-relative — the cube IS the sound source) and then delegates to A_SpawnFly. (12) A_SpawnFly decrements reactiontime by 1 first; returns silently if still > 0. On hit-zero: spawn MT_SPAWNFIRE at target.x/y/z, play sfx_telept on the fog, roll ONE P_Random for monster type via pickSpawnFlyType weighted distribution (r<50→TROOP, r<90→SERGEANT, r<120→SHADOWS, r<130→PAIN, r<160→HEAD, r<162→VILE, r<172→UNDEAD, r<192→BABY, r<222→FATSO, r<246→KNIGHT, else→BRUISER — TROOP/SERGEANT/SHADOWS together cover 47% of rolls; VILE only 2/256, UNDEAD 10/256), spawn the monster at target.x/y/z, lookForPlayers(allaround=true) on success → setMobjState(seestate), teleportMove the new monster (telefrag anything in spawn cell), removeMobj(cube). Vanilla P_SubstNullMobj allocates a static dummy mobj at world origin for null targets; we throw on null target to flag corruption. (13) wireBossSpecialsActions installs 24 STATES[] entries: PAIN_DIE5→aPainDie, COMMKEEN11→aKeenDie, FATT_DIE10/BOSS_DIE7/SPID_DIE11/BSPI_DIE7/CYBER_DIE10→aBossDeath (5), CYBER_RUN1→aHoof, SPID_RUN1+5+9/CYBER_RUN7→aMetal (4), BSPI_RUN1+7→aBabyMetal (2), BRAINEYESEE→aBrainAwake, BRAINEYE1→aBrainSpit, BRAIN_PAIN→aBrainPain, BRAIN_DIE1→aBrainScream, BRAIN_DIE4→aBrainDie, BRAINEXPLODE3→aBrainExplode, SPAWN1→aSpawnSound, SPAWN2/3/4→aSpawnFly (3). Total = 24 (BOSS_SPECIALS_ACTION_COUNT). All boss-special action functions guard `if (!context) return;` for safe early bootstrap.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c A_KeenDie/A_PainDie/A_BossDeath/CheckBossEnd/A_Hoof/A_Metal/A_BabyMetal/A_BrainAwake/A_BrainPain/A_BrainScream/A_BrainExplode/A_BrainDie/A_BrainSpit/A_SpawnSound/A_SpawnFly + sounds.h sfxenum_t + info.c state→action mappings (step 11-008); confirmed against src/ai/bossSpecials.ts (~600 lines) and test/ai/boss-specials.test.ts (104 tests, 533 expect() calls)
