## F-111

- fact: Pain/death/fall/explode action functions (p_enemy.c A_Pain, A_Scream, A_XScream, A_PlayerScream, A_Fall, A_Explode — 6 action functions in src/ai/stateTransitions.ts). All guard `if (!context) return;` on the module-level StateTransitionContext singleton (setStateTransitionContext/getStateTransitionContext/clearStateTransitionContext). Context exposes rng, startSound (nullable Mobj origin + sfxId), radiusAttack (Mobj spot, Mobj|null source, number damage — source is nullable to mirror vanilla P_DamageMobj accepting NULL for barrel-without-target), gameMode (() => GameMode). Sound IDs pulled verbatim from sounds.h sfxenum_t: SFX_SLOP=31, SFX_PLDETH=54, SFX_PDIEHI=55, SFX_PODTH1=56, SFX_PODTH2=57, SFX_PODTH3=58, SFX_BGDTH1=59, SFX_BGDTH2=60. Action constants: EXPLODE_DAMAGE=128 (universal rocket/barrel splash payload), PLAYER_SCREAM_GIB_HEALTH=-50 (strict `<`, not `<=`). Parity-critical vanilla quirks: (1) A_Pain plays `info.painsound` on actor origin; zero painsound silently no-ops; consumes NO RNG. (2) A_Scream's pod cycling (`deathsound ∈ {SFX_PODTH1, SFX_PODTH2, SFX_PODTH3}`) consumes exactly ONE P_Random and plays `SFX_PODTH1 + (roll % 3)`; bg cycling (`deathsound ∈ {SFX_BGDTH1, SFX_BGDTH2}`) consumes exactly ONE P_Random and plays `SFX_BGDTH1 + (roll % 2)`; every other deathsound is played verbatim with ZERO RNG; deathsound==0 is silent with ZERO RNG. (3) A_Scream routes the sound through `S_StartSound(NULL, ...)` (world-relative, distance-unattenuated) ONLY for MT_SPIDER and MT_CYBORG; every other monster type uses the actor as sound origin. (4) A_XScream always plays SFX_SLOP on the actor regardless of monster type; consumes no RNG. (5) A_PlayerScream uses strict `mo.health < -50` — a player corpse at exactly -50 health still plays SFX_PLDETH; only `< -50` triggers SFX_PDIEHI. Combined with `gameMode === "commercial"` requirement, any non-commercial WAD (shareware/registered/retail/indetermined) always plays SFX_PLDETH regardless of damage. (6) A_Fall is literally `actor.flags &= ~MF_SOLID` — MF_CORPSE (set by P_KillMobj earlier), MF_SHOOTABLE (cleared by P_KillMobj), MF_NOGRAVITY, MF_TRANSLATION, and every other bit are left untouched. Idempotent. Does NOT require context. (7) A_Explode passes `thingy.target` straight through as the P_RadiusAttack source — a barrel that detonated without ever being damaged has target==null, which propagates to P_DamageMobj as null source (no kill credit assigned). PAIN_DEATH_ACTION_COUNT=69 STATES[] entries wired by wirePainDeathActions: 19 aPain (one painstate-2 per monster, CYBER_PAIN has no PAIN2 so the single frame is wired directly); 19 aScream (one deathstate-chain frame per monster with deathsound + BEXP2 barrel pre-explosion + COMMKEEN3); 6 aXScream (PLAYER/POSSESSED/SHOTGUY/CHAINGUY/TROOP/WOLFSS xdeath chains — no xdeath for SERGEANT/HEAD/BRUISER/KNIGHT/SKULL/VILE/UNDEAD/FATSO/PAIN/SPIDER/BABY/CYBORG/KEEN); 22 aFall (corpse-settle frames in both ordinary and extreme death chains; PAIN elemental DIE5 calls A_PainDie owning corpse settle + lost-soul spawn — deferred to 11-008); 2 aExplode (S_EXPLODE1 rocket, S_BEXP4 barrel); 1 aPlayerScream (PLAY_DIE2). Revenant (UNDEAD/SKEL) uses SKEL_DIE3→aScream and SKEL_DIE4→aFall (one tic later than other monsters). Spider mastermind and arachnotron use SPID_DIE1/BSPI_DIE1 for scream and SPID_DIE2/BSPI_DIE2 for fall — compressed 2-frame death sequence. Cyberdemon uses CYBER_DIE2 scream and CYBER_DIE6 fall. Mancubus/Archvile/Cacodemon/Baron/Hell Knight/Lost Soul all have no xdeath chain. TROO_XDIE uses XDIE4 (not XDIE3) for fall — longer xdeath sequence than POSSESSED/SHOTGUY/CHAINGUY/SSWV which use XDIE3. The "raise" half of the step title refers to raisestate state chains (POSS_RAISE1..POSS_RAISE4 etc.) walked during resurrection — those frames have no action pointers of their own; A_VileChase (deferred to 11-008) drives the transition. PAIN_PAIN2→aPain and PAIN_DIE2→aScream are wired; PAIN_DIE5 (A_PainDie) and PAIN_DIE6 (corpse removal) deferred. COMMKEEN3→aScream and KEENPAIN2→aPain wired; A_KeenDie in COMMKEEN11 deferred to 11-008.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c A_Pain/A_Scream/A_XScream/A_PlayerScream/A_Fall/A_Explode, info.c state→action mappings, sounds.h sfxenum_t table (step 11-007); confirmed against src/ai/stateTransitions.ts (461 lines) and test/ai/state-transitions.test.ts (50 tests, 315 expect() calls)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 11-008, 12-004, 17-010

## F-115

- fact: Animated textures and flats (p_spec.c P_InitPicAnims + the animation half of P_UpdateSpecials) live in src/specials/animations.ts. ANIMDEFS[] is the 22-entry vanilla source table in exact p_spec.c order: 9 flats (NUKAGE1→NUKAGE3, FWATER1→FWATER4, SWATER1→SWATER4, LAVA1→LAVA4, BLOOD1→BLOOD3, RROCK05→RROCK08, SLIME01→SLIME04, SLIME05→SLIME08, SLIME09→SLIME12) followed by 13 textures (BLODGR1→BLODGR4, SLADRIP1→SLADRIP3, BLODRIP1→BLODRIP4, FIREWALA→FIREWALL, GSTFONT1→GSTFONT3, FIRELAV3→FIRELAVA, FIREMAG1→FIREMAG3, FIREBLU1→FIREBLU2, ROCKRED1→ROCKRED3, BFALL1→BFALL4, SFALL1→SFALL4, WFALL1→WFALL4, DBRAIN1→DBRAIN4). Every vanilla cycle uses speed=8 (one frame advance per 8 tics). MAXANIMS=32 is the vanilla cap (the source list of 22 fits comfortably). Filtering rule: initPicAnims(resolver) walks ANIMDEFS in order, calling resolver.checkTextureNumForName for textures and resolver.checkFlatLumpForName (i.e. W_CheckNumForName, NOT R_CheckFlatForName) for flats — flats use the raw lump-space check because R_FlatNumForName aborts on miss. When the start-name lookup returns -1 the animdef is silently dropped (the vanilla "different episode" fall-through — on shareware DOOM1.WAD only NUKAGE/FWATER/LAVA/BLOOD/FIREWALA/FIREMAG/FIREBLU/ROCKRED/FIRELAV3 resolve; every Doom II flat (RROCK/SLIME/SWATER) and every Doom II texture (BLODGR/SLADRIP/BLODRIP/GSTFONT/BFALL/SFALL/WFALL/DBRAIN) is dropped). numpics = picnum - basepic + 1; if < 2 the implementation throws with message "P_InitPicAnims: bad cycle from <start> to <end>" to match vanilla I_Error. updateAnimTranslation(anims, leveltime, textureTranslation, flatTranslation) implements the per-tic rotation: for each anim, for i in [basepic, basepic+numpics), pic = basepic + ((Math.trunc(leveltime/speed) + i) % numpics); table[i] = pic (table = textureTranslation for istexture, flatTranslation otherwise). Key vanilla subtleties preserved byte-for-byte: (1) At leveltime=0 the update does NOT reset translation to identity — when basepic%numpics != 0 the initial write is a non-trivial permutation (e.g. NUKAGE at basepic=10, numpics=3: translation[10]=11, [11]=12, [12]=10 on the very first tic). Vanilla relies on R_InitTextures/R_InitFlats to have seeded the surrounding slots with identity before P_UpdateSpecials first runs. (2) The update is idempotent within a single tic and only overwrites [basepic, picnum] — unanimated slots retain whatever value the translation tables hold. (3) Integer division uses Math.trunc toward zero; leveltime is always non-negative so the `%` sign ambiguity never surfaces. (4) The cycle period is numpics\*speed tics exactly — e.g. FWATER (numpics=4, speed=8) rotates back to its t=0 permutation every 32 tics. Renderer contract: translation tables are Int32Array of length numtextures+1 / numflats+1 seeded by R_InitTextures/R_InitFlats; updateAnimTranslation only mutates the animated slices. The source table is Object.freeze'd so callers cannot mutate the vanilla cycle list at runtime.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_spec.c P_InitPicAnims + animdefs[] + animation loop of P_UpdateSpecials (step 12-001); r_data.c R_InitTextures/R_InitFlats translation-table lifecycle; confirmed against src/specials/animations.ts (~235 lines) and test/specials/animations.test.ts (20 tests, 272 expect() calls)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-002 (door specials share the P_UpdateSpecials per-tic cadence), 12-010 (active-special save hooks should persist leveltime alongside anim state), 13-005 (wall-column fetch reads texturetranslation on every column), 13-009 (visplane spans read flattranslation), 17-008, 17-010

## F-116

- fact: Vertical door specials (p*doors.c T_VerticalDoor, EV_DoDoor, EV_VerticalDoor, EV_DoLockedDoor, P_SpawnDoorCloseIn30, P_SpawnDoorRaiseIn5Mins) live in src/specials/doors.ts. Direction sentinel values are `closing=-1, waiting=0, opening=1, initialWait=2`; the same ints double as T_MovePlane's `direction` argument (doors always pass `floorOrCeiling=1` to move the ceiling, `crush=false`). VDOORSPEED=FRACUNIT*2 (2 world units per tic, 3 seconds full-open at 32u height); VDOORWAIT=150 tics (~4.3s) — blaze doors use speed*4 but share the same wait. DOOR_CEILING_OFFSET=4·F is the vanilla visual "lip" between topheight and the lowest neighbor ceiling (P_FindLowestCeilingSurrounding(sec) - 4·F). CLOSE30_TICS=30*TICRATE=1050; RAISE_IN_5MINS_TICS=5*60\*TICRATE=10500. The 8 vldoor_e types are `normal=0, close30ThenOpen=1, close=2, open=3, raiseIn5Mins=4, blazeRaise=5, blazeOpen=6, blazeClose=7` in canonical p_spec.h order. Parity-critical vanilla quirks preserved byte-for-byte: (1) On close-crush, `close` and `blazeClose` DO NOT reverse (they continue descending); every other type reverses to opening AND plays `sfx_doropn` — even blazeRaise (NOT the blaze sound sfx_bdopn). This asymmetry is load-bearing vanilla behavior, not a bug. (2) Opening-side pastdest: `normal`/`blazeRaise` enter waiting with topwait countdown; `open`/`blazeOpen`/`close30ThenOpen` remove the thinker and clear sector.specialdata. T_MovePlane opening with crush=false cannot crush, so there is no opening-crush case to handle. (3) Closing-side pastdest: `normal`/`close` remove silently; `blazeRaise`/`blazeClose` remove AND play sfx_bdcls (blaze doors are the only types whose arrival-at-floor emits sound); `close30ThenOpen` does NOT remove — it enters waiting with topcountdown=CLOSE30_TICS for the 30-second pause before re-opening. (4) Re-activation path in evVerticalDoor only applies to line specials 1, 26, 27, 28, 117 (the repeatable codes). On lines 31-34 and 118 (one-shot keyed/blaze), the function falls through to creation — overwriting sector.specialdata with a fresh thinker and orphaning the previous door. This "orphan-thinker" potential is vanilla (the old thinker is still in the P_RunThinkers ring; it finishes its cycle writing into a sector now controlled by a second thinker). (5) Monster guard (JDC comment in source): if the triggering player is null AND the existing door is NOT currently closing, evVerticalDoor silently returns 0 — monsters may only re-OPEN a closing door, never close one. A closing door CAN be re-opened by a monster (flips direction to opening). (6) One-shot `line.special = 0` is written ONLY for vld_open / vld_blazeOpen variants (lines 31-34 and 118) — every EV*\* call site that writes to the linedef is confined to this path. (7) raiseIn5Mins uses initialWait=2 to queue the first raise; on countdown expire the type MUTATES to `normal` so the rest of the cycle (open → wait → close) runs identically to a normal door. Both spawners (spawnDoorCloseIn30 for sector special 10, spawnDoorRaiseIn5Mins for sector special 14) clear sector.special after arming. (8) evDoDoor's sound policy: close types always play sfx_dorcls / sfx_bdcls; open/raise types play the open sound ONLY when topheight !== sector.ceilingheight — doors already at their destination stay silent. (9) Key-denial messages differ between manual (-K suffix, "open this door") and tagged (-O suffix, "activate this object") codes: PD_BLUEK/REDK/YELLOWK for lines 26-28/32-34; PD_BLUEO/REDO/YELLOWO for lines 99/133-137. sfx_oof (34) is routed via the `startPlayerSound` callback (world-relative null origin) to distinguish from sector sounds. Architecture: movePlane and findLowestCeilingSurrounding are injected via a DoorCallbacks bundle to break a cyclic import with floor/ceiling movers (deferred to 12-003/12-005). DoorSector is the minimal sector contract (ceilingheight/floorheight/special/specialdata/tag); later steps must satisfy it with the full runtime sector type. VerticalDoor extends ThinkerNode; REMOVED is set on its `action` field in the closing-pastdest branch and opening-pastdest-for-remove branch, unlinked by ThinkerList.run on the NEXT tic (matching vanilla P_RunThinkers semantics).
- source: Chocolate Doom p_doors.c (T_VerticalDoor, EV_DoDoor, EV_VerticalDoor, EV_DoLockedDoor, P_SpawnDoorCloseIn30, P_SpawnDoorRaiseIn5Mins) + p_spec.h vldoor_e / result_e; sounds.h sfxenum_t table (step 12-002); confirmed against src/specials/doors.ts (~740 lines) and test/specials/doors.test.ts (44 tests, 1242 expect() calls)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-003 (ceiling-movers share the movePlane + findLowestCeilingSurrounding callbacks — one implementation shared across doors/floors/ceilings), 12-005 (floor-movers with doDoor for boss-death tag 666 / 667 triggers), 12-006 (P_SpawnSpecials must call spawnDoorCloseIn30 on sector special 10 and spawnDoorRaiseIn5Mins on special 14 at level load), 12-009 (P_UseLines wires manual door line specials 1/26-28/31-34/117/118 through evVerticalDoor), 17-008 (orphan-thinker and crush-reverse-plays-doropn as vanilla regressions to guard)

## F-117

- fact: TypeScript `const enum` narrows class-field types across assignments in tests — a known TS control-flow pattern. After `door.direction = DoorDirection.opening;` in a test, the type of `door.direction` is narrowed from the full enum union to the literal `DoorDirection.opening` for every subsequent read in the same scope; calls like `tVerticalDoor(door)` do NOT reset this narrowing (TS does not track param mutations). The generic `toBe<T>` overload then rejects comparisons against other members: `expect(door.direction).toBe(DoorDirection.waiting)` errors with "Argument of type 'DoorDirection.waiting' is not assignable to parameter of type 'DoorDirection.opening'". Same effect on `ThinkerNode.action` (narrowed to `ThinkFunction` after assignment) and `Player.message` (narrowed to `null` after `player.message = null`). Workaround in tests: use explicit `expect<T>(x).toBe(y)` to widen the matcher's type parameter — e.g. `expect<DoorDirection>(door.direction).toBe(DoorDirection.waiting)`, `expect<string | null>(player.message).toBe(PD_YELLOWK)`, `expect<ThinkFunction | typeof REMOVED | null>(door.action).toBe(REMOVED)`. Bun's test.d.ts declares two toBe overloads: `toBe(expected: T): void` (T inferred from receiver, narrowed) and `toBe<X = T>(expected: NoInfer<X>): void` (X explicit, NoInfer prevents re-inference from the argument). Passing an explicit generic on `expect` resolves the matcher's T against the widened type and the narrow second overload is no longer needed. This is test-only — production code reads inside a `switch (door.direction)` statement narrow per-case, which is the intended behavior.
- source: Test diagnosis during step 12-002; Bun bun-types 1.3.12 test.d.ts `toBe(expected: T)` and `toBe<X = T>(expected: NoInfer<X>)` declarations (lines 976-977); TS 5.x control-flow-on-properties narrowing behavior
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-003, 12-005, 12-009 (any future specials step that mutates class-field unions in tests will hit the same narrowing — apply the same `expect<T>(x)` pattern), 17-010

## F-119

- fact: A_VileAttack victim launch velocity is plain integer division `1000*FRACUNIT / mass` in vanilla (p_enemy.c `actor->target->momz = 1000*FRACUNIT/actor->target->info->mass;`), NOT a FixedDiv. For all in-game mass values (cyberdemon 1000, pinky 400, zombie 100, imp 100, lost soul 50, etc.) the result is `(1000*FRACUNIT/mass) | 0` and fits in a JS safe integer without intermediate overflow. Using `FixedDiv(1000*FRACUNIT, mass*FRACUNIT)` is numerically equivalent (proof: `FixedDiv(a,b) = (a<<16)/b = ((1000*FRACUNIT)<<16)/(mass*FRACUNIT) = 1000*FRACUNIT/mass` when the saturation branch is not taken, and `absA>>14 = 4000 < mass*FRACUNIT` for mass≥1) but slower (one extra multiply + saturation branch) and obscures the C reference. The implementation in src/ai/attacks.ts uses plain division.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_enemy.c A_VileAttack (line ~1336); src/core/fixed.ts fixedDiv definition; algebraic verification across mass ∈ [1, 1000]
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 11-006 locks this in; 17-010 regression sweep

## F-118

- fact: Lift / platform specials (p_plats.c T_PlatRaise, EV_DoPlat, EV_StopPlat, P_ActivateInStasis, P_AddActivePlat, P_RemoveActivePlat) live in src/specials/platforms.ts. Plats only ever move the FLOOR plane: T_MovePlane is always called with `floorOrCeiling = 0`. Vanilla constants: PLATSPEED=FRACUNIT (1 world unit per tic, 4× for downWaitUpStay, 8× for blazeDWUS, 1/2 for raiseAndChange + raiseToNearestAndChange); PLATWAIT=3 seconds (`PLATWAIT_TICS = TICRATE * PLATWAIT = 105`); MAXPLATS=30 (fixed slot array, vanilla `I_Error("P_AddActivePlat: no more plats!")` on overflow — preserved as a JS throw). The 5 plattype_e values: `perpetualRaise=0, downWaitUpStay=1, raiseAndChange=2, raiseToNearestAndChange=3, blazeDWUS=4`. The 4 plat_e status values: `up=0, down=1, waiting=2, inStasis=3` (the integers `up=0` and `down=1` double as the result of `P_Random()&1` for perpetualRaise's randomized initial direction). Plat sounds (sounds.h sfxenum_t order with sfx_None=0): SFX_PSTART=18, SFX_PSTOP=19, SFX_STNMOV=22. Parity-critical vanilla quirks preserved byte-for-byte: (1) The down branch calls `T_MovePlane(sector, speed, low, false, 0, -1)` with `crush = false` LITERAL — vanilla never reads `plat.crush` for the descending leg. The up branch passes `plat.crush` through. (2) Crush-reverse (`up → down + sfx_pstart`) is gated `if (res === crushed && !plat.crush)`. Since EV_DoPlat sets `crush = false` for every type, the crush-reverse path is the always-true case in production; the false branch (continue rising into the obstacle) only triggers if a caller manually sets `plat.crush = true`. (3) Up-pastdest sound is `sfx_pstop` for ALL plat types; the count is set to `plat.wait` even though raiseAndChange / raiseToNearestAndChange use `wait = 0` (waiting state runs once with `count = -1` after decrement, never satisfying `count === 0`, so no second sfx_pstart fires — both are removed in the same tic before that matters). (4) Removal on up-pastdest applies to `downWaitUpStay`, `blazeDWUS`, `raiseAndChange`, `raiseToNearestAndChange` (4 of the 5 types); `perpetualRaise` stays alive and bounces between low and high forever. (5) During an up move, `raiseAndChange` and `raiseToNearestAndChange` re-fire `sfx_stnmov` every 8 leveltime tics via `if (!(leveltime & 7))` BEFORE the pastdest check, so the move-completion tic also re-plays sfx_stnmov if its leveltime is a multiple of 8 (the tic also plays sfx_pstop). All other plat types are silent during travel. (6) Waiting branch chooses next direction by `plat.sector.floorheight === plat.low ? up : down` (NOT `=== high`) — a plat that completed a down move is now at low, so up is next; one that completed a perpetualRaise up move is at high, so down is next. (7) Vanilla T_PlatRaise's switch falls through from `waiting` to `in_stasis` (no `break` between cases). Both cases are no-ops past the `--count` check, so the missing break is observationally identical to having one. We model both cases explicitly with `break`. (8) EV_DoPlat for `perpetualRaise` calls P_ActivateInStasis(line.tag) BEFORE iterating sectors; the in-stasis activation happens even when the line-tag iteration creates no new plats, but the integer return value only counts newly-created plats. (9) Floor-clamp parity: every type that reads `findLowestFloorSurrounding` clamps `low = min(neighbors, floorheight)` so a sector whose neighbors are all higher cannot push the floor UP via the down branch; perpetualRaise additionally clamps `high = max(neighbors, floorheight)`. (10) `raiseAndChange` and `raiseToNearestAndChange` set `wait = 0`, copy `sec.floorpic = line.frontFloorpic` (sides[line.sidenum[0]].sector->floorpic) BEFORE the move starts, and play `sfx_stnmov` immediately. `raiseToNearestAndChange` ALSO clears `sec.special = 0` so any sector damage stops once the lift completes (the comment in vanilla is "NO MORE DAMAGE, IF APPLICABLE"). (11) Stasis lifecycle: EV_StopPlat saves `oldstatus = status`, sets `status = inStasis`, and detaches the action (vanilla `thinker.function.acv = NULL`; we set `action = null` so ThinkerList.run skips the node but keeps it in the ring). P_ActivateInStasis restores `status = oldstatus` and re-attaches the closure-wrapped tPlatRaise action. EV_StopPlat ignores plats already in stasis (the `oldstatus` is preserved) and only matches non-stasis plats with the requested tag; P_ActivateInStasis ignores non-matching tags and non-stasis plats. (12) ActivePlats registry is a 30-slot array. P_AddActivePlat scans linearly for the first NULL slot (so freed slots are reused; insertion order is not stable across remove/add cycles). P_RemoveActivePlat scans linearly for the plat instance, clears `sector.specialdata`, marks `action = REMOVED`, and frees the slot — throws if the plat is not registered (vanilla I_Error). Architecture: all side effects (movePlane, three find-floor lookups, optional sound, pRandom, getLevelTime) are injected via PlatCallbacks so the same T_MovePlane implementation can be shared across doors / plats / floors / ceilings without cyclic imports. tPlatRaise takes ActivePlats explicitly so it can call `plats.remove(plat)` on up-pastdest for non-perpetual types; evDoPlat wraps the call in `(t) => tPlatRaise(t, plats)` to satisfy the `ThinkFunction` action signature. PlaneMoveResult is re-exported from doors.ts (one source of truth for the T_MovePlane return enum). PlatLine carries `tag` and `frontFloorpic` (precomputed by the caller from the linedef's front sidedef's sector); types that do not change the floorpic ignore the field and callers may pass any value (typically 0).
- source: Chocolate Doom p_plats.c (T_PlatRaise, EV_DoPlat, P_ActivateInStasis, EV_StopPlat, P_AddActivePlat, P_RemoveActivePlat) + p_spec.h plat_e/plattype_e/MAXPLATS/PLATSPEED/PLATWAIT; sounds.h sfxenum_t table (step 12-003); confirmed against src/specials/platforms.ts (~430 lines) and test/specials/platforms.test.ts (33 tests, 106 expect() calls)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-004 (floor movers — EV_DoFloor / T_MoveFloor share the same movePlane + findLowest/HighestFloor / findNextHighestFloor callbacks; the PlatCallbacks bundle is the prototype for the floor's larger callback set), 12-005 (ceiling movers complete the trio; the cross-cutting T_MovePlane lives with one of these), 12-009 (line-trigger dispatch: WR/W1/SR/S1/G1 lift codes 10/15/22/49/53/62/87/88 wire through evDoPlat; line 54/89 wires through evStopPlat; perpetualRaise tags activate in-stasis plats), 12-010 (active-special save hooks must persist plat status/oldstatus/count/low/high so a savegame mid-cycle resumes correctly; the in-stasis NULL-action shape needs special encode to preserve oldstatus across save/load), 17-010

## F-120

- fact: Floor movers (p_floor.c T_MoveFloor, EV_DoFloor) live in src/specials/floors.ts. Floors only ever move the FLOOR plane: T_MovePlane is always called with `floorOrCeiling = 0`. Vanilla constants: FLOORSPEED=FRACUNIT (1 world unit per tic; turboLower + raiseFloorTurbo use *4); FLOOR_8_UNIT_OFFSET=8*FRACUNIT (turboLower bump + raiseFloorCrush clearance); FLOOR_24_UNIT_OFFSET=24*FRACUNIT (raiseFloor24 + raiseFloor24AndChange); FLOOR_512_UNIT_OFFSET=512*FRACUNIT (raiseFloor512). The 13 floor_e values in canonical p_spec.h order: `lowerFloor=0, lowerFloorToLowest=1, turboLower=2, raiseFloor=3, raiseFloorToNearest=4, raiseToTexture=5, lowerAndChange=6, raiseFloor24=7, raiseFloor24AndChange=8, raiseFloorCrush=9, raiseFloorTurbo=10, donutRaise=11, raiseFloor512=12`. FloorDirection: `down=-1, up=1` (same integers passed directly as T_MovePlane's `direction` argument). Floor sounds (sounds.h sfxenum_t order with sfx_None=0): SFX_STNMOV=22, SFX_PSTOP=19. Parity-critical vanilla quirks preserved byte-for-byte: (1) T_MoveFloor plays `sfx_stnmov` every 8 leveltime tics (`!(leveltime & 7)`) regardless of direction and regardless of whether the move made progress this tic — callback is `callbacks.startSectorSound(sector, SFX_STNMOV)` gated on `(leveltime & 7) === 0` placed AFTER movePlane returns and BEFORE the pastdest branch. (2) On pastdest: clear `sector.specialdata = null`, run the direction-gated texture/special swap, mark thinker REMOVED, play `sfx_pstop`. The swap is direction-gated via two switch blocks that in vanilla fall through to `default: break` — observationally a single-case match, but we model both switches explicitly: `direction === up` handles `donutRaise` (copies `floor.texture → sector.floorpic` + `floor.newspecial → sector.special`), `direction === down` handles `lowerAndChange` (same two writes). (3) On arrival tic if `leveltime` is a multiple of 8, both `sfx_stnmov` (scrape) AND `sfx_pstop` (arrival) fire in the same tic — preserved parity quirk. (4) EV_DoFloor skips sectors whose `specialdata !== null` without bumping the return counter (`rtn` only counts newly-created thinkers). Sectors with mismatched tags are ignored. EV_DoFloor returns 1 if ANY mover was created, 0 otherwise. (5) `turboLower` raises its destination by 8 units ONLY when the highest surrounding floor differs from the starting floorheight: `dest = findHighestFloorSurrounding(sector); if (dest !== sector.floorheight) dest += 8*FRACUNIT;` — a sector with no strictly-higher neighbor stays at floorheight (no bump, no travel). The speed is 4*FLOORSPEED. (6) `raiseFloor` / `raiseFloorCrush` share a `case` fall-through: `dest = findLowestCeilingSurrounding(sector); if (dest > sector.ceilingheight) dest = sector.ceilingheight;` then `raiseFloorCrush` subtracts 8*FRACUNIT. Vanilla writes this as `dest -= 8*FRACUNIT * (type == raiseFloorCrush)` — we use an `if (type === raiseFloorCrush)` branch. `raiseFloorCrush` is the ONE type that sets `floor.crush = true`; every other type ships `crush = false`. (7) `raiseFloor24AndChange` mutates `sector.floorpic` + `sector.special` IMMEDIATELY at creation time (copying from `line.frontFloorpic` + `line.frontSpecial`), not at pastdest. The move itself is a vanilla 24-unit raise. (8) `lowerAndChange` seeds `floor.texture = sector.floorpic` BEFORE the adjacent-sector scan, so an unmatched neighbor lookup leaves the sector's own floorpic plus `newspecial=0`. On match (first two-sided neighbor whose floorheight equals `dest`), copy `match.floorpic → floor.texture` + `match.special → floor.newspecial`. Swap is deferred to pastdest (guarded by the `direction === down` switch). (9) `raiseToTexture` targets `floorheight + findShortestLowerTexture(sec)` — vanilla inlines the texture-table scan; we delegate via `FloorCallbacks.findShortestLowerTexture` so texture metadata lives outside the specials layer. Vanilla returns INT_MAX when no two-sided line has a valid bottom texture; callers forward the sentinel unchanged. (10) `donutRaise` has NO construction case in EV_DoFloor's switch — the type exists in `floor_e` solely so T_MoveFloor's pastdest branch can run the texture/special swap for donut-raised sectors. EV_DoDonut (step 12-006) constructs donutRaise movers directly and overwrites direction/speed/destheight/texture/newspecial. In our impl, `EV_DoFloor(FloorType.donutRaise, ...)` falls through to `default: break` — the mover is created with `direction=up, speed=FLOORSPEED, floordestheight=0, texture=0, newspecial=0` (class defaults). Callers must overwrite those fields or the thinker completes on tic 1 with a no-op swap. (11) All side effects (movePlane + five neighbor lookups + optional sound + getLevelTime) are injected via FloorCallbacks so the cross-cutting T_MovePlane can be shared with doors/plats/ceilings without cyclic imports. The five neighbor lookups are: `findLowestFloorSurrounding`, `findHighestFloorSurrounding`, `findNextHighestFloor(sector, currentHeight)`, `findLowestCeilingSurrounding`, `findShortestLowerTexture`, plus a separate `findAdjacentSectorAtFloorHeight(sector, height)` for lowerAndChange's neighbor scan (returns `{floorpic, special} | null`). PlaneMoveResult is re-exported from `./doors.ts` — one source of truth across doors/plats/floors/ceilings. FloorSector is `{floorheight, ceilingheight, floorpic, special, specialdata, tag}` — extends PlatSector's contract exactly. FloorLine is `{tag, frontFloorpic, frontSpecial}` — the caller precomputes both front-side fields from `sides[line.sidenum[0]].sector`. Types that don't consume either field ignore them; callers may pass `0`.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_floor.c (T_MoveFloor, EV_DoFloor) + p_spec.h floor_e; sounds.h sfxenum_t table (step 12-003); confirmed against src/specials/floors.ts (~440 lines) and test/specials/floors.test.ts (35 tests, 93 expect() calls)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-005 (ceiling movers — T_MoveCeiling + EV_DoCeiling share the same movePlane + findLowest/HighestCeiling callbacks; the FloorCallbacks bundle is the prototype for the ceiling's symmetric lookup set — ceilings need findLowestCeilingSurrounding + findHighestCeilingSurrounding, not the floor-flavored lookups), 12-006 (stairs-and-donut — EV_BuildStairs constructs bare FloorMove thinkers directly with speed/direction override; EV_DoDonut constructs a donutRaise-typed FloorMove for the outer sector AND a lowerFloor thinker for the inner sector — both share T_MoveFloor's pastdest swap logic), 12-009 (line-trigger dispatch — dozens of line specials wire through evDoFloor: WR/W1/SR/S1 codes 18/19/23/30/36/37/38/60/64/65/66/67/68/69/70/71/82/83/84/91/92/93/94/96/98/101/102/119/128/129/130/131/132/140/141 cover all 13 floor_e types via the line-special → FloorType table), 17-008 (vanilla regression suite: donutRaise pastdest swap + lowerAndChange pastdest swap + raiseFloorCrush=true crush path + turboLower 8-unit-bump-only-when-differs + raiseFloor24AndChange creation-time mutation + sfx_stnmov every-8-tics gate + arrival-tic-plays-both-sounds), 17-010 (regression sweep)

## F-121

- fact: The blockmap validcount generation counter must use C int32 wrap-around semantics, not unbounded JS number growth. Chocolate Doom stores `validcount` as `int` and writes each line's stamp via `ld->validcount = validcount` — both values share the same 32-bit signed wrap. In TypeScript our stamp array is Int32Array (so writes silently truncate to int32), which means the generation counter must also be forced into int32 via `(current + 1) | 0` on increment; otherwise after 2^31 increments the JS number would diverge from the int32 stamp (comparison would stop matching and every line would be wrongly re-visited within a single query). The incrementValidCount function in src/map/blockmapIter.ts applies `| 0` to keep current and stamps in the same int32 domain.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_maputl.c P_BlockLinesIterator + r_main.c validcount global (int); Int32Array truncation semantics; audit pass on step 08-008
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-009 (intercepts iteration uses the same validcount convention — apply the same int32 wrap guard if an independent generation counter is introduced), 17-010

## F-122

- fact: Ceiling movers and crushers (p_ceilng.c T_MoveCeiling, EV_DoCeiling, P_ActivateInStasisCeiling, EV_CeilingCrushStop, P_AddActiveCeiling, P_RemoveActiveCeiling) live in src/specials/ceilings.ts. Ceilings only ever move the CEILING plane: T_MovePlane is always called with `floorOrCeiling = 1`. Vanilla constants: CEILSPEED=FRACUNIT (fastCrushAndRaise uses 2×), CEILWAIT=150 (declared in p_spec.h but never read by p_ceilng.c — every cadence is derived from `leveltime & 7`), MAXCEILINGS=30, CEILING_8_UNIT_OFFSET=8*FRACUNIT. The 6 ceiling_e values in canonical p_spec.h order: `lowerToFloor=0, raiseToHighest=1, lowerAndCrush=2, crushAndRaise=3, fastCrushAndRaise=4, silentCrushAndRaise=5`. CeilingDirection: `down=-1, inStasis=0, up=1` (integers passed directly to T_MovePlane, with 0 as the in-stasis sentinel — the action is detached on stasis so T_MoveCeiling's 0-case is defensive). Ceiling sounds (sounds.h sfxenum_t indices): SFX_STNMOV=22, SFX_PSTOP=19. Parity-critical vanilla quirks preserved byte-for-byte: (1) The UP branch passes `crush = false` LITERAL to T_MovePlane — vanilla never forwards `ceiling.crush` on the upward leg; only the DOWN branch passes `ceiling.crush` through. (2) Every 8 leveltime tics (`!(leveltime & 7)`) the thinker plays `sfx_stnmov` EXCEPT for `silentCrushAndRaise`, which stays silent during travel in BOTH directions. Cadence is independent of direction and independent of the move result. (3) UP-pastdest switch: `raiseToHighest` → removed; `silentCrushAndRaise` → plays `sfx_pstop` then sets `direction = -1`; `fastCrushAndRaise` / `crushAndRaise` → set `direction = -1` silently; every other type is a no-op. (4) DOWN-pastdest switch uses vanilla C fall-through: `silentCrushAndRaise` plays `sfx_pstop` + falls into `crushAndRaise` which resets `speed = CEILSPEED` + falls into `fastCrushAndRaise` which sets `direction = 1` — so silent plays pstop AND resets speed AND reverses; crushAndRaise resets speed AND reverses (no sound); fastCrushAndRaise ONLY reverses (no sound, no speed reset — fast-crushers keep their CEILSPEED*2 forever). `lowerAndCrush` / `lowerToFloor` → removed; all other types are no-ops at DOWN-pastdest. We encode the fall-through explicitly as three separate `case` branches to keep the behavior readable. (5) DOWN-crushed (movePlane returned crushed, not pastdest): `silentCrushAndRaise` / `crushAndRaise` / `lowerAndCrush` drop to `speed = CEILSPEED / 8` — the canonical grinding-crush cadence. `fastCrushAndRaise` / `lowerToFloor` / `raiseToHighest` keep their current speed (fast-crushers are intentionally unthrottled; the other two don't participate in crushing logic). (6) EV_DoCeiling reactivates in-stasis ceilings BEFORE iterating sectors, but ONLY for the three crusher types `crushAndRaise` / `silentCrushAndRaise` / `fastCrushAndRaise`. Vanilla uses a fall-through into `default: break`; we encode the crusher-whitelist explicitly. The return counter reflects NEWLY CREATED ceilings only — stasis wakeups do NOT bump `rtn`. (7) EV_DoCeiling sets `ceiling.crush = false` before the per-type switch; only the three crusher types (`crushAndRaise`, `silentCrushAndRaise`, `fastCrushAndRaise`) override to `true`. `lowerAndCrush` and `lowerToFloor` ship `crush = false` — the crush behavior of `lowerAndCrush` comes from its DOWN-pastdest reversal (plus the crushed-speed-reduction if the descent is obstructed), not from forwarding `crush=true` to T_MovePlane. (8) EV_DoCeiling construction fall-through: `silentCrushAndRaise` and `crushAndRaise` set `topheight = sec.ceilingheight` then fall through to share bottomheight / direction / speed with `lowerAndCrush` / `lowerToFloor`. `fastCrushAndRaise` sets its own topheight + bottomheight without fall-through. `lowerAndCrush` uses `bottomheight = floorheight + 8*FRACUNIT`; `lowerToFloor` uses `bottomheight = floorheight` (NO 8-unit clearance). `raiseToHighest` calls `findHighestCeilingSurrounding(sec)` for topheight and sets `direction = up`. (9) ActiveCeilings registry is SILENT on overflow AND on missing-lookup — P_AddActiveCeiling returns without inserting when every slot is occupied (no I_Error, unlike plats); P_RemoveActiveCeiling exits its loop without ever matching when the ceiling is not registered. Both quirks preserved byte-for-byte. (10) P_ActivateInStasisCeiling restores `direction = olddirection` and re-attaches T_MoveCeiling on every matching-tag entry whose `direction === 0` (inStasis). Non-matching tags and non-stasis entries are untouched. (11) EV_CeilingCrushStop saves `olddirection = direction`, detaches the action (`action = null`), sets `direction = inStasis`, and returns 1 if any match was found. Already-stasis entries are skipped (preserving their existing olddirection). Architecture: all side effects (movePlane + findHighestCeilingSurrounding + optional startSectorSound + getLevelTime) are injected via CeilingCallbacks so the shared T_MovePlane from doors/plats/floors can be reused without cyclic imports. tMoveCeiling takes ActiveCeilings explicitly so it can call `ceilings.remove(ceiling)` on pastdest for non-crusher types; evDoCeiling wraps the call in `(t) => tMoveCeiling(t, ceilings)` to satisfy the ThinkFunction action signature. PlaneMoveResult is re-exported from `./doors.ts`. CeilingSector is `{floorheight, ceilingheight, special, specialdata, tag}` (no floorpic — ceilings never mutate sector visuals, unlike donutRaise / lowerAndChange on the floor side). CeilingLine is `{tag}` only — ceiling movers do not read front-side texture data at creation time.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_ceilng.c (T_MoveCeiling, EV_DoCeiling, P_AddActiveCeiling, P_RemoveActiveCeiling, P_ActivateInStasisCeiling, EV_CeilingCrushStop) + p_spec.h ceiling_e/ceiling_t/MAXCEILINGS/CEILSPEED/CEILWAIT; sounds.h sfxenum_t table (step 12-003); confirmed against src/specials/ceilings.ts (~560 lines) and test/specials/ceilings.test.ts (57 tests, 145 expect() calls)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-006 (stairs-and-donut is floor-only, but the ceilings pattern — explicit fall-through as separate case branches, injected callbacks, silent-overflow registry — extends to any future ceiling-adjacent specials), 12-009 (line-trigger dispatch: WR/W1/SR/S1/G1 ceiling codes 6/25/44/72/73/75/76/77/141/150/151/152/166/167/182/183/184/185/186/187/200/201/202/203/204 wire through evDoCeiling; lines 57/73 stop crushers via evCeilingCrushStop; lines 77/141/163/164/165 activate in-stasis crushers via pActivateInStasisCeiling — the three crusher types in EV_DoCeiling's reactivation whitelist), 12-010 (active-special save hooks must persist ceiling type/direction/olddirection/speed/topheight/bottomheight/crush/tag so a savegame mid-crush resumes correctly; the in-stasis NULL-action shape needs special encode like plats), 17-010 (regression sweep: silent exemption from sfx_stnmov + silent's pstop-at-both-reversals + fastCrushAndRaise's no-speed-reset-ever + crushed speed reduction excluding fast-crushers + silent overflow/missing in ActiveCeilings)

## F-123

- fact: Stair builders and donut pairs (p_floor.c EV_BuildStairs + p_spec.c EV_DoDonut) live in src/specials/stairsDonut.ts. Both helpers construct bare FloorMove thinkers directly — no new thinker action is introduced; they reuse tMoveFloor and the FloorType.donutRaise slot left open by step 12-004. Vanilla constants: STAIR_8_UNIT_SIZE = 8*FRACUNIT, STAIR_16_UNIT_SIZE = 16*FRACUNIT, STAIR_BUILD8_SPEED = FLOORSPEED/4, STAIR_TURBO16_SPEED = FLOORSPEED\*4, DONUT_SPEED = FLOORSPEED/2. StairType values: `build8=0, turbo16=1` matching canonical stair_e order. Parity-critical vanilla quirks preserved byte-for-byte: (1) EV_BuildStairs starter thinker: `type=FloorType.lowerFloor` LITERALLY — stairs borrow the lowerFloor slot but never invoke its neighbor lookups; `direction=up`, `crush=true` (vanilla-parity emulation of Chocolate Doom's `STAIRS_UNINITIALIZED_CRUSH_FIELD_VALUE = 10`, a truthy sentinel that compensates for vanilla leaving the crush field uninitialized — so stair plates KEEP crushing things rather than reverting on a would-be squash), `speed=per-type`, `floordestheight=starter.floorheight+stairsize`. Every hop also writes `crush=true` (vanilla re-initializes the sentinel for each new thinker). (2) The stair-walk texture is `sec->floorpic` sampled EXACTLY ONCE at the starter before the do-while, then frozen — every hop compares `back.floorpic` against this frozen `texture`, never re-reading from the current sec. (3) Directed traversal: the inner `for (i=0; i<sec->linecount; i++)` selects a line only when `sec->lines[i]->frontsector == sec` — lines whose FRONT is the back-sector hop in the reverse direction are ignored. Combined with the ML_TWOSIDED guard this means stair chains are asymmetric and the authoring direction matters. (4) `height += stairsize` is performed BEFORE the `P_SectorActive(floor_special, tsec)` check — if the matched back-sector already has specialdata, the vanilla `continue` advances to the next line WITHOUT rolling back height. A later successful hop therefore starts one or more stairsize multiples too high; this is an observable vanilla parity quirk. (5) The outer `rtn = 1` flip happens AFTER the specialdata-skip check but BEFORE any thinker is spawned — a tag-matching starter with clean specialdata always bumps rtn, even when `stairsize` ends up 0 (unreachable for build8/turbo16 but the pattern matches vanilla). (6) EV_DoDonut `rtn = 1` flip happens BEFORE s2/s3 validation — a malformed donut whose s2 ends up null still reports `rtn = 1` and aborts the OUTER loop with `break`, not `continue`. This means subsequent tag-matching sectors are NOT processed after one malformed pillar. (7) `s2 = getNextSector(s1->lines[0], s1)` — always s1's FIRST linedef in declaration order. `getNextSector` returns null when ML_TWOSIDED is unset OR when the back side is missing; our implementation gates only on ML_TWOSIDED (matching vanilla) — a flagged line with a null backsector still passes the ML check and then returns null via the second clause. (8) Inner `for (i=0; i < s2->linecount; i++)` selects the FIRST line whose raw `backSector` is neither s1 nor null. Vanilla only checks `s3 == s1` — lines whose backsector happens to equal s2 (self) are NOT skipped. Real Doom maps rely on the authoring convention that the inner donut line has rim as front and pillar as back, so iterating rim.lines yields `s3 = line->backsector = pillar = s1` which IS skipped; test geometry must match this convention (linkLine(outer, pillar) for the inner edge, linkLine(outer, reference) for the outer edge). (9) Donut outer-rim mover: `FloorType.donutRaise`, `direction=up`, `speed=FLOORSPEED/2`, `destheight=s3.floorheight`, `texture=s3.floorpic`, `newspecial=0`, `crush=false`. The pastdest swap in tMoveFloor writes `texture → s2.floorpic` and `newspecial → s2.special` so s2 visually inherits s3's floor with a cleared special slot. (10) Donut inner-hole mover: `FloorType.lowerFloor`, `direction=down`, `speed=FLOORSPEED/2`, `destheight=s3.floorheight`, `crush=false`. After both are spawned, `break` out of the s2.lines loop — exactly one donut pair per pillar. (11) DonutOverrun buffer-overrun emulation is exposed via the optional `DonutCallbacks.onDonutOverrun(line, pillar) => {floorheight, floorpic}` hook; when the hook is undefined, null-back-sector lines are skipped silently. Save-compat tests that depend on the overrun bytes must supply the hook. (12) Both helpers skip sectors whose specialdata!==null WITHOUT incrementing rtn (matching vanilla); they add thinkers to the ThinkerList and back-fill sector.specialdata with the new FloorMove. Architecture: StairsDonutSector extends FloorSector with `readonly lines: readonly StairsDonutLinedef[]`; StairsDonutLinedef exposes `{flags, frontSector, backSector}`. Both interfaces are the minimal subset needed to reproduce vanilla traversal — all other sector state flows through the existing FloorCallbacks bridge from step 12-004.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_floor.c (EV_BuildStairs) + p_spec.c (EV_DoDonut, DonutOverrun) + p_spec.h (stair_e) + p_spec.c (getNextSector); confirmed against src/specials/stairsDonut.ts (~335 lines) and test/specials/stairs-donut.test.ts (25 tests, 87 expect() calls)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-009 (line-trigger dispatch: W1/S1/WR/SR stair codes 7/8/100/127 wire through evBuildStairs with the StairType from the line-special table; W1/S1 donut code 9 wires through evDoDonut; both helpers already match the line-tag iteration pattern used by evDoFloor/evDoCeiling so the dispatch table just forwards the line + callbacks), 12-010 (save hooks must persist stair and donut mover state as FloorMove thinkers — same field set as other floors; no new serialization shape needed), 17-008 (vanilla regression suite: directed stair traversal + frozen starter texture + stair height-bump-before-specialdata-skip + donut rtn-before-s2-validation + donut s2=null aborts outer loop + donut overrun-via-optional-hook + donutRaise pastdest texture/special swap), 17-010 (regression sweep)

## F-124

- fact: Switches and held buttons (p_switch.c P_InitSwitchList, P_StartButton, P_ChangeSwitchTexture + p_spec.c P_UpdateSpecials button half) live in src/specials/switches.ts. Vanilla constants: BUTTONTIME=35 (1-second hold before revert), MAXBUTTONS=16 (fixed-capacity button slot array), MAXSWITCHES=50 (outer `alphSwitchList[]` iteration bound), SFX_SWTCHN=23 (sfx_swtchn, press + release sound), SFX_SWTCHX=24 (sfx_swtchx, exit-switch-only press variant), EXIT_SWITCH_SPECIAL=11 (line special that selects the exit sound variant). ButtonWhere enum matches bwhere_e: `top=0, middle=1, bottom=2`. ALPH_SWITCH_LIST has exactly 40 pairs in canonical source order: 19 episode-1 + 10 episode-2 + 11 episode-3. gamemode → episode threshold: `shareware|indetermined → 1`, `registered|retail → 2`, `commercial → 3` (vanilla's default `episode = 1` then overridden by gamemode tests). Parity-critical vanilla quirks preserved byte-for-byte: (1) P_ChangeSwitchTexture clears `line.special = 0` BEFORE the `line.special === 11` exit-sound check when useAgain=false — because special 11 is only invoked with useAgain=0 in vanilla's use-line dispatch, this ordering means the stock exit switch NEVER emits sfx_swtchx in vanilla gameplay; the code path is reachable only via a hand-forged useAgain=true call. We preserve the ordering (do not hoist the check) so demo and regression parity stays intact. (2) The switchlist scan walks `i` from 0 to `numswitches*2-1` and at each i tests top → mid → bottom with an if/else-if cascade. The FIRST match returns; when a side uses the same switch texture on both top and bottom (or any pair of slots), only the top (or first in cascade order) flips. Cross-pair cases: if the side carries pair-0's off texture on bottom and pair-1's off texture on top, pair-0 matches first at i=0 and only bottom flips — top is left untouched. (3) The replacement texture is `switchlist[i ^ 1]`: XOR with 1 toggles between even (off) and odd (on) positions regardless of which frame currently faces the caller, so pressing on→off and off→on share one code path. (4) The press sound plays at `buttonlist->soundorg` — vanilla C pointer-to-first-element semantics. In TypeScript that's `buttons[0].soundorg`. On a fresh level (no prior presses) buttons[0] is fully zeroed so soundorg=null and vanilla S_StartSound(null, sfx) plays at world origin. Once any button has been armed, subsequent press sounds broadcast from THAT first button's stored sector, NOT from the newly-pressed line's own sector. This is a documented vanilla bug we preserve. (5) P_StartButton scans all MAXBUTTONS slots for a same-line dedup hit BEFORE allocating — a repeat press on an already-armed line silently does nothing (no new slot, no timer reset). Only on no-match does it fill the first slot where btimer===0. A full button list throws (vanilla I_Error equivalent) so test suites should exercise overflow intentionally. (6) On timer expiry, P_UpdateSpecials restores the original texture at `slot.where` and plays sfx_swtchn at the SLOT'S stored soundorg (not buttons[0].soundorg), then memsets the slot to zero. The restore sound is always sfx_swtchn even for the exit-switch case where the press emitted sfx_swtchx. (7) initSwitchList outputs a flattened `[off0, on0, off1, on1, …]` array with a trailing `-1` sentinel at index `numswitches*2`; total length is always `numswitches*2 + 1`. The sentinel matches vanilla `switchlist[numswitches*2] = -1` even though the sentinel is never read by subsequent scans. Architecture: SwitchSide is the mutable `{toptexture, midtexture, bottomtexture}` subset of side_t (all int texture indices); SwitchLine is `{special}` only (switches never read dx/dy/tag/etc.); Button wraps `{line, side, where, btexture, btimer, soundorg}` as a plain record so `createButtonList()` can pre-allocate 16 slots and `resetButton(slot)` emulates memset. Side effects flow through `SwitchCallbacks.startSound(origin, sfx)` — one callback, no sector lookup needed because Button pre-binds soundorg at press time. The module does NOT call into door/floor/ceiling code; P_UseSpecialLine is the vanilla caller that gates changeSwitchTexture behind EV_DoDoor/EV_DoFloor/etc. return values, and that glue lives in step 12-009.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_switch.c (P_InitSwitchList, P_StartButton, P_ChangeSwitchTexture) + p_spec.c P_UpdateSpecials button half + p_spec.h (MAXBUTTONS, MAXSWITCHES, BUTTONTIME, bwhere_e, button_t, switchlist_t) + sounds.h sfxenum_t table (step 12-007); confirmed against src/specials/switches.ts (~380 lines) and test/specials/switches.test.ts (57 tests, 648 expect() calls)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future*steps: 12-009 (line-trigger dispatch: every one-shot switch code wires through `changeSwitchTexture(line, frontSide, false, ...)` after the EV*\_ call returns non-zero; every repeatable code wires through `changeSwitchTexture(..., true, ...)` — the return-value guard is what prevents switches from flipping when the underlying EV\_\_ rejected the activation; see p_spec.c cases 42/43/45/46/60/61/62/63/64/65/66/67/68/69/70/99/114/122/123/126/127/132/123 for repeatable and 7/9/11/14/15/18/20/21/23/29/41/49/50/55/71/101/103 for one-shot), 12-010 (active-special save hooks must persist button slots: `{line ID, side ID, where, btexture, btimer, soundorg ID}` per slot; vanilla's static-BSS buttonlist[] serializes as a 16-entry array and reloads via re-running P_StartButton for each armed slot), 15-001 (sfx_swtchn/sfx_swtchx are lumps DSSWTCHN/DSSWTCHX — verify the loader resolves them at index 23/24), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) special 11 one-shot emits sfx_swtchn not sfx_swtchx, (b) same-texture-on-multiple-slots flips top only, (c) buttons[0].soundorg press quirk, (d) P_StartButton dedup skips same-line repeat, (e) restore sound is always sfx_swtchn), 17-010 (final gate: level-end exit switch press sequence + door-switch round-trip + 16-button overflow stress)

## F-125

- fact: Per-tic sector-special dispatch (p_spec.c P_PlayerInSpecialSector) lives in src/specials/sectorSpecials.ts. The routine handles the six sector-special ids that touch the player directly — 4 (strobe hurt), 5 (hellslime), 7 (nukage), 9 (secret marker), 11 (E1M8 exit super damage), 16 (super hellslime) — and throws on any other id (vanilla I_Error "P_PlayerInSpecialSector: unknown special"). All other sector ids (1 blink, 2 fast-strobe, 3 slow-strobe, 8 glowing, 10 door-close-30s, 12 sync-slow-strobe, 13 sync-fast-strobe, 14 door-raise-5min, 17 fire-flicker) are rendering/timer effects installed by the one-shot P_SpawnSpecials scan and never reach this tick routine because the caller gates on `sector.special !== 0` AFTER the one-shot scan has already cleared many of them; 1/2/3/8/10/12/13/14/17 never reach here. Vanilla constants: DAMAGE_TICK_MASK=0x1f (fires exactly once every 32 tics, ~0.91s at 35Hz), CF_GODMODE=2 (d_player.h cheat_t bit), IRONFEET_BYPASS_THRESHOLD=5 (P_Random()<5 = ~1-in-51), EXIT_DAMAGE_HEALTH_THRESHOLD=10 (player.health<=10 triggers G_ExitLevel on every case-11 tic), per-case damage amounts DAMAGE_HELLSLIME=10, DAMAGE_NUKAGE=5, DAMAGE_STROBE_SUPER=20, DAMAGE_EXIT_SUPER=20. NOTE: the existing src/player/movement.ts exports CF_NOMOMENTUM=2 which conflicts numerically with vanilla's d_player.h (where CF_NOCLIP=1, CF_GODMODE=2, CF_NOMOMENTUM=4) — our sectorSpecials.ts uses the correct vanilla CF_GODMODE=2; the movement.ts constant is out of scope for this step but flagged as a future fix for step 17-008. Parity-critical vanilla quirks preserved byte-for-byte: (1) Airborne guard `player.mo.z !== sector.floorheight` runs BEFORE any case dispatch — a jumping/rising/falling player in a damage sector takes no damage and a secret is not credited. The check uses strict inequality, not floor-touching tolerance; on an elevator platform the feet must exactly match floorheight on that tic. (2) The leveltime gate `(leveltime & 0x1f) === 0` fires on tics 0, 32, 64, 96, … — a player who enters a damage sector on leveltime=33 waits 31 tics for the first hit. (3) Cases 5 (hellslime) and 7 (nukage) gate ONLY on `!pw_ironfeet`: radiation suit fully suppresses these damage types — no random draw, no damage. (4) Cases 4 and 16 share the SAME dispatch body via vanilla C fall-through (`case 16:` falls through to `case 4:`). The gate is `!pw_ironfeet || random<5`: the radiation suit only reduces the hit rate to roughly 1/51, it does NOT suppress damage; P_Random() IS consumed every tic when ironfeet is active (via C short-circuit `||` — unsuited players skip the random draw because the first operand is already true). This is a parity-sensitive RNG-consumption pattern: a suited player in a strobe sector consumes one P_Random per tic even on non-damage tics, advancing the deterministic stream. (5) Case 9 (secret) is consumed immediately on touch: `player.secretcount++` and `sector.special=0`. The leveltime tick gate does NOT apply — secrets credit on any tic, not just every 32nd. The airborne guard still applies. Clearing special to 0 means the caller's outer `special !== 0` gate will skip this sector on all subsequent tics; re-entering a collected secret does nothing. (6) Case 11 (E1M8 exit super damage) runs FOUR steps every tic in vanilla order: (a) `player.cheats &= ~CF_GODMODE` — godmode is stripped every tic regardless of leveltime so IDDQD cannot prevent the finale from killing the player; (b) if leveltime gate fires, `P_DamageMobj(player.mo, NULL, NULL, 20)` — damage ignores ironfeet entirely (no suit check), so a suited player still dies; (c) `player.health <= 10` → `G_ExitLevel()`. The health check runs EVERY tic, not only on damage tics. A player who enters this sector already at 10 HP exits on their first in-sector tic without needing damage applied. A player at 15 HP hit by the 20-damage tick ends at -5 (clamped to 0) — the post-damage health satisfies `<=10` and exits on the same tic. (7) P_DamageMobj is a callback side effect in our split: the vanilla function writes `player->health` directly (via the player-branch `player->health -= damage; if (player->health < 0) player->health = 0`), so the post-damage health check on case 11 observes the reduced value. Our SectorSpecialPlayer interface declares `health: number` (not readonly) precisely so the caller's damage callback can mutate the same object reference before the post-damage comparison. (8) The RNG stream is threaded as a callbacks.random() hook rather than imported — tests can feed a deterministic sequence without touching the global RNG state; the production caller forwards to rng.pRandom. (9) Unknown-special error: vanilla I_Error takes a format string; we throw a plain Error with "P_PlayerInSpecialSector: unknown special N" so host error handling (step 07-008) can catch and surface it. Architecture: SectorSpecialMobj is `{z}` read-only; SectorSpecialSector is `{floorheight readonly, special mutable}`; SectorSpecialPlayer is the mutable `{mo, powers readonly, cheats, health, secretcount}` subset — cheats/health/secretcount are writable because vanilla writes them. Side effects flow through SectorSpecialCallbacks.damage(amount), exitLevel(), and random() — three callbacks, no module imports of the damage or exit pipelines.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_spec.c P_PlayerInSpecialSector (lines 1025-1091) + d_player.h cheat_t enum (CF_NOCLIP=1, CF_GODMODE=2, CF_NOMOMENTUM=4) + powertype_t (pw_ironfeet=3) + p_inter.c P_DamageMobj player-branch health decrement; confirmed against src/specials/sectorSpecials.ts (~230 lines) and test/specials/sector-specials.test.ts (49 tests, 69 expect() calls)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-009 (line-trigger dispatch: sector-special types 9 and 11 are set at map authoring time; no line-trigger changes this dispatch but line trigger "secret exit" codes 51/52 and normal exit 11/52 are orthogonal to sector-special 11), 12-010 (active-special save hooks: case 9 mutates sector.special — the serialized map-state must capture post-collection specials; case 11 clears CF_GODMODE from player.cheats — persist the cheats mask verbatim), 15-001 (no sfx calls from this path — P_DamageMobj emits damage sounds via its own pipeline), 16-007 (savegame player-mobj serialization must include player.secretcount, player.cheats bitmask, player.health, player.powers[IRONFEET=3]), 17-001 (level-start state-hash must include per-sector.special values so a freshly-collected secret shows special=0 in the deterministic hash), 17-002 (bundled demo parity: E1M8 finale demo exercises case 11 — CF_GODMODE strip + 20/tick damage + health<=10 exit; strobe hurt sectors in early maps exercise case 4 random consumption), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) case-4/16 RNG consumption when ironfeet active, (b) case-11 godmode strip, (c) case-11 health check every tic not every damage tic, (d) airborne guard blocks secret collection, (e) case-9 one-shot consumption clearing sector.special, (f) movement.ts CF_NOMOMENTUM=2 bug should be reconciled to CF_NOMOMENTUM=4 so CF_GODMODE and CF_NOMOMENTUM do not collide), 17-010 (final gate integration)

## F-126

- fact: Line-trigger dispatch (p*spec.c P_CrossSpecialLine + P_ShootSpecialLine, p_switch.c P_UseSpecialLine) lives in src/specials/lineTriggers.ts as `pCrossSpecialLine(line, side, thing, callbacks, gameVersion=doom_1_9)`, `pShootSpecialLine(thing, line, callbacks)`, and `pUseSpecialLine(thing, line, side, callbacks): boolean`. Vanilla eligibility sets, exactly: NON_TRIGGER_PROJECTILE_TYPES = [MT_ROCKET=33, MT_PLASMA=34, MT_BFG=35, MT_TROOPSHOT=31, MT_HEADSHOT=32, MT_BRUISERSHOT=16] (blocked from firing cross specials on gameversion > exe_doom_1_2); MONSTER_CROSS_SPECIALS = [39, 97, 125, 126, 4, 10, 88] (the complete non-player cross whitelist); MONSTER_USE_SPECIALS = [1, 32, 33, 34] (manual door + three locked manual doors; the locked-door helper rejects null-player activators internally but the outer gate still lets monsters *attempt* the press); MONSTER_SHOOT_SPECIALS = [46] (the only shoot-eligible special for monsters). GameVersion enum: `doom_1_2=0, doom_1_9=1`. Parity-critical quirks preserved byte-for-byte: (1) Pre-1.2 gate: `gameversion <= exe_doom_1_2 && line.special > 98 && line.special !== 104` early-returns — special 104 (scroll-texture-left retrigger in 1.2) is the sole above-98 exception. Post-1.2 gate instead filters non-player projectiles via NON_TRIGGER_PROJECTILE_TYPES. Both paths feed into the same non-player MONSTER_CROSS_SPECIALS whitelist check so pre-1.2 does NOT widen monster cross eligibility — it only changes WHICH specials a projectile is allowed to attempt before the monster-whitelist gate. (2) TRIGGERS vs RETRIGGERS: one-shot TRIGGERS set `line.special = 0` AFTER dispatching the EV*\_ call — vanilla's exact ordering lets an EV\_\_ callback read the pre-zero special for tag resolution. The two exit TRIGGERS 52 (gExitLevel) and 124 (gSecretExitLevel) skip the reset because the engine transitions to the next map before any subsequent tic re-reads the line. RETRIGGERS leave line.special intact so the line re-fires. Cases 125 (monster-only one-shot teleport) and 126 (monster-only retrigger) gate the EV*Teleport call on `thing.player === null`; case 125 clears line.special ONLY inside the non-player branch — a player crossing a 125 line does nothing and leaves the line armed for a later monster. Case 40 dispatches BOTH evDoCeiling(raiseToHighest=1) and evDoFloor(lowerFloorToLowest=1) before clearing special. (3) P_UseSpecialLine back-side gate (side === 1): only special 124 passes; every other side-1 use returns false without dispatch. Special 124 on the back passes the gate AND falls through the big switch without a matching case, returning true but firing nothing (a vanilla no-op success). The MANUALS group — 1, 26, 27, 28, 31, 32, 33, 34, 117, 118 — calls evVerticalDoor with NO switch flip, no line.special mutation. SWITCHES (useAgain=0): 7, 9, 11, 14, 15, 18, 20, 21, 23, 29, 41, 49, 50, 51, 55, 71, 101, 102, 103, 111, 112, 113, 122, 127, 131, 133, 135, 137, 140 — `if (EV**()) changeSwitchTexture(line, 0)` guard pattern EXCEPT cases 11 (exit) and 51 (secret exit) flip the switch UNCONDITIONALLY *before* the exit call because the exit never returns. BUTTONS (useAgain=1): 42, 43, 45, 60, 61, 62, 63, 64, 65, 66, 67, 68, 69, 70, 99, 114, 115, 116, 123, 132, 134, 136, 138, 139 — same guard pattern EXCEPT 138 and 139 (evLightTurnOn is void in vanilla, so the flip must be unconditional). Plat amounts: case 14 → amount=32, case 15 → amount=24, case 66 → amount=24, case 67 → amount=32, case 62 → amount=1 (the vanilla tag-forwarding "amount=1" quirk in the BUTTONS plat). Locked-door dispatch: cases 99/134/136 (BUTTONS) and 133/135/137 (SWITCHES) all call evDoLockedDoor(VDT*BLAZE_OPEN, thing) — the helper internally rejects null-player activators. (4) P_ShootSpecialLine NEVER guards changeSwitchTexture on the EV\** return value; cases 24 (evDoFloor raiseFloor → useAgain=0), 46 (evDoDoor openDoor → useAgain=1), 47 (evDoPlat raiseToNearestAndChange → useAgain=0) flip the switch unconditionally. Non-players are restricted to special 46. (5) Light brightness arguments: cases 12 (cross one-shot) / 80 (cross retrigger) → bright=0 (match-nearest-darker); cases 13 / 81 → bright=255; cases 35 / 79 → bright=35; case 17 fires evStartLightStrobing; case 104 fires evTurnTagLightsOff; case 138 (button) → bright=255; case 139 (button) → bright=35. (6) The LineTriggerLine interface exposes `special` (mutable, trigger-reset target), `flags` (readonly, ML*SECRET gate for monster use), `tag` (readonly, forwarded to every EV\*\*), `frontFloorpic` and `frontSpecial` (readonly, forwarded to floor/plat helpers for change-on-activation). LineTriggerThing is `{type: MobjType, player: unknown | null}` — `type` is consulted ONLY by the non-player projectile filter; `player` is the discriminator for player-vs-monster dispatch. All side effects (17 methods: evDoDoor, evDoLockedDoor, evVerticalDoor, evDoPlat, evStopPlat, evDoFloor, evDoCeiling, evCeilingCrushStop, evBuildStairs, evDoDonut, evTeleport, evLightTurnOn, evStartLightStrobing, evTurnTagLightsOff, changeSwitchTexture, gExitLevel, gSecretExitLevel) flow through LineTriggerCallbacks so the dispatcher has no direct imports of the door/plat/floor/ceiling/teleport/exit subsystems. Inline const integers (VDT_NORMAL=0, VDT_CLOSE_30_THEN_OPEN=1, VDT_CLOSE=2, VDT_OPEN=3, VDT_BLAZE_RAISE=5, VDT_BLAZE_OPEN=6, VDT_BLAZE_CLOSE=7; FT_LOWER_FLOOR=0 through FT_RAISE_FLOOR_512=12; PT_PERPETUAL_RAISE=0 through PT_BLAZE_DWUS=4; CT_LOWER_TO_FLOOR=0 / CT_LOWER_AND_CRUSH=2 / CT_CRUSH_AND_RAISE=3 / CT_FAST_CRUSH_AND_RAISE=4 / CT_SILENT_CRUSH_AND_RAISE=5; STR_BUILD8=0, STR_TURBO16=1) mirror the canonical p_spec.h enum orders locked by F-115/F-120/F-122/F-123/F-124 but are kept local so case dispatch does not need to import the enums at the call site; the `as VerticalDoorType` / `as FloorType` / etc. casts retain type safety.
