## F-127

- fact: Active-special save hooks (p_plats.c activeplats[MAXPLATS=30] + p_ceilng.c activeceilings[MAXCEILINGS=30] + p_switch.c buttonlist[MAXBUTTONS=16] registries) live in src/specials/activeSpecials.ts as three snapshot/restore pairs: snapshotActivePlats/restoreActivePlats, snapshotActiveCeilings/restoreActiveCeilings, snapshotButtons/restoreButtons. Exports: 3 plain-data snapshot interfaces (ActivePlatSnapshot {sectorIndex, type, speed, low, high, wait, count, status, oldstatus, crush, tag, inStasis}; ActiveCeilingSnapshot {sectorIndex, type, bottomheight, topheight, speed, crush, direction, olddirection, tag, inStasis}; ButtonSnapshot {lineIndex, sideIndex, where, btexture, btimer, soundorgIndex}), 3 positional fixed-length array types (ActivePlatsSnapshot = readonly (ActivePlatSnapshot | null)[] length MAXPLATS; ActiveCeilingsSnapshot length MAXCEILINGS; ButtonListSnapshot length MAXBUTTONS), 6 snapshot/restore functions. Parity-critical invariants preserved byte-for-byte: (1) Slot positions round-trip unchanged — snapshotActivePlats/snapshotActiveCeilings emit a positional readonly array whose `null` entries match empty slots AND whose indices match live slots exactly; the restore path assigns `registry.slots[i] = plat` directly (bypassing the first-null-wins semantics of `plats.add(plat)`) so the exact vanilla BSS layout `activeplats[i]` / `activeceilings[i]` is preserved across save/load. This matters because evStopPlat's non-deterministic-but-stable "first matching-tag plat found via slot scan" behavior depends on the slot order. (2) In-stasis plats round-trip with `action === null` AND `status === PlatStatus.inStasis` AND `inStasis: true` in the snapshot; the restore path checks the `inStasis` flag to decide whether to attach the tPlatRaise closure — if true it leaves `action = null` so ThinkerList.run() skips the thinker (matching vanilla evStopPlat which sets `thinker.function.acv = NULL`). `oldstatus` round-trips so pActivateInStasis can resume the plat at its pre-stasis direction. (3) In-stasis ceilings round-trip with `action === null` AND `direction === CeilingDirection.inStasis` (0) AND `inStasis: true`; `olddirection` preserves for pActivateInStasisCeiling. (4) Active (non-stasis) plats restore with the exact tPlatRaise action closure that evDoPlat installs — the closure captures the REBUILT registry (not the original) via `plat.action = entry.inStasis ? null : (t) => tPlatRaise(t, plats)` inside the restore loop; this ensures a pastdest transition inside the restored closure removes the plat from the correct live registry, not from the saved snapshot. Same pattern for ceilings with tMoveCeiling over the rebuilt ActiveCeilings. (5) Each restored plat/ceiling gets `sector.specialdata = plat/ceiling` written on its resolved sector (matching evDoPlat/evDoCeiling initialization) AND is pushed onto the ThinkerList via `thinkerList.add()` so the next tic picks it up. Callers must restore against a freshly-initialized (empty) level whose sector/line tables the savegame layer has already loaded. (6) Buttons round-trip as 16 positional entries mirroring vanilla `buttonlist[MAXBUTTONS]`. A slot is considered "active" when `btimer !== 0` — the snapshot emits `null` for `btimer === 0` slots AND the restore path calls `resetButton(slot)` for those nulls (memset-equivalent zero). Active slots serialize `line` / `side` / `soundorg` as caller-supplied integer indices; the snapshot carries an integer `-1` sentinel for null references (a `line === null` or `side === null` value is atypical but defended against here because the caller's `updateButtons` restore-branch already handles null sides). Callers supply matching reverse-resolver callbacks to the restore path; a `-1` index bypasses the resolver entirely and decodes back to `null`. (7) Neither snapshot function mutates the source registries — they read `plats.slots[i]` / `ceilings.slots[i]` / `buttons[i]` and emit plain data. Neither restore function depends on registry state beyond the fixed array length; both create fresh registries and backfill slot-by-slot. Architecture: the snapshot signatures take resolver callbacks (`sectorIndexOf: (sector: S) => number`, `lineIndexOf`/`sideIndexOf`/`soundorgIndexOf`) rather than importing sector/line tables, keeping activeSpecials.ts free of map-loader dependencies; the 16-007/16-008 savegame layer will wire resolvers against its own id tables. Generic typing (`<S extends PlatSector>` / `<S extends CeilingSector>`) lets consumers pass their concrete sector types without widening the snapshot interface. The module imports ActivePlats/Platform/PlatStatus/tPlatRaise/MAXPLATS from ./platforms.ts, ActiveCeilings/Ceiling/CeilingDirection/tMoveCeiling/MAXCEILINGS from ./ceilings.ts, and MAXBUTTONS/resetButton from ./switches.ts — no cross-dependency into doors/floors/stairs/lineTriggers. Button.soundorg is typed `unknown` in switches.ts so the soundorgIndexOf callback takes `unknown` too; test-side mapping uses an explicit cast to the concrete origin type for `origins.indexOf(...)` to satisfy TS.
- source: Chocolate Doom p_plats.c (activeplats, P_AddActivePlat, P_RemoveActivePlat, P_ActivateInStasis, EV_StopPlat) + p_ceilng.c (activeceilings, P_AddActiveCeiling, P_RemoveActiveCeiling, P_ActivateInStasisCeiling, EV_CeilingCrushStop) + p_switch.c (buttonlist, P_StartButton, P_ChangeSwitchTexture) + p_spec.c P_UpdateSpecials button half + p_tick.c P_ArchiveSpecials/P_UnArchiveSpecials patterns; confirmed against src/specials/activeSpecials.ts (~370 lines) and test/specials/active-specials.test.ts (25 tests, 294 expect() calls).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 16-007 (player/mobj/sector serialization consumes these snapshot interfaces — the top-level save writer calls snapshotActivePlats/snapshotActiveCeilings/snapshotButtons BEFORE serializing the thinker list, because the resulting slot indices anchor the per-thinker class tags; the load path must restore in reverse: sectors first, then lines, then snapshots into fresh registries, then the thinker list deserializer skips over plats/ceilings already in the registry), 16-008 (special-thinker serialization: for registry-tracked thinkers (Platform/Ceiling), the thinker-list writer marks them as "registry-owned" via a class tag and omits re-emitting their Platform/Ceiling state because this module already captured it; for FloorMove/Door/StairsDonut thinkers that are NOT in a per-type registry, the thinker-list writer owns the full serialization), 16-009 (loadgame restore order: P_UnArchiveSpecials calls restoreActivePlats/restoreActiveCeilings/restoreButtons to rebuild the registries + ThinkerList entries from the snapshot, then the thinker-list restore path adds Door/Floor/Stair/Donut movers; the inStasis check ensures `action === null` on stasis entries so the post-restore tic scan skips them correctly), 16-010 (vanilla limit enforcement: MAXPLATS=30 and MAXCEILINGS=30 and MAXBUTTONS=16 are enforced by the fixed array length; a snapshot with more than MAXPLATS non-null entries or whose array length exceeds the constant is an authoring/compat error — this should surface as a savegame-format error during load), 17-002 (bundled demo parity: demos that lift a plat into stasis mid-level and reactivate it via pActivateInStasis must round-trip through the snapshot/restore cycle without observable state change; the `inStasis` flag + `oldstatus` + `status === PlatStatus.inStasis` triple-encoding protects against a future refactor that drops any one of the three), 17-007 (save/load round-trip suite: the primary test vector is save-mid-crusher-descent → reload → observe next pastdest writes to REBUILT registry, not the original; the closure capture pattern locks this behavior), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) slot-index preservation across save/load cycle, (b) action-null stasis marker on both plats and ceilings, (c) closure capture over rebuilt registry for pastdest removal, (d) -1-sentinel null line/side/soundorg encoding for buttons, (e) resetButton invocation for `null` snapshot entries on restore), 17-010 (final gate: full savegame round-trip against vanilla oracle including mid-level plat-stasis state and held-button timer decrement across save boundary).

## F-128

- fact: Projection and detail constants (r_main.h lighting/FOV + r_main.c R_ExecuteSetViewSize derivation + r_bsp.c MAXSEGS + r_plane.c MAXVISPLANES/MAXOPENINGS) live in src/render/projection.ts. Exports: the reusable vanilla constants SCREENWIDTH (re-exported from host/windowPolicy.ts so renderer call sites have a single render-scope source), SCREENHEIGHT (re-exported), FIELDOFVIEW=2048 (BAM units spanning one quadrant of the 4096-entry finetangent lookup; R_InitTextureMapping consumes this to build viewangletox), SBARHEIGHT=32 (st_stuff.h ST_HEIGHT — status-bar pixel height clipped out of the view window when setblocks<10); the seven lighting constants LIGHTLEVELS=16, LIGHTSEGSHIFT=4, LIGHTSCALESHIFT=12, MAXLIGHTSCALE=48, LIGHTZSHIFT=20, MAXLIGHTZ=128, NUMCOLORMAPS=32 (drive R_InitLightTables and the per-sector scalelight/zlight arrays consumed by column/span drawers and wall/plane light selection); three renderer limits MAXSEGS=SCREENWIDTH/2+1=161 (r_bsp.c drawsegs_t cap, I_Error on overflow), MAXVISPLANES=128 (r_plane.c visplane cap, I_Error on overflow — pinned in F-024), MAXOPENINGS=SCREENWIDTH*64=20480 (shared openings pool for floor/ceiling clip spans, I_Error on overflow — pinned in F-024 as "derived from SCREENWIDTH*64"); setblocks bounds MIN_SETBLOCKS=3 and MAX_SETBLOCKS=11 (vanilla menu clamp); const enum DetailMode {high=0, low=1} matching vanilla `detailshift` bit encoding. The computeViewport(setBlocks, detailShift) function reproduces R_ExecuteSetViewSize byte-for-byte: when setBlocks===11 it pins scaledViewWidth=SCREENWIDTH and viewHeight=SCREENHEIGHT (full screen, no status bar); otherwise scaledViewWidth = setBlocks\*32 and viewHeight = (setBlocks\*168/10) & ~7 (rounds DOWN to the next multiple of 8). viewWidth = scaledViewWidth >> detailShift, so low detail halves horizontal sampling (centerX and centerXFrac also halve). centerX=viewWidth>>1, centerY=viewHeight>>1, centerXFrac=centerX<<FRACBITS, centerYFrac=centerY<<FRACBITS, projection=centerXFrac (vanilla assigns `projection = centerxfrac` verbatim). viewWindowX=(SCREENWIDTH-scaledViewWidth)>>1 always. Parity-sensitive quirk: viewWindowY uses the scaledViewWidth===SCREENWIDTH gate, NOT a setBlocks===11 gate — both setBlocks=10 (scaledViewWidth=320, viewHeight=168) AND setBlocks=11 (scaledViewWidth=320, viewHeight=200) pin viewWindowY=0; setBlocks<10 uses (SCREENHEIGHT-SBARHEIGHT-viewHeight)>>1. Clamp behavior: setBlocks below MIN_SETBLOCKS clamps to 3, above MAX_SETBLOCKS clamps to 11; detailShift's `(n | 0) === 0` branch selects DetailMode.high, any other value selects DetailMode.low (matches vanilla where only bit-0 of `detailshift` participates in the `>>` — e.g. `detailshift=3` produces identical output to `detailshift=1`, not a double-shift). Vanilla setblocks sweep pins: 3→96x48, 4→128x64, 5→160x80, 6→192x96, 7→224x112, 8→256x128, 9→288x144, 10→320x168, 11→320x200 — each (viewWidth,viewHeight) pair is a load-bearing byte-level invariant for later visplane/wall-clip tests. The module is pure arithmetic with no Win32 or runtime dependencies and introduces no new runtime state — later phase-13 steps consume these constants and the Viewport interface directly.
- source: Chocolate Doom r_main.h (FIELDOFVIEW, LIGHTLEVELS, LIGHTSEGSHIFT, LIGHTSCALESHIFT, MAXLIGHTSCALE, LIGHTZSHIFT, MAXLIGHTZ, NUMCOLORMAPS, centerx/centery/projection/viewwindowx/viewwindowy declarations) + r_main.c R_ExecuteSetViewSize (setblocks, detailshift, scaledviewwidth, viewheight, viewwidth, centerx, centery, centerxfrac, centeryfrac, projection arithmetic) + r_bsp.c MAXSEGS + r_plane.c MAXVISPLANES/MAXOPENINGS + i_video.h SCREENWIDTH=320/SCREENHEIGHT=200 + st_stuff.h ST_HEIGHT=32; confirmed against src/render/projection.ts (~160 lines) and test/render/projection-constants.test.ts (54 tests, 84 expect() calls).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 13-002 (visplane/openings/clip limits — MAXVISPLANES/MAXOPENINGS/MAXSEGS are re-imported from here; F-128 is the authoritative source), 13-003 (column/span drawers — centerX/centerY/projection and the lighting ramp consume NUMCOLORMAPS/MAXLIGHTSCALE/MAXLIGHTZ/LIGHTSCALESHIFT/LIGHTZSHIFT), 13-005 (wall-column fetch — scale selection indexes into scalelight[MAXLIGHTSCALE]), 13-006/13-007 (wall paths — projection=centerXFrac for perspective divisor; detail shift gates x-step accumulation), 13-008/13-009 (visplane build/render — MAXVISPLANES cap + yslope[SCREENHEIGHT] + MAXOPENINGS pool), 13-010 (sky semantics — skyflatnum uses viewHeight for vertical clipping), 13-011 (sprite projection — centerX/centerY/projection), 14-002 (status bar rendering uses SBARHEIGHT), 14-005 (menu view-size slider writes setblocks 3..11; computeViewport callers must pipe through here on every setviewsize change), 17-004 (framebuffer CRC suite must exercise every setblocks value and both detail modes — 18 distinct viewport configurations), 17-010 (final gate: viewport switching during demo playback must match vanilla without a single-pixel off).

## F-129

- fact: Visplane-openings and clip-limit facade (r*bsp.c cliprange_t/solidsegs/drawsegs + r_plane.c visplane_t/openings + r_defs.h drawseg_t/visplane_t/SIL\*\* flags) lives in src/render/renderLimits.ts as a thin renderer-facing module that re-exports MAXOPENINGS/MAXSEGS/MAXVISPLANES from ./projection.ts (F-128 remains the byte-level authority for those pool counts) and adds the values that are scoped narrowly to the BSP clip and visplane machinery. Exports: MAXDRAWSEGS=256 (vanilla hard cap on the per-frame `drawsegs[]` table — r_bsp.c `R_StoreWallRange` I_Errors with "R_DrawPlanes: drawsegs overflow" on overflow); VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED=0xff (the byte vanilla writes via `memset(check->top, 0xff, sizeof(check->top))` in `R_FindPlane`/`R_CheckPlane` to mark a visplane column as untouched; `R_DrawPlanes` also writes `top[minx-1]` and `top[maxx+1]` as this sentinel as the spanmaker fencepost); CEILINGCLIP_DEFAULT=-1 (the value `R_ClearPlanes` fills `ceilingclip[]` with — one row above the top scanline so the first ceiling span renders at y=0); CLIPRANGE_SENTINEL_FIRST_LOW=-0x7FFFFFFF and CLIPRANGE_SENTINEL_LAST_LOW=-1 (the `solidsegs[0] = { .first = -0x7FFFFFFF, .last = -1 }` low-end sentinel pair `R_ClearClipSegs` writes so `R_ClipSolidWallSegment` never walks off the front); CLIPRANGE_SENTINEL_LAST_HIGH=+0x7FFFFFFF (the `solidsegs[1].last` sentinel paired with `.first = viewwidth` so every column past the view right edge is already clipped); OPENINGS_BYTES_PER_ENTRY=2 (vanilla `short openings[MAXOPENINGS]` — 2 bytes per entry); OPENINGS_POOL_BYTES=MAXOPENINGS\*2=40960 (total byte footprint of the shared openings pool); RENDER_POOL_LIMITS (frozen RenderPoolLimits record: maxDrawsegs/maxOpenings/maxSegs/maxVisplanes/screenHeight/screenWidth — single-object snapshot for allocators that want one import); const enum Silhouette { none=0, bottom=1, top=2, both=3 } matching r_defs.h SIL_NONE/SIL_BOTTOM/SIL_TOP/SIL_BOTH bit flags (top|bottom===both so callers OR them together for drawseg sprite-clip selection); three interfaces — ClipRange {first, last} mirroring vanilla cliprange_t (half-open horizontal range of already-clipped columns stored in `solidsegs[]`), Visplane {height, picnum, lightlevel, minx, maxx, top: Uint8Array(SCREENWIDTH), bottom: Uint8Array(SCREENWIDTH)} mirroring r_defs.h visplane_t with `minx=SCREENWIDTH`/`maxx=-1` as the empty-plane sentinel (`minx > maxx` means untouched), Drawseg {curlineIndex, x1, x2, scale1, scale2, scalestep, silhouette, bsilheight, tsilheight, sprtopclip, sprbottomclip, maskedtexturecol} mirroring r_defs.h drawseg_t with `sprtopclip/sprbottomclip/maskedtexturecol === -1` sentinels for unused opening-pool offsets. Exports: `floorclipDefault(viewHeight)` returning `viewHeight | 0` — the per-frame value `R_ClearPlanes` writes into every `floorclip[]` entry (tracks the active viewport viewHeight so the clip default matches the setblocks slider). Parity-critical invariants locked by the 32-test suite (test/render/render-limits.test.ts): MAXDRAWSEGS=256 exact; MAXSEGS and MAXOPENINGS derivation `SCREENWIDTH/2+1=161` and `SCREENWIDTH*64=20480`; MAXVISPLANES=128 cross-reference to F-024; OPENINGS_POOL_BYTES exactly 40960; Silhouette flag bit-field arithmetic (top|bottom===both, none|x===x for every x); R_ClearPlanes clip defaults (ceilingclip fills to -1, floorclip fills to |0-truncated viewHeight, 168/200/48 round-trip); floorclipDefault truncates fractional input via |0 (168.9→168, -1.5→-1); CLIPRANGE_SENTINEL_FIRST_LOW and CLIPRANGE_SENTINEL_LAST_HIGH stay inside int32 so `| 0` is a no-op (no BigInt promotion); the sentinel pair flanks the viewWidth properly (`solidsegs[0].last < 0 < viewWidth < solidsegs[1].last`); VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED=0xff fits in a single Uint8 slot; the fresh-visplane post-memset top[] is all 0xff across SCREENWIDTH columns; an empty Visplane has `minx > maxx`; RENDER_POOL_LIMITS is Object.frozen() and mirrors the constants exactly; pool caps gate the overflow guards (writing (MAX+1)-th entry is the I_Error trigger for drawsegs/visplanes/openings). Parity-sensitive edge case locked: the low-end sentinel uses `-0x7FFFFFFF`NOT`INT_MIN=-0x80000000`— vanilla chose the symmetric`±0x7FFFFFFF`pair so the clip walker's`solidsegs[start-1].last < lastclip-1`comparison stays well-formed without overflow (INT_MIN would decrement to 0x7FFFFFFF and break the walk). Architecture: the module imports only from ./projection.ts (MAXOPENINGS/MAXSEGS/MAXVISPLANES/SCREENHEIGHT/SCREENWIDTH); no Win32 or runtime dependencies. The Visplane interface uses Uint8Array(SCREENWIDTH) for top/bottom because vanilla uses`byte`arrays; this means column indices >255 cannot be represented — a non-issue at SCREENHEIGHT=200 but a constraint future widescreen work must respect. Drawseg uses plain number fields because vanilla`drawseg_t`uses`fixed_t` (int32) and short column indices; a concrete allocator can pack these into typed-array pools in a later step without changing the interface.
- source: Chocolate Doom r_bsp.c (MAXDRAWSEGS=256, cliprange_t, solidsegs[MAXSEGS+1], R_ClearClipSegs sentinel init, R_ClipSolidWallSegment/R_ClipPassWallSegment clip walk, R_StoreWallRange drawsegs overflow I_Error) + r_plane.c (MAXVISPLANES=128, MAXOPENINGS=SCREENWIDTH\*64, R_ClearPlanes ceilingclip=-1/floorclip=viewheight init, R_FindPlane/R_CheckPlane memset 0xff, R_DrawPlanes top fencepost) + r_defs.h (visplane_t byte arrays, drawseg_t fields, SIL_NONE/SIL_BOTTOM/SIL_TOP/SIL_BOTH flag bits); confirmed against src/render/renderLimits.ts (~244 lines) and test/render/render-limits.test.ts (32 tests, 370 expect() calls).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 13-003 (column/span drawers consume Visplane.top/bottom Uint8Array layout and the VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED 0xff sentinel as the span-search terminator), 13-005 (wall-column fetch emits drawsegs[] entries whose silhouette/bsilheight/tsilheight flags are this module's Silhouette enum values), 13-006/13-007 (solid-wall and two-sided wall paths allocate drawsegs[] and push ClipRange entries into solidsegs[]; the CLIPRANGE_SENTINEL_FIRST_LOW/LAST_HIGH sentinels bookend the walk), 13-008/13-009 (visplane build/render allocate from the MAXVISPLANES pool; openings[] pool uses OPENINGS_POOL_BYTES and Int16Array for the per-column top/bottom fencepost storage), 13-012 (sprite sort+clip reads drawseg.sprtopclip/sprbottomclip/maskedtexturecol offsets and their -1 sentinels), 13-013 (masked midtextures walk drawseg.maskedtexturecol opening offsets), 14-004 (automap rendering doesn't share this pool but status-bar refresh respects viewWindowY/viewHeight via floorclipDefault), 16-007/16-008 (save/load: visplane/drawseg/opening pools are per-frame and not serialized; ClipRange is per-frame only; Visplane.top/bottom are reset every frame via R_ClearPlanes), 17-004 (framebuffer CRC suite exercises drawseg/visplane/opening pool usage at every setblocks value), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) solidsegs ±0x7FFFFFFF sentinels NOT INT_MIN/MAX, (b) visplane top 0xff sentinel fencepost, (c) ceilingclip -1 / floorclip viewheight defaults, (d) empty-visplane minx>maxx invariant, (e) silhouette bit-field OR composition), 17-010 (final gate: any overflow I_Error triggers a parity-breaking crash vs vanilla).

## F-130

- fact: Column and span drawer primitives (r*draw.c R_DrawColumn + R_DrawSpan) live in src/render/drawPrimitives.ts. Exports 6 numeric constants: COLUMN_HEIGHT_MASK=127 (dc_source index mask — vanilla `(frac>>FRACBITS)&127` masking wraps wall-texture columns at 128 rows because the composite column buffer is hard-coded 128 tall); FLAT_DIMENSION=64 (r_draw.c flat tile edge); FLAT_SIZE=4096 (64*64 byte row-major flat buffer); FLAT*Y_SHIFT=FRACBITS-6=10 (right shift `yfrac>>(16-6)` extracts the 6 low bits of the integer V ALREADY multiplied by 64 row-stride); FLAT_Y_MASK=(FLAT_DIMENSION-1)*FLAT\*DIMENSION=4032=0xFC0 (isolates bits 6..11 of the shifted V — the row index times the 64-byte row stride); FLAT_X_MASK=FLAT_DIMENSION-1=63=0x3F (isolates bits 0..5 of the shifted U — the column index within the 64-column flat). FLAT_Y_MASK and FLAT_X_MASK partition the bottom 12 bits disjointly (their `&` is 0 and their `|` is FLAT_SIZE-1=4095), so vanilla's `spot = ((yfrac>>10)&4032) + ((xfrac>>16)&63)` produces identical results whether you write `+` or `|`; vanilla uses `+` and we follow suit to stay a direct port. Exports two readonly interfaces: ColumnDrawJob {x, yl, yh, textureMid, iscale, centerY, source: Uint8Array, colormap: Uint8Array} and SpanDrawJob {x1, x2, y, xFrac, yFrac, xStep, yStep, source: Uint8Array, colormap: Uint8Array} — both mirror the vanilla dc\**/ds\_\_ global state blocks with no runtime dependencies. Exports two drawer functions: `rDrawColumn(job, framebuffer, screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH)` and `rDrawSpan(job, framebuffer, screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH)`. Parity-critical invariants preserved byte-for-byte: (1) rDrawColumn early-exits on `count = yh - yl < 0` matching vanilla's `if (count < 0) return;` guard — yl > yh means no pixels written, not a degenerate loop. rDrawSpan has NO such guard — vanilla's R*DrawSpan omits the `count < 0` check, so the do-while continues indefinitely if x2 < x1 (identical to vanilla's behavior where the caller is trusted to ensure x2 >= x1). (2) do-while(count--) writes count+1 pixels: count=0 runs once, count=N runs N+1 times. For rDrawColumn, yh-yl pixels means yh-yl+1 writes (inclusive both ends); for rDrawSpan, x2-x1+1 writes. (3) rDrawColumn per-row destination stride is `screenWidth` bytes (column-major access into the linear framebuffer); rDrawSpan per-column stride is 1 byte (`dest++`) matching row-major access. (4) rDrawColumn accumulator: `frac = textureMid + (yl - centerY) * iscale`, then `frac += iscale`each row. The`(yl - centerY) \* iscale`term biases frac so that at yl=centerY, frac equals textureMid — matching vanilla's convention of`dc_texturemid`being the fixed-point V at the view center row. (5) rDrawColumn source index:`source[(frac >> FRACBITS) & COLUMN_HEIGHT_MASK]`— the`>>`is signed int32 so negative frac (views above centerY of a texture starting "below 0") produces correct wrap-around via two's-complement sign-extend plus the mask: e.g. frac=-FRACUNIT (i.e. -65536) gives`-65536 >> 16 = -1`, `-1 & 127 = 127`— so the column starts at source[127] and walks forward. (6) rDrawSpan spot arithmetic:`((yFrac >> FLAT_Y_SHIFT) & FLAT_Y_MASK) + ((xFrac >> FRACBITS) & FLAT_X_MASK)`. The y-part shift-by-10-then-mask-by-4032 simultaneously extracts the bottom 6 bits of the integer V AND multiplies by the 64-byte row stride in a single operation (bits 6..11 of `yfrac>>10`are bits 16..21 of yfrac = the integer V). The x-part shift-by-16-then-mask-by-63 extracts the bottom 6 bits of the integer U. Both operations preserve sign-extension under negative fracs, so the spot is ALWAYS in [0, FLAT_SIZE-1] regardless of xFrac/yFrac sign. (7) Accumulator updates are wrapped through`| 0` (`frac = (frac + iscale) | 0`, `xFrac = (xFrac + xStep) | 0`, `yFrac = (yFrac + yStep) | 0`) so JS float64 precision never diverges from C int32 two's-complement addition — defensive against future parity bugs where a caller passes near-INT_MAX iscale. At realistic iscale values (<2^21) and <200 rows per column, frac stays well within 2^31 and the `| 0`is effectively a no-op, but the truncation locks bit-exact parity in all paths. (8) Colormap is a 256-entry Uint8Array applied as`colormap[source[index]]`on every pixel — the light-diminishing ramp vanilla's R_InitLightTables builds. rDrawColumn and rDrawSpan treat colormap as opaque, so callers wire fullbright / dimmed / invulnerability / black colormap pointers directly without the primitive knowing which ramp is active. Architecture: the module imports only FRACBITS (from ../core/fixed.ts) and SCREENWIDTH (from ./projection.ts); no Win32 or runtime dependencies. The primitives operate on framebuffer-absolute coordinates — the caller pre-folds`viewWindowX`/`viewWindowY`into x/yl/yh/x1/x2/y, matching vanilla's precomputed`columnofs[]`/`ylookup[]` tables. No bounds checking (vanilla's RANGECHECK guard is compiled out in release builds); callers pre-clip to the viewport. ColumnDrawJob and SpanDrawJob are readonly to discourage accidental mutation mid-frame. Deferred to later 13-\* steps: R_DrawFuzzColumn (13-014 fuzz/invisibility), R_DrawTranslatedColumn (player color swap), R_DrawColumnLow/R_DrawSpanLow (low-detail variants not exercised by reference-run detailshift=0 pin F-128).
- source: Chocolate Doom r_draw.c R_DrawColumn (`count = dc_yh - dc_yl; if (count < 0) return; dest = ylookup[dc_yl] + columnofs[dc_x]; fracstep = dc_iscale; frac = dc_texturemid + (dc_yl - centery) * fracstep; do { *dest = dc_colormap[dc_source[(frac >> FRACBITS) & 127]]; dest += SCREENWIDTH; frac += fracstep; } while (count--);`) + R_DrawSpan (`xfrac = ds_xfrac; yfrac = ds_yfrac; dest = ylookup[ds_y] + columnofs[ds_x1]; count = ds_x2 - ds_x1; do { spot = ((yfrac >> (16-6)) & (63*64)) + ((xfrac >> 16) & 63); *dest++ = ds_colormap[ds_source[spot]]; xfrac += ds_xstep; yfrac += ds_ystep; } while (count--);`); confirmed against src/render/drawPrimitives.ts (~240 lines) and test/render/column-span-draw.test.ts (30 tests, 192_083 expect() calls — the count includes a 200x320 canary sweep inside "writes into the correct column" and "writes into the correct row" tests).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 13-004 (patch decode/draw builds composited Uint8Array source buffers for sprite patches and calls rDrawColumn with the decoded column), 13-005 (wall-column fetch converts a drawseg into a per-column ColumnDrawJob, computes dc_iscale from the scale table, and calls rDrawColumn), 13-006 (solid-wall path invokes rDrawColumn once per column of a one-sided line), 13-007 (two-sided wall path invokes rDrawColumn for upper/lower textures and queues midtexture draws for 13-013), 13-009 (visplane span render walks a visplane's top/bottom columns and invokes rDrawSpan per scanline; the 0xff sentinel from F-129 terminates the span search), 13-010 (sky semantics routes through rDrawColumn with a fixed dc_colormap pointer so sky pixels never dim — but the primitive is unaware of that), 13-011 (sprite projection calls rDrawColumn for each sprite column — masked pixels handled via the source buffer having the masked-column post format), 13-013 (masked midtextures call rDrawColumn with a colormap pointer plus a per-column source that respects post delta offsets), 13-014 (fuzz/invisibility adds a SEPARATE R_DrawFuzzColumn primitive that shares the ColumnDrawJob shape but replaces the colormap indirection with a noise-table lookup; it does NOT extend rDrawColumn itself, keeping the fast path free of conditionals), 17-001 (level-start state hash does not include framebuffer contents, but 17-004 does), 17-004 (framebuffer CRC suite exercises rDrawColumn and rDrawSpan for every visible frame — the parity-critical invariants locked here gate the CRC match), 17-010 (final gate: any per-pixel divergence from vanilla reports as a CRC mismatch, traced back to one of rDrawColumn/rDrawSpan).

## F-131

- fact: DOOM patch lump decode and draw (v_video.c V_DrawPatch + the patch_t / column_t / post_t layout shared with r_data.c R_GetColumn) lives in src/render/patchDraw.ts. Exports: 5 numeric constants PATCH_HEADER_BYTES=8 (width + height + leftOffset + topOffset at int16 LE each), PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES=4 (int32 LE per column in the offset table), PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER=0xff (sentinel topDelta that terminates a column's post chain), POST_HEADER_BYTES=3 (topDelta + length + leading-pad before the pixel run), POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES=1 (pad byte after the pixel run so the next post starts at `cursor + POST_HEADER_BYTES + length + POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES`). Exports 4 interfaces: PatchHeader {width, height, leftOffset, topOffset} — width/height are int16 LE bounding-box dims, leftOffset/topOffset are SIGNED int16 LE sprite-origin adjustments the draw path subtracts from the caller's (x, y); PatchPost {topDelta, length, pixels: Uint8Array} — topDelta is the row offset within the patch where pixels[0] lands; pixels is a length-byte slice copy of the lump data so decoded patches survive source-buffer reclamation; PatchColumn = readonly PatchPost[]; DecodedPatch {header, columns} — exactly header.width columns, each frozen. Exports two functions: `decodePatch(buffer: Uint8Array): DecodedPatch` and `drawPatch(patch, x, y, framebuffer, screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH, screenHeight=SCREENHEIGHT): void`. decodePatch reads the header at offset 0, reads `width` column offsets from the PATCH_HEADER_BYTES..PATCH_HEADER_BYTES+width*4 range, then walks each column's post chain by cursor advance: topDelta byte (break on 0xff), length byte, skip one leading-pad byte, slice `length` pixel bytes, skip one trailing-pad byte, loop. Every level of the returned structure (outer object, header, columns array, each column's post array, each post object) is Object.freeze'd so consumers cannot accidentally mutate decoded assets. pixels are `buffer.slice(start, start + length)` copies rather than subarray views — this matches vanilla's patch_t-in-Z_Malloc lifetime where the lump cache owns the bytes until the lock is released but the decoded patch can outlive the lock if we re-reference. RangeError is thrown for: buffer too small for the header, buffer too small for the column-offset table, a column offset outside [0, buffer.length), a post header extending past the buffer end, a post pixel run extending past the buffer end — all fatal by the same rules the vanilla `Z_CheckHeap` + out-of-bounds memory read would hit. drawPatch mirrors V_DrawPatch byte-for-byte: `originX = x - leftOffset; originY = y - topOffset`, then for each column 0..width-1 computes `screenX = originX + col`, skips columns with `screenX < 0 || screenX >= screenWidth`, and for each post computes `postTopY = originY + topDelta` and writes pixels[row] at framebuffer[(postTopY + row) * screenWidth + screenX] for row 0..length-1 with the per-pixel `screenY < 0 || screenY >= screenHeight` clip. Parity-critical invariants preserved byte-for-byte: (1) The post chain ends at a bare 0xff byte — NO length/pad bytes follow, the decoder checks only the topDelta byte before the break. (2) Per-post byte layout matches vanilla: `source = (byte *)column + 3` skips topDelta+length+leading-pad, the pixel run is `length` bytes, the next post starts at `(byte *)column + length + 4` = POST_HEADER_BYTES + length + POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES bytes past the current post header. (3) leftOffset / topOffset are SIGNED — v_video.c declares `SHORT(patch->leftoffset)` which casts through `(short)`; a sprite with leftOffset=-5 subtracts -5 from x (i.e. adds 5), shifting the art rightward so the sprite's visual center column lands at the draw-origin x. (4) Gaps between posts leave the framebuffer untouched — vanilla's "transparent pixel" semantics come from the lack of a write, not from a sentinel value; the mask-pattern test locks this by pre-filling with a canary byte and asserting the canary survives in the gap rows. (5) Empty columns (post chain === [0xff]) skip the entire screenX column — useful for sparse sprites whose bounding box includes all-transparent edge columns. (6) DOOM1.WAD uses the plain "single-topdelta" encoding — each post's topDelta is absolute (row offset from patch top, not delta-chained); the later DeePsea "tall patch" extension (where successive topDeltas chain by summing when they regress) is NOT present in the shareware IWAD so this decoder treats topDelta as absolute. (7) Per-pixel bounds clipping (both screenX and screenY) silently skips out-of-framebuffer writes. Vanilla on DOS had a RANGECHECK_DRAW debug assert that I_Error'd on out-of-bounds patches and was compiled out in release — release behavior was "write into wrong memory". Uint8Array silently discards negative indices but WOULD WRAP on indices past length (because large-index writes are ignored, but a moderately-large index within the array — e.g. y=SCREENHEIGHT causes `screenY * screenWidth + screenX` to overflow the array and be silently ignored too, while y=-1 causes `-1 * screenWidth + 0 = -320` which is also negative and silently ignored — BUT y=SCREENHEIGHT-1 writing into row SCREENHEIGHT-1 + pixel past col SCREENWIDTH-1 would wrap to the next row in-array). The explicit per-axis clip is therefore REQUIRED to avoid accidental row-wrap artifacts, and is a safe deliberate divergence from vanilla's unchecked release behavior since every in-bounds pixel is parity-identical. (8) No colormap, no scaling, no blending — drawPatch is the pure V-layer copy primitive (HUD/menu/status-bar/finale/title-screen backgrounds); the lit scaled column path used by sprites and walls routes through rDrawColumn in drawPrimitives.ts, which accepts a pre-composited Uint8Array column via ColumnDrawJob.source rather than raw post data. (9) PatchPost.pixels is a `buffer.slice(...)` COPY rather than `buffer.subarray(...)` view — slice allocates a new backing buffer and copies the bytes, so a decoded patch can outlive the source lump buffer. This matters if the lump cache is reclaimed between decode and draw; a subarray view would dangle. The extra copy cost (~1KB per typical sprite patch) is a one-time initialization expense amortized over many draws. (10) screenWidth and screenHeight are plain parameters with defaults (not derived from the framebuffer Uint8Array .length) because vanilla uses SCREENWIDTH/SCREENHEIGHT as hard-coded constants — a caller that builds a smaller framebuffer (e.g. for a preview or menu mini-map) can pass custom dimensions and the clipping follows. Architecture: the module imports only SCREENWIDTH and SCREENHEIGHT from ./projection.ts; no Win32, runtime, or WAD-layer dependencies. decodePatch takes a raw Uint8Array (the lump bytes) — the caller is responsible for locating the patch lump in the WAD directory via assets/patchCatalog.ts and reading the bytes via the WAD loader; this separation keeps patchDraw.ts pure and means the same decoder works for patches stored in PWADs or synthetic test fixtures. The test file uses a `buildPatchLump({width, height, leftOffset, topOffset, columns: [[{topDelta, pixels}, ...]]})` synthetic-fixture helper that byte-for-byte matches the on-disk format (little-endian int16/int32, 3-byte post header, 1-byte trailing pad, 0xff column terminator); real DOOM1.WAD patch data parses identically through decodePatch when exercised by a future integration test.
- source: Chocolate Doom v_video.c V_DrawPatch (`y -= SHORT(patch->topoffset); x -= SHORT(patch->leftoffset); for (; col < w; x++, col++, desttop++) { column = (column_t *)((byte *)patch + LONG(patch->columnofs[col])); while (column->topdelta != 0xff) { source = (byte *)column + 3; dest = desttop + column->topdelta * SCREENWIDTH; count = column->length; while (count--) { *dest = *source++; dest += SCREENWIDTH; } column = (column_t *)((byte *)column + column->length + 4); } }`) + r_defs.h patch_t / column_t / post_t layouts + DOOM1.WAD patch lump inspection (shareware IWAD uses plain single-topdelta encoding, no DeePsea tall-patch chaining); confirmed against src/render/patchDraw.ts (~240 lines) and test/render/patch-draw.test.ts (29 tests, 64_411 expect() calls — high count comes from a full-framebuffer canary sweep in the "fully off-screen patch leaves the framebuffer entirely at the canary value" test).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 13-005 (wall-column fetch reads PATCH_HEADER_BYTES + columnOffsets table to resolve per-column post chains for composite texture columns; the decodePatch parser is NOT called directly because R_GetColumn composites multiple patches into a 128-tall column buffer rather than decoding a whole patch — but the PATCH_HEADER_BYTES/PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES/POST_HEADER_BYTES/POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES/PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER constants are load-bearing for that composite path), 13-011 (sprite projection walks DecodedPatch columns and queues ColumnDrawJob per post for rDrawColumn, using the post.pixels buffer as ColumnDrawJob.source with dc_yl/dc_yh derived from the post.topDelta + sprite.screenScale projection), 13-013 (masked midtextures call drawPatch's per-post walk but route through rDrawColumn with the colormap applied, so the masked-texture path cannot reuse drawPatch directly — it needs a separate walker that respects post topDelta offsets while invoking the lit column primitive), 14-001 (UI font and patch assets feed decodePatch for every HUD glyph, menu patch, and status-bar face; the decoder output feeds drawPatch for unlit screen-space blits), 14-002 (status-bar widgets and face render via drawPatch with patch.leftOffset/topOffset pre-baked so widgets land at fixed screen coordinates), 14-003 (HUD messages route through the font's PatchCatalog → decodePatch → drawPatch pipeline), 14-004 (automap line-drawing does NOT use drawPatch, but the automap's marker patches do), 14-005 (menu tree draws cursor/selector patches via drawPatch), 14-006 (intermission stats draws digit patches + WI\* background patches via drawPatch), 14-007 (finale text draws character patches via drawPatch + background patches via drawPatch), 14-008 (title/credit/help/demo sequencing transitions between full-screen background patches via drawPatch), 17-001 (level-start state hash does not include framebuffer contents, so patchDraw is not exercised by the level-start hash), 17-004 (framebuffer CRC suite exercises drawPatch for every HUD element and menu screen — a per-pixel divergence reports as a CRC mismatch traced back to drawPatch's post walker or decodePatch's column parser), 17-010 (final gate: every title/intermission/finale/menu screen is a drawPatch composition; any per-pixel divergence from vanilla V_DrawPatch reports as a parity failure).

## F-132

- fact: Wall-texture column fetch (r_data.c R_GetColumn + R_GenerateLookup + R_GenerateComposite + R_DrawColumnInCache) lives in src/render/wallColumns.ts. Exports: the texture-wrap mask helper `computeTextureWidthMask(width): number` reproducing vanilla's `j = 1; while (j*2 <= width) j <<= 1; return j - 1;` (power-of-2 widths return `width - 1`; non-power-of-2 widths return the mask of the largest power of 2 that fits, e.g. width=96 → mask=63 so columns 64..95 wrap back to 0..31 — the well-known "non-power-of-2 texture premature wrap" quirk that rarely triggers in DOOM1.WAD because every shareware wall texture has a power-of-2 width); `prepareWallTexture(name, width, height, patches): PreparedWallTexture` running the full two-pass composite build; `getWallColumn(texture, col): Uint8Array` returning `texture.columns[col & widthMask]`. The two interfaces — WallPatchPlacement {originX, originY, patch: DecodedPatch} (mirrors r_defs.h texpatch_t with signed originX/originY to support patches extending past the left/top edges) and PreparedWallTexture {name, width, height, widthMask, composite: Uint8Array, columns: readonly Uint8Array[]} (the frozen full record). Parity-critical invariants preserved byte-for-byte: (1) Per-column patch counting walks every placement's horizontal span `[max(0, originX), min(width, originX + patchWidth))` and increments `patchCount[x]` for every covered texture column. Columns with `patchCount[x] > 1` are flagged composite; columns with `patchCount[x] === 1` alias the single-patch reference. The last placement to cover a single-patch column provides the reference (matching vanilla where `collump[x]` / `colofs[x]` are unconditionally overwritten by each patch and the composite-flag check happens afterwards). (2) Composite size is `height * compositeColumnCount` bytes — each composite column gets exactly `texture.height` bytes regardless of the patch heights involved. Composite columns are laid out sequentially in the composite buffer in texture-column order. (3) The composite-build pass iterates patches in list order. For each patch's covered columns that are flagged composite, every post is memcpy'd into `composite[destOffset + position..destOffset + position + count)` where `position = originY + topDelta` and `count = post.length` adjusted by the two vanilla clips (top-clip when position < 0; bottom-clip when position + count > cacheHeight). Later patches overwrite earlier ones pixel-by-pixel at overlapping positions — non-overlapping posts leave earlier patch's pixels intact. (4) R_DrawColumnInCache vanilla BUG faithfully reproduced: when `position < 0`, count is reduced by |position| but the source pointer stays at `pixels[0]` (NOT advanced to `pixels[|position|]`). The observable effect: a post that extends above the texture top draws its TOP pixels at the cache's row 0 instead of its intended row 0 being the |position|-th pixel from the top; the bottom |position| rows of the post are silently dropped. This bug only triggers when a patch is placed at `originY + topDelta < 0` (originY < -topDelta); in DOOM1.WAD textures patches typically have originY=0 and posts starting at topDelta=0 so the bug doesn't manifest, but the reproduction is parity-critical for any PWAD or edge case that does trigger it. (5) Single-patch column retrieval: for a column with `patchCount[x] === 1`, the returned Uint8Array is the first post's `pixels` Uint8Array from the single covering patch — matches vanilla's `return cache + colofs[x]` where `colofs[x] = columnOffsets[x - x1] + 3` and `+3` skips topDelta+length+leadingPad to land at pixel bytes. The returned buffer length equals the first post's length (NOT texture.height); callers that read past that length would get `undefined` in JS where vanilla reads raw lump bytes — this is undefined behavior on both sides, the common case has post.length === texture.height for solid wall patches. If the patch's column has no posts (empty column, just 0xFF terminator), the returned buffer is a zero-length Uint8Array. (6) Composite column retrieval: returns `composite.subarray(offset, offset + height)` — a live view into the composite buffer, so mutation of either propagates. Returned buffer length is exactly `texture.height`. (7) No-patch-coverage columns (patchCount === 0, which can happen with sparse patch placements even though DOOM1.WAD never emits them) return a zero-length Uint8Array rather than uninitialized memory; vanilla reads whatever Z_Malloc returned (undefined behavior). Our zero-length buffer is a safe divergence from undefined behavior. (8) `getWallColumn(tex, col)` masks `col` through `tex.widthMask` using JS's int32 bitwise AND, which correctly wraps negative col values via two's-complement (e.g., `-1 & 63 === 63`, `-65 & 63 === 63`). (9) Reference stability: repeated fetches of the same column return the SAME Uint8Array instance — `columns[col]` is computed once in prepareWallTexture and never recomputed. Composite columns alias the shared composite buffer so mutating one row changes all columns derived from the same composite buffer offset window (this matters only for tests, not for runtime behavior). Architecture: imports only from ./patchDraw.ts (DecodedPatch + PatchColumn type), no runtime or Win32 dependencies; the patch decoding is done upstream via decodePatch so wallColumns operates on structured DecodedPatch objects rather than raw lump bytes. The PATCH_HEADER_BYTES/PATCH_COLUMN_OFFSET_BYTES/POST_HEADER_BYTES/POST_TRAILING_PAD_BYTES/PATCH_COLUMN_END_MARKER constants from F-131 are NOT directly imported here because the decoded patch already provides the structured view — but those constants remain load-bearing in the patch-decoding step upstream. The WallPatchPlacement `patch` field is the full DecodedPatch not just its column list, so originX/originY/width/height are all accessible without a separate interface; a future step that wants lazy patch loading (instead of eager decode) would swap `patch: DecodedPatch` for a lazy accessor without changing prepareWallTexture's logic.
- source: Chocolate Doom r_data.c R_GetColumn (`col &= texturewidthmask[tex]; lump = texturecolumnlump[tex][col]; ofs = texturecolumnofs[tex][col]; if (lump > 0) return (byte *)W_CacheLumpNum(lump, PU_CACHE) + ofs; if (!texturecomposite[tex]) R_GenerateComposite(tex); return texturecomposite[tex] + ofs;`) + R_GenerateLookup (two-pass: first counts patchcount[x] and records collump[x]/colofs[x]; second marks patchcount[x] > 1 columns as composite with `collump[x] = -1; colofs[x] = texturecompositesize; texturecompositesize += texture->height;`) + R_GenerateComposite (`block = Z_Malloc(compositesize, PU_STATIC, ...); for each patch: for covered columns where collump[x] < 0: patchcol = realpatch + columnofs[x-x1]; R_DrawColumnInCache(patchcol, block + colofs[x], patch->originy, texture->height);`) + R_DrawColumnInCache (`while (patch->topdelta != 0xff) { source = (byte*)patch + 3; count = patch->length; position = originy + patch->topdelta; if (position < 0) { count += position; position = 0; } if (position + count > cacheheight) count = cacheheight - position; if (count > 0) memcpy(cache + position, source, count); patch = (column_t*)((byte*)patch + patch->length + 4); }`) + r_data.c R_InitTextures width-mask derivation (`j = 1; while (j*2 <= texture->width) j <<= 1; texturewidthmask[i] = j - 1;`); confirmed against src/render/wallColumns.ts (~165 lines) and test/render/wall-column-fetch.test.ts (32 tests, 8_757 expect() calls — the high count is driven by a full 64×128 sweep in the "full-width single patch: every column aliases its patch post pixels" test).

- future_steps: 13-006 (solid-wall path consumes getWallColumn per column of a one-sided line; the wall renderer walks x from x1..x2, computes the texture U at each column via the xToAngle table + seg parameters, and calls getWallColumn(tex, u) to fetch the pixel buffer that feeds rDrawColumn's dc_source), 13-007 (two-sided wall path calls getWallColumn for upper/lower textures with the same per-column U mapping; midtextures are handled separately via R_DrawMaskedColumn which does NOT use getWallColumn), 13-013 (masked midtextures bypass getWallColumn — they walk per-post using decodePatch's PatchColumn structure directly because the masked draw respects post gaps, which getWallColumn's composite does not preserve), 14-005 (menu backgrounds are full-screen flats or patches, neither of which uses getWallColumn; menu texture-size preview widgets also use drawPatch not getWallColumn), 17-001 (level-start state hash does not include prepared wall textures — they're deterministic from WAD content so they don't affect the state hash; the level-start hash captures player/mobj state which is independent of renderer caches), 17-004 (framebuffer CRC suite exercises getWallColumn for every on-screen wall column — a per-byte divergence in composite generation or the R_DrawColumnInCache bug reproduction would surface as a CRC mismatch traced back to wallColumns), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) non-power-of-2 width mask wrap, (b) R_DrawColumnInCache top-clip bug shifting pixels down and dropping the bottom, (c) later-patch-overwrites-earlier composite order, (d) per-column patch count threshold of >1 for composite flagging, (e) single-patch column returns first-post pixels NOT the whole column), 17-010 (final gate: any divergence from vanilla's R_GetColumn output reports as a byte-level framebuffer mismatch; the 32-test suite locks the column-fetch contract).

## F-133

- fact: Solid-wall renderer (r_segs.c R_RenderSegLoop midtexture branch + r_bsp.c R_ClipSolidWallSegment's post-seg terminal-update invariants + r_plane.c visplane marking) lives in src/render/solidWalls.ts. Exports: 3 numeric constants HEIGHTBITS=12 (right-shift applied to topfrac/bottomfrac to produce an integer screen row), HEIGHTUNIT = 1 << HEIGHTBITS = 4096 (r_segs.c HEIGHTUNIT; one row of vertical step in fixed-point), INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR=0xffff_ffff (numerator for the dc_iscale = 0xffffffffu / rw_scale unsigned division in R_RenderSegLoop). Exports 2 interfaces: SolidWallSegment {rwX, rwStopX, topFrac, topStep, bottomFrac, bottomStep, midTexture: PreparedWallTexture, midTextureMid, scale, scaleStep, wallLights: readonly Uint8Array[], markCeiling, ceilingPlane: Visplane | null, markFloor, floorPlane: Visplane | null, textureColumnFor: (x: number) => number} carries every per-seg value R_RenderSegLoop needs — with textureColumnFor abstracted as a caller-supplied closure so the xtoviewangle/finetangent/rw_centerangle/rw_distance chain stays owned by the BSP traversal step (future 13-007+) rather than leaking into this module's scope; SolidWallRenderContext {framebuffer: Uint8Array, screenWidth?: number, viewHeight, centerY, ceilingClip: Int16Array, floorClip: Int16Array} carries per-frame clip state (screenWidth defaults to SCREENWIDTH for vanilla-sized framebuffers). Exports 1 function: `renderSolidWall(seg, ctx): void`. The loop walks `x = rwX; x < rwStopX; x += 1` and for each column: (1) captures `ceilingHere = ceilingClip[x]` and `floorHere = floorClip[x]` at loop top so later visplane marking and the terminal-update reads the ORIGINAL (pre-close) values; (2) computes `yl = (topFrac + HEIGHTUNIT - 1) >> HEIGHTBITS` (ceiling divide — rounds up to the next integer row) then clamps `yl = max(yl, ceilingHere + 1)`; (3) if markCeiling && ceilingPlane !== null, computes `top = ceilingHere + 1; bottom = yl - 1`, clamps `bottom = min(bottom, floorHere - 1)`, and writes `ceilingPlane.top[x] = top; ceilingPlane.bottom[x] = bottom` iff `top <= bottom`; (4) computes `yh = bottomFrac >> HEIGHTBITS` (floor divide — rounds down, NO `+ HEIGHTUNIT - 1` bias) then clamps `yh = min(yh, floorHere - 1)`; (5) if markFloor && floorPlane !== null, computes `top = yh + 1; bottom = floorHere - 1`, clamps `top = max(top, ceilingHere + 1)`, and writes `floorPlane.top[x] = top; floorPlane.bottom[x] = bottom` iff `top <= bottom`; (6) resolves `texturecolumn = textureColumnFor(x)`; computes `index = scale >> LIGHTSCALESHIFT` and clamps `index = min(index, MAXLIGHTSCALE - 1)`; picks `colormap = wallLights[index]`; computes `iscale = (INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR / (scale >>> 0)) | 0` — the `>>> 0` coerces scale to uint32 before division to match C's unsigned division, and the `| 0` sign-extends the quotient back to int32 that fixed_t expects (for scales < 2 the quotient exceeds 0x7FFFFFFF and sign-extends to negative, matching vanilla's `unsigned / unsigned → unsigned` that is then interpreted as signed); fetches `source = getWallColumn(midTexture, texturecolumn)`; calls `rDrawColumn({x, yl, yh, textureMid: midTextureMid, iscale, centerY, source, colormap}, framebuffer, screenWidth)`; (7) writes the TERMINAL update AFTER drawing: `ceilingClip[x] = viewHeight | 0; floorClip[x] = -1` — these close the column so any subsequent seg or sprite seeing `ceilingClip[x] = viewHeight` computes `yl >= viewHeight + 1 > yh` and skips drawing; (8) advances `topFrac = (topFrac + topStep) | 0; bottomFrac = (bottomFrac + bottomStep) | 0; scale = (scale + scaleStep) | 0` for the next column. Parity-critical invariants locked by the 32-test suite: (1) HEIGHTBITS=12 and HEIGHTUNIT=4096 match r_segs.c macros; (2) INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR=0xffffffff matches vanilla's uint32 max; (3) yl ceiling divide: topFrac=3*HEIGHTUNIT → yl=3; topFrac=2*HEIGHTUNIT+1 → yl=3 (rounds up); (4) yh floor divide: bottomFrac=4*HEIGHTUNIT+HEIGHTUNIT-1 → yh=4 (no bias); (5) yl clamps to ceilingHere+1 (never draws above the ceiling); (6) yh clamps to floorHere-1 (never draws below the floor); (7) inverted ceiling/floor clips (ceilingClip > floorClip) produce yl > yh and rDrawColumn's count<0 guard short-circuits — but the terminal-update still runs so ceilingClip[x] = viewHeight and floorClip[x] = -1; (8) ceiling visplane marking uses ORIGINAL ceilingHere NOT the post-close viewHeight (captured at loop top); the guard `top <= bottom` skips the mark when yl is already clamped to ceilingHere+1 (top == yl, bottom == yl-1, top > bottom); (9) ceiling visplane bottom clamp to floorHere-1 prevents the mark from extending past the opposite clip; (10) floor visplane marking is symmetric: top = yh+1, bottom = floorHere-1, top clamps UP to ceilingHere+1; guard `top <= bottom` skips when yh is already clamped to floorHere-1; (11) markCeiling=false skips ceiling marking entirely even with ceilingPlane supplied; markFloor=false skips floor marking; (12) wallLights[scale >> LIGHTSCALESHIFT] per column — each column's scale is a different light bucket; (13) wallLights index clamps to MAXLIGHTSCALE-1 (prevents OOB read into walllights); (14) iscale = 0xffffffff / scale truncated to int32 via `(num / (scale >>> 0)) | 0` — for scale=0x100 iscale=16777215=0xFFFFFF, for scale=0x10000 iscale=65535=0xFFFF, for scale=1 iscale=-1 (sign-extends the 0xFFFFFFFF quotient); (15) rDrawColumn's frac walks the source column in powers-of-2-wrapped indices (& 127) so even negative iscales produce deterministic texture samples; (16) textureColumnFor is called with every covered screen column (x = rwX..rwStopX-1) in order; (17) getWallColumn wraps via PreparedWallTexture.widthMask — a 48-wide non-power-of-2 texture (mask=31) with textureColumnFor returning 40..43 reads columns 8..11 (premature wrap); (18) the terminal update ceilingClip[x]=viewHeight / floorClip[x]=-1 runs AFTER rDrawColumn so a second seg sharing a column with a closed-off first seg's column sees yl clamped to viewHeight+1 > yh=-2 and draws nothing there (cover-and-close semantics); (19) scaleStep advances scale every column (verified via per-column lighting bucket selection); (20) midTextureMid shifts the starting frac (frac = textureMid + (yl - centerY) * iscale) — shifting midTextureMid shifts which source row lands at centerY; (21) screenWidth defaults to SCREENWIDTH when the context omits it (SCREENWIDTH-stride framebuffer); (22) columns outside [rwX, rwStopX) are left entirely untouched (framebuffer, ceilingClip, floorClip all preserved); (23) rwStopX <= rwX draws nothing (empty range). Architecture: imports only from ./drawPrimitives.ts (rDrawColumn), ./projection.ts (LIGHTSCALESHIFT, MAXLIGHTSCALE, SCREENWIDTH), ./renderLimits.ts (Visplane type), and ./wallColumns.ts (getWallColumn, PreparedWallTexture type); no runtime or Win32 dependencies; pure arithmetic + typed-array writes. The caller owns the framebuffer, clip arrays, visplane records, and walllights table; this function mutates them in place. The textureColumnFor closure pattern keeps this module's scope tight to the solid-wall loop without depending on the xtoviewangle/finetangent tables that are not yet built — future wall-renderer glue (13-007+) will provide a closure that does `const angle = (rwCenterangle + xtoviewangle[x]) >>> ANGLETOFINESHIFT; const texturecolumn = (rwOffset - FixedMul(finetangent[angle], rwDistance)) >> FRACBITS; return texturecolumn;` matching vanilla's R_StoreWallRange inner formula.
- source: Chocolate Doom r_segs.c R_RenderSegLoop midtexture branch (`while (rw_x < rw_stopx) { yl = (topfrac + HEIGHTUNIT - 1) >> HEIGHTBITS; if (yl < ceilingclip[rw_x] + 1) yl = ceilingclip[rw_x] + 1; if (markceiling) { top = ceilingclip[rw_x] + 1; bottom = yl - 1; if (bottom >= floorclip[rw_x]) bottom = floorclip[rw_x] - 1; if (top <= bottom) { ceilingplane->top[rw_x] = top; ceilingplane->bottom[rw_x] = bottom; } } yh = bottomfrac >> HEIGHTBITS; if (yh >= floorclip[rw_x]) yh = floorclip[rw_x] - 1; if (markfloor) { top = yh + 1; bottom = floorclip[rw_x] - 1; if (top <= ceilingclip[rw_x]) top = ceilingclip[rw_x] + 1; if (top <= bottom) { floorplane->top[rw_x] = top; floorplane->bottom[rw_x] = bottom; } } if (midtexture) { dc_yl = yl; dc_yh = yh; dc_texturemid = rw_midtexturemid; dc_source = R_GetColumn(midtexture, texturecolumn); dc_iscale = 0xffffffffu / (unsigned)rw_scale; colfunc(); ceilingclip[rw_x] = viewheight; floorclip[rw_x] = -1; } rw_x++; scale += rw_scalestep; topfrac += topstep; bottomfrac += bottomstep; }`) + r_bsp.c R_ClipSolidWallSegment (caller frames that decide to invoke this path at all — solid wall segs cover the full visible column so they own both visplane marks and the terminal clip update) + r_plane.c visplane top/bottom arrays (ceilingplane->top / ceilingplane->bottom are per-column Uint8Array-like buffers that R_DrawPlanes later reads for span generation — we write Uint8Array indices 0..viewheight-1 matching vanilla's `short` narrow range); confirmed against src/render/solidWalls.ts (~290 lines) and test/render/solid-walls.test.ts (32 tests, 1489 expect() calls, 9 describe groups — the count density is appropriate for the combination of loop-state, clipping, visplane marking, and lighting invariants).

## F-134

- fact: Two-sided (pass-through) wall renderer (r_segs.c `R_RenderSegLoop` else-branch for segs with both a front and back sector — windows, portals, steps, lintels) lives in src/render/twoSidedWalls.ts. Exports: 3 numeric constants HEIGHTBITS=12, HEIGHTUNIT=4096, INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR=0xffffffff (all RE-EXPORTED from ./solidWalls.ts so the two renderers share identical fixed-point scale conventions); 2 readonly interfaces TwoSidedWallSegment {rwX, rwStopX, topFrac, topStep, bottomFrac, bottomStep, topTexture: PreparedWallTexture | null, topTextureMid, pixHigh, pixHighStep, bottomTexture: PreparedWallTexture | null, bottomTextureMid, pixLow, pixLowStep, scale, scaleStep, wallLights: readonly Uint8Array[], markCeiling, ceilingPlane: Visplane | null, markFloor, floorPlane: Visplane | null, textureColumnFor: (x: number) => number, maskedTextureCol: Int16Array | null} and TwoSidedWallRenderContext {framebuffer: Uint8Array, screenWidth?: number, viewHeight, centerY, ceilingClip: Int16Array, floorClip: Int16Array} (same shape as SolidWallRenderContext so both renderers can mutate a shared per-frame clip state); 1 function renderTwoSidedWall(seg, ctx): void. The loop walks `x = rwX; x < rwStopX; x += 1` and for each column: (1) captures `ceilingHere = ceilingClip[x]` and `floorHere = floorClip[x]` at loop top for visplane marking; (2) computes `yl = (topFrac + HEIGHTUNIT - 1) >> HEIGHTBITS` (ceiling divide) clamped to `max(yl, ceilingHere + 1)`; (3) if markCeiling && ceilingPlane, writes the ceiling visplane mark using `top = ceilingHere + 1; bottom = yl - 1; bottom = min(bottom, floorHere - 1)` with the `top <= bottom` guard; (4) computes `yh = bottomFrac >> HEIGHTBITS` (floor divide) clamped to `min(yh, floorHere - 1)`; (5) if markFloor && floorPlane, writes the floor visplane mark using `top = yh + 1; bottom = floorHere - 1; top = max(top, ceilingHere + 1)` with the same guard; (6) resolves `texturecolumn = textureColumnFor(x)`, computes `index = scale >> LIGHTSCALESHIFT` clamped to `min(index, MAXLIGHTSCALE - 1)` picking `colormap = wallLights[index]`, and computes `iscale = (INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR / (scale >>> 0)) | 0` matching vanilla's unsigned-into-signed quirk; the same texturecolumn/colormap/iscale feed BOTH the upper and lower texture draws — one closure call per column; (7) TOP BRANCH (when `topTexture !== null`): reads `mid = pixHigh >> HEIGHTBITS` (floor divide — NOT ceiling divide like yl — because pixHigh is the back-sector ceiling row, which becomes the bottom of the upper texture), advances `pixHigh = (pixHigh + pixHighStep) | 0` INSIDE the branch, clamps `mid = min(mid, floorHere - 1)`, then if `mid >= yl` fetches the upper texture column via `getWallColumn(topTexture, texturecolumn)` and calls `rDrawColumn({x, yl, yh: mid, textureMid: topTextureMid, iscale, centerY, source, colormap})`, writing `ceilingClip[x] = mid` after the draw; if `mid < yl` (no upper pixels fit), writes `ceilingClip[x] = yl - 1` instead — so the opening is still closed off down to yl - 1 and the next seg starting at this column sees the correct clip; when `topTexture === null` AND `markCeiling` is true writes `ceilingClip[x] = yl - 1`; when both are false, `ceilingClip[x]` is left UNTOUCHED (the live clip persists for sprites and opposite-side visplane pass-through); (8) BOTTOM BRANCH (when `bottomTexture !== null`): reads `mid = (pixLow + HEIGHTUNIT - 1) >> HEIGHTBITS` (CEILING divide — symmetric opposite of the top-branch floor divide because pixLow is the back-sector floor row, which becomes the top of the lower texture), advances `pixLow = (pixLow + pixLowStep) | 0` INSIDE the branch, reads `ceilingNow = ceilingClip[x]` — LIVE post-top-update value — and clamps `mid = max(mid, ceilingNow + 1)` so the bottom texture never overlaps the upper texture just drawn in step 7, then if `mid <= yh` fetches the lower texture column and calls `rDrawColumn({x, yl: mid, yh, textureMid: bottomTextureMid, ...})`, writing `floorClip[x] = mid` after the draw; if `mid > yh` writes `floorClip[x] = yh + 1`; when `bottomTexture === null` AND `markFloor` is true writes `floorClip[x] = yh + 1`; when both are false, `floorClip[x]` is left UNTOUCHED; (9) MASKED BRANCH (when `maskedTextureCol !== null`): writes `maskedTextureCol[x] = texturecolumn` (the RAW unmasked U value — vanilla stores `texturecolumn` before the masked pass applies the width mask via the opposite texture's widthMask); (10) advances `topFrac = (topFrac + topStep) | 0; bottomFrac = (bottomFrac + bottomStep) | 0; scale = (scale + scaleStep) | 0` for the next column. Parity-critical invariants locked by the 32-test suite (test/render/two-sided-walls.test.ts): (1) HEIGHTBITS/HEIGHTUNIT/INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR re-exports match ./solidWalls.ts identity (same numeric constants, same semantics); (2) pass-through behavior: seg with `topTexture=null, bottomTexture=null, markCeiling=false, markFloor=false` leaves ceilingClip and floorClip entirely untouched for every covered column (confirms NO terminal close); (3) ceiling visplane marking captures ORIGINAL ceilingHere at loop top (not post-top-branch-update), guards on `top <= bottom`, clamps to `floorHere - 1`, skipped when markCeiling=false or ceilingPlane=null; (4) floor visplane marking is symmetric with `top = yh + 1, bottom = floorHere - 1, top = max(top, ceilingHere + 1)`; (5) top-branch pixHigh uses FLOOR divide (`pixHigh >> HEIGHTBITS`), bottom-branch pixLow uses CEILING divide (`(pixLow + HEIGHTUNIT - 1) >> HEIGHTBITS`) — the divide-direction asymmetry is load-bearing (swapping them shifts upper/lower textures by one row); (6) top-branch `mid` clamps DOWN to `floorHere - 1` (upper texture never extends below front floor); bottom-branch `mid` clamps UP to the LIVE `ceilingClip[x]` post-top-update value plus 1 (bottom texture never overlaps the upper texture just drawn at this column); (7) pixHigh advances ONLY when topTexture is non-null (the `pixHigh += pixHighStep` is INSIDE the `if (topTexture)` branch — when topTexture is null, pixHigh is never read and never updated, matching vanilla's `if (toptexture)` gated initialization); same holds for pixLow/pixLowStep; (8) `mid < yl` (top branch no-draw) still closes ceiling to `yl - 1`; `mid > yh` (bottom branch no-draw) still closes floor to `yh + 1`; (9) when topTexture is null but markCeiling is true, writes `ceilingClip[x] = yl - 1` (vanilla's "no top wall but plane marked" branch); when markCeiling is false too, leaves ceilingClip untouched (critical for sprite pass-through); (10) maskedTextureCol records RAW unmasked texturecolumn (not `& widthMask`); (11) same texturecolumn feeds both upper and lower draws in the same column — one closure call per column; (15) rwStopX <= rwX draws nothing; (16) running after a closed-off solid-wall column with `ceilingClip=viewHeight, floorClip=-1` produces `yl = viewHeight + 1 > yh = -2` so the upper and lower draws both short-circuit via rDrawColumn's count<0 guard, but the ceilingClip/floorClip writes still run (`mid < yl` writes `yl - 1 = viewHeight` preserving the close; `mid > yh` writes `yh + 1 = -1` preserving the close). Architecture: imports only from ./drawPrimitives.ts (rDrawColumn), ./projection.ts (LIGHTSCALESHIFT, MAXLIGHTSCALE, SCREENWIDTH), ./renderLimits.ts (Visplane type), ./solidWalls.ts (HEIGHTBITS, HEIGHTUNIT, INVERSE_SCALE_NUMERATOR), ./wallColumns.ts (getWallColumn, PreparedWallTexture type); no runtime or Win32 dependencies; pure arithmetic + typed-array writes. The caller owns the framebuffer, clip arrays, visplane records, walllights table, and maskedTextureCol buffer; this function mutates them in place. Shares the textureColumnFor closure pattern with solidWalls.ts so the xtoviewangle/finetangent table resolution stays owned by future wall-renderer glue (later 13-\* steps) rather than leaking into this module. The maskedTextureCol Int16Array typing constrains stored values to [-32768, 32767]; vanilla uses `short` (int16) so this matches exactly — texture U columns in DOOM1.WAD are always << 32768 wide. The lack of a terminal close (cover-and-close semantics of solidWalls.ts) is the single most important semantic difference: a two-sided wall exposes the opening to sprites drawn AFTER this seg, and to the opposite-sector's visplane spans drawn during R_DrawPlanes, so the clip MUST remain live for any column where only an upper OR only a lower texture is drawn.

pixhighstep = -FixedMul(rw_scalestep, worldtop); }` — pixhigh is only initialized when toptexture is present) and the matching `if (bottomtexture)` pixlow init; confirmed against src/render/twoSidedWalls.ts (~384 lines) and test/render/two-sided-walls.test.ts (32 tests, 2723 expect() calls, 11 describe groups — constants re-export, pass-through, ceiling visplane, floor visplane, top texture, bottom texture, top/bottom interaction, masked midtexture, texture column resolution, lighting/iscale, vanilla full-frame invariants).

## F-135

- fact: Visplane pool and R_ClearPlanes/R_FindPlane/R_CheckPlane build helpers (r_plane.c visplane management) live in src/render/visplanes.ts. Exports: 2 re-exported numeric constants MAXVISPLANES=128 (from ./projection.ts — the vanilla visplane pool capacity, matches vanilla's `#define MAXVISPLANES 128`) and VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED=0xff (from ./renderLimits.ts — the per-column untouched-column sentinel written into the plane's top Uint8Array at allocation/split time); 1 interface VisplanePool {planes: readonly Visplane[], count: number, screenWidth: number} carrying the pre-allocated visplane ring plus vanilla's `lastvisplane - visplanes` offset as `count`; 3 functions createVisplanePool(options?: {screenWidth?: number}): VisplanePool, clearPlanes(pool): void, findPlane(pool, height, picnum, lightlevel, skyFlatNum): Visplane, checkPlane(pool, plane, start, stop): Visplane. createVisplanePool allocates MAXVISPLANES frozen Visplane records eagerly (each with `top = new Uint8Array(screenWidth)` and `bottom = new Uint8Array(screenWidth)` so the ring never reallocates) and initializes every slot to the empty-plane state (height=0, picnum=0, lightlevel=0, minx=screenWidth, maxx=-1); screenWidth defaults to SCREENWIDTH. clearPlanes simply sets pool.count=0 to reset the pool for a new frame — stale top/bottom contents from the previous frame's planes are left in place, and findPlane refills `top` with VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED on the next allocation so the sentinel is fresh. findPlane implements R_FindPlane exactly: (1) if picnum === skyFlatNum, local effectiveHeight and effectiveLight are BOTH collapsed to 0 before the scan — so every sky-tagged plane merges into one pool entry regardless of source sector height/lightlevel; (2) linear scan from index 0 to pool.count-1 returning the FIRST plane whose (height, picnum, lightlevel) matches the effective triple (first-match-wins semantics, not best-match); (3) on no match, throws RangeError("R_FindPlane: no more visplanes") when count === MAXVISPLANES else allocates slot `pool.planes[pool.count]` and post-increments count (mirroring vanilla's `lastvisplane++` pointer arithmetic) with `minx = screenWidth`, `maxx = -1`, `top.fill(VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED)`, `bottom` LEFT UNTOUCHED. checkPlane implements R_CheckPlane's intersection/union walker: (1) compute `intrl, intrh, unionl, unionh` via `if (start < plane.minx) {intrl=plane.minx; unionl=start} else {unionl=plane.minx; intrl=start}` and the symmetric pair on stop/maxx — the "intersection" bounds are the inward pair, the "union" bounds are the outward pair; (2) walk `x = intrl; while (x <= intrh && plane.top[x] === VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED) x++;` looking for the first column in the intersection that's already been touched by a prior checkPlane+wall-renderer pass; (3) if `x > intrh` (no touched column in intersection, including the degenerate intrl>intrh empty-intersection case that arises when start/stop is disjoint from [minx, maxx]), EXTEND in place: `plane.minx = unionl; plane.maxx = unionh` and return the same plane reference; (4) otherwise SPLIT: throw RangeError("R_CheckPlane: no more visplanes") on pool overflow, else allocate `pool.planes[pool.count]` and post-increment count with `(height, picnum, lightlevel)` copied from the input plane, `minx = start, maxx = stop` (NOT the union — the new plane covers exactly the caller's requested range), `top.fill(VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED)`, `bottom` LEFT UNTOUCHED, and return the new plane. Parity-critical invariants locked byte-for-byte by the 42-test suite (test/render/visplane-build.test.ts, 1154 expect() calls, 11 describe groups): (1) MAXVISPLANES=128 exported identity from projection.ts; (2) VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED=0xff exported identity from renderLimits.ts; (3) createVisplanePool allocates exactly MAXVISPLANES slots with top/bottom arrays sized to screenWidth; (4) initial minx=screenWidth, maxx=-1 (so minx > maxx means empty — used by R_DrawPlanes's skip predicate); (5) clearPlanes sets count=0 without touching per-slot state; (6) findPlane first call allocates slot 0 and post-increments count to 1; (7) findPlane matches on (height, picnum, lightlevel) triple and returns the SAME reference for repeated matches; (8) findPlane sky collapse: picnum=skyFlatNum forces the allocation/match to use height=0 and lightlevel=0 even when the caller passes non-zero values, so two sky planes at different ceiling heights share ONE pool entry; (9) linear first-match-wins: a later duplicate triple is never found because the scan returns the earlier match; (10) findPlane pool overflow throws RangeError at exactly `count === MAXVISPLANES`; (11) findPlane on fresh allocation refills `top` with 0xff across the full screenWidth range and leaves `bottom` untouched (stale bottom bytes from the previous frame's allocation survive); (12) checkPlane on freshly-found plane (minx=screenWidth, maxx=-1) hits the empty-intersection branch — intrl=plane.minx=screenWidth > intrh=stop so the walker loop never executes — and EXTENDS the plane's range to [start, stop]; (13) checkPlane extending a populated plane (minx=10, maxx=20) with a NEW range [5, 25] whose intersection [10, 20] has all-0xff top columns EXTENDS to union [5, 25]; (14) checkPlane on a populated plane where the intersection has at least ONE non-0xff top column SPLITS — allocates a new slot with same (height, picnum, lightlevel), minx=start, maxx=stop, top refilled with 0xff; the original plane's minx/maxx are UNCHANGED and its top remains whatever it was; (15) split inherits height/picnum/lightlevel from the original plane (not the current find params) — this is why callers get back the original plane from findPlane, then pass IT to checkPlane; (16) checkPlane empty intersection via disjoint ranges: [start=30, stop=40] with plane.minx=5, maxx=10 produces intrl=plane.minx=5, unionl=start=30 (since start > plane.minx, the "else" branch runs: unionl=plane.minx=5, intrl=start=30, WAIT — I mis-stated; re-reading: the if checks `start < plane.minx`. For start=30 > plane.minx=5, the else branch sets unionl=plane.minx=5, intrl=start=30. On stop=40 > plane.maxx=10, intrh=plane.maxx=10, unionh=stop=40. intrl=30 > intrh=10 → loop never executes → extend to minx=5, maxx=40. This is the "gaps don't split" quirk: a non-overlapping range extends the plane rather than allocating a new one, because no touched column exists in the empty intersection); (17) checkPlane pool overflow on split throws RangeError at `count === MAXVISPLANES`; (18) checkPlane preserves the ORIGINAL plane's minx/maxx on split (does NOT touch them); (19) returned reference identity: extend returns the same object; split returns a different object from the pool's next slot; (20) bottom array NEVER touched by findPlane or checkPlane — callers (solidWalls / twoSidedWalls) own all writes to bottom[x], and R_DrawPlanes uses top[x]===0xff as the untouched sentinel rather than reading bottom[x] for sentinel detection; (21) the full-frame workflow (clearPlanes + multiple findPlane allocations + interleaved checkPlane splits/extends + per-plane top[x] writes via direct mutation) reproduces vanilla's frame-level visplane lifecycle. Architecture: module imports only MAXVISPLANES and SCREENWIDTH from ./projection.ts, Visplane type and VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED from ./renderLimits.ts. No Win32 or runtime dependencies, no dynamic allocation beyond the initial pool creation — every frame reuses the same 128 pre-allocated Visplane objects. The pool is a single shared structure; callers must clear at frame start, populate via findPlane during BSP traversal, and drain via R_DrawPlanes at frame end. The caller-supplied `skyFlatNum` parameter keeps this module free of WAD-lump-lookup state (the sky flatnum comes from the flat texture catalog — a future step will resolve SKY1/SKY2/SKY3 flatnum at renderer init and pass it in per frame). The `screenWidth` field on VisplanePool locks the top/bottom array size so callers can't accidentally create a pool sized for one screenWidth and try to use it with a different framebuffer width. The `count` field is public and mutable so callers can observe pool usage (useful for testing and diagnostics); the read-only `planes` array prevents accidental external allocation of new Visplane objects.
- source: Chocolate Doom r_plane.c R_ClearPlanes (`for (i = 0; i < viewwidth; i++) { floorclip[i] = viewheight; ceilingclip[i] = -1; } lastvisplane = visplanes; lastopening = openings; for (angle = 0; angle < SLOPERANGE / 2; angle++) { dy = ... }` — the `lastvisplane = visplanes` is the count=0 equivalent; we don't reset floorclip/ceilingclip here because those belong to the solidWalls/twoSidedWalls context), R_FindPlane (`if (picnum == skyflatnum) { height = 0; lightlevel = 0; } for (check = visplanes; check < lastvisplane; check++) { if (height == check->height && picnum == check->picnum && lightlevel == check->lightlevel) break; } if (check < lastvisplane) return check; if (lastvisplane - visplanes == MAXVISPLANES) I_Error("R_FindPlane: no more visplanes"); lastvisplane++; check->height = height; check->picnum = picnum; check->lightlevel = lightlevel; check->minx = SCREENWIDTH; check->maxx = -1; memset(check->top, 0xff, sizeof(check->top)); return check;`), R_CheckPlane (`if (start < pl->minx) { intrl = pl->minx; unionl = start; } else { unionl = pl->minx; intrl = start; } if (stop > pl->maxx) { intrh = pl->maxx; unionh = stop; } else { unionh = pl->maxx; intrh = stop; } for (x = intrl; x <= intrh; x++) if (pl->top[x] != 0xff) break; if (x > intrh) { pl->minx = unionl; pl->maxx = unionh; return pl; } if (lastvisplane - visplanes == MAXVISPLANES) I_Error("R_CheckPlane: no more visplanes"); pl = lastvisplane++; pl->minx = start; pl->maxx = stop; pl->height = ...; pl->picnum = ...; pl->lightlevel = ...; memset(pl->top, 0xff, sizeof(pl->top)); return pl;`); confirmed against src/render/visplanes.ts (~256 lines) and test/render/visplane-build.test.ts (42 tests, 1154 expect() calls, 11 describe groups — createVisplanePool/MAXVISPLANES identity, clearPlanes, findPlane allocation, findPlane linear scan first-match, findPlane sky collapse, findPlane pool overflow, checkPlane extend, checkPlane split, checkPlane pool overflow, full-frame workflow, typing exports).
