## F-136

- fact: Visplane span renderer (r_plane.c R_MakeSpans + R_MapPlane + non-sky branch of R_DrawPlanes) lives in src/render/visplaneSpans.ts. Exports: 1 re-exported constant VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED=0xff (from ./renderLimits.ts for caller convenience — the boundary-sentinel value that callers compare against when they have a plane in hand); 1 callback type CloseSpanCallback = (y, x1, x2) => void; 1 interface PlaneSpanCache {spanStart, cachedHeight, cachedDistance, cachedXStep, cachedYStep: Int32Array} carrying the per-y scratch/cache arrays; 1 interface VisplaneSpanContext {planeHeight, planeZLight, fixedColormap, flatSource, viewX, viewY, viewAngle, baseXScale, baseYScale, ySlope, distScale, xToViewAngle, cachedHeight, cachedDistance, cachedXStep, cachedYStep, spanStart, framebuffer, screenWidth?} carrying per-plane + per-frame state; 4 functions createPlaneSpanCache(viewHeight): PlaneSpanCache, makeSpans(x, t1, b1, t2, b2, spanstart, closeSpan): void, mapPlaneSpan(y, x1, x2, ctx): void, renderVisplaneSpans(plane, ctx): void. createPlaneSpanCache allocates five zero-initialized Int32Arrays sized to viewHeight; cachedHeight[y]=0 is the cold-cache sentinel (a plane with planeHeight=0 would hit the cache on first access and read cachedDistance=0, which matches FixedMul(0, ySlope)=0 exactly — a benign accidental match). makeSpans implements R_MakeSpans as a four-while-loop column-diff walker that takes the previous column's (t1, b1), the current column's (t2, b2), the spanstart Int32Array, and a close-span callback. The four loops run in strict vanilla order: (1) close-top `while (t1 < t2 && t1 <= b1) { closeSpan(t1, spanstart[t1], x-1); t1++; }`, (2) close-bottom `while (b1 > b2 && b1 >= t1) { closeSpan(b1, spanstart[b1], x-1); b1--; }`, (3) start-top `while (t2 < t1 && t2 <= b2) { spanstart[t2] = x; t2++; }`, (4) start-bottom `while (b2 > b1 && b2 >= t2) { spanstart[b2] = x; b2--; }`. Local copies of t1/b1/t2/b2 (coerced via `| 0`) ensure caller args are unchanged on return. The close-span callback receives `x-1` (not `x`) because column `x` is the FIRST column that no longer contains the span — vanilla's R_MapPlane draws inclusive `[x1, x2]`. mapPlaneSpan implements R_MapPlane: checks `cachedHeight[y] === planeHeight`, on miss recomputes `distance = FixedMul(planeHeight, ySlope[y])`, `xStep = FixedMul(distance, baseXScale)`, `yStep = FixedMul(distance, baseYScale)` and writes all four values into the cache; on hit reuses the cached triple. Then unconditionally computes `length = FixedMul(distance, distScale[x1])`, `angleIndex = ((viewAngle + xToViewAngle[x1]) >>> ANGLETOFINESHIFT) & FINEMASK`, `xFrac = viewX + FixedMul(finecosine[angleIndex], length)`, `yFrac = -viewY - FixedMul(finesine[angleIndex], length)`. Colormap selection: if ctx.fixedColormap !== null use fixedColormap; else compute `index = distance >> LIGHTZSHIFT`, clamp `if (index >= MAXLIGHTZ) index = MAXLIGHTZ - 1` (NO lower clamp — matches vanilla, which also doesn't clamp negative buckets), and use `planeZLight[index]`. Emits via rDrawSpan({x1, x2, y, xFrac, yFrac, xStep, yStep, source: flatSource, colormap}, framebuffer, screenWidth ?? SCREENWIDTH). renderVisplaneSpans is the non-sky branch of R_DrawPlanes: early-returns on empty planes (`minx > maxx`, the R_ClearPlanes/createVisplanePool initial state), then walks `x = plane.minx; x <= plane.maxx + 1; x++` with synthesized boundary sentinels. At `x = plane.minx` on the first iteration, t1=VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED (0xff) and b1=0 — these are LOCAL variables, NOT written into plane.top[-1]/plane.bottom[-1]. At `x = plane.maxx + 1` the loop uses t2=VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED, b2=0 for the same reason. Otherwise reads `t2 = plane.top[x]` and `b2 = plane.bottom[x]`. Calls makeSpans(x, t1, b1, t2, b2, ctx.spanStart, closeSpan) where closeSpan is an inline closure that calls mapPlaneSpan(y, x1, x2, ctx). Parity-critical invariants locked byte-for-byte by the 41-test suite (test/render/visplane-span-render.test.ts, 1559 expect() calls, 5 describe groups): (1) createPlaneSpanCache allocates 5 separate Int32Arrays of size viewHeight with no aliasing; (2) makeSpans no-op when both t1>=t2 for close-top AND t2>=t1 for start-top AND b1<=b2 for close-bottom AND b2<=b1 for start-bottom (entirely quiet column transition); (3) makeSpans with t1=0xff (left boundary) takes the start-top path for every row `t2..b2`, writing `spanstart[y] = x` — no closeSpan invocations; (4) makeSpans with t2=0xff (right boundary) takes the close-top path for every row the previous column held open, and the close-bottom path for every row below — closes ALL open spans in vanilla order; (5) makeSpans identical columns (t1=t2, b1=b2) is a no-op; (6) makeSpans top-grows (t2 < t1) starts spans at new top rows; top-shrinks (t2 > t1) closes spans at removed top rows; bottom-shrinks (b2 < b1) closes spans at removed bottom rows; bottom-grows (b2 > b1) starts spans at new bottom rows; (7) makeSpans widens (t2 < t1 AND b2 > b1) and narrows (t2 > t1 AND b2 < b1) correctly combine the four-loop logic; (8) makeSpans disjoint ranges (prev=10..20, curr=30..40) close all of 10..20 AND start all of 30..40; (9) caller-argument immutability: after makeSpans returns, callers can read their original t1/b1/t2/b2 unchanged; (10) closeSpan receives `x - 1` as x2 (not x), so a span from x=5 to x=9 that closes on column 10 emits (y, 5, 9); (11) mapPlaneSpan cache MISS on first call writes new (planeHeight, distance, xStep, yStep) into cache; HIT on second call with same planeHeight reuses the cache (no FixedMul calls to verify — we assert the cached values are read); INVALIDATION on third call with different planeHeight overwrites the cache; (12) framebuffer writes at `dest = y * screenWidth + x1` show the source[(yFrac >> FLAT_Y_SHIFT & FLAT_Y_MASK) + (xFrac >> FRACBITS & FLAT_X_MASK)] byte run through colormap; (13) fixedColormap !== null overrides planeZLight — every span uses fixedColormap regardless of distance; (14) planeZLight bucket selection: with distance=bucket<<LIGHTZSHIFT, planeZLight[bucket] is chosen; (15) MAXLIGHTZ-1 clamp when `distance >> LIGHTZSHIFT >= MAXLIGHTZ` (tested with planeHeight=1000*FRACUNIT, ySlope=4*FRACUNIT giving distance=262144000, bucket=250 clamped to 127); (16) xFrac = viewX + FixedMul(cos, length); yFrac = -viewY - FixedMul(sin, length) — with known viewX/viewY/angle/length values the framebuffer pixel at dest=y*screenWidth+x1 matches source[ computed spot index] through the chosen colormap; (17) xToViewAngle[x1] offsets the angle correctly (not xToViewAngle[x1+1] or similar off-by-one); (18) write count: rDrawSpan writes exactly `(x2 - x1 + 1)` framebuffer bytes per span; (19) screenWidth override: passing screenWidth=160 in ctx uses 160 as the framebuffer row stride (verified by writing at y=5, x1=10 and reading framebuffer[5*160+10]); (20) renderVisplaneSpans empty plane (minx>maxx) is a no-op — framebuffer unchanged; (21) single-column plane (minx=maxx) with top[x]=50, bottom[x]=60 emits exactly one column's worth of spans (11 rows, one span per row since left boundary closes immediately at right boundary); (22) uniform rectangular plane (minx=10, maxx=20, top[x]=30 bottom[x]=40 for all x in range) emits 11 spans, one per row, each spanning x=10..20; (23) staircase plane (varying top[x] and bottom[x] per column) emits spans at the correct row/column boundaries; (24) mid-plane VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED column (plane.top[x]=0xff for x=15 in the middle of a minx=10, maxx=20 plane) closes all open spans at column 14 and re-opens them at column 16 (0xff is treated as "no span here" because every close-top/close-bottom comparison hits `0xff >= b1` or `t1 >= 0xff` which a valid row value can't satisfy — Wait, ACTUALLY reading my test: when t1=0xff we SKIP close-top (since 0xff < t2 is never true for valid t2<200), so mid-0xff column ONLY starts new spans via start-top/start-bottom. But the PREVIOUS column's spans stay open, held in spanstart[y], until the NEXT non-0xff column closes them. Actually reading again: when curr-column is 0xff, the next iteration compares t1=0xff vs t2=nextTop. Close-top runs for `0xff < nextTop` — impossible. Close-bottom runs for `b1 > nextBot && b1 >= t1`: with b1=0 from the 0xff column's bottom, close-bottom is `0 > nextBot`, never true. So spans DO stay open across a 0xff column — this is the "island" effect, where a 0xff hole in the middle of a plane does NOT split spans, because the sentinel arrangement makes the loops quiet. This is vanilla behavior.); (25) cache persistence across planes at same height: plane1 at planeHeight=H populates cache; plane2 at same planeHeight=H reuses cache without recomputing distance; (26) cache invalidation on different planeHeight: plane3 at planeHeight=H' overwrites cache; (27) boundary safety: plane.minx=0 and plane.maxx=SCREENWIDTH-1 do not write to plane.top[-1] or plane.top[SCREENWIDTH] — sentinels are synthesized in local variables; (28) plane-array immutability: plane.top[] and plane.bottom[] are unchanged after renderVisplaneSpans; (29) V-shape plane (top[x] high at ends, low in middle) correctly emits spans; (30) SCREENWIDTH default=320; VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED re-export identity=0xff; rDrawSpan-equivalence (calling rDrawSpan directly with the same args that mapPlaneSpan would compute produces the same framebuffer). Architecture: module imports fixedMul from ../core/fixed.ts, ANGLETOFINESHIFT/FINEMASK/finecosine/finesine from ../core/trig.ts, rDrawSpan from ./drawPrimitives.ts, LIGHTZSHIFT/MAXLIGHTZ/SCREENWIDTH from ./projection.ts, Visplane type + VISPLANE_TOP_UNFILLED from ./renderLimits.ts. Pure arithmetic + typed-array writes, no Win32 or runtime dependencies. Caller owns the framebuffer, the PlaneSpanCache (reused across frames), the view-space tables, and the per-plane state. The visplaneSpans module is the downstream drain for the visplane pool from step 13-008 — R_DrawPlanes iterates the pool and dispatches each non-sky plane through renderVisplaneSpans. Sky planes (picnum === skyFlatNum) are NOT handled here; they route through R_DrawColumn and are scheduled for step 13-010.
- source: Chocolate Doom r_plane.c R_MakeSpans (`void R_MakeSpans(int x, int t1, int b1, int t2, int b2) { while (t1 < t2 && t1 <= b1) { R_MapPlane(t1, spanstart[t1], x - 1); t1++; } while (b1 > b2 && b1 >= t1) { R_MapPlane(b1, spanstart[b1], x - 1); b1--; } while (t2 < t1 && t2 <= b2) { spanstart[t2] = x; t2++; } while (b2 > b1 && b2 >= t2) { spanstart[b2] = x; b2--; } }`), R_MapPlane (`void R_MapPlane(int y, int x1, int x2) { fixed_t distance; fixed_t length; unsigned index; if (planeheight != cachedheight[y]) { cachedheight[y] = planeheight; distance = cacheddistance[y] = FixedMul(planeheight, yslope[y]); ds_xstep = cachedxstep[y] = FixedMul(distance, basexscale); ds_ystep = cachedystep[y] = FixedMul(distance, baseyscale); } else { distance = cacheddistance[y]; ds_xstep = cachedxstep[y]; ds_ystep = cachedystep[y]; } length = FixedMul(distance, distscale[x1]); angle = (viewangle + xtoviewangle[x1]) >> ANGLETOFINESHIFT; ds_xfrac = viewx + FixedMul(finecosine[angle], length); ds_yfrac = -viewy - FixedMul(finesine[angle], length); if (fixedcolormap) ds_colormap = fixedcolormap; else { index = distance >> LIGHTZSHIFT; if (index >= MAXLIGHTZ) index = MAXLIGHTZ - 1; ds_colormap = planezlight[index]; } ds_y = y; ds_x1 = x1; ds_x2 = x2; spanfunc(); }`), R_DrawPlanes non-sky branch (`for (pl = visplanes; pl < lastvisplane; pl++) { if (pl->minx > pl->maxx) continue; if (pl->picnum == skyflatnum) { ... } else { int x; ds_source = W_CacheLumpNum(firstflat + flattranslation[pl->picnum], PU_STATIC); planeheight = abs(pl->height - viewz); light = (pl->lightlevel >> LIGHTSEGSHIFT) + extralight; if (light >= LIGHTLEVELS) light = LIGHTLEVELS - 1; if (light < 0) light = 0; planezlight = zlight[light]; pl->top[pl->maxx + 1] = 0xff; pl->top[pl->minx - 1] = 0xff; stop = pl->maxx + 1; for (x = pl->minx; x <= stop; x++) R_MakeSpans(x, pl->top[x-1], pl->bottom[x-1], pl->top[x], pl->bottom[x]); W_ReleaseLumpNum(firstflat + flattranslation[pl->picnum]); } }`); confirmed against src/render/visplaneSpans.ts (~398 lines with extensive parity-note docstring) and test/render/visplane-span-render.test.ts (41 tests, 1559 expect() calls, 5 describe groups — createPlaneSpanCache, makeSpans column-diff walker, mapPlaneSpan R_MapPlane cache+span emission, renderVisplaneSpans full pipeline, typing exports).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 13-010 (sky-semantics dispatch: R_DrawPlanes branches on `pl->picnum == skyflatnum` BEFORE calling R_MakeSpans; the sky path fetches the sky texture via texturetranslation[skytexture], sets dc_iscale=pspriteiscale, dc_texturemid=skytexturemid, and for each column x in [minx, maxx] computes angle=(viewangle + xtoviewangle[x])>>ANGLETOSKYSHIFT, sets dc_x=x, dc_source=R_GetColumn(skytexture, angle), dc_yl=pl->top[x], dc_yh=pl->bottom[x], and calls colfunc — completely bypassing the makeSpans/mapPlaneSpan pipeline; the visplane pool and top/bottom writes are unchanged, only the draw dispatch differs), 13-011 (flat texture lookup: firstflat+flattranslation[picnum] resolves the flat lump; W_CacheLumpNum loads it as a 4096-byte tile; this module consumes that via ctx.flatSource and assumes the caller has already done the lookup. The lightlevel→planezlight reduction `(pl->lightlevel >> LIGHTSEGSHIFT) + extralight` clamped to [0, LIGHTLEVELS-1] is also a caller responsibility; this module takes planezlight directly), 13-012 (R_DrawPlanes orchestration: the top-level loop over the visplane pool that dispatches each plane through either the sky column path or renderVisplaneSpans; this is the wrapper that owns flat caching, lightlevel resolution, planeheight computation from pl->height - viewz, and the per-plane fixedColormap check), 16-007 / 17-004 (framebuffer CRC: every floor and ceiling pixel in a vanilla frame traces through makeSpans → mapPlaneSpan → rDrawSpan; divergence in any of the four while-loop orders, the close-span `x-1` offset, the per-y cache invalidation, the angle computation via ANGLETOFINESHIFT, the xFrac/yFrac sign conventions, or the LIGHTZSHIFT clamp produces a per-pixel mismatch and fails the frame CRC), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) close-span gets `x-1` not `x` — this is the single most-common off-by-one mistake when porting R_MakeSpans; (b) yFrac is `-viewY - FixedMul(sin, length)` — the leading `-viewY` is the V-axis flip; a buggy port using `viewY + ...` will show flats upside-down; (c) the four while-loop order matters for spanstart[y] when a row transitions from "closed on prev column" to "open on curr column" in the same call — close-top/close-bottom must finish before start-top/start-bottom because a row may appear in both; (d) cachedheight=0 is the initial state and is also a valid planeHeight — callers whose very first plane has planeHeight=0 will see a "false hit" on the cache, but the cached distance/xStep/yStep will also be 0 (FixedMul(0, anything) = 0), so the output is correct by coincidence; (e) boundary sentinel 0xff works because `0xff < t2` is never true for valid t2 < viewHeight <= 200, so close-top skips; `b1 > b2 && b1 >= t1` with b1=0 fails `b1 > b2` for any valid b2>=0, so close-bottom skips; (f) vanilla writes pl->top[minx-1] and pl->top[maxx+1] to 0xff — in C this relies on pad1/pad2/pad3/pad4 bytes in visplane_t; in JS typed arrays this is out-of-bounds, so this module synthesizes the sentinel in local variables instead; output is identical because the only reads of those bytes are in comparisons that 0 never satisfies), 17-010 (final gate: per-pixel floor/ceiling span parity).

## F-137

- fact: Sky rendering semantics (r*sky.h + r_sky.c + r_plane.c R_DrawPlanes sky branch + r_bsp.c R_Subsector ceiling-plane allocation + r_segs.c outdoor-step upper-wall collapse) live in src/render/sky.ts. Exports: 4 constants SKY_FLAT_NAME="F_SKY1" (r_sky.h SKYFLATNAME — the flat lump name the map loader resolves to `skyflatnum`; every visplane whose `picnum === skyflatnum` is routed through the sky draw path), ANGLETOSKYSHIFT=22 (r_sky.h — right shift from a 32-bit BAM angle `(viewangle + xtoviewangle[x])` to a 10-bit (1024-column) virtual sky column index; the shift is unsigned so the full angle_t range wraps into [0, 1024)), SKY_TEXTURE_MID=(SCREENHEIGHT/2)\_FRACUNIT=100<<16=0x640000 (r_sky.c R_InitSkyMap — written once at startup and never updated, so every sky column draws with row 100 pinned at the viewport center regardless of setblocks or detailshift), SKY_COLORMAP_INDEX=0 (r_plane.c `dc_colormap = colormaps` — the first colormap row; sky is always drawn full-bright and vanilla's comment calls out that INVUL inverse mapping does NOT invert the sky as a result); 1 interface SkyRenderContext {skyTexture: PreparedWallTexture, viewAngle: number, xToViewAngle: Int32Array, baseColormap: Uint8Array, iscale: number, textureMid: number, centerY: number, framebuffer: Uint8Array, screenWidth?: number}; 6 functions computePspriteIscale(viewWidth): number, computeSkyIscale(pspriteIscale, detailShift): number, computeSkyColumnAngle(viewAngle, xToViewAngleAtX): number, isSkyVisplane(plane, skyFlatNum): boolean, shouldCollapseSkyUpper(frontCeilingPic, backCeilingPic, skyFlatNum): boolean, renderSkyVisplane(plane, ctx): void. computePspriteIscale returns `(FRACUNIT * SCREENWIDTH / viewWidth) | 0`matching r_main.c R_ExecuteSetViewSize`pspriteiscale = FRACUNIT*SCREENWIDTH/viewwidth`; throws RangeError on viewWidth<=0. At viewWidth=SCREENWIDTH (setblocks=11, high detail) the return is FRACUNIT; at viewWidth=SCREENWIDTH/2 (low-detail full screen) the return is 2*FRACUNIT. computeSkyIscale returns `pspriteIscale >> detailShift` matching r_plane.c `dc_iscale = pspriteiscale >> detailshift`; the arithmetic-right-shift is safe because pspriteIscale is always positive. The net iscale for setblocks=11 is FRACUNIT in BOTH detail modes: high-detail viewWidth=320 → pspriteIscale=FRACUNIT → sky iscale=FRACUNIT; low-detail viewWidth=160 → pspriteIscale=2*FRACUNIT → sky iscale=(2*FRACUNIT)>>1=FRACUNIT. computeSkyColumnAngle returns `((viewAngle + xToViewAngleAtX) >>> 22) | 0` — the unsigned shift (`>>>`) is critical; with a signed shift (`>>`) a viewAngle of 0xFFFFFFFF would produce -1 instead of 0x3FF. The caller passes the result directly to getWallColumn, which masks via PreparedWallTexture.widthMask (256-wide DOOM sky has widthMask=255, so the 10-bit index wraps four times per full rotation — matching vanilla's comment "The default sky map is 256 columns and repeats 4 times on a 320 screen"). isSkyVisplane is a single-line `plane.picnum === skyFlatNum` predicate — the per-frame dispatch test that routes sky-tagged planes to renderSkyVisplane instead of renderVisplaneSpans. shouldCollapseSkyUpper is `frontCeilingPic === skyFlatNum && backCeilingPic === skyFlatNum` — the r_segs.c predicate for "hack to allow height changes in outdoor areas" where the upper wall is NOT drawn and the sky visplane extends from the back sector's ceiling instead of the front sector's. renderSkyVisplane implements r_plane.c R_DrawPlanes sky-branch byte-for-byte: early-returns on `plane.minx > plane.maxx`; iterates `x = plane.minx; x <= plane.maxx; x++`; per-column reads `yl = plane.top[x]`, `yh = plane.bottom[x]`; gates the draw on `yl <= yh` (empty columns silently skipped — matches vanilla `if (dc_yl <= dc_yh)`); computes angle via computeSkyColumnAngle; fetches column via getWallColumn(skyTexture, angle); calls rDrawColumn({x, yl, yh, textureMid, iscale, centerY, source, colormap: baseColormap}, framebuffer, screenWidth). The rDrawColumn call uses the SUPPLIED baseColormap (typically colormaps[0], the full-bright row) regardless of any invulnerability override the caller may have; this is the `dc_colormap = colormaps` pin that makes INVUL not invert the sky. Parity-critical invariants locked byte-for-byte by the 30-test suite (test/render/sky.test.ts, 76 expect() calls, 8 describe groups — sky constants / computePspriteIscale / computeSkyIscale / computeSkyColumnAngle / isSkyVisplane / shouldCollapseSkyUpper / renderSkyVisplane normal path / renderSkyVisplane edge cases): (1) SKY_FLAT_NAME==="F_SKY1", ANGLETOSKYSHIFT===22, SKY_TEXTURE_MID===100<<FRACBITS===0x640000===(SCREENHEIGHT/2)*FRACUNIT, SKY_COLORMAP_INDEX===0; (2) computePspriteIscale at viewWidth=SCREENWIDTH returns FRACUNIT; at viewWidth=SCREENWIDTH/2 returns 2*FRACUNIT; at viewWidth=288 returns `(FRACUNIT * 320 / 288) | 0` = 0x11C71; rejects viewWidth=0 and viewWidth=-1 with RangeError; (3) computeSkyIscale identity at detailShift=0 and halving at detailShift=1; net iscale for setblocks=11 is FRACUNIT in both detail modes; (4) computeSkyColumnAngle: viewAngle=1<<22 → index=1; viewAngle=0x3FF<<22 → index=0x3FF; viewAngle=0xFFFFFFFF → index=0x3FF (not -1, proving `>>>` not `>>`); viewAngle=0x80000000 + xToViewAngle=0x80000000 → index=0 (proving 32-bit modular addition wraps); (5) isSkyVisplane true on picnum match, false otherwise; (6) shouldCollapseSkyUpper true only when both ceilingpics match skyFlatNum (tested with pic=177 for sky, 12/34 for non-sky); (7) renderSkyVisplane normal path draws columns in [minx, maxx] range, reads yl/yh from plane.top/bottom, skips empty columns, writes via supplied colormap (tested with inverting colormap), routes xToViewAngle through computeSkyColumnAngle so different xToViewAngle[x] produces different sky columns per screen column, wraps angle via widthMask (4-wide sky with widthMask=3 produces identical output at angle 0 vs angle 4), viewAngle rotation by 1<<22 advances every column by one sky column (viewAngle=0 → col 0, viewAngle=1<<22 → col 1); (8) renderSkyVisplane edge cases: empty plane (minx>maxx) is a no-op (framebuffer unchanged); column with top>bottom skips drawing that column (tested with a top=3 bottom=0 column sandwiched between valid columns — it stays untouched); single-column plane (minx=maxx) draws exactly one column; iscale=2\*FRACUNIT steps through sky rows 0,2,4,6 instead of 0,1,2,3. Architecture: module imports FRACUNIT from ../core/fixed.ts, rDrawColumn from ./drawPrimitives.ts, SCREENHEIGHT/SCREENWIDTH from ./projection.ts, Visplane type from ./renderLimits.ts, getWallColumn + PreparedWallTexture type from ./wallColumns.ts. Pure arithmetic + framebuffer writes, no Win32 or runtime dependencies. The caller owns the framebuffer, the sky texture, and the view-angle tables; renderSkyVisplane mutates only the framebuffer bytes that the sky column paints. The module is the downstream drain for the sky branch of R_DrawPlanes — the visplane pool from step 13-008 now has its full dispatch covered (non-sky → renderVisplaneSpans from step 13-009, sky → renderSkyVisplane from this step).
- source: Chocolate Doom r_sky.h (`#define SKYFLATNAME "F_SKY1"`, `#define ANGLETOSKYSHIFT 22`, `extern int skytexture; extern int skytexturemid;`), r_sky.c `R_InitSkyMap` (`void R_InitSkyMap (void) { skytexturemid = SCREENHEIGHT/2*FRACUNIT; }`), r_plane.c R_DrawPlanes sky branch (`if (pl->picnum == skyflatnum) { dc_iscale = pspriteiscale>>detailshift; dc_colormap = colormaps; dc_texturemid = skytexturemid; for (x=pl->minx; x <= pl->maxx; x++) { dc_yl = pl->top[x]; dc_yh = pl->bottom[x]; if (dc_yl <= dc_yh) { angle = (viewangle + xtoviewangle[x])>>ANGLETOSKYSHIFT; dc_x = x; dc_source = R_GetColumn(skytexture, angle); colfunc(); } } continue; }`), r_main.c R_ExecuteSetViewSize (`pspriteiscale = FRACUNIT*SCREENWIDTH/viewwidth;`), r_bsp.c R_Subsector (`if (frontsector->ceilingheight > viewz || frontsector->ceilingpic == skyflatnum) { ceilingplane = R_FindPlane(frontsector->ceilingheight, frontsector->ceilingpic, frontsector->lightlevel); } else ceilingplane = NULL;`), r_segs.c R_StoreWallRange outdoor-step hack (`if (frontsector->ceilingpic == skyflatnum && backsector->ceilingpic == skyflatnum) { worldtop = worldhigh; }`), r_segs.c markceiling gate (`if (frontsector->ceilingheight <= viewz && frontsector->ceilingpic != skyflatnum) { markceiling = false; }`); confirmed against src/render/sky.ts (~270 lines with extensive parity-note docstring) and test/render/sky.test.ts (30 tests, 76 expect() calls, 8 describe groups).
- confidence: high

fuzz similarly bypasses the sector colormap for the fuzz column), 14-004 (automap draws the sky-capped sector walls as plain one-sided lines — the automap does NOT render the sky itself; compatibility surface is that the sky visplane still exists in the pool but renderSkyVisplane is not called on automap frames), 16-007 / 17-004 (framebuffer CRC: every sky-capped pixel in a vanilla frame traces through renderSkyVisplane → rDrawColumn; divergence in the angle computation, the texture-mid pin, the iscale derivation, or the colormap pin produces a per-pixel mismatch and fails the frame CRC — most common porting mistakes are (a) using signed shift `>>` instead of `>>>` in computeSkyColumnAngle, producing wrong columns when viewangle wraps around 0xFFFFFFFF; (b) forgetting the `dc_colormap = colormaps` pin and applying the sector lightlevel, causing the sky to dim at distance; (c) updating `skytexturemid` from the view-height derivation instead of pinning it at 100\*FRACUNIT, causing the sky to shift vertically as the status bar appears/disappears), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) INVUL powerup does NOT invert the sky — the `dc_colormap = colormaps` assignment happens BEFORE the per-column loop, overriding any fixedcolormap override the sector might set; (e) sky texture wraps via the wall-texture widthMask, so a 256-wide sky at angle 256 draws column 0 just like angle 0 — four full wraps per rotation), 17-010 (final gate: per-pixel sky parity against the reference executable).

## F-138

- fact: BinaryReader (src/core/binaryReader.ts) rejects negative `byteLength` arguments to `readBytes` and `readAscii` via a centralized check in `#boundsCheck` that throws RangeError. Without this guard, a negative byteLength passes the `offset + byteCount > buffer.length` check (since it makes the left side smaller), then `Buffer.subarray(offset, offset + negative)` returns an empty buffer while `this.#offset += negative` silently rewinds the cursor — a parser consuming an untrusted WAD lump size could retreat past already-parsed bytes and desynchronize. The guard also centralizes the negative check for `skip`, so the explicit guard that was previously duplicated in `skip` has been removed. Test coverage: test/core/binary-reader.test.ts now asserts that `readBytes(-1)` and `readAscii(-1)` throw RangeError AND leave the cursor untouched, and that `readBytes(0)` / `readAscii(0)` return empty values without advancing the cursor.
- source: src/core/binaryReader.ts `#boundsCheck` (`if (byteCount < 0) throw new RangeError(...)` leading the existing offset+count>length check), src/core/binaryReader.ts `readBytes` / `readAscii` / `skip` (all route through `#boundsCheck`), test/core/binary-reader.test.ts (4 new tests added under the readBytes / readAscii describe blocks).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 05-001 / 05-009 / 16-003 (WAD parsers that read lump sizes and demo headers from untrusted data must trust the reader to throw rather than silently rewind on negative sizes; this guarantee removes the need for callers to pre-validate each length field), 17-010 (final gate: parsers for save games, demos, and WAD lumps all funnel through BinaryReader, so the negative-size rejection is part of the trust boundary between untrusted file bytes and the parity-critical game state).

## F-139

- fact: Sprite projection (r_things.c `R_ProjectSprite` / `R_NewVisSprite` / `R_ClearSprites` plus the `MINZ` + `MAXVISSPRITES` + `FF_FRAMEMASK` + `FF_FULLBRIGHT` constants) lives in src/render/spriteProjection.ts. Exports: 4 constants MINZ=FRACUNIT*4=0x40000 (r_things.c near-clip threshold; any `tz < MINZ` is silently rejected), MAXVISSPRITES=128 (r_things.c pool size — vanilla `vissprite_t vissprites[MAXVISSPRITES]`, inlined literal not a named `#define` in chocolate-doom), FF_FRAMEMASK=0x7FFF (p_pspr.h low-15-bit frame mask), FF_FULLBRIGHT=0x8000 (p_pspr.h bit-15 full-bright flag); 7 interfaces SpriteMetrics {offset, topOffset, width: Int32Array}, SpriteFrame {rotate: boolean, lump: readonly number[8], flip: readonly boolean[8]}, SpriteDef {numFrames, frames: readonly SpriteFrame[]}, VisSprite {x1, x2, gx, gy, gz, gzt, startFrac, scale, xIscale, textureMid, patch, colormap: Uint8Array|null, mobjFlags}, VisSpritePool {sprites: readonly VisSprite[128], overflow: VisSprite, count}, ProjectableThing {x, y, z, angle, sprite, frame, flags} (structural decoupling from Mobj for unit testing), SpriteProjectionContext {viewX, viewY, viewZ, viewCos, viewSin, projection, centerXFrac, viewWidth, detailShift, sprites, spriteMetrics, fixedColormap: Uint8Array|null, spriteLights: readonly Uint8Array[], colormaps: Uint8Array}; 4 functions createVisSpritePool()→VisSpritePool, clearSprites(pool)→void, newVisSprite(pool)→VisSprite (returns pool.overflow when count===MAXVISSPRITES — vanilla silently drops overflow sprites into a shared scratch slot), projectSprite(thing, ctx, pool)→VisSprite|null. Internal helper pointToAngleFromView(dx, dy)→Angle mirrors r_main.c R_PointToAngle with caller-supplied `(x - viewx, y - viewy)` preamble. Parity invariants locked byte-for-byte by the 36-test suite (test/render/sprite-projection.test.ts, 869 expect() calls, 10 describe groups): (1) View-space transform order: `trX = thing.x - viewX`, `trY = thing.y - viewY`; `gxt = FixedMul(trX, viewCos)`, `gyt = -FixedMul(trY, viewSin)` (gyt NEGATED — this is the load-bearing sign on viewsin that produces a forward-axis `tz = gxt - gyt`); second pair flips both: `gxt = -FixedMul(trX, viewSin)`, `gyt = FixedMul(trY, viewCos)`, then `tx = -(gyt + gxt)`. (2) Rejection gate order: (a) `tz < MINZ` (tested with tz = 1*FRACUNIT rejected, tz = -200*FRACUNIT rejected, tz = MINZ accepted); (b) `|tx| > tz << 2` (tested with thing at (100<<16, 500<<16) where tx=-500<<16 exceeds 4*tz=400<<16); (c) `x1 > viewWidth` (strict `>`, not `>=` — tested with narrow viewport=80 and sprite pushed off the right); (d) `x2 < 0` (tested with narrow width=1<<16 and thing at +380<<16). (3) Sprite rotation formula: `rot = (((ang - thing.angle + 0x90000000) >>> 0) >>> 29) & 7` — UNSIGNED shift `>>>` on the full 32-bit angle_t wraparound; `0x90000000` = `(ANG45/2)*9` biases the 45-degree sector reduction so viewer-facing lands in slot 0. With viewAngle=0 and thing directly ahead (ang=0): thing.angle=ANG180→rot=0 (facing viewer), thing.angle=0→rot=4 (back), thing.angle=ANG90→rot=2 (right side), thing.angle=ANG270→rot=6 (left side). (4) `rotate === false` always picks lump[0]/flip[0] regardless of angle. (5) `vis.scale = xscale << detailShift` (low-detail doubles the per-column scale; tested with detailShift=1 → scale = xscale*2). (6) `vis.xIscale = FixedDiv(FRACUNIT, xscale)` negated when flip; startFrac = 0 for non-flipped, `width[lump] - 1` for flipped. (7) Clip adjustment: `vis.x1 = max(0, x1)`, `vis.x2 = min(viewWidth - 1, x2)`; when x1 was clamped (rawX1 < 0), `vis.startFrac += vis.xIscale * (vis.x1 - x1)`to re-sync the texture U at the first painted column. (8) Colormap priority order: (1st)`MF_SHADOW`flag (0x40000) → null, even when fixedColormap and FF_FULLBRIGHT are also set; (2nd) fixedColormap override (invul / light-amp) → that row, even when FF_FULLBRIGHT is set; (3rd) FF_FULLBRIGHT → colormaps (row 0 of COLORMAP); (4th) default`spriteLights[xscale >> (LIGHTSCALESHIFT - detailShift)]`clamped to MAXLIGHTSCALE - 1 = 47. The shift`(12 - detailShift)`means low-detail uses`xscale >> 11`instead of`xscale >> 12`, which DOUBLES the computed index before clamping — so light-diminishing ramps twice as fast in screen-column terms but matches vanilla's per-world-distance behavior because low-detail also halves the viewport width. (9) Frame index lookup uses `frame & FF_FRAMEMASK`to mask off the full-bright bit (tested with`frame = 1 | FF_FULLBRIGHT`selecting frames[1]). (10) Pool overflow: once 128 sprites are projected, the 129th`projectSprite`call returns and fills`pool.overflow`; `pool.count`does NOT advance past MAXVISSPRITES. Architecture: module imports Angle/ANG90/ANG180/ANG270/angleWrap from ../core/angle.ts, FRACBITS/FRACUNIT/fixedDiv/fixedMul from ../core/fixed.ts, slopeDiv/tantoangle from ../core/trig.ts, LIGHTSCALESHIFT/MAXLIGHTSCALE from ./projection.ts. Pure arithmetic with no Win32, renderer-draw, or runtime dependencies. The caller owns the sprite tables (SpriteDef[] + SpriteMetrics) and the view-frame state (SpriteProjectionContext); projectSprite populates the next pool slot via newVisSprite and returns the same reference. Module is the upstream source for phase-13 sprite sort/clip/draw stages (13-012 sprite-sort-and-clip consumes`VisSprite`ordered by`scale`desc; 13-013 masked-midtextures reuses the`textureMid`/`xIscale`/`startFrac`/`colormap`set; 13-014 fuzz-and-invisibility reads`colormap === null` as the MF_SHADOW signal).
- source: Chocolate Doom r_things.c `R_ProjectSprite` (view-space transform, 6 rejection gates, rotation formula, scale/flip/clip-adjust, colormap priority), r_things.c `R_NewVisSprite` (`vissprite_p < &vissprites[MAXVISSPRITES] ? vissprite_p++ : &overflowsprite`), r_things.c `R_ClearSprites` (`vissprite_p = vissprites;`), p_pspr.h `#define FF_FULLBRIGHT 0x8000` and `#define FF_FRAMEMASK 0x7fff`, r_defs.h `vissprite_t` struct (all 14 fields preserved), r_defs.h `spriteframe_t` struct (rotate + lump[8] + flip[8]), r_defs.h `spritedef_t` struct (numframes + spriteframe_t \*spriteframes), r_main.c `R_PointToAngle` (full 8-octant `tantoangle[SlopeDiv(y, x)]` implementation); confirmed against src/render/spriteProjection.ts (~550 lines with exhaustive docstring), test/render/sprite-projection.test.ts (36 tests, 869 expect() calls, 10 describe groups).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 13-012 (sprite-sort-and-clip consumes the VisSprite record by `scale` descending, builds the doubly-linked vsprsortedhead list, and runs R_DrawVisSprite with per-column clip bounds from the seg silhouette; the colormap/patch/startFrac/xIscale/scale/textureMid fields this step writes are read unmodified there), 13-013 (masked-midtextures reuse the exact rDrawMaskedColumn parameter tuple `{textureMid, iscale=xIscale, startFrac, colormap}` this step populates for visprites — the masked midtexture is just a VisSprite with `patch = midtexturenum` and scale lookup via the seg's scale1/scale2 pair), 13-014 (fuzz-and-invisibility reads `vis.colormap === null` as the MF_SHADOW signal and routes those columns through R_DrawFuzzColumn instead of R_DrawColumn — the colormap priority order established here is the source of truth for when fuzz fires), 17-010 (per-pixel parity gate: every visible monster / projectile / pickup pixel in a vanilla frame traces through `projectSprite → newVisSprite → draw` so divergence in any of the 10 invariants above produces framebuffer CRC mismatches — most common porting mistakes are (a) signed shift `>>` in the rotation formula instead of `>>>` — breaks when `ang - thing.angle` wraps negative, producing wrong sprite patch; (b) flipping the `gyt = -FixedMul(trY, viewSin)` sign — produces tz in the wrong half-plane and clips every sprite; (c) using `>=` instead of `>` on the `x1 > viewWidth` gate — loses the last column of sprites touching the right edge; (d) forgetting the `vis.startFrac += xIscale * (vis.x1 - x1)` clip adjustment — produces garbage texture sampling on left-clipped sprites; (e) checking FF_FULLBRIGHT before fixedColormap in the priority order — inverts invul behavior on muzzle-flash frames).

## F-140

- fact: Sprite sort-and-clip (r*things.c `R_SortVisSprites` + `R_DrawSprite` clip phase + `R_DrawMasked` orchestrator + r_main.c `R_PointOnSegSide`) lives in src/render/spriteClip.ts (~563 lines with exhaustive parity docstring). Exports: 5 silhouette/sentinel constants SIL_NONE=0, SIL_BOTTOM=1, SIL_TOP=2, SIL_BOTH=3 (r_defs.h `SIL*_`bit flags where`top | bottom === both`), CLIP_UNSET=-2 (r_things.c R_DrawSprite sentinel for clipbot/cliptop "first-write-wins"), CLIP_TOP_DEFAULT=-1 (the `-1`that replaces any residual CLIP_UNSET in cliptop when no seg wrote it); 3 interfaces SpriteClipDrawSeg {x1, x2, scale1, scale2, silhouette, bsilheight, tsilheight, sprtopclip: Int16Array|null, sprbottomclip: Int16Array|null, maskedtexturecol: Int16Array|null, v1x, v1y, v2x, v2y} (structural decoupling from a full DrawSeg — carries only the 14 fields sprite-clip reads), RenderMaskedSegRange callback type`(ds, x1, x2) => void`(injected masked-midtexture renderer invoked on behind-sprite segs AND on drawMasked's final pass), DrawVisSprite callback type`(spr, clipbot, cliptop) => void`(injected visprite renderer that receives the per-column clip arrays produced by clipVisSprite); 1 buffer-factory interface SpriteClipBuffers {clipbot, cliptop, mfloorclip, mceilingclip: Int16Array[viewWidth]} (the four scratch arrays R_DrawSprite consumes); 4 functions createSpriteClipBuffers(viewWidth)→SpriteClipBuffers, pointOnSegSide(x, y, ds)→0|1 (R_PointOnSegSide with vertical/horizontal shortcuts + sign-bit XOR quick decision + FixedMul cross-product fallback), sortVisSprites(pool)→VisSprite[] (returns a new array ordered ascending by scale — farthest first for painter's-algorithm back-to-front draw — using a stable sort to match vanilla selection-sort first-match tie-break), clipVisSprite(spr, drawsegs, buffers, viewHeight, renderMaskedSegRange)→void (the R_DrawSprite clip phase: writes per-column clipbot/cliptop for the sprite via reverse-allocation drawseg scan; invokes renderMaskedSegRange for behind-sprite segs with masked-texture columns; leaves unmodified slots at CLIP_UNSET which the caller replaces with`viewHeight`for clipbot and`-1`for cliptop), drawMasked(pool, drawsegs, buffers, viewHeight, renderMaskedSegRange, drawVisSprite)→void (R_DrawMasked orchestrator: sorts sprites, for each sprite resets clipbot/cliptop to CLIP_UNSET, calls clipVisSprite, finalizes remaining CLIP_UNSET cells via the viewHeight/-1 defaults, invokes drawVisSprite; then for each drawseg not already fully consumed by a sprite's behind-sprite branch, invokes renderMaskedSegRange with the full`[ds.x1, ds.x2]`range — vanilla's "draw any remaining masked midtextures" pass). Parity invariants locked byte-for-byte by the 36-test suite (test/render/sprite-sort-clip.test.ts, 166 expect() calls, 6 describe groups): (1) sentinel/silhouette constants match r_defs.h/r_things.c exactly; (2) createSpriteClipBuffers returns zero-initialized Int16Array[viewWidth] × 4 with no aliasing between the four arrays; (3) pointOnSegSide: vertical shortcut (ldx===0) returns`x <= v1x ? 1 - (ldy > 0 ? 1 : 0) : (ldy < 0 ? 1 : 0)`, horizontal shortcut (ldy===0) returns `y <= v1y ? (ldx < 0 ? 1 : 0) : 1 - (ldx < 0 ? 1 : 0)`, sign-bit XOR quick decision when dx and dy have opposite signs from ldx/ldy, FixedMul cross-product fallback `(dy >> FRACBITS) _ (ldx >> FRACBITS) - (ldy >> FRACBITS) \* (dx >> FRACBITS) < 0 ? 1 : 0`; (4) sortVisSprites ascending by scale (10 < 100 < 1000 order), empty pool → [], equal-scale preserves pool allocation order (stable sort matching vanilla first-match); (5) clipVisSprite reverse-allocation walk (last drawseg in array visited first); disjoint-filter skips drawsegs with `ds.x1 > spr.x2 || ds.x2 < spr.x1`; no-silhouette-no-masked-column skip `ds.silhouette === 0 && ds.maskedtexturecol === null`; first-write-wins guard via `clipbot[x] === CLIP_UNSET`/`cliptop[x] === CLIP_UNSET`checks before writing, so a nearer seg's sprtopclip value over-rides a farther seg's — the LATER drawseg in the reverse walk CANNOT overwrite the EARLIER (nearer) seg's write; scale comparison uses`max(scale1, scale2)`and`min(scale1, scale2)`per-seg because scale varies across [x1,x2]; behind-sprite branch`scale < spr.scale || (lowscale < spr.scale && pointOnSegSide === 0)`fires the renderMaskedSegRange callback for`[max(ds.x1, spr.x1), min(ds.x2, spr.x2)]`and short-circuits silhouette clipping (the sprite paints OVER the seg's masked texture); silhouette adjustment`silhouette &= ~SIL_BOTTOM`when spr.gz >= ds.bsilheight (sprite's feet at or above seg's bottom silhouette),`silhouette &= ~SIL_TOP`when spr.gzt <= ds.tsilheight (sprite's top at or below seg's top silhouette) — if both clears fire, the silhouette becomes SIL_NONE and the seg has nothing to contribute; per-column writes: if`(silhouette & SIL_BOTTOM) && ds.sprbottomclip`then`clipbot[x] === CLIP_UNSET → clipbot[x] = ds.sprbottomclip[x]`, same pattern for SIL_TOP+sprtopclip; (6) drawMasked orchestrator: iterates sorted sprites; for each sprite resets clipbot[x]/cliptop[x] to CLIP_UNSET across the sprite's [x1, x2] range; calls clipVisSprite; finalizes remaining CLIP_UNSET as clipbot[x] = viewHeight and cliptop[x] = CLIP_TOP_DEFAULT; calls drawVisSprite with the final clipbot/cliptop; after all sprites, iterates drawsegs in forward order and for each seg with `maskedtexturecol !== null`that was NOT already rendered by a behind-sprite branch, calls renderMaskedSegRange for the full`[ds.x1, ds.x2]` range (the vanilla "post-sprite masked midtextures" pass). Architecture: module imports FRACBITS from ../core/fixed.ts, VisSprite + VisSpritePool + MAXVISSPRITES from ./spriteProjection.ts. Pure arithmetic + callback invocation, no Win32, no direct framebuffer writes, no draw-primitive dependencies. The caller owns the drawseg pool, the visprite pool, the scratch buffers, and the two render callbacks; the module produces the per-column clip arrays the DrawVisSprite callback reads to suppress the sprite's column rendering where a seg silhouette covers it. Module is the downstream consumer of sprite-projection (13-011 populates the pool that sortVisSprites walks) AND the upstream driver for masked-midtextures (13-013 defines the RenderMaskedSegRange callback this module invokes on behind-sprite segs and on the post-sprite pass) AND for the sprite-draw primitive (13-014 defines the DrawVisSprite callback this module invokes for each sprite after clipVisSprite populates clipbot/cliptop).
- source: Chocolate Doom r_things.c `R_SortVisSprites` (selection-sort by `ds->scale` descending for the doubly-linked vsprsortedhead list — the implementation here sorts ascending by scale using Array.prototype.sort with stable comparator, which produces the same back-to-front painter order when iterating the returned array in index order), r_things.c `R_DrawSprite` (the clip phase — resets clipbot/cliptop to -2, reverse-walks drawsegs, applies the disjoint/no-contribution filter, scale/lowscale comparison, behind-sprite branch with R_RenderMaskedSegRange + continue, silhouette adjustment via bsilheight/tsilheight, per-column first-write-wins writes into clipbot/cliptop via sprbottomclip/sprtopclip, final CLIP_UNSET → viewheight/-1 replacement before R_DrawVisSprite call), r_things.c `R_DrawMasked` (orchestrator — sorts sprites via R_SortVisSprites, iterates sorted list back-to-front calling R_DrawSprite then R_DrawVisSprite, then final pass that calls R_RenderMaskedSegRange for any drawseg with `maskedtexturecol` whose range was not already rendered by the sprite loop's behind-sprite branch, then renders player weapon sprites via R_DrawPlayerSprites), r_main.c `R_PointOnSegSide` (vertical/horizontal shortcuts and sign-bit XOR quick decision with FixedMul cross-product fallback — the four-case pattern that makes this function a hot-path constant-time classifier), r_defs.h `SIL_NONE=0 / SIL_BOTTOM=1 / SIL_TOP=2 / SIL_BOTH=3` (silhouette bit flags), r_defs.h `drawseg_t` (x1/x2/scale1/scale2/silhouette/bsilheight/tsilheight/sprtopclip/sprbottomclip/maskedtexturecol fields preserved structurally in SpriteClipDrawSeg), r_things.c `MAXVISSPRITES=128` (pool capacity inherited from ./spriteProjection.ts); confirmed against src/render/spriteClip.ts (~563 lines with exhaustive docstring), test/render/sprite-sort-clip.test.ts (36 tests, 166 expect() calls, 6 describe groups — constants / createSpriteClipBuffers / pointOnSegSide / sortVisSprites / clipVisSprite / drawMasked).

the `[r1, r2]` sub-range used in the behind-sprite branch is narrower than the full `[ds.x1, ds.x2]` pass so the callback must NOT assume `ds.x1`/`ds.x2` as the column bounds), 13-014 fuzz-and-invisibility (defines the concrete DrawVisSprite callback that routes `vis.colormap === null` columns through rDrawFuzzColumn instead of rDrawColumn — the clipbot/cliptop arrays produced by this module gate which rows get drawn regardless of which column primitive is selected), 14-004 automap (automap path does NOT invoke drawMasked — sprites and masked midtextures are only rendered on the world view, the automap is a separate overlay pass), 17-004 (per-sprite and per-seg-midtexture framebuffer CRC gate — the reverse-drawseg walk order, the first-write-wins guard, and the behind-sprite branch conditions all trace into the per-pixel output; flipping any invariant produces visible z-fighting or missing/extra pixels on sprite-seg overlaps), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) the selection-sort stable tie-break on equal-scale sprites matches vanilla's first-allocated-wins visual layering when two sprites project to the exact same scale — subtle in the wild but load-bearing for demo-compat; (b) the `CLIP_UNSET = -2` sentinel is distinct from `CLIP_TOP_DEFAULT = -1` — confusing the two would cause viewHeight to be written as top-clip leaving no visible sprite pixels; (c) the `scale < spr.scale` OR-branch fires even when lowscale > spr.scale, meaning a seg whose NEAREST column is farther than the sprite is always behind the sprite regardless of its farthest column; (d) the `pointOnSegSide === 0` check is "sprite on FRONT side" — vanilla's `!R_PointOnSegSide` idiom — and must pair with `lowscale < spr.scale` (the seg's farthest column is closer than the sprite) to fire the behind-sprite branch for side-clipping segs), 17-010 (final parity gate: every sprite pixel in a vanilla frame is decided by this module's clipbot/cliptop output; any mismatch in the drawseg walk direction, the scale/lowscale comparison, the pointOnSegSide sign convention, or the first-write-wins guard produces per-pixel framebuffer divergence at the sprite-seg overlap).

## F-141

- fact: Masked midtexture rendering (r*segs.c `R_RenderMaskedSegRange` + r_things.c `R_DrawMaskedColumn` for the non-fuzz path) lives in src/render/maskedTextures.ts (~363 lines with exhaustive parity-note docstring). Exports: 1 constant MAXSHORT=0x7fff=32767 (signed int16 max, mirrors doomtype.h `MAXSHORT` and r_segs.c's `maskedtexturecol[dc_x] = MAXSHORT` done-flag); 2 interfaces MaskedDrawSeg extends SpriteClipDrawSeg + {scaleStep, textureMid, midTextureWidthMask, wallLights: readonly Uint8Array[], fixedColormap: Uint8Array|null, maskedColumnFor: (col: number) => PatchColumn} and MaskedSegRenderContext {framebuffer, screenWidth?=SCREENWIDTH, centerY, centerYFrac}; 1 function renderMaskedSegRange(seg, x1, x2, ctx)→void. The function walks columns in [x1, x2] inclusive: (a) null-guards maskedtexturecol/sprtopclip/sprbottomclip (early-return on null — vanilla allocates all three for any seg with a masked midtexture, but defensive guard preserves safety); (b) computes `spryscale = seg.scale1 + (x1 - seg.x1) * scaleStep`at entry, advances by scaleStep per column (before OR after each column regardless of draw/skip — vanilla's`spryscale += rw_scalestep`runs unconditionally outside the done-flag check); (c) per column, skips when`maskedtexturecol[x] === MAXSHORT`(done-flag from prior pass); (d) resolves colormap via`fixedColormap !== null ? fixedColormap : wallLights[spryscale >> LIGHTSCALESHIFT clamped to [0, MAXLIGHTSCALE-1]]` — vanilla clamps only upper-bound (`index >= MAXLIGHTSCALE → MAXLIGHTSCALE-1`), this implementation adds a lower clamp to 0 as a JS safety guard (vanilla scenes never produce a negative bucket because spryscale > 0 in practice); (e) computes `iscale = 0xffffffff / (spryscale >>> 0) | 0`— the unsigned 32-bit divide matches vanilla byte-for-byte including the overflow pattern where`0xffffffff / 1 | 0 === -1`when truncated to int32; (f) computes`sprtopscreen = centerYFrac - fixedMul(textureMid, spryscale)`(the fixed-point screen row of texture row 0 before per-post adjust); (g) fetches the PatchColumn via`seg.maskedColumnFor(texCol & widthMask)`— the two's-complement AND handles negative texCol correctly because JS`&`interprets operands as int32; (h) iterates each PatchPost in the column:`topscreen = sprtopscreen + spryscale*topDelta`, `bottomscreen = topscreen + spryscale*length`, `yl = (topscreen + FRACUNIT - 1) >> FRACBITS`(ceiling),`yh = (bottomscreen - 1) >> FRACBITS`(floor minus one); (i) clips`yh >= sprbottomclip[x] → yh = sprbottomclip[x] - 1`FIRST, then`yl <= sprtopclip[x] → yl = sprtopclip[x] + 1`SECOND (vanilla order); (j) if`yl <= yh`, paints the framebuffer via inline drawPostColumn with `dc_texturemid = textureMid - (post.topDelta << FRACBITS)`so per-post`frac`accumulator indexes`post.pixels[0..length-1]`regardless of post position within the texture; (k) sets`maskedtexturecol[x] = MAXSHORT`AFTER the post loop to flag the column done for subsequent drawMasked passes. The inline drawPostColumn helper mirrors r_draw.c R_DrawColumn WITHOUT the`& 127`composite mask — the mask is safe to omit because yl/yh clipping keeps`frac >> FRACBITS`in`[0, post.length-1]`throughout the inner loop; mask is only needed for composite wall columns (128-row fixed-height) which are not masked posts. The do/while loop structure matches vanilla's`do { ... } while (count--)`where`count = yh - yl`so the loop runs`count+1`times. Parity invariants locked byte-for-byte by the 31-test suite (test/render/masked-midtextures.test.ts, 326 expect() calls, 10 describe groups): (1) MAXSHORT constant is 0x7fff=32767 and round-trips through Int16Array; (2) null guards for maskedtexturecol/sprtopclip/sprbottomclip return early without side effects; (3) MAXSHORT-flagged columns are skipped and not overwritten; empty x1>x2 range is a no-op; (4) single-post draw paints pixels at the expected rows (topDelta=4 length=4 → rows 4..7 with pixels 0x11/0x22/0x33/0x44) and writes MAXSHORT done-flag after; (5) multi-post column paints each post at its topDelta offset (post1 at topDelta=2 rows 2-3, post2 at topDelta=5 rows 5-6); empty column (zero posts) still sets MAXSHORT; (6) sprtopclip raises yl to sprtopclip+1, sprbottomclip lowers yh to sprbottomclip-1, full closure (topClip >= bottomClip) suppresses draw and still flags done; (7) spryscale advances by scaleStep across columns regardless of MAXSHORT skip; (x1 - seg.x1) * scaleStep offset applied when x1 is inside seg range; (8) widthMask wraps texCol via`col & widthMask`(covers positive wrap via 130 & 127 = 2, negative wrap via -1 & 63 = 63 two's-complement, and non-power-of-2 wrap); (9) colormap selection (fixedColormap override beats wallLights at any scale, wallLights[5] selected for scale = 5<<LIGHTSCALESHIFT, clamp to MAXLIGHTSCALE-1=47 when scale is very large, bucket=0 selected when scale is small); (10) post position arithmetic (post topDelta shifts yl by spryscale \_ topDelta when textureMid = centerYFrac, per-post dc_texturemid subtracts`topDelta << FRACBITS` so frac at yl maps to pixels[0], clipped yl advances frac into the post so first painted pixel is at the clip boundary, sprtopscreen = centerYFrac - FixedMul(textureMid, spryscale) shifts position by textureMid); (11) scale-varying draw (doubled spryscale stretches the post vertically by ~2); (12) default screenWidth falls back to SCREENWIDTH=320 when ctx.screenWidth is omitted. Architecture: module imports fixedMul/FRACBITS/FRACUNIT from ../core/fixed.ts, PatchColumn type from ./patchDraw.ts, LIGHTSCALESHIFT/MAXLIGHTSCALE/SCREENWIDTH from ./projection.ts, SpriteClipDrawSeg type from ./spriteClip.ts. Pure arithmetic + typed-array writes, no Win32 or runtime dependencies. Caller owns the drawseg list, per-seg post resolver (`maskedColumnFor` callback — plumbed from the midtexture's DecodedPatch columns or from a composite-column chain rebuilt by R_GenerateComposite), the per-frame view state, and the integration with drawMasked from ./spriteClip.ts that dispatches the callback.
- source: Chocolate Doom r*segs.c `R_RenderMaskedSegRange` (spryscale init from ds.scale1 + (x1-ds.x1)\_ds.scalestep, per-column loop with maskedtexturecol[x]!=MAXSHORT gate, colormap/iscale/sprtopscreen/texCol computation, R_DrawMaskedColumn call, `maskedtexturecol[dc_x] = MAXSHORT` done-flag, `spryscale += rw_scalestep` advance), r_things.c `R_DrawMaskedColumn` (basetexturemid save/restore pattern, per-post topscreen/bottomscreen/yl/yh computation, sprbottomclip/sprtopclip clipping order, per-post `dc_texturemid -= column->topdelta << FRACBITS` adjustment, colfunc() call, `for (column = (column_t *)((byte *)column + column->length + 4)`post chain walk), r_draw.c`R_DrawColumn`(do/while inner loop with`frac += fracstep`and`*dest = dc_colormap[dc_source[(frac >> FRACBITS) & 127]]`mask — the mask is OMITTED in this module because post-based source is length-exact rather than composite 128-row-padded), doomtype.h`#define MAXSHORT ((short)0x7fff)`(done-flag sentinel), r_data.c`texturewidthmask[]`(largest power-of-2 ≤ width minus one —`compulateTextureWidthMask`in ./wallColumns.ts produces identical values), r_defs.h`column_t`struct (topdelta/length/pixels — structurally preserved as PatchPost in ./patchDraw.ts), r_segs.c`ds->x1, ds->x2, ds->scale1, ds->scalestep, ds->maskedtexturecol, ds->sprtopclip, ds->sprbottomclip` drawseg fields consumed here via MaskedDrawSeg interface; confirmed against src/render/maskedTextures.ts (~363 lines with exhaustive docstring), test/render/masked-midtextures.test.ts (31 tests, 326 expect() calls, 10 describe groups).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 13-014 fuzz-and-invisibility (vanilla's R_DrawFuzzColumn is the third colfunc alongside R_DrawColumn and R_DrawTranslatedColumn — fuzz-rendering reads the SAME dc_yl/dc_yh/dc_iscale/dc_texturemid context this module populates but substitutes a fuzz-offset table for the source read; a masked midtexture with `MF_SHADOW`-equivalent semantics would route through that primitive instead of drawPostColumn but the outer iteration structure is identical), 14-002 composite-textures (when a midtexture is multi-patch, R_GenerateComposite builds a single composite PatchColumn chain per texture column; the `maskedColumnFor` callback provides the indirection point for the caller to return composite chains vs. raw single-patch DecodedPatch columns), 17-004 (per-pixel parity gate — every masked midtexture pixel in a vanilla frame traces through R_RenderMaskedSegRange + R_DrawMaskedColumn so the four invariants here — spryscale advance, MAXSHORT done-flag, post clip order yh-then-yl, per-post dc_texturemid — must match bit-exactly against the reference frame CRCs), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) iscale = 0xffffffff / spryscale is an UNSIGNED divide — vanilla's `dc_iscale = 0xffffffffu / (unsigned)spryscale`; JS `(0xffffffff / (spryscale >>> 0)) | 0` preserves the same bit pattern including the negative-int32 truncation for small spryscale; (b) texCol & widthMask wrap via JS bitwise AND works for negative texCol because JS treats operands as two's-complement int32; (c) dc_texturemid per-post is basetexturemid - (post.topDelta << FRACBITS) — vanilla saves basetexturemid, modifies dc_texturemid per post, and restores at exit; this module recomputes per post without mutation so the seg.textureMid is never aliased; (d) the inner column-draw loop omits the & 127 composite mask — vanilla's R_DrawColumn has it because wall composite columns are 128-row padded, but post-based source is length-exact so the mask is both unnecessary and arguably incorrect for posts with length != 128; the yl/yh clipping guarantees frac/FRACUNIT stays in [0, post.length-1]; (e) MAXSHORT=0x7fff as a done-flag is distinct from -1 or 0 — using any other sentinel would allow the drawMasked post-sprite pass to re-draw columns already rendered by the clipVisSprite behind-sprite branch, producing double-writes; (f) the post clip order yh-then-yl matches vanilla; reversing would not change output for non-overlapping clips but could produce off-by-one for degenerate fully-closed columns where topclip >= bottomclip).

## F-142

- fact: Fuzz column primitive (r_draw.c `R_DrawFuzzColumn` + the MF_SHADOW-triggered `vis->colormap = NULL` branch in r_things.c `R_ProjectSprite` that routes a sprite through the fuzz primitive — the vanilla "partial invisibility" dither used by the Spectre monster and the Blur Sphere powerup) lives in src/render/fuzz.ts (~222 lines with exhaustive parity docstring). Exports: 3 constants FUZZ_TABLE_SIZE=50 (r_draw.c `#define FUZZTABLE 50` — the counter wraps back to 0 after emitting the 50th entry), FUZZ_COLORMAP_INDEX=6 (r_draw.c uses `colormaps[6*256 + dest[fuzzoffset[fuzzpos]]]` — colormap row 6 of the 32-ramp COLORMAP lump, a mid-brightness light level that makes the fuzz overlay visible regardless of the underlying sector lightlevel), FUZZ_COLORMAP_OFFSET=1536 (`6 * 256` — byte offset into the `colormaps` lump for the fuzz ramp); 1 frozen table FUZZ_OFFSETS (50 entries of `+1` or `-1` mirroring the vanilla `fuzzoffset[FUZZTABLE]` table — vanilla stores `±SCREENWIDTH` so `dest[fuzzoffset[fuzzpos]]` is a one-row-above/below pointer-arithmetic access; this module stores the row sign and multiplies by `screenWidth` at call time so the primitive works with any framebuffer stride; the sequence is byte-for-byte vanilla including the cluster breaks that defeat a naive alternating pattern); 1 interface FuzzColumnJob {x, yl, yh, viewHeight, colormaps: Uint8Array}; 4 functions getFuzzPos()→number, setFuzzPos(pos)→void (validates integer in [0, 50) and throws RangeError otherwise — test-only pin helper, vanilla never writes the counter outside the increment inside R_DrawFuzzColumn), resetFuzzPos()→void (counter back to 0, matching vanilla's static initializer), rDrawFuzzColumn(job, framebuffer, screenWidth=SCREENWIDTH)→void. Parity invariants locked byte-for-byte by the 35-test suite (test/render/fuzz.test.ts, 919 expect() calls, 9 describe groups): (1) FUZZ_TABLE_SIZE=50, FUZZ_COLORMAP_INDEX=6, FUZZ_COLORMAP_OFFSET=1536=6*256; (2) FUZZ_OFFSETS has exactly 50 entries all ±1 matching vanilla fuzzoffset[] sign sequence byte-for-byte, frozen via Object.freeze (strict-mode mutation throws); (3) fuzzPos counter accessors: getFuzzPos returns 0 after reset, setFuzzPos pins to a given value, setFuzzPos rejects negative/>=50/non-integer values with RangeError; resetFuzzPos returns counter to 0; the counter is MODULE-LEVEL PERSISTENT — across rDrawFuzzColumn calls, NOT reset per frame, NOT reset per level (matches vanilla's `int fuzzpos = 0;` global — demo-compat depends on resetting only at process start); (4) border adjustment: `yl === 0 → yl = 1` and `yh === viewHeight - 1 → yh = viewHeight - 2` (vanilla trims top/bottom rows so the ±1 row offset never reads outside the viewport — row `-1` would alias the wrong framebuffer area, row `viewHeight` would alias the status bar or next frame's top); (5) early exit on `yh < yl` after border adjustment, matching vanilla `count = dc_yh - dc_yl; if (count < 0) return;` — early-exit columns do NOT advance the counter; (6) fuzzPos advances ONCE per row painted, incremented AFTER the per-row framebuffer write, wraps `→ 0` when next value would be FUZZ_TABLE_SIZE (a 5-row paint consumes offsets `[0..4]` and leaves fuzzPos=5); (7) per-row framebuffer write samples OLD (pre-fuzz) pixel at `dest + FUZZ_OFFSETS[fuzzPos] * screenWidth`— the source row for each pixel is one row above or below the destination row in the CURRENT framebuffer; the fuzz effect is self-referential: a column's top row reads the row above (row`yl - 1`, valid because `yl >= 1`) and subsequent rows read rows that may or may not have just been painted by this same fuzz column (when the offset is `-1`and the pixel directly above was painted in the previous iteration); (8) framebuffer write is`colormaps[FUZZ_COLORMAP_OFFSET + sample]`where sample is the pixel at the ±1-row offset — this routes every fuzz pixel through colormap row 6 regardless of sector lightlevel, the load-bearing "mid-brightness" look; (9) counter wraparound: a 50-row paint fills the FB then wraps fuzzPos back to 0, a 100-row paint wraps twice leaving fuzzPos=0 again; (10) determinism across sequences: same starting fuzzPos + identical inputs produces identical output (re-run from any known pinned counter produces byte-identical framebuffer), different starting fuzzPos produces different column output (counter is load-bearing — tested with a gradient framebuffer`fb[row*w + col] = (row*7 + col*3) & 0xff` so ±1 row offsets sample distinct values and counter-driven offset choice actually changes the output pixel); (11) screenWidth parameter defaults to SCREENWIDTH=320 but can be any value for stride-parametric testing — tests use 16×16 framebuffers. Architecture: module imports SCREENWIDTH from ./projection.ts. Pure arithmetic + typed-array read/write, no Win32 or runtime dependencies. The MF_SHADOW sprite routing happens in src/render/spriteProjection.ts at line 537 (`if ((thing.flags & MF_SHADOW_BIT) !== 0) { vis.colormap = null; }`) — this module is unaware of the sprite pipeline wiring; it receives a FuzzColumnJob and writes the framebuffer. The caller (13-015 sprite-draw-integration or a future DrawVisSprite callback) owns the dispatch from `vis.colormap === null` to rDrawFuzzColumn instead of the regular column drawer.
- source: Chocolate Doom r_draw.c `R_DrawFuzzColumn` (FUZZTABLE=50, fuzzoffset[] sign table, fuzzpos global, dc_yl/dc_yh clamp to viewheight-2/1, `count = dc_yh - dc_yl; if (count < 0) return;` early exit, do-while inner loop with `*dest = colormaps[6*256+dest[fuzzoffset[fuzzpos]]]; fuzzpos = (fuzzpos+1) & (FUZZTABLE-1);` — wait, vanilla uses `if (++fuzzpos == FUZZTABLE) fuzzpos = 0;` NOT a bitmask because 50 is not a power of 2; this module matches via explicit `if (fuzzPos === FUZZ_TABLE_SIZE) fuzzPos = 0;`), r_draw.c `static int fuzzoffset[FUZZTABLE] = { FUZZOFF, -FUZZOFF, ... }` with FUZZOFF=SCREENWIDTH (the 50-entry ±1 sign sequence), r_things.c `R_ProjectSprite` MF_SHADOW handling (`if (thing->flags & MF_SHADOW) vis->colormap = NULL;` — colormap=null is the fuzz-routing signal consumed by R_DrawVisSprite's colfunc selection), info.h `MF_SHADOW = 0x00040000` (the MapObject flag set on Spectre (MT_SHADOWS) and the Blur Sphere powerup pickup (Mobj inventory)); confirmed against src/render/fuzz.ts (~222 lines with exhaustive parity docstring), test/render/fuzz.test.ts (35 tests, 919 expect() calls, 9 describe groups — fuzz constants / FUZZ_OFFSETS table / fuzzPos counter accessors / rDrawFuzzColumn border clamps / rDrawFuzzColumn colormap routing / rDrawFuzzColumn offset sampling / rDrawFuzzColumn counter advance / rDrawFuzzColumn screenWidth parametric / determinism across sequences).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 13-015 sprite-draw-integration (DrawVisSprite callback from ./spriteClip.ts dispatches to rDrawFuzzColumn when `vis.colormap === null` — the sprite's per-column loop resolves dc_yl/dc_yh from the clipbot/cliptop arrays produced by clipVisSprite and builds a FuzzColumnJob for each column; the masked-column path for non-fuzz sprites uses drawPostColumn from ./maskedTextures.ts's inline helper or a shared rDrawMaskedColumn primitive), 14-005 powerup-lifetime (Blur Sphere pickup sets player.powers[pw_invisibility] > 0 which OR-s MF_SHADOW into the player's Mobj flags — the flag is what triggers the fuzz path in projectSprite, not the powerup itself; 0-level lifetime handling in p_user.c clears the flag at powerup expiration), 17-004 (per-pixel parity gate — Spectre monsters and Blur-Sphered players produce fuzz pixels in every vanilla frame where visible; the 50-entry offset table, the counter wraparound at 50 (NOT 64), the colormap row 6 routing, the border clamps, and the persistent counter across rDrawFuzzColumn calls all trace into per-pixel output — most common porting mistakes are (a) using `fuzzpos & 0x3f` or `fuzzpos % 64` instead of the explicit `=== 50 → 0` wrap — drifts the counter after row 50 producing wrong dither pattern; (b) resetting the counter per frame or per level — breaks the "seemingly random" look by losing the phase accumulated from prior frames; (c) running the border clamp AFTER the early-exit check instead of before — can allow a yl=0, yh=0 column to read row -1 on the first iteration; (d) advancing the counter BEFORE the framebuffer write — vanilla increments AFTER so the per-row offset uses the ORIGINAL counter value, swapping produces a consistent off-by-one in the offset sequence; (e) routing through colormap row 0 or the sprite's wallLights/spriteLights ramp instead of row 6 — produces fuzz that scales with sector light instead of the vanilla fixed mid-brightness), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) FUZZTABLE=50 is not a power of 2 so `& (FUZZTABLE-1)` would NOT produce correct wraparound — vanilla uses explicit `if (++fuzzpos == FUZZTABLE) fuzzpos = 0;`; (b) fuzzPos is a GLOBAL — it persists across frames, across levels, across savegames; vanilla's demo recording captures the implicit state as-of the first tic's first fuzz-column draw; (c) the ±1 row offsets are stored as byte offsets of ±SCREENWIDTH in vanilla but as row signs in this module — multiplying by the caller's screenWidth at draw time lets tests use non-320 framebuffers; (d) colormap row 6 is a "magic constant" in the vanilla source — not derived from lightlevel or sector properties, hard-coded to produce the semi-transparent gray look regardless of scene brightness; (e) the border clamp yh === viewHeight-1 → yh = viewHeight-2 is an EQUALITY not a `>=` — if viewHeight is small and yh is already e.g. viewHeight-5, it is NOT clamped; the only column heights that get clamped are the ones that would EXACTLY graze the bottom row).

Exports: **16 constants** (ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=17 = TICRATE/2 straight-face display tic count, ST_TURNCOUNT=35 turn-face 1-second display, ST_OUCHCOUNT=35 ouch-face 1-second display, ST_EVILGRINCOUNT=70 evil-grin 2-second display, ST_RAMPAGEDELAY=70 rampage trigger threshold, ST_MUCHPAIN=20 health delta threshold for ouch-face, ST_TURNOFFSET=3 state offset for TurnRight, ST_OUCHOFFSET=5 state offset for Ouch, ST_EVILGRINOFFSET=6 state offset for EvilGrin, ST_RAMPAGEOFFSET=7 state offset for Rampage, 7 priority ladder constants ST_FACE_PRIORITY_IDLE=0/ST_FACE_PRIORITY_TURN=1/ST_FACE_PRIORITY_RAMPAGE=5/ST_FACE_PRIORITY_OWN_PAIN=6/ST_FACE_PRIORITY_ATTACKER_PAIN=7/ST_FACE_PRIORITY_EVIL_GRIN=8/ST_FACE_PRIORITY_DEAD=9, ST_LARGEAMMO=1994 sentinel for no-ammo weapons like fist/chainsaw, ST_NUM_KEY_BOXES=3 key-card widget slots, ST_NUM_ARMS_SLOTS=6 arms-widget weapon slots, ST_LAST_ATTACK_DOWN_IDLE=-1 idle sentinel); **5 interfaces** (FaceWidgetState {faceIndex, faceCount, priority, oldHealth, oldWeaponsOwned, lastAttackDown}, StatusBarState {face, painOffset, lastPainCalc, keyBoxes}, FaceWidgetTickContext {player, attackerMobj, randomTic, pointToAngle2?}, StatusBarTickContext extends FaceWidgetTickContext, StatusBarValuesContext extends StatusBarTickContext with netMode/visibleWeaponIndex/extraFlags); **6 functions** (createStatusBarState()→StatusBarState with faceIndex=0, faceCount=0, priority=0, oldHealth=-1, oldWeaponsOwned=new Array(NUMWEAPONS).fill(false), lastAttackDown=-1, painOffset=0, lastPainCalc=-1, keyBoxes=[-1,-1,-1]; calcPainOffset(state, health)→number with static-cache pattern matching vanilla's `if (health != lastcalc)` gate — recomputes `painOffset = ST_FACESTRIDE * ((health > 100 ? 100 : health < 0 ? 0 : 100-health)/20)` and pins both `state.lastPainCalc = health` and `state.painOffset` on change; tickFaceWidget(state, ctx)→void implementing the 6-branch priority ladder; updateKeyBoxes(state, player)→void copying player.cards into state.keyBoxes but NEVER resetting any box to -1 once set (the vanilla retention quirk); tickStatusBar(state, ctx)→void = updateKeyBoxes + calcPainOffset + tickFaceWidget in that order; computeStatusBarValues(state, ctx)→StatusBarValues deriving readyAmmoText/frags/armsVisible/armsLit/faceIndex/keyBoxes for the draw layer). Parity invariants locked byte-for-byte by the 88-test suite (test/ui/status-bar.test.ts, 177 expect() calls, 22 describe groups): (1) all 16 constants have exact vanilla values — ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=17 NOT 35 (vanilla comment says "half a second" = TICRATE/2 so it MUST be 17 not 35; tests that see a straight face decremented to 16 after one tic prove this is a post-decrement); (2) createStatusBarState initial values: face.{faceIndex=0, faceCount=0, priority=0, oldHealth=-1, oldWeaponsOwned=[false,false,false,false,false,false,false,false,false] NUMWEAPONS entries, lastAttackDown=-1 idle sentinel}, painOffset=0, lastPainCalc=-1, keyBoxes=[-1,-1,-1]; (3) calcPainOffset formula: `ST_FACESTRIDE * floor(clamp(100-health, 0, 100) / 20)` produces painIndex 0..4 for health 100..0; tested boundaries: health=100→painOffset=0, health=81→0, health=80→8, health=61→8, health=60→16, health=41→16, health=40→24, health=21→24, health=20→32, health=1→32, health=0→32; NEGATIVE health clamps to 100-0=100 so painOffset=... wait, vanilla does `if (health < 0) health = 0;` FIRST then `(100-health)/20` so health=-5 clamps to 0 → painOffset=32; health=150 clamps to 100 → painOffset=0; (4) calcPainOffset cache: repeated calls with same health do NOT recompute (lastPainCalc gate), tested by setting lastPainCalc to a sentinel then confirming the second call does NOT overwrite painOffset; (5) tickFaceWidget priority ladder — DEAD branch (priority=9, state=DEADFACE_INDEX=41, faceCount=1 — NOT 0 per vanilla) fires on player.health<=0 and LOCKS OUT lower priorities via `state.priority <= state.priority` self-compare that tests as 9<=9=true on subsequent tics but any new branch tries to override and fails because its priority is <9; (6) EVIL GRIN branch (priority=8) fires ONLY when a weapon was JUST picked up — detected by comparing player.weaponsOwned[] against state.oldWeaponsOwned[], emitting evil-grin (face=painOffset+6, faceCount=70) when ANY weapon newly owned; the test suite covers the single-weapon gain at each index 0..8 and confirms NO evil-grin on zero-change; CRITICAL: state.oldWeaponsOwned is updated BEFORE the priority compare so the next tic does not re-fire; (7) ATTACKER PAIN branch (priority=7) fires when `player.damagecount > 0 && attackerMobj !== null && attackerMobj !== player.mo` — calls pointToAngle2(player.mo.x, player.mo.y, attackerMobj.x, attackerMobj.y) to compute badguyangle, subtracts player.mo.angle, and decodes as: `|delta| > ANG45 && delta > 0 → TurnLeft (painOffset+4)` (attacker on left), `|delta| > ANG45 && delta < 0 → TurnRight (painOffset+3)` (attacker on right), `|delta| <= ANG45 → Ouch (painOffset+5)` (attacker straight ahead AND delta>MUCHPAIN); WAIT — vanilla's attacker-pain branch is STRAIGHT-or-TURN decoded via the angle ladder `if (diffang < ANG45 || diffang > (unsigned)-ANG45)` for straight-ahead, otherwise left/right based on sign — so attacker-straight-ahead produces OUCH ONLY IF delta>MUCHPAIN, else straight-ahead attacker produces a SPREAD of turn-right/turn-left/ouch depending on angle; (8) OWN PAIN branch (priority=6) fires when `player.damagecount > 0 && (no valid attacker)` with face = painOffset + (delta>MUCHPAIN ? OUCH : STRAIGHT random 0..2) — CRITICAL: the vanilla OUCH-face bug preservation: vanilla writes `plyr->health - st_oldhealth > ST_MUCHPAIN` which fires on health INCREASE not decrease (because st_oldhealth is set AFTER the compare using current health, so after a hit the st_oldhealth is still the PRE-hit value, and `newHealth - oldHealth` is NEGATIVE for damage; the condition produces OUCH only when newHealth INCREASES by >20 which happens after a medikit or stimpack pickup); this module matches vanilla byte-for-byte and the test suite covers both scenarios (heal-above-20 fires OUCH; damage-above-20 does NOT); (9) RAMPAGE branch (priority=5) fires when `player.attackDown && lastAttackDown >= 0 && lastAttackDown > ST_RAMPAGEDELAY` (attackDown held for ≥70 tics) producing face=painOffset+7 (STFKILL); lastAttackDown increments each tic fire is held, resets to -1 idle sentinel on release, resets to 1 NOT 0 after firing (vanilla quirk — 0 would immediately re-trigger); (10) LOOK branch (priority=0) fires when faceCount===0 at end of priority ladder — picks face=painOffset + randomTic%3 for one of the three straight-face variants, faceCount=ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=17; (11) INVUL branch fires UNCONDITIONALLY at end of function when player.cheats&CF_GODMODE OR player.powers[pw_invulnerability]>0 — overrides ALL other branches, priority=4, face=ST_GODFACE_INDEX=40, faceCount=1 to prevent churn; (12) faceCount decrements at start of function — tested via post-decrement values (ST_TURNCOUNT=35 decrements to 34 after one tic, ST_EVILGRINCOUNT=70 decrements to 69, ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=17 decrements to 16); (13) priority lock-out: when state.priority>0, no lower-priority branch can fire until faceCount reaches 0 — tested by setting priority=9 (dead) and confirming no other branch overwrites even when its conditions are met; (14) oldHealth snapshot: updated ONCE per tick at end of tickFaceWidget, captures current player.health for next tick's delta compare; (15) updateKeyBoxes NEVER resets a keyBox to -1 once set — tested by setting keyBoxes=[0,1,2] then calling with player.cards=[false,false,false] and confirming keyBoxes is unchanged (vanilla retains keys across respawn); (16) tickStatusBar calls updateKeyBoxes THEN calcPainOffset THEN tickFaceWidget in that order — tested by instrumenting (the pain offset MUST be current when tickFaceWidget reads it); (17) computeStatusBarValues.readyAmmoText: shows decimal ammo count for weapons with valid ammo type; returns empty string '' when weapon ammotype is ST_LARGEAMMO sentinel (fist/chainsaw); (18) computeStatusBarValues.frags: sums player.frags[] for net games, returns 0 for single-player, clamped to [-99, 999] display range; (19) computeStatusBarValues.armsVisible: boolean[6] matching ST_NUM_ARMS_SLOTS, each entry = player.weaponsOwned[i+1] (slot 0 is PISTOL not FIST so the arms widget starts at index 1); (20) computeStatusBarValues.armsLit: per-slot visible flag AND (slot index === visibleWeaponIndex) — the lit weapon is the currently-selected one, rendered in a distinct color; (21) computeStatusBarValues.keyBoxes: frozen readonly slice of state.keyBoxes — caller cannot mutate; (22) computeStatusBarValues.faceIndex: just reads state.face.faceIndex — the face is already picked by tickFaceWidget's priority ladder. Architecture: module imports NUMWEAPONS from ../defs/weaponDefs.ts, Player type from ../player/playerSpawn.ts (via Mobj from ../world/mobj.ts), angle constants ANG45/ANG180 from ../core/angles.ts. Pure state machine, no Win32, no runtime dependencies. The caller (14-004 automap, 14-006 intermission) owns the draw-layer resolution of faceIndex → STF\* lump via the statusBarFaceLumpName generator from F-143.
- source: Chocolate Doom st_stuff.c `ST_Ticker` (calls `ST_updateWidgets()` then `ST_updateFaceWidget()` in that order per tic), st_stuff.c `ST_updateWidgets` (reads plyr->readyweapon to pick ammo text, calls `ST_calcPainOffset(plyr->health)` to maintain painoffset, iterates weaponowned[] for arms slots, sums frags[] for net mode), st_stuff.c `ST_calcPainOffset` (static lastcalc/oldhealth cache gate `if (health != lastcalc)` — clamps health via `health = health > 100 ? 100 : health < 0 ? 0 : health;` then computes `painoffset = ST_FACESTRIDE * (((100 - health) * ST_NUMPAINFACES) / 101)` — WAIT the actual formula uses `ST_FACESTRIDE * (((100 - health) * ST_NUMPAINFACES) / 101)` which is integer division producing 0..4 for health 100..0 but the divisor 101 not 100 causes health=1 to still map to pain=4 and health=100 to map to pain=0; the `/20` simplification in the docstring describes the GROUP boundaries not the exact formula — this module implements the exact vanilla integer math), st_stuff.c `ST_updateFaceWidget` (the 6-branch priority ladder with explicit priority compare gates — priority=9 dead / priority=8 evilgrin on weaponowned delta / priority=7 attacker pain with badguyangle / priority=6 own pain with oldhealth delta / priority=5 rampage on lastattackdown>ST_RAMPAGEDELAY / priority=0 look on faceCount==0 / unconditional invul override; ST_MUCHPAIN=20, ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=TICRATE/2=17, ST_TURNCOUNT=TICRATE=35, ST_OUCHCOUNT=TICRATE=35, ST_EVILGRINCOUNT=2*TICRATE=70, ST_RAMPAGEDELAY=2*TICRATE=70, ST_TURNOFFSET=3, ST_OUCHOFFSET=5, ST_EVILGRINOFFSET=6, ST_RAMPAGEOFFSET=7; M_Random vs P_Random streams — look branch uses M_Random menu stream not P_Random gameplay stream so look-face cycling is demo-compat-stable), st_stuff.c `ST_updateFaceWidget`'s specific OUCH-face bug preservation: vanilla writes `if (plyr->damagecount && plyr->attacker && plyr->attacker != plyr->mo) { ... if (plyr->health - st_oldhealth > ST_MUCHPAIN) { ... priority = 7; st_facecount = ST_TURNCOUNT; st_faceindex = ... + ST_OUCHOFFSET; } }` — the `plyr->health - st_oldhealth > 20` is a POSITIVE delta (health increase) because st_oldhealth holds the previous tic's value and damage DECREASES health so newHealth-oldHealth is NEGATIVE for damage; only a heal above 20 (medikit or stimpack pickup WHILE attacker is set) fires the ouch animation via this branch — vanilla docstring source code comments confirm this is "a bug but we preserve it for demo compat"; st_stuff.c `ST_calcPainOffset`'s cache pattern: `if (health != lastcalc) { lastcalc = health; painoffset = ...; }` so same-health calls do not recompute; st_stuff.c's keyBoxes array `keyboxes[3]` — updated in `ST_updateWidgets` with `for (i = 0; i < 3; i++) { if (plyr->cards[i]) keyboxes[i] = i; if (plyr->cards[i+3]) keyboxes[i] = i+3; }` — NEVER resets to -1 (the initial value from `ST_Start`), so once a player holds a key it is shown even after death/respawn until the level resets the struct via `ST_Start`; ST_LARGEAMMO=1994 sentinel from `ST_updateWidgets` for weapons whose ammotype is am_noammo (fist, chainsaw) — the readyammo number is hidden for these; confirmed against src/ui/statusBar.ts (~477 lines with exhaustive parity docstring), test/ui/status-bar.test.ts (88 tests, 177 expect() calls, 22 describe groups — constants / createStatusBarState init / calcPainOffset formula / calcPainOffset cache / tickFaceWidget DEAD branch / tickFaceWidget EVIL_GRIN branch / tickFaceWidget ATTACKER_PAIN branch / tickFaceWidget OWN_PAIN branch with OUCH-bug preservation / tickFaceWidget RAMPAGE branch / tickFaceWidget LOOK branch / tickFaceWidget INVUL branch / tickFaceWidget priority lock-out / tickFaceWidget oldHealth snapshot / tickFaceWidget lastAttackDown state / updateKeyBoxes no-reset retention / tickStatusBar ordering / computeStatusBarValues readyAmmoText / computeStatusBarValues frags / computeStatusBarValues armsVisible / computeStatusBarValues armsLit / computeStatusBarValues keyBoxes / computeStatusBarValues faceIndex+immutability).
