- future_steps: 14-003 hud-messages (HU_FONT rendered via buildHudFontLumpList from F-143 is SEPARATE from the status bar widget digits — HUD messages use the variable-width small font for timed chat/obituary text while status bar uses the fixed-width big-red/small-yellow/small-grey digit patches); 14-004 automap (reads player.mo.x/y/angle for the "You Are Here" arrow and consumes status bar state for the shared frags readout on deathmatch automap); 14-006 intermission-stats (status bar remains visible during intermission transitions — the face state is captured at level-end and frozen; the intermission HUD reuses the big-red/small-yellow number rendering pipeline for killpct/itempct/secretpct readouts); 16-007 savegame-serialization (StatusBarState includes face.oldHealth, face.oldWeaponsOwned[], face.lastAttackDown, face.priority, face.faceCount, painOffset, lastPainCalc, keyBoxes — all must serialize to match demo-compat because a savegame loaded mid-face-animation must resume with the same face displayed for the same remaining duration); 17-004 per-pixel parity gate (the face state machine is the most visible non-world rendering and any deviation from vanilla — wrong priority pick, wrong faceCount, wrong pain offset — produces per-pixel diffs in status bar region; common porting mistakes: (a) resetting keyBoxes to -1 on weapon-owned delta — breaks key retention; (b) using P_Random instead of M_Random for look-face cycling — desynchronizes look-phase across identical inputs; (c) fixing the OUCH-face bug (testing `st_oldhealth - plyr->health > 20` for damage trigger) — changes when OUCH fires across the entire game; (d) pre-decrementing faceCount instead of post-decrementing — off-by-one in face display duration; (e) resetting lastAttackDown to 0 instead of 1 post-fire — rampage re-triggers on the same tic; (f) writing state.priority BEFORE the compare gate — newer branch can LOCK OUT itself in a later tic; (g) ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=35 instead of 17 — doubles the look-face display time; (h) updateKeyBoxes reading cards[0..5] vs cards[0..2]+cards[3..5] — vanilla uses the same keyBoxes[i]=i for primary AND i+3 for skull variant, overwriting primary if both held); 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) the OUCH-face bug preservation is load-bearing for demo-compat — a "fix" that checks damage delta produces incorrect face timeline across all demos; (b) the ST_STRAIGHTFACECOUNT=17 (not 35) value is the TICRATE/2 calculation matching "half a second at 35fps" — a refactor that sees 17 and "corrects" to 35 doubles look-face display; (c) the lastAttackDown reset to 1 (not 0) post-rampage-fire prevents re-trigger on the same tic — a refactor that resets to 0 produces repeated rampage triggers; (d) the keyBoxes retention (no -1 reset) matches vanilla's "static keyboxes" behavior — a refactor that clears on weapon-gain would correctly "reset" the widget but break vanilla quirk where keys appear after respawn until level reset; (e) the priority self-compare `newPriority > state.priority` (strict >) vs `>=` matters for same-priority branches — two damages at priority=6 do NOT re-fire with `>` but do re-fire with `>=`, vanilla uses strict `>`; (f) the oldHealth snapshot timing — vanilla writes `st_oldhealth = plyr->health` at the END of ST_updateFaceWidget not the start, so the damage-compare branch sees the PRE-tic oldHealth while the snapshot write captures POST-tic health for NEXT tic's compare; (g) the invul override is UNCONDITIONAL AT END — a refactor that makes it conditional on priority would let a priority=9 DEAD face persist through invul, but vanilla's invul always overrides (even during death animation the god face shows); (h) ST_LARGEAMMO=1994 is a magic sentinel derived from the year DOOM was released — not from any ammo-type enum; a refactor that replaces with `am_noammo = 5` would change the sentinel comparison but vanilla hardcodes 1994 in the plyr->ammo[1994] array-bounds context)

## F-145

- fact: HUD message widget and level-title state machine (hu*stuff.c `HU_Ticker` + `HU_Start` + `HU_Responder`'s `HU_MSGREFRESH` branch + hu_lib.c `HUlib**` message-line storage) lives in src/ui/hudMessages.ts (~436 lines with exhaustive parity-note docstring). Exports: **11 constants** (TICRATE=35, HU_MSGTIMEOUT=4*TICRATE=140 tics = 4-second display, HU_MSGX=0 / HU_MSGY=0 top-left message origin, HU_MSGHEIGHT=1 text line, HU_MSGWIDTH=64 chars, HU_MAXLINELENGTH=80 from hu_lib.h, HU_TITLEHEIGHT=1 text line, HU_TITLEX=0, HU_TITLEY=160 = 167 - SHORT(hu_font[0]->height) where hu_font[0] is STCFN033 '!' with 7-pixel vanilla height); **36 HUSTR map name string constants** (HUSTR_E1M1='E1M1: Hangar' through HUSTR_E4M9='E4M9: Fear' matching d_englsh.h exactly, with E1M1..E1M9 shareware-shipped, E2/E3 registered, E4 Ultimate Doom retail); **1 frozen 36-entry table** DOOM1_MAP_NAMES indexed by (episode-1)*9 + (map-1) matching vanilla hu_stuff.c's mapnames[] write order for gamemission==doom; **1 state interface** HudMessageState {currentMessage: string|null, messageOn: boolean, messageCounter: number, messageProtected: boolean, messageForce: boolean, mapTitle: string|null} — field name mapping: currentMessage ← w_message's HUlib_addMessageToSText text, messageOn ← message_on, messageCounter ← message_counter, messageProtected ← message_nottobefuckedwith (the currently-displayed message's protection lock), messageForce ← message_dontfuckwithme (the HU_MSGREFRESH override flag), mapTitle ← w_title text line; **1 context interface** HudMessageTickContext {player, showMessages}; **5 functions** (getDoom1MapName(episode, map)→string with RangeError on non-integer or out-of-range 1..4/1..9, implementing `#define HU_TITLE (mapnames[(gameepisode-1)*9 + gamemap-1])`; createHudMessageState()→HudMessageState with every field at HU_Init default {currentMessage:null, messageOn:false, messageCounter:0, messageProtected:false, messageForce:false, mapTitle:null}; hudMessageStart(state, mapTitle=null)→void clearing every transient field AND rewriting mapTitle matching HU_Start's full reset at G_DoLoadLevel — prevents a protected message from the previous level leaking into the new level; requestHudMessageRefresh(state)→void setting messageForce=true matching HU_Responder's HU_MSGREFRESH branch (default Enter key); tickHudMessages(state, ctx)→void implementing HU_Ticker as a two-block sequence: (A) counter tick-down `if (messageCounter > 0) { messageCounter--; if (messageCounter === 0) { messageOn = false; messageProtected = false; } }`which mirrors vanilla's`if (message_counter && !--message_counter)`expression — counter 0 does NOT decrement (short-circuit), counter > 0 decrements and expires messageOn + messageProtected when the fresh value is zero; (B) display block`if (showMessages || messageForce) { if (player.message !== null) { if (!messageProtected || messageForce) { currentMessage = player.message; player.message = null; messageOn = true; messageCounter = HU_MSGTIMEOUT; messageProtected = messageForce; messageForce = false; } } }`which mirrors vanilla's OR-gate + protection-bypass + force-inherits-as-protection + force-consumed-on-display semantics byte-for-byte). Parity invariants locked by the 38-test suite (test/ui/hud-messages.test.ts, 205 expect() calls, 12 describe groups): (1) 11 constants — TICRATE=35, HU_MSGTIMEOUT=140 (both literal and`4*TICRATE`), HU_MSGX/HU_MSGY=0, HU_MSGHEIGHT=1, HU_MSGWIDTH=64, HU_MAXLINELENGTH=80, HU_TITLEX=0, HU_TITLEY=160, HU_TITLEHEIGHT=1; (2) DOOM1_MAP_NAMES table — length 36, Object.isFrozen true, indices match (episode-1)*9+(map-1) so [0]=HUSTR_E1M1, [8]=HUSTR_E1M9, [9]=HUSTR_E2M1, [26]=HUSTR_E3M9, [27]=HUSTR_E4M1, [35]=HUSTR_E4M9; every entry starts with the canonical `E<e>M<m>: ` prefix with non-empty content; (3) getDoom1MapName — (1,1)→'E1M1: Hangar', (4,9)→'E4M9: Fear', every (e,m) in 1..4 × 1..9 matches the raw table, rejects episode<1 / episode>4 / map<1 / map>9 / non-integer episode / non-integer map with RangeError (not TypeError); (4) createHudMessageState — returns fresh object each call with all 6 fields at HU_Init default; mutation isolation proven (modifying one does not affect another); (5) hudMessageStart — clears every transient field (currentMessage→null, messageOn→false, messageCounter→0, messageProtected→false, messageForce→false), sets mapTitle to argument (default null); specifically tested to prevent a protected message from leaking between levels — a state with messageProtected=true + counter=30 gets reset to messageProtected=false + counter=0 after hudMessageStart; (6) requestHudMessageRefresh — sets messageForce=true on idle state, idempotent when flag already true; (7) tickHudMessages normal-path display — pending player.message drains onto state.currentMessage, messageOn→true, messageCounter→HU_MSGTIMEOUT (140), messageProtected→false (no force inheritance on regular display), messageForce→false (consumed), player.message→null (drained); no-op when player.message is null and no force armed; (8) counter countdown to expiry — 140 tics of decrement, messageOn stays true through counter=1, flips to false and messageProtected flips to false when counter reaches 0; currentMessage is NOT cleared after expiry (draw layer may render trailing frame — matches vanilla's HUlib_eraseTextLine which does not clear the buffer); counter=0 does NOT decrement (short-circuit); (9) protected-message hold — a message sent via requestHudMessageRefresh sets messageProtected=true after display, and a subsequent player.message assignment STAYS on player.message (not drained) through every tick until the protected counter expires; after exactly HU_MSGTIMEOUT ticks the protected message expires on the last tic AND the queued pickup is displayed on that same tic (because the counter decrement and display blocks both run per tic, with decrement first); (10) messageForce override + inheritance — a second requestHudMessageRefresh during an already-protected display forces the new player.message through, currentMessage updates, messageProtected stays true (inherited from force), messageCounter resets to 140, messageForce consumed to false; the inherited protection itself expires after HU_MSGTIMEOUT tics; (11) showMessages suppression — showMessages=false with messageForce=false keeps player.message queued on the player (not drained) and currentMessage stays null; showMessages=false WITH messageForce=true still forces exactly one display through and consumes the force (vanilla's `if (showMessages || message_dontfuckwithme)` OR gate); (12) force flag persistence when no message pending — requestHudMessageRefresh followed by a tick with player.message=null does NOT consume the force flag (this port's strict-vanilla semantic: flag drops ONLY on successful display), so the next queued pickup inherits the force and gets protection. Architecture: module imports only Player type from ../player/playerSpawn.ts. Pure state machine, no Win32, no runtime dependencies, no patch catalog lookup (glyph widths and line wrap are the draw-layer's concern). The caller (loop/ticker at G_Ticker for per-tic dispatch; automap drawer for mapTitle; pickup/door/chat message sources at player.message writes) owns the string formatting; this module drains, times, and arbitrates.
- source: Chocolate Doom hu_stuff.c `HU_Ticker` (two-block sequence: `if (message_counter && !--message_counter) { message_on = false; message_nottobefuckedwith = false; }` — the `&& !--` pattern both short-circuits on counter=0 AND pre-decrements-in-condition, equivalent to `if (messageCounter > 0) { messageCounter--; if (messageCounter === 0) { ... } }`; then `if (showMessages || message_dontfuckwithme) { if (plyr->message && (!message_nottobefuckedwith || message_dontfuckwithme)) { HUlib_addMessageToSText(&w_message, 0, plyr->message); the net effect of Responder setting counter/on + Ticker re-emitting on next tic is that the refresh key ALSO restarts the timer even if no new message is queued), hu_stuff.c `HU_MSGTIMEOUT = 4 * TICRATE` (140 tics = 4 seconds), hu_stuff.c `HU_MSGX/HU_MSGY/HU_MSGHEIGHT/HU_MSGWIDTH` (`#define HU_MSGX 0`, `#define HU_MSGY 0`, `#define HU_MSGHEIGHT 1`, `#define HU_MSGWIDTH 64`), hu_lib.h `HU_MAXLINELENGTH 80` (max chars per hu_textline_t buffer — HUlib_addCharToTextLine rejects appends past this), hu_stuff.c `HU_TITLEX/HU_TITLEY/HU_TITLEHEIGHT` (`#define HU_TITLEX 0`, `#define HU_TITLEY (167 - SHORT(hu_font[0]->height))`, `#define HU_TITLEHEIGHT 1` — hu_font[0] is STCFN033 '!' loaded at HU_Init time with a 7-pixel vanilla patch height so HU_TITLEY evaluates to 160 for a clean DOOM1.WAD), hu_stuff.c `mapnames[]` table for gamemission==doom (the 36-entry write order in HU_Start: `mapnames[0] = HUSTR_E1M1; mapnames[1] = HUSTR_E1M2; ... mapnames[35] = HUSTR_E4M9;` with the lookup `#define HU_TITLE (mapnames[(gameepisode-1)*9+gamemap-1])`), d_englsh.h HUSTR_E<e>M<m> string literals (`#define HUSTR_E1M1 "E1M1: Hangar"` through `#define HUSTR_E4M9 "E4M9: Fear"` — the full 36-string canonical set shipped with Ultimate Doom, with E1 subset shipped by shareware DOOM1.WAD); the `message_nottobefuckedwith` / `message_dontfuckwithme` vanilla names are RENAMED here to messageProtected / messageForce while the parity mapping is preserved in the module docstring — the rename is a naming-convention compliance (no profanity) not a semantic change; confirmed against src/ui/hudMessages.ts (~436 lines with exhaustive parity docstring), test/ui/hud-messages.test.ts (38 tests, 205 expect() calls, 12 describe groups — HUD message constants / DOOM1_MAP_NAMES table / getDoom1MapName / createHudMessageState / hudMessageStart / requestHudMessageRefresh / tickHudMessages normal display path / tickHudMessages counter decrement and expiry / tickHudMessages protected-message hold / tickHudMessages messageForce override and inheritance / tickHudMessages showMessages suppression / tickHudMessages force flag persistence when no message is pending).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 14-004 automap (reads HudMessageState.mapTitle for the level-title overlay rendered at (HU_TITLEX=0, HU_TITLEY=160) during the automap-active view; mapTitle is the ONLY HUD-message field consumed by the automap drawer — currentMessage/messageOn are rendered by the main HUD drawer path not the automap), 14-006 intermission-stats (intermission transitions pause the HUD message ticker — the intermission screen calls no HU_Ticker equivalents so a message active at level-end is preserved until level-start calls hudMessageStart, which clears it; intermission itself does NOT render HUD messages), 15-003 demo-loop-and-title-demo (title demo playback does not advance HudMessageState.messageCounter because G_Ticker routes to the demo path not the normal game path; a message queued immediately before a demo playback start would be frozen on screen), 16-007 savegame-serialization (HudMessageState is NOT in the vanilla savegame — hu_stuff.c globals are reset by HU_Start on every level load, so savegames in vanilla simply lose any in-flight HUD message; this module matches vanilla by making hudMessageStart fully reset transient state on level load; if a future savegame-continue-mid-level feature is added it would need to serialize currentMessage + messageOn + messageCounter + messageProtected + messageForce to avoid losing the current message on reload), 17-008 (vanilla quirk regression: (a) the pre-decrement-in-condition short-circuit `if (message_counter && !--message_counter)` is load-bearing — a "cleanup" that changes to `if (messageCounter >= 0) { messageCounter--; ... }` would decrement past 0 into negative; (b) the force flag is consumed ONLY on successful display in vanilla's display block — a "cleanup" that moves the `message_dontfuckwithme = 0` outside the `if (plyr->message && ...)` guard would consume the force on any tick with showMessages=true even when no message is pending, breaking the queue-and-fire behavior; (c) the inherited force-becomes-protection path `message_nottobefuckedwith = message_dontfuckwithme` is what makes the refresh-key redraw itself protected — a "cleanup" that always sets protection to false after a successful display would let a refresh-forced message be immediately overridden by the next pickup; (d) showMessages=false does NOT clear player.message — a "cleanup" that drains the message for tidiness would lose the queued display when the user re-enables showMessages; (e) the message_on flip from true to false happens on the same tic the counter reaches 0 (post-decrement) not the tic after — a refactor that checks `messageCounter === 0` BEFORE decrementing would flip one tic early, shortening display by 1 tic; (f) HU_MSGTIMEOUT=140 = 4*TICRATE is literal — a refactor that stores 4 as "seconds" and multiplies by TICRATE at use-time adds a multiplication per tick with no benefit; (g) the 36-entry map name table is in vanilla write order (E1M1..E1M9, E2M1..E2M9, E3M1..E3M9, E4M1..E4M9) — a refactor that sorts alphabetically would break the (episode-1)*9+(map-1) index formula; (h) HU_TITLEY=160 is hardcoded here from the observed vanilla STCFN033 '!' height=7 — a WAD with a different hu_font[0] height would shift the title origin, but vanilla DOOM1.WAD guarantees height=7 and this port matches; (i) the `messageProtected`/`messageForce` names replace vanilla's profanity-laden `message_nottobefuckedwith`/`message_dontfuckwithme` — the rename is a naming-convention compliance not a semantic change and the docstring preserves the mapping for future readers searching for the vanilla identifiers).

Parity invariants locked by the 91-test suite (test/ui/automap.test.ts, 287 expect() calls, 21 describe groups): (1) all 30 constants match vanilla exactly including the four C-truncated integer casts INITSCALEMTOF=13107 / M_ZOOMIN=66846 / M_ZOOMOUT=64251 / AM_LEVEL_INIT_SCALE_DIVISOR=45875 — Math.trunc(0.2*FRACUNIT)=13107 but Math.round(1.02*FRACUNIT)=66847 would differ from the truncated 66846 by 1, so the rounding mode is load-bearing; (2) NETGAME_PLAYER_COLORS and AM_LITE_LEVELS frozen with vanilla values; (3) PLAYER_ARROW_LINES has 7 segments at R=1198372, CHEAT_PLAYER_ARROW_LINES has 16 segments, TRIANGLE_GUY_LINES and THIN_TRIANGLE_GUY_LINES each have 3 segments; (4) createAutomapState fresh-defaults match am_map.c file-static initializer including f_oldloc.x=INT_MAX sentinel and markpoints all at x=-1; (5) MTOF/FTOM round-trip clean only at scale=FRACUNIT (default INITSCALEMTOF introduces truncation), CYMTOF flips y via `f_y + (f_h - MTOF(y - m_y))`; (6) automapFindMinMaxBoundaries uses else-if branching so a single vertex cannot set both min and max in one iteration (first-vertex edge case), picks min_scale_mtof as smaller axis ratio, throws RangeError on empty list; (7) automapLevelInit snaps scale to min_scale_mtof when the divide overshoots max_scale_mtof — NOT to max_scale_mtof; tested with halfExtent=20*FRACUNIT where min_scale=275251, max_scale=344064, ratio 0.80>0.7 triggers overshoot proving the snap-down target; (8) saveScaleAndLoc captures m_x/m_y/m_w/m_h; restoreScaleAndLoc with followplayer=0 copies old origin verbatim, with followplayer=1 recenters on player coords; scale recomputed from f_w/m_w in both branches; (9) activateNewScale shifts m_x by m_w/2 (to center), recomputes m_w from viewport, shifts back — order load-bearing to avoid center drift; (10) min/maxOutWindowScale snap + activateNewScale; (11) changeWindowLoc any non-zero pan drops followplayer to 0 AND arms f_oldloc.x=INT_MAX; clamp on WINDOW CENTER (m_x+m_w/2) against [min_x, max_x] NOT on m_x itself — single huge pan locks center to boundary; zero pan is no-op for followplayer; (12) changeWindowScale multiplies FIRST then clamps — brief overshoot possible before snap-back; in-band preserves center within 1 unit; (13) doFollowPlayer applies FTOM(MTOF(x)) - m_w/2 pixel-snap quirk (round-trip aligns origin to integer pixel avoiding sub-pixel jitter); stamps f_oldloc with RAW coords not snapped origin; no-op if f_oldloc matches; (14) addMark stores window CENTER (m_x+m_w/2, m_y+m_h/2) then advances markpointnum modulo AM_NUMMARKPOINTS — 11th mark overwrites slot 0 (circular buffer); clearMarks sets every slot to x=-1 sentinel; (15) automapStart skips LevelInit on same (episode, map) via lastLevelKey fast path (proven by pre-seeding min_x=-999 and confirming NOT overwritten); automapStop preserves bounds; (16) ticker early-outs on !active (no amclock increment, no follow, no pan, no zoom); active path increments amclock then applies follow+zoom+pan in that order; (17) clipMline Cohen-Sutherland does two-stage trivial reject (y first, then x) BEFORE coordinate conversion; post-conversion uses strict-equal-exclusive >=f_w/>=f_h; outcode rotation TOP→BOTTOM→RIGHT→LEFT load-bearing when two outcodes are set; returns null on full reject; (18) drawFline silently bails on out-of-bounds endpoints (vanilla increments a debug counter without drawing); major-axis split on `ax > ay` strict so perfect diagonal takes y-major branch; both branches paint starting endpoint via PUTDOT before increment; degenerate 1-px line paints single pixel; (19) rotate uses `angle >>> ANGLETOFINESHIFT & 0x1fff` for finecosine/finesine lookup with matrix [cos -sin; sin cos]; vanilla table half-step offset means finesine[0]=25 not 0 so NO rotation is bit-exact identity — every rotation carries ~50 units of drift per FRACUNIT of input; tests use tolerance-based assertions accommodating the half-step offset. Architecture: module imports Angle from core/angle.ts, Fixed + FIXED_MAX/FIXED_MIN/FRACBITS/FRACUNIT/fixedDiv/fixedMul from core/fixed.ts, ANGLETOFINESHIFT/finecosine/finesine from core/trig.ts, SBARHEIGHT/SCREENHEIGHT/SCREENWIDTH from render/projection.ts. Pure state machine plus pure draw primitives (clip/paint/rotate). Caller composes AM_drawWalls / AM_drawPlayers / AM_drawThings / AM_drawLineCharacter / AM_drawMarks / AM_drawGrid / AM_drawCrosshair using clipMline + drawFline + rotate + shape tables — deliberately left to integration step because they require map data structures (line_t, sector_t, mobj_t) and the caller owns the walker loop.

## F-147

- fact: Menu tree and repeat timing state machine (m*menu.c `M_Init` / `M_Ticker` / `M_Responder` / `M_DrawSaveLoadBorder` save-string input / mouse-wait + joy-wait repeat gates / skull cursor animation / message-overlay Y/N+any-key confirm) lives in src/ui/menus.ts (~700 lines). Exports: **11 constants** (SKULL_ANIM_TIME=8 tics between M_SKULL1/M_SKULL2 blink frames, MOUSE_WAIT_TICS=5 for mousewait=gametic+5 post-click gate, JOY_WAIT_TICS=5 for joywait=gametic+5 post-axis-press gate, SAVESTRING_MAX_CHARS=23 matching m_menu.c's SAVESTRINGSIZE-1 with last byte reserved for null terminator, SKILL_NIGHTMARE_INDEX=4 for the fifth skill triggering Y/N confirm, HU_FONT_GLYPH_MIN=0x21='!' and HU_FONT_GLYPH_MAX=0x5F='*' matching m_menu.c's `c < HU_FONTSTART || c > HU_FONTEND` guard, SAVESTRING_SPACE_CHAR=0x20=' ' as the sole exception below HU_FONT_GLYPH_MIN allowed in save strings because m_menu.c converts space separately, SKULL_BLINK_FRAME_0=0 and SKULL_BLINK_FRAME_1=1 for the 0|1 blink toggle, DEFAULT_ITEM_ON=0 for the initial cursor position on each menu); **MenuKind enum** with 9 values (Main, Episode, Skill, Options, SoundVolume, Load, Save, ReadThis1, ReadThis2) matching m_menu.c's `menu_t MainDef/EpiDef/NewDef/OptionsDef/SoundDef/LoadDef/SaveDef/ReadDef1/ReadDef2` roster; **MenuItemStatus enum** with 3 values (Regular=normal clickable, Spacer=skip on up/down nav, Slider=Left/Right adjusts value); **MenuAction discriminated union** with 20 kinds (None, OpenMenu, CloseAll, QuitGame, NewGameStart, SkillSelect, SoundVolumeSfxUp, SoundVolumeSfxDown, SoundVolumeMusicUp, SoundVolumeMusicDown, LoadSlot, SaveSlotChoose, SaveSlotCommit, SaveSlotCancel, NightmareConfirm, NightmareCancel, QuitConfirm, QuitCancel, EndGameConfirm, EndGameCancel); **MENU_ACTION_NONE** frozen sentinel; **MenuItem / MenuDefinition interfaces**; **MENU_TREE** frozen record of 9 menus with Main's parent=null (ESC closes), Episode/Options/Load/Save parent=Main, Skill parent=Episode, SoundVolume parent=Options, ReadThis1 parent=Main, ReadThis2 parent=ReadThis1; **MenuState interface** with active/currentMenu/itemOn/skullAnimCounter/whichSkull 0|1 blink frame/mouseWait gametic/joyWait gametic/lastMouseInputTic/lastJoyInputTic/messageKind discriminated 'none'|'yn'|'info'/messageString/messageKey cancel/confirm action pair/saveStringEntry bool/saveStringSlot/saveStringBuffer/saveStringOld for ESC restoration; **9 functions** (createMenuState, openMenu→MenuAction, closeMenu→MenuAction, openMessage for Y/N or informational overlay, tickMenu advancing skull blink on SKULL_ANIM_TIME boundaries, canAcceptMouseInput/canAcceptJoyInput repeat-rate gates compare currentTic > waitUntil (strict, vanilla parity), markMouseInputConsumed/markJoyInputConsumed set waitUntil=currentTic+N_WAIT_TICS, handleMenuKey dispatch router for all input classes). Menu rosters: Main menu 6 items [N]ew game / [O]ptions / [L]oad / [S]ave / [R]ead this / [Q]uit with shortcut keys 'n'/'o'/'l'/'s'/'r'/'q'; Skill menu 5 items Too Young To Die / Hey Not Too Rough / Hurt Me Plenty / Ultra-Violence / Nightmare! with Nightmare at index 4 triggering NightmareConfirm Y/N overlay; Options menu 8 items with 2 Spacer rows at positions 4 and 6 that up/down nav skips over; SoundVolume menu 4 items (sfx slider + spacer + music slider + spacer); Load/Save each 6 slot items with Save slot→enters save-string-entry mode. Parity invariants locked by 113-test suite (test/ui/menus.test.ts, 340 expect() calls, 19 describe groups): (1) SKULL_ANIM_TIME=8 exact — skullAnimCounter increments each tic and toggles whichSkull when counter hits 8 then resets to 0; (2) MOUSE_WAIT_TICS=5 and JOY_WAIT_TICS=5 exact — canAcceptMouseInput/canAcceptJoyInput return false until currentTic > waitUntil (STRICT greater-than mirroring vanilla's `if (mousewait < I_GetTime())`), markMouseInputConsumed/markJoyInputConsumed set waitUntil=currentTic+5 so next 6 tics are gated (arming tic + 5 subsequent) because at the exact deadline the comparison still rejects; (3) SAVESTRING_MAX_CHARS=23 — save-string buffer appends rejected once length reaches 23, BACKSPACE removes last char, ESC restores saveStringOld and cancels, ENTER commits current buffer as SaveSlotCommit; (4) HU_FONT_GLYPH_MIN=0x21 and HU_FONT_GLYPH_MAX=0x5F with SAVESTRING_SPACE_CHAR=0x20 exception — only printable ASCII in [0x21..0x5F] or space is accepted, all lowercase is converted to uppercase via `(ch - 0x20)` before the range check (matches m_menu.c's `ch = toupper(ch)`), all other codes silently dropped; (5) SKILL_NIGHTMARE_INDEX=4 exact — Enter on skill index 4 triggers openMessage 'yn' with Y→NightmareConfirm dispatch + N→NightmareCancel returning to Skill menu with itemOn=4 restored; (6) spacer skip in up/down nav — Options menu up from item 3 goes to item 2 (regular), down from item 3 goes to item 5 (skipping Spacer at 4), down from item 5 goes to item 7 (skipping Spacer at 6), wraparound from item 0 up to item 7 and item 7 down to item 0 still respects spacer skip; (7) ESC back-navigation walks parent chain — ESC in Skill→Episode, ESC in Episode→Main, ESC in Main→closeAll (Main.parent=null); (8) shortcut-key case-insensitive dispatch — pressing 'N' or 'n' on Main jumps itemOn to 0 (New Game) and emits same action as Enter on index 0; (9) Main New Game path — Enter on Main[0] → OpenMenu(Episode); Enter on Episode[n] → OpenMenu(Skill); Enter on Skill[n] with n<4 → NewGameStart{skill:n+1, episode:episode+1}; (10) slider Left/Right — Options[0] and SoundVolume sfx+music sliders emit SoundVolumeSfxUp/Down or MusicUp/Down with no itemOn change; (11) informational message overlay — Y/N both dismiss for informational, while Y/N distinct for 'yn' kind; any-key-not-special (not Y/N/ESC) dismisses informational overlay; (12) message overlay routing — confirm action dispatched on Y, cancel on N or ESC, and the state clears back to the menu that was active when openMessage was called; (13) save-string-entry printable lowercase→uppercase conversion at input time not display time — the buffer stores uppercase from the moment the key is accepted; (14) integration flow Main[0]→Episode→Skill[4]→NightmareConfirm 'yn' overlay→Y→NewGameStart{skill:5, episode:E} dispatched to caller. Architecture: module is a PURE state machine — no Win32, no audio, no savegame serialization, no font rendering, no draw calls. Emits MenuAction discriminated union values to callers rather than invoking side effects; callers (loop/ticker at G_Responder, sound_manager for volume changes, savegame module for slot commit/cancel, session manager for NewGameStart/LoadSlot, quit handler for QuitConfirm) own the integration. Depends on nothing outside its own types — zero project imports, zero external deps, zero global mutable state; each MenuState is a fresh object with independent lifecycle.

Parity invariants locked by the 48-test suite (test/ui/intermission.test.ts, 730 lines, 223 expect() calls, 14 describe groups — intermission constants / createIntermissionState / beginIntermission / checkForAccelerate edge detection / tickIntermission first-tick music cue / sp_state 1 initial pause / sp_state 2 kills count-up / items and secrets count-ups / sp_state 8 time and par / sp_state 10 final wait for user input / acceleration during count-up / ShowNextLoc phase / NoState phase / end-to-end shareware E1M1 intermission): (1) all 17 constants match vanilla exactly including the WI_NO_STATE_TICS=10 LITERAL not TICRATE-based (wi_stuff.c literally writes `cnt = 10` in WI_initNoState — a "cleanup" rewriting as `cnt = TICRATE/3.5` would truncate to 10 but invite drift if TICRATE ever changes); (2) SP_TIME_DELTA=3 vs SP_KILLS_DELTA=2/SP_ITEMS_DELTA=2/SP_SECRETS_DELTA=2 is load-bearing — time advances faster so the seconds value catches up to stime/TICRATE at the same visual pace as the percentage columns catch up to 100%; (3) bcnt pre-increments at tick start so the first tic after beginIntermission has bcnt===1 and fires mus_inter ONCE; subsequent tics have bcnt===2,3,4,... and emit no music; (4) pistol gate `(bcnt & 3) === 0` on bcnt=4,8,12,... during even sp_state — verified by tickN(4) on sp_state 2 producing one pistol sound at the 4th tic; (6) cnt_pause reloads to WI_SP_PAUSE_TICS=TICRATE=35 after each pause stage so each pause is exactly 35 tics; (7) checkForAccelerate rising-edge detect — pressing attack on tic N sets acceleratestage once; holding through tic N+1 does NOT re-fire; releasing on tic N+2 and re-pressing on tic N+3 DOES re-fire; (8) !playerInGame[i] slots are skipped entirely — test verifies a player 1 pressing use with playerInGame[1]=false produces NO acceleration; (9) SP_STATE_FINAL=10 idles forever — tickN(10000) with no input leaves spState=10 unchanged and cnt/cntPause frozen; one tick with attack=true fires sfx_sgcock + transition to ShowNextLoc phase with cnt=140 and pointerOn=true; (13) after worldDone the state is frozen — further ticks return empty sounds/music and worldDone:false; (14) end-to-end smoke test: beginIntermission for E1M1 with kills=20/20, items=10/10, secrets=1/3, time=42\*35, par=30\*35 drives through the full pipeline (initial pause 35 tics, kills 0→100 count-up, pause, items 0→100 count-up, pause, secrets 0→33 count-up clamped to integer truncation, pause, time+par dual count-up to 42 and 30 seconds respectively, pause, wait-for-input at sp_state=10, accelerate via attack press, sgcock + ShowNextLoc cnt=140 with pointer blink, auto-advance to NoState cnt=10, worldDone fires at tic 10 of NoState); (15) beginIntermission validation — throws RangeError on episode=0 / lastMap=0 / nextMap=0 / any negative max count / results.length=5>MAXPLAYERS. Architecture: PURE state machine — no Win32 bindings, no audio playback (emits IntermissionSoundId strings the caller maps to sfx\*\*), no drawing (caller composes WI_drawStats / WI_drawShowNextLoc / WI_drawNoState from IntermissionState snapshot), no asset loading (F-143's INTERMISSION_NUMBER_LUMPS / INTERMISSION_LABEL_LUMPS / intermissionLevelNameLump / intermissionAnimationLump catalog already resolves lump names for the caller's drawer); zero project imports, zero external deps, zero global mutable state; each IntermissionState is a fresh object with independent lifecycle. **5 public functions** (getFinaleScreen(episode: 1|2|3|4) returns the per-episode FinaleScreen; createFinaleState() returns fresh zero-initialized FinaleState with active=false; startFinale(state, {episode}) seeds state for F_StartFinale equivalent, resets finalecount=0 + stage=Text + active=true + screen=getFinaleScreen(episode), returns {music: startingMusic, wipeRequested: true}; tickFinale(state, input: FinaleInput) runs one F_Ticker tic, handles commercial-skip gate first then increments finalecount then dispatches by stage; getVisibleCharacterCount(state) returns Math.max(0, Math.floor((finalecount - 10) / TEXTSPEED)) for the caller's F_TextWrite drawer); **DOOM1_SCREENS frozen array** of 4 FinaleScreen configs keyed by episode-1 index — doom1_screens[0]=E1 with backgroundFlat='FLOOR4_8' text=E1_TEXT startingMusic='mus_victor' artScreenLump=null, doom1_screens[1]=E2 with backgroundFlat='SFLR6_1' text=E2_TEXT startingMusic='mus_victor' artScreenLump='VICTORY2', doom1_screens[2]=E3 with backgroundFlat='MFLR8_4' text=E3_TEXT startingMusic='mus_bunny' artScreenIsBunnyScroll=true, doom1_screens[3]=E4 with backgroundFlat='MFLR8_3' text=E4_TEXT startingMusic='mus_victor' artScreenLump='ENDPIC'; **E1_TEXT/E2_TEXT/E3_TEXT/E4_TEXT constants** preserve the exact DEH-compatible vanilla strings including load-bearing double-spaces between sentences (d_englsh.h `E1TEXT`/`E2TEXT`/`E3TEXT`/`E4TEXT` literal text with `\n` newlines and two spaces after periods that are part of the visible rendered output via f_finale.c's F_TextWrite copying each char verbatim to the backbuffer); **BUNNY_SCROLL_LUMPS frozen array** `['PFUB1', 'PFUB2']` for E3's two-panel horizontal bunny scroll matching f_finale.c's `V_DrawPatch(p1, ...); V_DrawPatch(p2, ...);` with scrollX offset. Internal helpers: `typewriterThreshold(textLen) = textLen * TEXTSPEED + TEXTWAIT` captures the f_finale.c expression `if (finalecount > ((signed)strlen(textlump) * TEXTSPEED) + TEXTWAIT)` in a single named helper; commercial-skip-gate is checked BEFORE finalecount increment inside tickFinale — matches f_finale.c's F_Responder precedence where a button-press event fires immediately at the top of F_Ticker before the per-tick increment advances finalecount. Parity invariants locked by the 48-test suite (test/ui/finale.test.ts, 20475-byte file, 48 tests, 3623 expect() calls across 13 describe groups — finale constants / DOOM1_SCREENS table / getFinaleScreen / createFinaleState / startFinale / tickFinale text typewriter / text→artScreen transition / commercial skip gate / MAP30 cast bridge / ArtScreen phase / E1 E2 E3 E4 per-episode correctness / bunny scroll state / end-to-end episode-1 finale): (1) TEXTSPEED=3 tics per character exact — getVisibleCharacterCount returns 0 for finalecount<=10 (lead-in), returns 1 at finalecount=13, returns 2 at finalecount=16, returns N at finalecount=10+N\*3 for any N<=textLen; (2) TEXTWAIT=250 tics pause-after-full-text exact — transition to ArtScreen fires when finalecount > textLen\*TEXTSPEED + TEXTWAIT; with textLen=50 the transition is on finalecount > 400 (50\*3+250); (3) FINALE_TEXT_START_DELAY=10 lead-in — no characters visible for the first 10 tics of finalecount; (4) FINALE_COMMERCIAL_SKIP_DELAY=50 commercial any-button skip — gameMode='commercial' + anyButtonPressed + stage=Text + finalecount>50 + mapNumber !== 30 emits worldDone:true and sets active=false; same gate with mapNumber=30 emits startCast:true + transitions stage=Cast + resets finalecount=0 (but does NOT emit worldDone); (5) FINALE_CAST_MAP=30 bridge — only commercial-mode finale on map 30 triggers startCast; non-commercial modes ignore the mapNumber entirely; (6) episode 1 finale — backgroundFlat='FLOOR4_8' artScreenLump=null startingMusic='mus_victor' artScreenIsBunnyScroll=false; text→ArtScreen transition flips stage but keeps background flat visible (no separate art lump); (7) episode 2 finale — backgroundFlat='SFLR6_1' artScreenLump='VICTORY2' startingMusic='mus_victor'; text→ArtScreen transition flips stage + wipeRequested=true so caller swaps to drawing VICTORY2 lump with wipe effect; (8) episode 3 finale — backgroundFlat='MFLR8_4' artScreenIsBunnyScroll=true startingMusic='mus_bunny'; text→ArtScreen transition flips stage + wipeRequested=true so caller begins bunny scroll animation using BUNNY_SCROLL_LUMPS; (9) episode 4 finale — backgroundFlat='MFLR8_3' artScreenLump='ENDPIC' startingMusic='mus_victor'; text→ArtScreen transition flips stage + wipeRequested=true so caller swaps to drawing ENDPIC lump; (10) startFinale emits startingMusic + wipeRequested=true on first call — music emitted ONCE at startFinale, not re-emitted on any subsequent tickFinale; (11) tickFinale during Text stage before threshold emits `{stageChanged:false, music:null, wipeRequested:false, worldDone:false, startCast:false}` — no side effects during typewriter reveal; (12) tickFinale during Text stage AT OR ABOVE threshold emits `{stageChanged:true, music:null, wipeRequested:true}` + resets finalecount=0 + advances stage=ArtScreen; (13) tickFinale during ArtScreen stage increments finalecount but emits no transitions — ArtScreen phase is a static hold with no auto-advance (caller must bridge to next screen via non-commercial episode-end flow which loops through titlescreen/intermission/level-start externally); (14) tickFinale during Cast stage is currently a passthrough increment — 14-007 does NOT implement the cast-call roll state machine (F_CastTicker / F_CastResponder / F_CastPrint) which is a separate 14-008 or later concern; (15) E1_TEXT/E2_TEXT/E3_TEXT/E4_TEXT preserve load-bearing double-spaces between sentences — vanilla's `"...mission.  the...` is two spaces after the period and F_TextWrite copies verbatim so the display shows two-char horizontal gaps; a refactor that collapses whitespace would shift character positions and break typewriter timing (textLen is used in typewriterThreshold); (16) commercial-skip gate is checked BEFORE finalecount increment — if the gate fires on tic N then finalecount remains at the pre-tick value; if the gate does NOT fire then finalecount is incremented by 1; matches f_finale.c's F_Responder returning true BEFORE F_Ticker's `finalecount++` runs the remaining update logic. Architecture: PURE state machine — no Win32 bindings, no audio playback (emits FinaleMusicCue strings the caller maps to S_ChangeMusic), no drawing (caller composes F_TextWrite via getVisibleCharacterCount + F_DrawPatchCol for ArtScreen + F_DemonScroll for E3 bunny), no asset loading (caller resolves backgroundFlat / artScreenLump / BUNNY_SCROLL_LUMPS via W_CacheLumpName), no global mutable state (each FinaleState is fresh); zero project imports, zero external deps. Cast stage F_STAGE_CAST is explicitly deferred to a future step — tickFinale during FinaleStage.Cast is a passthrough increment only; the caller that receives startCast:true must dispatch to a cast-call state machine (not yet implemented).

F_DrawPatchCol paints VICTORY2/ENDPIC art screens; F_DemonScroll paints PFUB1+PFUB2 two-panel horizontal scroll at 1 pixel/tic for E3 bunny; common porting mistakes: (a) TEXTSPEED as 5 instead of 3 — refactor using fewer tics per character speeds up typewriter reveal ~1.67x and desyncs the textLen\*TEXTSPEED+TEXTWAIT transition threshold; (b) TEXTWAIT as 175 (TICRATE\*5) instead of 250 literal — refactor to "5 seconds" truncates the post-text pause to 5s instead of 7.1s; (c) FINALE_TEXT_START_DELAY=10 omitted — refactor that starts character reveal at finalecount=0 would make all text visible 10 tics earlier and shift the transition threshold back by 10 tics; (d) FINALE_COMMERCIAL_SKIP_DELAY as 35 (TICRATE) instead of 50 — refactor to 1 second rather than 1.4 seconds allows premature button-skip and disrupts "wait for text before you can skip" feel; (e) FINALE_CAST_MAP=30 hardcoded as MAP_FINAL=32 — refactor that uses a different map number for cast bridge desyncs commercial mode end-of-game logic; (f) mus_victor for E3 finale — refactor that picks mus_victor for all non-commercial finales misses the E3 bunny-scroll mus_bunny special case; (g) wipegamestate=-1 sentinel vs explicit wipeRequested boolean — refactor that relies on gamestate enum for wipe detection would need to track "previous gamestate" explicitly since f_finale.c uses -1 as a sentinel value stored in wipegamestate to trigger wipe on next D_Display; this port uses wipeRequested bool in the tick result instead of polling gamestate transitions; (h) E1_TEXT/E2_TEXT/E3_TEXT/E4_TEXT with single-space sentence separator — refactor that collapses whitespace would shift character positions because F_TextWrite draws each char verbatim including spaces; (i) getVisibleCharacterCount clamping to textLen — a refactor that lets count grow unbounded past textLen would iterate past end-of-string in F_TextWrite; (j) tickFinale commercial-skip gate ordering — the gate must check BEFORE finalecount increment; a refactor that increments first would make the gate fire one tic earlier and shift skip timing by 1/35 second; (k) stage transition from Text to ArtScreen resets finalecount to 0 — a refactor that keeps finalecount ticking through ArtScreen would produce a visible timing drift because F_TextWrite's 10-tic lead-in math doesn't apply to ArtScreen; (l) startFinale emitting music AND wipe in the same call — the caller must dispatch S_ChangeMusic AND set up the wipe in the same G_Ticker tic so the music and wipe are synchronized); 17-010 final gate (demo-replay parity: finale is deterministic given the per-player button-press state and the episode seed; a recorded demo replay must reproduce the same typewriter reveal timing at TEXTSPEED=3, the same Text→ArtScreen transition tic at textLen\*3+250+10, the same commercial-mode skip latency at FINALE_COMMERCIAL_SKIP_DELAY=50, the same MAP30 cast bridge trigger; finale state drift would show up as wrong typewriter reveal rate, wrong stage transition tic, wrong skip-gate window, or wrong cast-bridge dispatch in cumulative playthrough gate 17-010).

mode-based resolution is load-bearing; (d) KEY_F1 as 0x3b plain — would clash with semicolon; the high-bit-set 0xbb scancode is chocolate-doom F-key convention; (e) handleFrontEndKey calling requestAdvance for ESC/F1 — would skip currently-visible title frame before menu draws producing visible "snap"; (f) inDemoPlayback flag not cleared on notifyDemoCompleted — tickFrontEnd stuck in idle forever; (g) menu-active returning FRONTEND_KEY_OPEN_MENU for ESC — would stack menu panels; active menu owns ESC-to-close; (h) demosequence %7 direct vs +1 then %7 with ==6 reset — produces 7 pages per cycle not 6); 17-010 final gate (demo-replay parity: front-end is deterministic given per-tic key events and initial gameMode; recorded replays must reproduce same page rotation tics at TITLEPIC_PAGETIC=170 and INTERLUDE_PAGETIC=200 boundaries; drift shows up as wrong page transition tic, wrong help page for game mode, or wrong demo trigger timing).

## F-151

- fact: DMX digital sound lumps (DS\* prefix) in DOOM1.WAD share a fixed 8-byte header (uint16LE format=0x0003, uint16LE sampleRate, uint32LE sampleCount) followed by exactly `sampleCount` bytes of unsigned 8-bit PCM. Verified across all 55 DS\* lumps in shareware DOOM1.WAD: every lump has format=3 and `lumpSize === 8 + sampleCount` with zero slack. 54 of 55 lumps sample at 11025 Hz — the sole exception is DSITMBK (item/backpack pickup) at 22050 Hz. The 2 documented DMX padding bytes live at indices 8 and lumpSize-1 of the lump (i.e. samples[0] and samples[sampleCount-1]); DOOM1.WAD does not use the 16-byte pad+pad pattern that chocolate-doom's ExpandSoundData strips conditionally. Separately, DP\* PC-speaker siblings use a 4-byte header (uint16LE format=0 + uint16LE commandCount) followed by `commandCount` command bytes and are NOT parseable with the DS\* DMX parser (DP lumps are format=0, not format=3). Lump-size range for DS\* in DOOM1.WAD: minSampleCount=197 (shortest sfx), maxSampleCount=18592 (DSBAREXP barrel explosion).
- source: Direct parse of all DS\*/DP\* lumps in D:\Projects\bun-win32\doom\universal-doom\DOOM1.WAD via parseSfxLump; Doom 1.9 i_sound.c DMX format layout; F-019 (DP/DS lump pairing in DOOM1.WAD); F-028 (DMX format summary) (step 15-001)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 15-002 eight-channel-allocator (allocator keys SFX instances by DS\* name + mobj origin; caller fetches via parseSfxLump before enqueuing), 15-003 attenuation-and-stereo-separation (attenuation multiplies against playableSampleCount not sampleCount so first/last padding bytes never contribute audible energy), 15-006 pcm-mixer (mixer reads `samples` buffer starting at `playableSampleStart` for `playableSampleCount` bytes at 11025 Hz with 4x upsample to 44100 Hz per F-033; DSITMBK requires 2x upsample instead of 4x so the mixer must key resampling on sampleRate not a constant), 15-012 audio-parity-harness (SHA-256 of concatenated raw `samples` buffers per DS\* lump name forms a stable oracle; DSITMBK's 22050 Hz special case must be called out explicitly in any DMX-format check)

## F-153

- fact: P_XYMovement has two vanilla-parity touch points easy to miss during direct port: (1) the skull-fly slam reset uses `P_SetMobjState(mo, mo->info->spawnstate)` — pointer-follow through `mobj_t::info`, not `mobjinfo[mo->type].spawnstate`. Under the standard spawn path these are equivalent because `mobj.info` is assigned `MOBJINFO[type]` at spawn, but DEHACKED patches or custom spawn paths that rebind `info` make the distinction load-bearing. (2) After the sub-step do-while loop closes, vanilla evaluates `if (player && player->cheats & CF_NOMOMENTUM) { momx = momy = 0; return; }` BEFORE the MF_MISSILE/MF_SKULLFLY early-return and BEFORE the friction block. CF_NOMOMENTUM = 4 in d_player.h `cheat_t` enum (CF_NOCLIP=1, CF_GODMODE=2, CF_NOMOMENTUM=4). The flag is a debug aid (not an ID/KF-style cheat) that zeros horizontal momentum every tic without running friction — makes the player stop on a dime after every move completes. Vanilla's P_ExplodeMissile (same file) uses `mobjinfo[mo->type].deathstate`, NOT `mo->info->deathstate`, so the `info` pointer is only load-bearing for the skull-fly slam path.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 p_mobj.c `P_XYMovement` lines 119-243 + `P_ExplodeMissile` lines 98-115 (via WebFetch of the master branch URL); d_player.h cheat_t enum lines 59-65; F-094, F-095 (mobj lifecycle) (step 09-005 audit pass)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 10-008 powerup-timers-and-palette-effects (cheats subsystem wires `player.cheats` as a typed number field; xyMovement already reads it defensively via `hasNoMomentumCheat` helper so no additional integration required — just populate `player.cheats`); 16-001 default-cfg-parser (CF_NOMOMENTUM is not persisted to config; cheats are runtime-only so the cfg parser skips it); 17-003 scripted-input-core-mechanics (scripted-input tests that toggle CF_NOMOMENTUM must flip the bit on `mobj.player.cheats` between tics and re-run xyMovement to see zero-momentum frames); 17-008 vanilla-quirk-regression-suite (regression tests for both quirks: (a) skull-fly slam still transitions to spawnstate after DEHACKED-style info rebinding — verify by setting `mobj.info` to a synthesized MobjInfo with a different spawnstate than MOBJINFO[mobj.type] and confirming the state transition follows `mobj.info`; (b) CF_NOMOMENTUM player skips friction — verify frame-by-frame momentum sequence is exactly [startMom, 0, 0, 0, ...] rather than the geometric friction decay [startMom, startMom*0xE800>>16, ...]).

## F-152

- fact: Eight-channel SFX allocator (s_sound.c S_GetChannel / S_StopChannel / S_StopSound) lives in src/audio/channels.ts (~280 lines). Vanilla snd_channels=8 is fixed-size; each channel_t slot stores {sfxinfo, origin, handle, pitch}. The allocation algorithm runs two ordered loops: (1) free-or-origin loop scans cnum=0..snd_channels and breaks on the FIRST slot meeting either `!sfxinfo` (free slot wins, no eviction) OR `(origin && origin == channel.origin)` (origin match wins via S_StopChannel + reuse); (2) eviction loop runs ONLY when loop 1 reached cnum==snd_channels (all slots occupied with non-matching origins) and breaks on the FIRST slot meeting `channel.sfxinfo->priority >= sfxinfo->priority` (i.e. less-or-equally-important sound). Returns -1 (mapped to null in TS) when every occupied slot holds a strictly more-important sound. **Priority is INVERTED: lower numeric value = more important** (e.g. telept=32 is more important than pistol=64, plat-stop=100 is least important). The `>=` test therefore allows equal-priority kicks (a 9th pistol shot evicts cnum=0's pistol). Origin dedup loop guards on `if (origin && ...)` so origin=NULL requests never participate in dedup — multiple anonymous (UI / global) sounds stack in different slots. The TS module is PURE: zero Win32 bindings, zero audio playback, zero global mutable state; each ChannelTable is an isolated mutable object. Exports: 8 constants (NUM_CHANNELS=8, CHANNEL_FREE_SFX=null, CHANNEL_NO_ORIGIN=null, CHANNEL_FREE_HANDLE=0, CHANNEL_FREE_PRIORITY=0, CHANNEL_FREE_PITCH=0, NORM_PRIORITY=64, NORM_PITCH=128); 3 interfaces (Channel{sfxId|null, origin|null, priority, handle, pitch}, ChannelTable{channels[], capacity}, AllocateChannelRequest); 8 public functions (createChannelTable, isChannelFree, findFreeChannel, findChannelByOrigin, findEvictableChannel, stopChannel, stopSound, allocateChannel, getOccupiedChannelCount). Parity invariants locked by 54-test suite: NUM_CHANNELS=8 and NORM_PRIORITY=64 and NORM_PITCH=128 exact; createChannelTable rejects 0/-1/non-integer/NaN capacities; allocateChannel free-slot path fills cnum=0..7 in ascending order; allocateChannel origin-dedup path reuses the matching slot WITHOUT searching for free slots first (vanilla early break); allocateChannel anonymous-origin (null) requests never trigger origin dedup; allocateChannel eviction path picks FIRST evictable cnum (priority >= request); allocateChannel returns null when all 8 slots hold strictly-higher-importance sounds; stopChannel / stopSound clear all slot fields back to free defaults; stopSound only stops the FIRST matching origin (vanilla `break`); stopChannel ignores out-of-range cnums without throwing.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 s_sound.c `S_GetChannel` (verbatim per WebFetch on the master branch URL); s_sound.c constants (snd_channels=8, NORM_PRIORITY=64, NORM_PITCH=128, NORM_SEP=128, S_CLOSE_DIST=200<<FRACBITS, S_CLIPPING_DIST=1200<<FRACBITS, S_STEREO_SWING=96<<FRACBITS); sounds.c S_sfx[] priority table (pistol=64, telept=32, plat-stop=100); F-026 (sfx-priority-eviction quirk); F-028 (DMX format and distance attenuation); F-151 (DS\* parser) (step 15-002); confirmed against src/audio/channels.ts (~280 lines) and test/audio/channel-allocation.test.ts (54 tests, 126 expect() calls across 12 describe groups).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 15-003 attenuation-and-stereo-separation (S_AdjustSoundParams runs BEFORE S_GetChannel and computes vol/sep — caller passes priority + handles attenuation upstream; the channel allocator does not see vol/sep, only the priority for eviction); 15-005 sound-start-stop-update-order (caller sequence is S_AdjustSoundParams -> S_StopSound(origin) -> S_GetChannel(origin, sfx); the channel allocator's allocateChannel is the S_GetChannel half — caller composes stopSound+allocateChannel in that order to mirror S_StartSound; S_StopChannel's usefulness-- bookkeeping on sfxinfo is the SFX cache's concern, not the channel table); 15-006 pcm-mixer (mixer iterates table.channels reading samples from each slot's sfxId-resolved SfxLump.samples and respects per-slot pitch + handle for hardware compositing); 15-011 music-device-integration (channel allocator is digital sfx only — music has its own MIDI/MUS scheduler); 17-010 final gate (channel allocation is in the demo-replay determinism scope: same priority+origin sequence must produce same cnum assignments tic-by-tic; common porting mistakes to flag in 17-010 quirk-regression suite: (a) reversed priority comparison `<= " instead of `>=`would make HIGH-importance sounds evictable instead of protected; (b) loop 1 free-slot break before origin check would miss origin dedup when free slots exist; (c) loop 1 origin check WITHOUT `origin &&`guard would crash on NULL-origin slots or cause spurious dedup against the default free-slot origin=null; (d) loop 2 search starting from cnum=last-loop1-cnum instead of 0 would skip earlier evictable slots; (e) S_StopChannel that doesn't reset`origin` would leak the last origin pointer into the next allocation's dedup check; (f) S_StopSound looping past the first match would stop multiple channels with the same origin which vanilla never does; (g) returning the slot index without populating sfxId/origin/priority would let the mixer read stale fields).

## F-154

- fact: Spatial attenuation + stereo separation (s_sound.c `S_AdjustSoundParams`) lives in src/audio/spatial.ts (~280 lines). Exports: **9 constants** (S_CLOSE_DIST=200\*FRACUNIT=13107200 matching s_sound.c `#define S_CLOSE_DIST (200*FRACUNIT)` — distance below which volume is not attenuated; S_CLIPPING_DIST=1200\*FRACUNIT=78643200 matching `#define S_CLIPPING_DIST (1200*FRACUNIT)` — distance above which sound is inaudible (except on MAP08 where it clamps); S_ATTENUATOR=1000 matching `#define S_ATTENUATOR ((S_CLIPPING_DIST - S_CLOSE_DIST) >> FRACBITS)` derived constant = (78643200 - 13107200) >> 16 = 1000 — the linear-rolloff denominator for `vol = snd_SfxVolume * (S_CLIPPING_DIST - approx_dist) / S_ATTENUATOR`; S_STEREO_SWING=96\*FRACUNIT=6291456 matching `#define S_STEREO_SWING (96*FRACUNIT)` — the stereo pan swing amplitude in fixed-point; NORM_SEP=128 matching `#define NORM_SEP 128` — the default center-panning separation value; BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME=15 matching the vanilla MAP08 branch's volume floor; BOSS_MAP_NUMBER=8 matching vanilla's `gamemap == 8` special-case guard; MIN_STEREO_SEP=32 the minimum separation value after S_STEREO_SWING swing; MAX_STEREO_SEP=224 the maximum separation value after S_STEREO_SWING swing); **4 interfaces** (SpatialListener{x, y, angle} — listener position in map coordinates and 32-bit BAM facing angle; SpatialSource{x, y} — source position in map coordinates; AdjustSoundParams{listener, source, sfxVolume, isBossMap} — full input structure for adjustSoundParams; AdjustSoundResult{audible, volume, separation} — the output tuple with audible bool, volume 0..sfxVolume integer, separation MIN_STEREO_SEP..MAX_STEREO_SEP integer); **1 public function** `adjustSoundParams(params: AdjustSoundParams): AdjustSoundResult` which computes the vanilla S_AdjustSoundParams return values: (1) approx_dist = approxDist2D(source.x - listener.x, source.y - listener.y) = |dx| + |dy| - min(|dx|,|dy|)/2 matching vanilla P_AproxDistance's Manhattan-minus-half-min formula; (2) if !isBossMap && approx_dist > S_CLIPPING_DIST return {audible:false, volume:0, separation:NORM_SEP} — the out-of-range branch; (3) rawAngle = R_PointToAngle2(listener.x, listener.y, source.x, source.y) uses the octant-based tantoangle LUT from core/trig.ts; (4) rel_angle = rawAngle + (0xffffffff - listener.angle) — this is the vanilla off-by-one quirk where the listener-angle subtraction uses `0xffffffff` (all-bits-set) instead of the true 2's-complement `-listener.angle`, producing a relative angle that is off by 1 (2^-32 of a full rotation) for non-zero listener.angle; (5) fineIdx = (rel_angle >>> ANGLETOFINESHIFT) & FINEMASK for the 8192-entry finesine table lookup; (6) sep = NORM_SEP - (fixedMul(S_STEREO_SWING, finesine[fineIdx]) >> FRACBITS); (7) if approx_dist < S_CLOSE_DIST: volume = sfxVolume (close-range flat passthrough); else if isBossMap: clamped = min(approx_dist, S_CLIPPING_DIST); ramp = (S_CLIPPING_DIST - clamped) >> FRACBITS; volume = BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME + trunc((sfxVolume - BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME) \* ramp / S_ATTENUATOR); else (non-boss normal range): ramp = (S_CLIPPING_DIST - approx_dist) >> FRACBITS; volume = trunc(sfxVolume \* ramp / S_ATTENUATOR). Vanilla off-by-one quirk: s_sound.c line `angle = angle + (0xffffffff - listener->angle)` is the SAFE 32-bit equivalent of `angle - listener->angle` under unsigned overflow EXCEPT when listener->angle == 0, in which case `0xffffffff - 0 = 0xffffffff` instead of `-0 = 0`; this shifts fineIdx by 1 when listener.angle=0 causing finesine[8191]=-25 lookup that produces sep=129 for a source AT the listener position (same x,y) instead of sep=128 — this is the "same-position sep=129" observable behavior locked by the test suite. MAP08 floor-of-15 branch: on `gamemap == 8` (THE BOSS map — shareware E1M8 is NOT this branch — vanilla s_sound.c only dispatches this branch for gamemode == commercial && gamemap == 8 which is MAP08 The Earth Base / MAP08 Tricks and Traps depending on which IWAD); the branch (a) clamps approx_dist to S_CLIPPING_DIST so far-away sources still produce some audio; (b) uses BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME=15 as the volume floor; (c) scales the remaining (sfxVolume - BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME) range linearly across the S_CLOSE_DIST..S_CLIPPING_DIST span; this is the well-known "MAP08 boss music always audible" quirk preserved for demo compat. Architecture: PURE computation — zero Win32 bindings, zero audio playback, zero drawing, zero asset loading, zero global mutable state; imports only from core/angle.ts (FINEANGLES, FINEMASK, ANGLETOFINESHIFT, ANG90 for octant dispatch), core/trig.ts (finesine, tantoangle), core/fixed.ts (FRACUNIT, FRACBITS, fixedMul); the function is idempotent and deterministic given the same inputs. The adjustSoundParams output is consumed BEFORE S_GetChannel — the caller sequence is `result = adjustSoundParams(...); if (!result.audible) return; cnum = allocateChannel({priority, ...}); if (cnum !== null) { channels[cnum].handle = I_StartSound(sfx, result.volume, result.separation, pitch); }` matching vanilla s_sound.c's S_StartSound composition. Parity invariants locked by the 49-test suite (test/audio/attenuation.test.ts, 140 expect() calls across 5 describe groups — spatial constants 9 tests / non-boss attenuation curve 12 tests / boss map floor-of-15 10 tests / stereo separation 13 tests / combined behaviour 5 tests): (1) S_CLOSE_DIST=200\*FRACUNIT, S_CLIPPING_DIST=1200\*FRACUNIT, S_ATTENUATOR=1000, S_STEREO_SWING=96\*FRACUNIT, NORM_SEP=128, BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME=15, BOSS_MAP_NUMBER=8 — all exact; (2) non-boss source at approx_dist > S_CLIPPING_DIST returns {audible:false, volume:0, separation:NORM_SEP} with separation forced to NORM_SEP not to the computed swing value (vanilla early return skips the pan swing); (3) non-boss source at approx_dist < S_CLOSE_DIST returns volume = sfxVolume exact (no linear attenuation in the close-range flat zone); (4) non-boss source in the middle range computes volume = trunc(sfxVolume \* (S_CLIPPING_DIST - approx_dist) >> FRACBITS / S_ATTENUATOR) with integer division toward zero via Math.trunc matching C's integer division semantics; (5) boss map source at approx_dist > S_CLIPPING_DIST DOES return audible with volume = BOSS_MAP_MIN_VOLUME=15 (clamped behavior) not {audible:false, volume:0}; (6) boss map source at approx_dist < S_CLOSE_DIST returns volume = sfxVolume (same close-range passthrough as non-boss); (7) boss map source in middle range computes volume = 15 + trunc((sfxVolume - 15) \* ramp / 1000) which can go NEGATIVE when sfxVolume < 15 (e.g. sfxVolume=8 midway produces 15 + trunc(-7 \* 500 / 1000) = 15 + (-3) = 12) — the boss floor is a linear-rolloff ADDITION not a MAX clamp; (8) stereo separation same-position source (dx=dy=0) with listener.angle=0 gives sep=129 — the vanilla off-by-one quirk's load-bearing signature at fineIdx=8191 producing finesine=-25 and sep=128-(-25>>16)=128-(-1)=129 since `(96\*FRACUNIT \* -25) >> FRACBITS = -96 \* 25 / 65536 ≈ -0.036` truncates to 0 under arithmetic-shift-right of negative... wait no the actual math: fixedMul(6291456, -25) uses 16x16 partial-product decomposition = (6291456 \* -25 + (1<<15)) >> 16 which for full-width int32 is -2401 >> 16 = -1 (rounding down under arithmetic shift), so sep = 128 - (-1) = 129; (9) stereo separation source due EAST of east-facing listener (source at (FRACUNIT, 0), listener at (0, 0, ANG0)) gives sep=129 (fineIdx=8191 same as same-position); (10) stereo separation source due NORTH of east-facing listener (source at (0, FRACUNIT), listener at origin facing east) gives sep=33 — finesine[2047]=65535 is the lookup matching 90-degree perpendicular-left swing producing sep=128-(96<<16\*65535>>16>>16)=128-(96\*65535>>16)=128-95=33 clamped to MIN_STEREO_SEP; (11) stereo separation source due SOUTH of east-facing listener (source at (0, -FRACUNIT)) gives sep=224 — finesine[6144]=-65535 is the 270-degree perpendicular-right swing producing sep=128-(-95)=223 wait check: fixedMul(96\*FRACUNIT, -65535) = (96\*FRACUNIT \* -65535) >> 16 ≈ -96\*65535 = -6291360 >> 16 = -96 under truncation toward minus-infinity for arithmetic-shift-right of negatives; sep = 128 - (-96) = 224 clamped to MAX_STEREO_SEP; (12) stereo separation source due WEST of east-facing listener (source at (-FRACUNIT, 0)) gives sep=128 — fineIdx=4095 finesine=25 producing sep=128-(96\*25>>16)=128-0=128 (the swing rounds to zero at the 180-degree anti-parallel point); (13) listener.angle rotations at ANG90 / ANG180 / ANG270 rotate the fineIdx correctly for perpendicular sources matching the 128-sep baseline at the listener-forward direction (east becomes front for ANG0, north becomes front for ANG90, etc.); (14) combined behavior at close range + perpendicular source produces volume = sfxVolume unchanged AND separation = swung value (close range does not disable stereo panning — only extreme distance out-of-range does that); (15) combined behavior on MAP08 + close range produces volume = sfxVolume (NOT 15 + full_ramp — the close-range branch runs BEFORE the boss-vs-non-boss branch in the state machine, so boss map close sounds play at full volume not at floor-of-15).
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 s_sound.c `S_AdjustSoundParams` (verbatim per WebFetch on the master branch URL: `approx_dist = P_AproxDistance(listener->x - source->x, listener->y - source->y); if (gamemap != 8 && approx_dist > S_CLIPPING_DIST) return 0; angle = R_PointToAngle2(listener->x, listener->y, source->x, source->y); if (angle > listener->angle) angle = angle - listener->angle; else angle = angle + (0xffffffff - listener->angle); angle >>= ANGLETOFINESHIFT; *sep = 128 - (FixedMul(S_STEREO_SWING, finesine[angle]) >> FRACBITS); if (approx_dist < S_CLOSE_DIST) *vol = snd_SfxVolume; else if (gamemap == 8) { if (approx_dist > S_CLIPPING_DIST) approx_dist = S_CLIPPING_DIST; *vol = 15 + ((snd_SfxVolume - 15) * ((S_CLIPPING_DIST - approx_dist) >> FRACBITS)) / S_ATTENUATOR; } else { *vol = snd_SfxVolume * ((S_CLIPPING_DIST - approx_dist) >> FRACBITS) / S_ATTENUATOR; } return (*vol > 0);`); s_sound.c constants (#define S_CLOSE_DIST 200<<FRACBITS; #define S_CLIPPING_DIST 1200<<FRACBITS; #define S_STEREO_SWING 96<<FRACBITS; #define NORM_SEP 128; #define S_ATTENUATOR ((S_CLIPPING_DIST - S_CLOSE_DIST) >> FRACBITS)); r_main.c `R_PointToAngle2` octant-based tantoangle LUT; tables.c finesine[] 10240-entry table; p_maputl.c `P_AproxDistance` Manhattan-minus-half-min; F-028 (DMX format and distance attenuation summary); F-151 (DS\* parser); F-152 (channel allocator) (step 15-003); confirmed against src/audio/spatial.ts (~280 lines) and test/audio/attenuation.test.ts (49 tests, 140 expect() calls across 5 describe groups).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future*steps: 15-004 sound-origin-updates (S_UpdateSounds polls active channels per tic and recomputes vol/sep via adjustSoundParams for each channel's origin relative to the listener — the update path consumes the same AdjustSoundResult but skips the audible:false early-return since the sound is already playing; instead it should reduce volume toward 0 and eventually call stopChannel when audible:false is returned for an ongoing sound); 15-005 sound-start-stop-update-order (caller sequence is adjustSoundParams → stopSound(origin) → allocateChannel → I_StartSound; the adjustSoundParams result feeds the I_StartSound volume+separation arguments BEFORE allocation — skipping allocation entirely when !result.audible); 15-006 pcm-mixer (mixer consumes volume (0..sfxVolume) and separation (32..224) per channel per tic to compute left/right gain pair: left_gain = clamp(volume * (256 - separation) / 256, 0, sfxVolume); right*gain = clamp(volume * separation / 256, 0, sfxVolume); this produces the stereo pan with full-volume center and reduced-volume wings); 17-008 vanilla-quirk-regression-suite (common porting mistakes to flag: (a) using `angle - listener->angle` directly without the `+ (0xffffffff - listener->angle)` off-by-one would produce sep=128 exact for same-position sources instead of the vanilla sep=129 signature; (b) computing volume with float division `Math.round` instead of `Math.trunc` would round-up at the midway point producing off-by-one volume values for fractional quotients — C integer division truncates toward zero not away; (c) MAX-clamping the boss-map volume to not-below-15 would diverge from vanilla's linear-rolloff-above-15 formula when sfxVolume<15; (d) skipping the close-range branch for boss maps would floor close-range boss sounds at 15 instead of sfxVolume; (e) using a FIX-based denominator > S_ATTENUATOR (e.g. `>> FRACBITS` the other end) would change the rolloff slope; (f) NORM_SEP=64 (off-by-two) would halve the stereo swing amplitude; (g) S_CLIPPING_DIST=1280 (off-by-80 common typo) would reduce audible radius by 7%); 17-010 final gate (spatial attenuation is in the demo-replay determinism scope indirectly — the mixer output PCM per tic is hashed by audioHash.ts so any adjustSoundParams divergence propagates to the mixed PCM hash; common porting mistakes documented above).

## F-155

- fact: Manual vertical door activation must preserve vanilla's occupied-`specialdata` aliasing quirk from `EV_VerticalDoor`. When a sector already has non-null `specialdata`, repeatable manual door specials `1`, `26`, `27`, `28`, and `117` do not always allocate a new door thinker. If the occupied thinker exposes a numeric `direction` and is already closing (`-1`), open-style repeatable lines mutate that existing thinker in place to reopen it (`direction = 1`). If the occupied thinker instead exposes the numeric `wait` carrier used by vanilla's platform aliasing path, close-style repeatable lines mutate that occupied thinker in place to close immediately by writing the matching close state instead of rejecting the activation. Monster activations keep the same restriction as vanilla: they may reopen an occupied closing thinker, but they may not force the occupied close-line path. This compatibility rule exists because vanilla treats `sector.specialdata` as a generic occupied-thinker pointer on this path and casts it through both door and platform views, so a demo-compatible port cannot assume occupied `specialdata` is always an actual door object.
- source: Chocolate Doom `p_doors.c` `EV_VerticalDoor` occupied-repeatable-line path (`if (sec->specialdata) { door = sec->specialdata; ... } else { ... plat = sec->specialdata; plat->wait = -1; plat->status = down; }`) plus the upstream `p_doors.c` structure definitions showing that vanilla mutates occupied `specialdata` through both `vldoor_t *` and `plat_t *` views on this code path; confirmed against `src/specials/doors.ts` and `test/specials/doors.test.ts` regression coverage for both the occupied `direction` reopen case and the occupied `wait` close case.
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 12-003 door-thinker-tick (preserve the numeric `direction` states that `evVerticalDoor` mutates on occupied thinkers, especially `DoorDirection.closing = -1` and `DoorDirection.up = 1`, so repeatable manual lines can reopen an occupied closing thinker without allocating a replacement); 12-004 platform-specials (the platform implementation is the other half of the aliasing quirk because vanilla's close-line occupied path writes through a platform-shaped view of `sector.specialdata`; keep the shared occupancy contract stable if thinker families continue to share sector ownership); 17-008 vanilla-quirk-regression-suite (lock the two load-bearing failures this audit found: allocating a fresh door on occupied repeatable manual lines, and rejecting occupied close-line activations unless `sector.specialdata` is already typed as a `VerticalDoor`).

## F-157

- fact: Finale parity has two load-bearing details that were easy to drift in docs: (1) `d_englsh.h` `E4TEXT` ends with the lowercase stanza `potential pain and gibbitude as a nation / of demons run amok among our cities. / / next stop, hell on earth!` and not the alternate "potential danger" wording; (2) Chocolate Doom's Doom-family `F_StartFinale` starts every episode with `mus_victor`, then `F_Ticker` switches to `mus_bunny` only on the `Text -> ArtScreen` transition for episode 3. `startFinale()` therefore emits only the initial music cue and `tickFinale()` owns the episode-3 transition cue.
- source: Chocolate Doom `d_englsh.h` `E4TEXT`; Chocolate Doom `f_finale.c` `F_StartFinale` and `F_Ticker`; confirmed against `src/ui/finale.ts` and `test/ui/finale.test.ts` during the 14-007 audit pass.
- confidence: high
- verified: verified

## F-157

- fact: Per-tic sound-origin update pass (s*sound.c `S_UpdateSounds`) lives in src/audio/soundOrigins.ts (~330 lines). Exports: **2 constants** (SOUND_UPDATE_LINK_MIN_VOLUME=1 matching vanilla `if (volume < 1) S_StopChannel` strict-less-than threshold; CHANNEL_UPDATE_STATE_UNUSED frozen placeholder `{isPlaying:false, sourcePosition:null, linkVolumeAdjust:null}` for free-slot filler); **1 type alias** (SoundUpdateActionKind = 'stop' | 'update-params'); **3 interfaces** (ChannelUpdateState{isPlaying:boolean, sourcePosition:SpatialSource|null, linkVolumeAdjust:number|null} — per-channel host/world snapshot indexed by cnum; SoundUpdateAction{kind, cnum, handle, volume?, separation?} — host-side effect record with `handle` preserved pre-clear so I_StopSound still works after the slot is freed; UpdateSoundsRequest{table, listener, listenerOrigin, sfxVolume, isBossMap, channelState[]} — full input surface with channelState length strictly equal to table.capacity); **2 public functions** (`updateSounds(request): SoundUpdateAction[]` runs the vanilla algorithm in order: (a) skip slot when channel.sfxId===null; (b) emit kind:'stop' action and stopChannel when state.isPlaying===false; (c) volume = sfxVolume baseline; (d) if state.linkVolumeAdjust !== null: volume += linkVolumeAdjust, early-stop when volume < 1 via `<` strict, clamp when volume > sfxVolume; (e) hasRemoteOrigin = channel.origin !== null && channel.origin !== listenerOrigin — anonymous/local slots emit NO mixer action; (f) throw TypeError when remote slot has sourcePosition===null; (g) delegate to adjustSoundParams with the link-adjusted volume as sfxVolume argument; (h) stop when !audible, else emit kind:'update-params' carrying result.volume + result.separation + pre-clear handle; `buildChannelUpdateStates(table, resolve): ChannelUpdateState[]` convenience helper that invokes resolve(cnum) once per slot in ascending order). The function is PURE modulo mutation of the passed-in ChannelTable (via stopChannel from channels.ts) — zero Win32 bindings, zero I_UpdateSound/I_SoundIsPlaying/I_UpdateSoundParams/I_StopSound direct calls, zero global mutable state; the host bridge (future step) is responsible for the I*\* syscalls before/after updateSounds. Parity-critical details locked by the 34-test suite (test/audio/sound-origins.test.ts, 67 expect() calls across 9 describe groups — constants 2 / input-validation 3 / empty-anonymous-local 4 / isPlaying-false-reap 4 / remote-origin-adjust 5 / sfx-link-branch 7 / multi-channel 4 / parity-edge 3 / helper 2): (1) link-stop fires BEFORE origin check via vanilla `continue` — a link that drops volume < 1 stops the channel even when it's anonymous or local, locked by the test "link-stop fires BEFORE the origin check — a remote slot also stops"; (2) strict `<` threshold: volume=0 stops but volume=1 survives, locked by paired tests; (3) link clamp direction is `> sfxVolume` not `>=`, so sfxVolume itself passes unclamped; (4) local slots (origin === listenerOrigin) keep the initial params from S_StartSound — the computed volume is DISCARDED, locked by "link does NOT reach the mixer for local slots" and "listener==origin skips adjust even when sourcePosition is far away"; (5) anonymous slots (origin === null) also skip adjust, mirroring vanilla `if (c->origin && ...)` guard; (6) isPlaying===false emits stop even for local / anonymous / remote — vanilla's handle-reap branch is unconditional, locked by three targeted tests per slot type; (7) handle field is captured from channel.handle BEFORE stopChannel clears the slot so the returned action carries the live handle, locked by the 0xdeadbeef preservation test; (8) actions preserve ascending cnum order for mixed channels, locked by the three-channel test with mixed action kinds; (9) adjustSoundParams output is forwarded verbatim — volume + separation — as the action payload, locked by expected === computed comparison tests; (10) MAP08 boss-map branch propagation keeps far sounds audible via isBossMap=true flag, locked by the floor-of-15 clamp test; (11) sfxVolume=0 produces an inaudible result for any remote distance and triggers stop, locked by the sfxVolume=0 test; (12) channelState length validation throws RangeError on both shorter and longer arrays; (13) remote slot without sourcePosition throws TypeError; (14) table is mutated so a stopped slot is re-allocatable in the same frame; (15) updateSounds emits at most one action per channel per pass — link-stop does not double-emit. Vanilla quirks preserved: the `c->origin && listener != c->origin` guard means local-origin sounds (player weapon/land/pain) keep their initial full-volume / NORM_SEP parameters across every tic — a port that always calls adjust would re-pan player footsteps, which is audible in demo parity.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 s_sound.c `S_UpdateSounds` (verbatim per WebFetch on the master branch URL: `I_UpdateSound(); for (cnum=0; cnum<snd_channels; cnum++) { c = &channels[cnum]; sfx = c->sfxinfo; if (c->sfxinfo) { if (I_SoundIsPlaying(c->handle)) { volume = snd_SfxVolume; sep = NORM_SEP; if (sfx->link) { volume += sfx->volume; if (volume < 1) { S_StopChannel(cnum); continue; } else if (volume > snd_SfxVolume) volume = snd_SfxVolume; } if (c->origin && listener != c->origin) { audible = S_AdjustSoundParams(listener, c->origin, &volume, &sep); if (!audible) S_StopChannel(cnum); else I_UpdateSoundParams(c->handle, volume, sep); } } else S_StopChannel(cnum); } }`); s_sound.c `S_StopChannel` reference (clears c->sfxinfo and c->origin and decrements c->sfxinfo->usefulness — the usefulness bookkeeping is the sfx-cache's concern per F-152 and not modeled in channels.ts/soundOrigins.ts); F-028 (DMX format + distance attenuation); F-151 (DS\* parser); F-152 (eight-channel allocator); F-154 (adjustSoundParams) (step 15-004); confirmed against src/audio/soundOrigins.ts (~330 lines) and test/audio/sound-origins.test.ts (34 tests, 67 expect() calls across 9 describe groups).

(f) running the link branch AFTER the isPlaying check inversion would skip the link-stop on handles that just finished playing — vanilla runs it inside the isPlaying-true branch only, so the ordering matters for the link-stop-of-finished-handle edge case; (g) using handle=0 as sentinel for "no handle" could collide with legitimate 0-handle allocations — our impl passes handle through verbatim including 0 which matches vanilla's no-remap behavior; (h) returning a free slot's state (sfxId===null) in the action array would emit spurious actions — our impl skips free slots entirely; (i) mutating channelState entries in place during iteration would corrupt the pass — our impl treats channelState as read-only from the function's perspective); 17-010 final gate (sound-origin updates are in the demo-replay determinism scope — the mixer output PCM per tic is hashed by audioHash.ts so any updateSounds divergence propagates to the mixed PCM hash via volume+separation+stopped-channels; additionally the per-tic action list is a deterministic function of the channel table + listener + per-channel state, so same inputs across runs produce same actions in same order across 35 Hz tics).

## F-158

- fact: Vanilla `S_StartSound` composition (s_sound.c) lives in src/audio/soundSystem.ts (~447 lines). Exports: **6 constants** (NUMSFX=109 matching sounds.h's enum terminator; SFX_ID_MIN=1 and SFX_ID_MAX=NUMSFX=109 bracketing the valid `sfx_id` range with the vanilla off-by-one quirk where `<= NUMSFX` accepts the terminator itself; START_SOUND_LINK_MIN_VOLUME=1 mirroring SOUND_UPDATE_LINK_MIN_VOLUME from F-157 so start and update paths share the same `<1` strict threshold; PITCH_CLAMP_MIN=0 and PITCH_CLAMP_MAX=255 matching the i_sound.c `Clamp(x)` bounds); **1 type alias** (`SfxPitchClass = 'saw' | 'static' | 'default'` with caller-resolved classification — 'saw' for sfx_sawup(10)..sfx_sawhit(13) with mask=15/swing=±8, 'static' for sfx_itemup(32)+sfx_tink(87) no perturbation, 'default' for every other sfx with mask=31/swing=±16); **3 interfaces** (StartSoundRequest{sfxId, priority, pitchClass, origin, sourcePosition, listener, listenerOrigin, sfxVolume, isBossMap, linkVolumeAdjust, linkPitch, rng, table} — 13 fields covering validation input + link branch + adjust branch + perturbation RNG + allocator target; StartSoundStartedResult{kind:'started', cnum, sfxId, volume, separation, pitch} carrying everything the host bridge needs to dispatch I_StartSound; StartSoundDroppedResult{kind:'link-silenced'|'inaudible'|'no-channel'} for the three vanilla early-returns); **1 result union type** (StartSoundResult); **1 result-kind alias** (StartSoundResultKind = 'started'|'link-silenced'|'inaudible'|'no-channel'); **1 public function** (`startSound(request): StartSoundResult`).
