the harness can hash ACTION SEQUENCES returned by lifecycle calls as a standalone parity oracle BEFORE any OPL synthesis runs — a divergence in the stop-song/play-song sequence or the intro→introa substitution would surface here before any audio bytes are produced; additionally the per-tic `advanceMusic` output is a deterministic function of (score + initial state + tics-advanced) so same inputs across runs produce same DispatchedMusEventEntry sequences); 17-002 bundled-demo-sync (title loop polls `S_ChangeMusic(mus_intro, true)` every tic during the title sequence — the same-music no-op is LOAD-BEARING for demo-tic determinism because a port that re-registers the song every tic would churn the OPL register state and desync demo playback audio); (b) applying the substitution unconditionally (not gating on the OPL device check) would substitute mus_introa even on GUS/MIDI devices where D_INTRO is the canonical choice, producing the OPL-tuned track on non-OPL hardware; (h) resetting the per-channel velocity cache mid-song (e.g., on pause/resume) would drop all dynamics on the first post-resume null-velocity play-note, audible as a flat-dynamics phrase on pause recovery — the fresh-scheduler-only-on-changeMusic semantic is LOAD-BEARING; (i) returning false from `isMusicPlaying` while paused would break menu logic that polls this predicate on mode transitions — vanilla `I_MusicIsPlaying` returns true for paused songs; (j) applying the substitution AFTER the NUMMUSIC range check would reject MUS_INTRO for a port that accidentally sets its sounds.h enum differently — vanilla applies substitution BEFORE validation so the invariant is "the substitution rule respects the device and WAD but not the validity of the input number"); ## F-165

- fact: Audio parity harness (src/audio/audioParity.ts) composes the digital sfx pipeline (channels.ts allocator, spatial.ts distance/stereo math, soundSystem.ts start path, soundOrigins.ts update pass, pcmMixer.ts mixer) and the music pipeline (musicSystem.ts lifecycle + musScheduler.ts event dispatch) behind a single per-tic step producing the deterministic mixed sfx buffer consumed by the audio-hash oracle (audioHash.ts, F-037 / O-017). Exports 3 numeric constants: HARNESS*TIC_RATE_HZ=35 (equals PRIMARY_TARGET.ticRateHz, the F-010 vanilla tic rate); HARNESS_SAMPLES_PER_TIC_STEREO=2520 (equals SAMPLES_PER_TIC * 2 = 1260 frames \_ 2 channels, the exact mix-buffer length emitted per runHarnessTic); HARNESS_SHA256_HEX_LENGTH=64 (32 bytes * 2 hex chars for the upper-case SHA-256 digest). Exports 4 interfaces: AudioParityHarnessOptions{music?, outputSampleRate?, ticRateHz?, channelCapacity?} forwarding music options to createMusicSystem and allowing sample-rate / tic-rate / channel-capacity overrides; AudioParityHarness{channelTable, music, voices: Map<cnum, MixerVoice>, outputSampleRate, ticRateHz, samplesPerTic, tic} — the mutable harness state owning the channel table, music system, and voice map; StartHarnessSfxInput{sfxLump, request} — parsed DMX lump plus the StartSoundRequest to forward; AudioParityTicOutput{tic, sfxFrames: Int16Array, activeChannels, dispatchedMusicEvents, sfxHash: string} — the per-tic snapshot. Exports 14 public functions: createAudioParityHarness(options?) seeds the channel table via createChannelTable(channelCapacity), seeds the music system via createMusicSystem(options.music), validates outputSampleRate % ticRateHz === 0 (RangeError otherwise so samplesPerTic stays integer), validates positive-integer constraints on all rates and capacity, and returns a fresh harness with voices = new Map() and tic = 0. startHarnessSfx(harness, {sfxLump, request}) forwards to startSound(request), asserts request.table === harness.channelTable (RangeError otherwise to prevent cross-harness aliasing), and on a 'started' result expands the playable region of the SfxLump via expandDmxSamples(playable, sfxLump.sampleRate, harness.outputSampleRate) → createMixerVoice(expanded, result.volume, result.separation) → installs the voice in harness.voices.set(cnum, voice) (replacing any prior voice on the same cnum, matching vanilla S_StartSound stopSound-before-allocate ordering); drop variants (link-silenced, inaudible, no-channel) leave the voice map unchanged. stopHarnessSfxByOrigin(harness, origin) delegates to findChannelByOrigin + channels.stopSound and deletes the matching voice entry; returns the freed cnum or null. updateHarnessSfx(harness, request) asserts table identity, forwards to updateSounds(request), then iterates the returned action list: 'stop' kind deletes the voice, 'update-params' kind rewrites the voice leftGain/rightGain IN PLACE via computeStereoGains(action.volume, action.separation) so the next mix uses the updated pan/volume (matching vanilla I_UpdateSoundParams(handle, volume, sep) which updates the device per-channel state WITHOUT restarting the sample). Music wrappers (changeHarnessMusic / startHarnessMusic / stopHarnessMusic / pauseHarnessMusic / resumeHarnessMusic / setHarnessMusicVolume) forward verbatim to musicSystem.ts and return the same MusicDeviceAction[] the caller would have seen directly. isHarnessMusicPlaying(harness) delegates to isMusicPlaying(harness.music). runHarnessTic(harness) advances the music scheduler by exactly one game tic via advanceMusic(harness.music, 1) (returns empty when paused/unloaded because the scheduler halts under pause), mixes every active voice into a fresh samplesPerTic*2 Int16Array via mixVoices([...harness.voices.values()], harness.samplesPerTic) (voices whose final sample lands in this tic contribute it and are then flagged 'finished' by the mixer), reaps every voice whose finished flag is true AND every voice whose channel slot is free (keeps voice map in sync with ChannelTable without touching the table), increments harness.tic, and hashes the stereo buffer with SHA-256 via hashPcmBuffer; returns {tic (pre-increment value matching AudioHashEntry.tic), sfxFrames, activeChannels (post-reap occupied count from getOccupiedChannelCount), dispatchedMusicEvents, sfxHash (upper-case hex)}. hashPcmBuffer(buffer: Int16Array) hashes the raw little-endian byte view via new Bun.CryptoHasher('sha256').update(new Uint8Array(buffer.buffer, buffer.byteOffset, buffer.byteLength)).digest('hex').toUpperCase() — matches the rest of the oracle hash machinery (O-001 / F-011 / F-012 file-hash manifests, PRIMARY_TARGET hashes, all stored in upper-case hex). toAudioHashEntry(output) converts a tic output into a frozen AudioHashEntry{tic, hash, activeChannels} ready for the audioHash.ts oracle payload. 47-test suite in test/audio/audio-parity.test.ts locks every parity invariant: constants (3 tests), createAudioParityHarness defaults + overrides + validation (7 tests), startHarnessSfx (5 tests — started path installs voice, table-identity guard, link-silenced skip, no-channel skip, same-origin voice replacement), stopHarnessSfxByOrigin (3 tests — origin match frees slot+voice, no-match no-op, null-origin no-op), updateHarnessSfx (3 tests — reap on not-playing, gain rewrite on update-params, table-identity guard), runHarnessTic sfx mixing (8 tests — Int16Array length = samplesPerTic*2, tic increment + pre-increment reporting, silent mix = 2520 zeros, activeChannels = occupied count, 64-char upper-case hex hash, silent-mix determinism across harnesses, identical-input hash equality across 5 tics, pistol vs shotgun hash divergence, finished-voice reaping, unfinished-voice carry-across), harness music integration (7 tests — isHarnessMusicPlaying reflects state, dispatchedMusicEvents during changeMusic, MUS_TICKS_PER_GAME_TIC elapsed per tic, pause halts dispatch + sfx continues, resume restarts dispatch, startHarnessMusic looping=false, setHarnessMusicVolume emits set-volume), hashPcmBuffer (4 tests — 64-char upper-case hex format, determinism, one-byte-flip divergence, empty-buffer canonical E3B0C442... SHA-256), toAudioHashEntry (1 test — frozen AudioHashEntry matches oracle shape), audio parity edge cases (3 tests — overlapping anonymous shots distinct cnums, voice position advances by samplesPerTic per tic, stop prevents next-tic mixing). Vanilla parity-critical behaviours preserved: (1) mix buffer is always exactly SAMPLES_PER_TIC * 2 Int16 slots — a port that emits a different frame count per tic would desync the audio-hash oracle; (2) voices are reaped AFTER the mix pass so the last sample still contributes (matching SDL_mixer consume-then-flag behaviour); (3) voices are also reaped when the underlying channel slot is free so orphan voices can never leak PCM into the next tic; (4) the harness defers to the underlying modules for every parity decision (pitch perturbation, link-volume early stop, same-music no-op, resume-before-stop ordering, unconditional setMusicVolume emission, pause-halts-scheduler) — this module is a composition layer that DOES NOT introduce new behaviour; (5) SHA-256 hex is UPPERCASE to match the rest of the oracle machinery; (6) activeChannels reports the ChannelTable occupied count (not voice-map size) so the oracle divergence-isolation signal between wrong-mix and wrong-channel-count stays faithful to vanilla snd_channels occupancy. Module-load sanity checks assert AUDIO_MAX_CHANNELS === NUM_CHANNELS and AUDIO_SAMPLE_RATE === DEFAULT_OUTPUT_SAMPLE_RATE so the oracle constants and pcmMixer defaults cannot silently drift apart. Architecture: PURE module — zero Win32 bindings, zero audio device calls, zero global mutable state beyond the caller-supplied harness; per-tic allocation budget is one Int16Array(samplesPerTic \* 2) for the mix buffer plus the dispatched-event array from advanceMusic; voice storage is Map<cnum, MixerVoice> keyed by channel index so lookup / reap / replacement are all O(1).
- source: src/audio/audioParity.ts (step 15-012); chocolate-doom 2.2.1 s_sound.c composition pattern (S_StartSound → S_GetChannel → I_StartSound → per-tic mixer pump + S_UpdateSounds at top of D_Display); i_sdlsound.c mixer callback (fills N stereo frames of signed-16-bit PCM per audio-device hardware interrupt, accumulating contributions from all active voices); F-010 (35 Hz vanilla tic rate); F-033 (44100 Hz output sample rate, 8 channels, OPL music device); F-037 / O-017 audio-hash oracle format (SHA-256 per SAMPLES_PER_TIC buffer + active channel count, entries sorted ascending by tic); F-151 (SFX lump parser — the parseSfxLump output the harness expands); F-152 (channel allocator — the createChannelTable + allocateChannel + getOccupiedChannelCount the harness delegates to); F-153 (spatial attenuation + stereo — computeStereoGains applied to voice gains); F-154 (sound origins update pass — the updateSounds action loop the harness reconciles); F-157 (sound start/update/stop ordering — startSound link-silenced / inaudible / no-channel / started result branches); F-159 (PCM mixer clipping-and-stepping — expandDmxSamples + createMixerVoice + mixVoices composed here); F-160 / F-161 (MUS parser + scheduler — advanceMusic consumer); F-164 (music device integration — the MusicSystemState the harness owns).

## F-166

- fact: AM_findMinMaxBoundaries in am_map.c initializes the max_x / max_y running sentinels to `-INT_MAX` (0x80000001 in two's complement = -2147483647), NOT to `INT_MIN` (0x80000000 = -2147483648). The min_x / min_y sentinels are `INT_MAX` (0x7FFFFFFF). This asymmetry matters because a map with a single vertex leaves max_x at the sentinel value after the scan (the vanilla scan uses `else if` so a vertex that updated min_x cannot simultaneously update max_x in the same iteration); the resulting max_w = max_x - min_x = `-INT_MAX - vertex.x` triggers deterministic integer wrap rather than the `INT_MIN - vertex.x` wrap. Concretely, `-FIXED_MAX` is the correct TypeScript constant for parity, not `FIXED_MIN`. Real DOOM maps have many vertices so both sentinels produce identical final bounds, but the documented invariant and degenerate-case behavior diverge by exactly one int32 ULP when the max sentinel is initialized wrong. Related step 14-004 audit (2026-04-22) caught a drift where the initial implementation used FIXED_MIN; the fix swaps to -FIXED_MAX to match the reference exactly.
- source: Chocolate Doom am_map.c (AM_findMinMaxBoundaries: `min_x = min_y = INT_MAX; max_x = max_y = -INT_MAX;`); src/ui/automap.ts automapFindMinMaxBoundaries (step 14-004 audit pass); src/core/fixed.ts FIXED_MAX (= 0x7FFF_FFFF).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 17-010 final gate (automap framebuffer CRC oracle runs against the renderer output; the max_x/max_y sentinel value is observable if a future test includes a single-vertex input or a degenerate map — matching vanilla's wrap behavior via -FIXED_MAX (not FIXED_MIN) is the load-bearing parity constraint for automap boundary computation on pathological inputs).

## F-167

- fact: Vanilla Doom `default.cfg` parser surfaces 43 variables in a fixed serialization order (mouse*sensitivity / sfx_volume / music_volume / show_messages / 10 key*\* / 4 mouseb / use_joystick + 4 joyb / screenblocks / detaillevel / 7 snd\_\* / usegamma / 10 chatmacro). Exactly 33 of the 43 values are typed `integer` and 10 are typed `string` (the chat macros). The Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 C-level hardcoded defaults are: `mouse_sensitivity=5`, `sfx_volume=8`, `music_volume=8`, `show_messages=1`, key bindings use DOS scan codes (`key_right=77=0x4D`, `key_left=75=0x4B`, `key_up=72=0x48`, `key_down=80=0x50`, `key_strafeleft=51=0x33`, `key_straferight=52=0x34`, `key_fire=29=0x1D`, `key_use=57=0x39`, `key_strafe=56=0x38`, `key_speed=54=0x36`), mouse buttons `mouseb_fire=0 / mouseb_strafe=1 / mouseb_forward=2`, joystick `use_joystick=0 / joyb_fire=0 / joyb_strafe=1 / joyb_use=3 / joyb_speed=2`, display `screenblocks=9 / detaillevel=0 / usegamma=0`, sound `snd_channels=8 / snd_musicdevice=3 / snd_sfxdevice=3 / snd_sbport=0 / snd_sbirq=0 / snd_sbdma=0 / snd_mport=0`, and the 10 chat macros with their vanilla HUSTR_CHATMACRO\* literal strings ("No" / "I'm ready to kick butt!" / "I'm OK." / "I'm not looking too good!" / "Help!" / "You suck!" / "Next time, scumbag..." / "Come here!" / "I'll take care of it." / "Yes"). The parser delegates integer / string / float handling to the generic primitives in `src/bootstrap/config.ts` (`parseConfigFileContent`, `parseConfigValue`, `buildDefinitionMap`), composes them into a frozen `VanillaDefaultCfg` typed object, and falls back to the hardcoded defaults for any variable missing from the input content. Unknown variable names in the input content are silently ignored (matching Chocolate Doom's `M_LoadDefaultCollection`). The reference bundle's stored `default.cfg` happens to coincide with the hardcoded defaults for every variable except typographic ordering differences, so the parser output of the reference file equals `createDefaultVanillaCfg()` when run on the reference. Key bindings are LOAD-BEARING as DOS scan codes (`key_use=57` is `0x39` space scan code, NOT ASCII 32) — a port that re-interprets these as ASCII / VK codes would misinterpret every configured binding; the `vanilla_keyboard_mapping` flag in `chocolate-doom.cfg` governs any downstream translation but the vanilla parser preserves the raw integer. Chat macros are quoted strings where `parseConfigValue` strips the outer double-quotes but preserves the literal contents including apostrophes (`"I'm OK."`), ellipsis (`"Next time, scumbag..."`), and punctuation — a port that unescapes backslashes or collapses whitespace would desync chat strings against the reference. Integer values accept both decimal (`snd_sbport 544`) and `0x`-prefixed hex (`snd_sbport 0x220`) forms with identical results. Empty quoted strings (`chatmacro5 ""`) parse to the empty JS string. The 41-test suite locks every invariant with 499 expect() calls covering the constant, the definitions table shape, the hardcoded defaults, every single-line parse form (integer / string / Windows line endings / blank lines / unknown variables / repeated variables / negative integers / zero / name-without-value), the reference bundle round-trip, and parity-sensitive edge cases (apostrophes in 3 chat macros, ellipsis preservation, dual-form snd_sbport, DOS-scan-code-vs-ASCII disambiguation for key_use, defaults-not-mutated invariant, definitions-table-not-mutated invariant).
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 m_config.c (doom_defaults_list, CONFIG_VARIABLE_INT macros), g_game.c (key bindings global initializers), m_menu.c (volume / mouse / show_messages / joystick globals), hu_stuff.c (HUSTR_CHATMACRO\* literals), reference/manifests/config-variable-summary.json (step 01-004), reference default.cfg (step 01-007), src/config/defaultCfg.ts + test/config/default-cfg-parse.test.ts (step 16-001).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future*steps: 16-002 host-extra-config-split (the `chocolate-doom.cfg` parser will share the same pattern: typed definition table + typed result object + generic primitives; the 43-variable vanilla namespace in F-167 is disjoint from the 113-variable extended namespace so the two parsers can run independently); 17-010 final gate (default.cfg parser output seeds `snd_channels` / `snd_musicdevice` / `snd_sfxdevice` into `createAudioParityHarness` options, `screenblocks` / `detaillevel` into the renderer projection constants, and the `key*\*`bindings into`src/input/keyboardMapping.ts` — the parser is load-bearing on the bootstrap path that reads config BEFORE the first tic, so a divergence here propagates to every downstream oracle via different initial subsystem state).

## F-168

- fact: SlopeDiv must coerce its denominator argument to uint32 before the `< 512` early-return, not just before the divide. The C signature is `SlopeDiv(unsigned num, unsigned den)`, so a caller that hands in a negative int (a stray signed `dx` / `dy` that escaped its `abs()` upstream) is reinterpreted as a very large positive value in C and falls through to the divide; the JS port without the explicit `>>> 0` would short-circuit to SLOPERANGE because `negative < 512` is true under JS signed comparison. The downstream `(num << 3) >>> 0` and `den >>> 8` already model the unsigned arithmetic correctly, so the fix is local: hoist `den = denominator >>> 0` and compare against `512` on the unsigned value. Verified by `slopeDiv(100, -1)` returning 0 (matches C `(100 << 3) / (0xFFFFFFFF >> 8) = 800 / 16777215 = 0`) instead of SLOPERANGE. The numerator does not need an analogous coercion because the only operation it feeds into is `(num << 3) >>> 0`, which already yields the same uint32 bit pattern regardless of whether `num` was signed or unsigned at the JS level.
- source: Chocolate Doom tables.c SlopeDiv + audit of src/core/trig.ts (step 04-006)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 08-006 point-on-side-and-node-traversal (callers there pass `abs(dx)` / `abs(dy)` so the negative-input path is unreachable in practice, but the parity-safe coercion is still the right contract); 17-010

## F-169

- fact: OPL2 20-bit phase wrap-around can be expressed as a single `(phase + delta) & OPL_PHASE_ACCUMULATOR_MASK` without any `Math.floor` / divide step — even for arbitrary negative or int32-sized deltas. JS bitwise `&` applies `ToInt32` (reduction mod 2^32) before masking, and `OPL_PHASE_ACCUMULATOR_MODULO` (1 << 20) divides 2^32 exactly, so the low-20-bit residue is preserved across int32 coercion. The prior `advanced - Math.floor(advanced / MODULO) * MODULO` formulation was correct but strictly slower. Applies to any power-of-two modular counter ≤ 2^31 stored as a JS number. Canonical pattern for future OPL / DSP wrap-arounds: `(accumulator + step) & MASK`.
- source: Audit of 15-010 opl-synthesis-core; src/audio/oplSynth.ts advancePhase after fix
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 15-011 music-device-integration (per-sample carrier / modulator phase loop); 17-010

## F-170

- fact: OPL Total-Level (TL) gain is a 64-entry constant (`tl ∈ [0, 63]`) so the full gain table `10^(-0.75 * tl / 20)` for `tl > 0` with `table[0] = 1` precomputes to 64 float64 values at module load. Exposing it as `OPL_TOTAL_LEVEL_GAIN_TABLE: Float64Array` lets per-sample callers look up the gain directly instead of paying a `Math.pow` call per invocation. The LUT is bitwise-equivalent to the `Math.pow` output at every index, so tests that use `toBe` on `computeTotalLevelGain(tl)` continue to pass without change. The sample-path attenuation pipeline (`applyTotalLevel`) replaces `Math.trunc(sample * gain)` with `(sample * gain) | 0` because `|sample| ≤ 32768` and `0 ≤ gain ≤ 1` keep the product strictly within int32 range where the two truncation operators agree; `| 0` elides the `Math.trunc` function call. Canonical pattern for future DSP-rate scalar LUTs: constant-domain integer inputs with ≤256 entries are cheap to precompute as a typed array at module load.
- source: Audit of 15-010 opl-synthesis-core; src/audio/oplSynth.ts OPL_TOTAL_LEVEL_GAIN_TABLE + applyTotalLevel after fix; canonical DOSBox / MAME OPL emulator TL-table precomputation pattern.
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 15-011 music-device-integration (per-operator TL gain lookup on every sample); 17-010

## F-171

- fact: The Chocolate Doom `chocolate-doom.cfg` extended namespace contains exactly 113 variables with zero overlap against the 43-variable `default.cfg` namespace. Its type split is 104 integers, 7 strings, and 2 floats (`mouse_acceleration`, `libsamplerate_scale`). The pristine C-level defaults differ from the reference file for `screen_width`, `screen_height`, and `screen_bpp` (all `0` before host auto-detect, `640/480/32` in the reference file) and `player_name` (empty string before `I_GetUserName`, `"stevp"` in the reference file). The three compatibility flags `vanilla_savegame_limit`, `vanilla_demo_limit`, and `vanilla_keyboard_mapping` default to `1`; `g_game.c` and `p_saveg.c` show the first two are load-bearing on demo-buffer growth and savegame-size enforcement. `opl_io_port` is stored in canonical hex form (`0x388`) and parses to integer `904`. Modern mouse and joystick extension bindings use `-1` as the unbound or disconnected sentinel, while menu and map key bindings stay in DOS scan-code units (`key_menu_activate = 1` is Escape scan code, not ASCII 27).
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `g_game.c` and `p_saveg.c`; reference `doom/universal-doom/default.cfg`; `src/config/hostConfig.ts`; `test/config/host-config.test.ts`.
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 16-010 vanilla-limit-enforcement; 17-010 final gate

## F-172

- fact: Chocolate Doom demo playback recognizes 3 on-disk demo layouts. Old demos omit the version byte entirely and use a 7-byte header (`skill`, `episode`, `map`, then `playeringame[4]`). Versioned vanilla demos use a 13-byte header (`version`, `skill`, `episode`, `map`, `deathmatch`, `respawnparm`, `fastparm`, `nomonsters`, `consoleplayer`, then `playeringame[4]`). Longtics demos keep the 13-byte header but use version byte `111` and widen each per-player tic command from 4 bytes to 5 bytes. `G_ReadDemoTiccmd` checks for the `0x80` end marker at the START of each tic before reading any player command bytes. Non-longtics angle turns are stored as one unsigned byte shifted left by 8 and then assigned to a signed 16-bit `short`; longtics stores the full angle turn as a signed 16-bit little-endian value. Compared to savegame `ticcmd_t`, demo commands serialize only `forwardmove`, `sidemove`, `angleturn`, and `buttons`; the `consistancy` and `chatchar` fields are omitted from the demo stream entirely.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `g_game.c` (`G_DoPlayDemo`, `G_ReadDemoTiccmd`, `G_BeginRecording`) and `p_saveg.c` (`saveg_read_ticcmd_t`); `src/demo/demoParse.ts`; `test/demo/demo-parse.test.ts` (step 16-003).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 16-004 demo-recorder; 16-005 demo-playback; 17-002 bundled-demo-sync; 17-010 final gate

## F-173

- fact: Chocolate Doom demo recording starts with a `0x20000`-byte buffer (`G_RecordDemo` default `maxsize`) and refuses to record a NEW tic once `demo_p > demoend - 16`; if `vanilla_demo_limit` is disabled, the buffer doubles in size and recording continues. `G_BeginRecording` writes 7-byte old-demo headers (no version/flags/consoleplayer) or 13-byte versioned headers; longtics uses version byte `111` with 5-byte commands, while vanilla Doom 1.9 uses version byte `109` with 4-byte commands. For non-longtics recording, the `lowres_turn` path in `G_BuildTiccmd` quantizes `angleturn` with a signed 16-bit carry: `desired = angleturn + carry`, `stored = (desired + 128) & 0xFF00`, `carry = desired - stored`, so successive small turns accumulate across tics. After bytes are written, `G_WriteDemoTiccmd` rewinds to the command start and immediately re-reads the bytes through `G_ReadDemoTiccmd`, normalizing the in-memory tic command to the exact serialized demo-stream representation. Demo recording serializes only `forwardmove`, `sidemove`, `angleturn`, and `buttons`; savegame-only `consistancy` and `chatchar` remain omitted.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `g_game.c` (`G_RecordDemo`, `G_BeginRecording`, `G_WriteDemoTiccmd`, `G_CheckDemoStatus`, and the `lowres_turn` block in `G_BuildTiccmd`), `p_saveg.c` (`saveg_write_ticcmd_t`), `src/demo/demoRecord.ts`, and `test/demo/demo-record.test.ts` (step 16-004).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 16-005 demo-playback; 16-010 vanilla-limit-enforcement; 17-002 bundled-demo-sync; 17-010 final gate

## F-174

- fact: Chocolate Doom demo playback is a two-phase process: `G_DoPlayDemo` validates the header and seeds runtime flags, while `G_ReadDemoTiccmd` only ends playback when the NEXT read sees `0x80` at the start of a tic. For the C1 Doom 1.9 target, versioned demos must carry version byte `109`; old demos (leading byte `0..4`) are rejected unless old-format playback is explicitly allowed; longtics demos (version `111`) are accepted only when the non-vanilla extension is enabled. During startup, `netdemo` and `netgame` become true if and only if `playeringame[1]` is set or playback was forced via the `-solo-net` / `-netdemo` equivalent flags; slot 2 or 3 alone does NOT trigger net mode because vanilla checks only slot 1. On completion, `G_CheckDemoStatus` resets `demoplayback`, `netdemo`, `netgame`, `deathmatch`, `respawnparm`, `fastparm`, `nomonsters`, and `consoleplayer`, clears only `playeringame[1..3]` (slot 0 is left untouched), and then either advances the attract loop or quits immediately when `singledemo` is set.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `g_game.c` (`G_DoPlayDemo`, `G_ReadDemoTiccmd`, `G_CheckDemoStatus`), `src/demo/demoPlayback.ts`, and `test/demo/demo-playback.test.ts` (step 16-005).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 17-002 bundled-demo-sync; 17-010 final gate

## F-175

- fact: Vanilla Doom savegames start with a fixed 50-byte header written by `P_WriteSaveGameHeader`: 24 bytes of save description (raw bytes, NUL-padded, no terminator if the field is completely full), followed by a 16-byte zero-padded version string field containing `version 109`, then 1 byte each for `gameskill`, `gameepisode`, and `gamemap`, then 4 raw `playeringame` bytes, and finally `leveltime` encoded as a 3-byte big-endian integer (`(leveltime >> 16) & 0xff`, `(leveltime >> 8) & 0xff`, `leveltime & 0xff`). `P_ReadSaveGameHeader` skips the description, compares the full zero-padded version field against the canonical `version 109` string, and returns `false` on version mismatch instead of raising an error. Because `leveltime` is stored in only 3 bytes, savegame writes preserve only the low 24 bits of the runtime integer.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `g_game.c` (`G_DoSaveGame`, `G_DoLoadGame`, comment `Description is a 24 byte text string`) and `p_saveg.c` (`P_WriteSaveGameHeader`, `P_ReadSaveGameHeader`); `src/save/saveHeader.ts`; `test/save/save-header.test.ts` (step 16-006).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 16-007 player-mobj-sector-serialization; 16-009 loadgame-restore; 17-010 final gate

## F-176

- fact: Vanilla Doom savegame core archives have three load-bearing binary layouts. `P_ArchivePlayers` pads each active player slot to the next 4-byte boundary before writing a fixed 280-byte `player_t` payload; after the 50-byte header, the first active player therefore starts at byte offset 52. `P_ArchiveThinkers` writes one-byte thinker class markers (`tc_mobj = 1`, `tc_end = 0`), pads each `tc_mobj` record start to the next 4-byte boundary, then writes a fixed 154-byte `mobj_t` payload. `P_ArchiveWorld` writes each sector as 7 int16 values (14 bytes: floor/ceiling heights, pics, light, special, tag) and each linedef as 3 int16 values plus 10 bytes per present side; sector heights and side row/texture offsets are serialized in map units via `>> FRACBITS` and restored via `<< FRACBITS`, so the savegame stores only the high 16 bits of those fixed-point values. `P_ArchiveWorld` omits absent sides entirely based on `sidenum[j] == -1`, and `mobj_t.player` is serialized as a 1-based player slot (`0` means null).
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `p_saveg.c` (`saveg_write_player_t`, `saveg_write_mobj_t`, `P_ArchivePlayers`, `P_ArchiveWorld`, `P_ArchiveThinkers`); `src/save/coreSerialization.ts`; `test/save/core-serialization.test.ts` (step 16-007).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 16-008 special-thinker-serialization; 16-009 loadgame-restore; 17-010 final gate

## F-177

- fact: The split specials save section in `src/save/specialSerialization.ts` is a fixed 3024-byte snapshot prefix followed by a `p_saveg.c`-ordered thinker stream. The snapshot prefix is exactly 30 active-plat entries _ 48 bytes + 30 active-ceiling entries _ 40 bytes + 16 button entries \* 24 bytes. Active plat and ceiling tables use `sectorIndex = -1` as the null-slot sentinel; button slots use `btimer = 0` as the null-slot sentinel. The thinker stream keeps the canonical vanilla class order `ceiling=0`, `door=1`, `floor=2`, `plat=3`, `flash=4`, `strobe=5`, `glow=6`, `end=7`. Registry-owned ceilings and plats serialize as 4-byte slot references only, keyed to the earlier snapshot tables, while direct door/floor/flash/strobe/glow thinkers serialize full payloads with the 12-byte thinker header and vanilla field widths (`door=40`, `floor=42`, `flash=36`, `strobe=36`, `glow=28`). The 42-byte floor payload is load-bearing because, when the section starts 4-byte aligned, it moves the following plat reference onto a 2-byte boundary and therefore yields only a 1-byte post-class pad instead of the more common 3-byte pad. The reader treats unknown thinker classes and plat/ceiling references to empty snapshot slots as save-format errors.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `p_saveg.c` (`P_ArchiveSpecials`, `P_UnArchiveSpecials`); `src/save/specialSerialization.ts`; `test/save/special-serialization.test.ts` (step 16-008).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 16-009 loadgame-restore; 17-007 save-load-roundtrip-suite; 17-008 vanilla-quirk-regression-suite; 17-010 final gate

## F-178

- fact: Vanilla `G_DoLoadGame` restores a save in a strict 6-stage sequence: read and version-check the 50-byte header; call `G_InitNew(gameskill, gameepisode, gamemap)` to reload the base level; restore the saved 24-bit `leveltime` because `G_InitNew` clobbers it; unarchive players, then world, then thinkers, then specials; and finally require a trailing `SAVEGAME_EOF` byte of `0x1D`. A header version mismatch returns early without touching the base level, while a missing or wrong EOF marker raises `I_Error("Bad savegame")`.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `g_game.c` (`G_DoLoadGame`), `p_saveg.c` (`P_ReadSaveGameHeader`, `P_ReadSaveGameEOF`), `p_saveg.h` (`SAVEGAME_EOF`), `src/save/loadgame.ts`, and `test/save/loadgame.test.ts` (step 16-009).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 16-010 vanilla-limit-enforcement; 17-007 save-load-roundtrip-suite; 17-010 final gate

## F-179

- fact: Vanilla Doom enforces the savegame size ceiling only AFTER writing the trailing EOF byte: `G_DoSaveGame` calls `P_WriteSaveGameEOF()` and then checks `ftell(save_stream) > SAVEGAMESIZE` with `SAVEGAMESIZE = 0x2C000`. The boundary is strict, so a final length of exactly `0x2C000` bytes is accepted while `0x2C001` and above raise `I_Error("Savegame buffer overrun")`. Setting `vanilla_savegame_limit = 0` disables this overrun check entirely.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `g_game.c` (`G_DoSaveGame`), `p_saveg.c` (`P_WriteSaveGameEOF`), `src/save/vanillaLimits.ts`, and `test/save/vanilla-limits.test.ts` (step 16-010).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 17-007 save-load-roundtrip-suite; 17-010 final gate

## F-180

- fact: The shareware C1 tic-0 level-start hash boundary is "after map load and mapthing spawning, before the first gameplay tic". For startup skill 2 (`Hurt me plenty`) this means: (1) automap state is still the pristine `createAutomapState()` file-static default because `AM_Start` has not run yet; (2) the player component is post-`playerReborn` / player-map-object spawn / `setupPsprites`, so the player owns fist+pistol, has 50 bullets, `pendingweapon = WP_NOCHANGE`, and the weapon psprite is already in its raise state; (3) the thinker population is built in original mapthing order with single-player filtering (`type 1` spawns the player avatar once, `types 2..4` and `11` do not spawn, `MTF_NOT_SINGLE` is skipped, and startup skill 2 requires `MTF_NORMAL`), and every spawned map object consumes one `P_Random()` call for `lastlook`; (4) the sectors component must include live `sector.special` values, post-init `line.special` values, and mutable sidedef texture-offset / texture-name state, while excluding framebuffer contents and renderer caches. The resulting shareware E1 thinker-count / `prndindex` pairs are: E1M1 92/92, E1M2 200/200, E1M3 310/54, E1M4 201/201, E1M5 216/216, E1M6 370/114, E1M7 267/11, E1M8 99/99, E1M9 192/192.

## F-182

- fact: `playerReborn()` seeds both `attackdown` and `usedown` true, so held input remains latched until a release is observed by the corresponding ready/use gate. In the scripted mechanics parity fixture this means a rocket-launcher attack held from respawn does not enter `MISSILE1` until a ready-state release clears `attackdown`, and a held use press does not activate repeatable door special `1` until release, after which the next re-press can reverse the active door without replaying the open sound. Both `DOOM.EXE` and `DOOMD.EXE` embed the distinct blue-key denial strings `You need a blue key to open this door` (manual `-K`) and `You need a blue key to activate this object` (tagged `-O`), so those branches can be locked without consulting the WAD.

## F-184

- fact: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `D_IdentifyVersion` handles unknown IWAD filenames with a single forward directory scan. The first encountered `MAP01` sets the mission to Doom II, while the first encountered `E1M1` sets the mission to Doom. If both naming schemes coexist in a non-standard IWAD, directory order decides the fallback mission; there is no unconditional global `MAP01`-over-`E1M1` priority.

## F-185

- fact: JavaScript typed-array constructors apply `ToIndex` to their length argument, so they silently coerce `NaN` and small negative fractions like `-0.5` to `0` and truncate positive fractions like `1.5` to `1`; only truly negative integer lengths throw. Public renderer/cache allocators therefore need an explicit `Number.isInteger(value) && value >= 0` guard when the Doom-side contract is "exact row count" rather than "best-effort index coercion."
- source: Audit of `src/render/visplaneSpans.ts` (step 13-009) plus direct Bun 1.3.12 probes of `new Int32Array(-0.5)`, `new Int32Array(1.5)`, and `new Int32Array(NaN)`.
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 13-010 sky-semantics; 15-012 audio-parity-harness; 17-010 final gate

## F-186

- fact: When a TypeScript API models a C pointer parameter as `number | null`, a raw numeric `0` must be normalized to `null` (or rejected) at the boundary to preserve vanilla pointer truthiness. Chocolate Doom's `if (origin && origin != listener)` sound-origin guard treats `0` exactly like `NULL`; a JS check of `origin !== null` incorrectly routes `0` through the spatial-adjust and origin-dedup branches.
- source: Chocolate Doom `src/doom/s_sound.c` `S_StartSound` pointer guard plus audit/fix of `src/audio/soundSystem.ts` and `test/audio/sound-order.test.ts` (step 15-005).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 15-004 sound-origin-updates; 15-011 music-device-integration; 17-010 final gate

The boundary is strict, so an exact 65536-byte composite buffer is accepted, and the next composite column triggers the `>64k` fatal path.

## F-191

- fact: The step `17-007` save/load parity fixture locks a synthetic C1 savegame with fixed section sizes `header=50`, `players=282`, `world=70`, `mobjs=313`, `specials=3025`, and `total=3741` bytes, plus a total SHA-256 of `027C8DAB34C3DEFEA02FA374BC249651DF7CA2DD8625D1EAB831FB0D9EB3D323`. - confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 17-008 vanilla-quirk-regression-suite; 17-010 final gate

## F-192

- fact: Chocolate Doom writes psprite state slots as `0` for null and raw positive `state - states` values for live psprites; on load, `saveg_read_pspdef_t` treats any non-positive value as null. By contrast, `saveg_write_mobj_t` writes raw zero-based `state - states` for mobjs and `saveg_read_mobj_t` unconditionally indexes `states[saveg_read32()]`, so negative mobj state indices are never canonical savegame output.
- source: Chocolate Doom 2.2.1 `p_saveg.c` (`saveg_read_pspdef_t`, `saveg_write_pspdef_t`, `saveg_read_mobj_t`, `saveg_write_mobj_t`) plus audit/fix of `src/save/coreSerialization.ts` and `test/save/core-serialization.test.ts` (step 16-007).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 16-009 loadgame-restore; 17-007 save-load-roundtrip-suite; 17-010 final gate

## F-193

- fact: In vanilla `am_map.c`, the file-static automap defaults initialize `scale_mtof` to `INITSCALEMTOF` but leave `scale_ftom` at C's zero-initialized default until `AM_LevelInit` computes the reciprocal. `doom_codex` intentionally normalizes `createAutomapState().scale_ftom` to `FixedDiv(FRACUNIT, INITSCALEMTOF)` so the exported pure automap helpers always start from a reciprocal scale pair; this affects only pre-`AM_LevelInit` snapshots, not observable vanilla automap runtime behavior.
- source: Chocolate Doom `src/doom/am_map.c` (`static fixed_t scale_mtof = (fixed_t)INITSCALEMTOF; static fixed_t scale_ftom;`), `src/ui/automap.ts`, and `test/parity/level-start-state-hash.test.ts` (audit of step 14-004).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 14-004 automap; 17-001 level-start-state-hashes; 17-010 final gate

## F-194

- fact: The step `17-008` quirk fixture locks 16 discrete parity boundaries across the existing pure modules: both bundled DOS executables share the anchor strings `Bad savegame`, `Demo is from a different game version!`, `game saved.`, `High detail`, `Low detail`, `Messages OFF`, `Messages ON`, `press a key.`, `Savegame`, `snd_channels`, `snd_musicdevice`, `snd_sfxdevice`, `You need a blue key to activate this object`, and `You need a blue key to open this door`; `CF_GODMODE` stays `2` while `CF_NOMOMENTUM` stays `4`; secret sectors credit only on-floor and clear their special immediately; E1M8 exit sectors strip godmode and exit even off the damage cadence; suited strobe sectors still consume one RNG call on non-damage tics; `dmxByteToInt16(128)` stays `128`; `computeStereoGains(127, 255)` stays `{ left: -1, right: 255 }`; `clipToInt16(-0.5)` and `applyTotalLevel(-1, 63)` both normalize back to positive zero; `mixVoices` zero-fills reused output buffers; YM3812 channel `3` uses operator offsets `8` and `11`; operator waveform decode masks `0xFF` down to waveform `3`; the multiplier-table tail stays `[20, 20, 24, 24, 30, 30]`; FM algorithm `0` returns only the carrier sample; and `advancePhase(0, -1)` wraps to `2^20 - 1` rather than clamping.
- source: `test/parity/fixtures/quirkCases.json`, `test/parity/quirk-regressions.test.ts`, `doom/universal-doom/DOOM.EXE`, and `doom/universal-doom/DOOMD.EXE` (step 17-008).
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 17-009 full-shareware-e1-acceptance; 17-010 final gate

## F-196

- fact: Bun 1.3.12 throws a `TypeError` when `Object.freeze()` is applied to a non-empty typed array, so parser APIs that expose typed-array views can only freeze the outer container unless they first copy the bytes into a different representation.
- source: Direct Bun 1.3.12 runtime probe in `doom_codex` (`Object.freeze(new Uint8Array([1, 2, 3]))`)
- confidence: high
- verified: verified
- future_steps: 05-004, 13-003, 17-010
